###### 2026.1.0-rc1 — first release under the new CalVer scheme (changes since 26.1.x Beta release 6):
- **Worlds and inventories from older BuildCraft versions keep their machines and items.** BuildCraft's block/item IDs shifted twice on the way to 26.1 — the eight historical submods (`buildcraftcore`, `buildcrafttransport`, …) were unified into the single `buildcraftunofficial` namespace, and a few items were renamed (e.g. chipsets went `redstone_<material>_chipset` → `chipset_<material>`). Without translation, every BuildCraft block and item in an older save silently turned to air or vanished from chests on load. A new [LegacyAliases](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/registry/LegacyAliases.java) registrar now maps every old ID — across all historical namespaces, both rename forms, and the data components on painted pipes / paintbrushes / fluid containers — onto its current equivalent, so loading a **1.21.11 or early-26.1** world restores placed pipes, engines, tanks (with their fluid contents) and full inventories. Worlds from **1.12.2** recover their *inventory* items (pipes, gears, machines, plugs); placed 1.12.2 machines can't be restored because Minecraft's pre-1.13 block flattening replaces unknown modded blocks with air before any mod code runs. Pre-1.13 metadata items that became several separate items (the redstone chipset's 8 damage variants, the 16 wire colours) collapse to a primary variant — the stack survives even if its exact variant differs. A table-driven game test asserts every registered alias resolves to a live entry.
- **The Guide Book no longer hitches (~0.75 s) the first time it's opened in a session.** Its content load — parsing all 155 pages, populating the 21 guide groups (333 members), and building the suffix-array search index ([GuideManager.reload0](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/GuideManager.java), measured at 758 ms on the render thread) — used to run lazily inside the first `openGuideScreen` call, freezing the game for the better part of a second the first time you opened the book. It now warms once at first world-join via a `ClientPlayerNetworkEvent.LoggingIn` listener in [BCLibClient](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/BCLibClient.java), so the cost is absorbed into the "Loading world" screen and every guide open is instant. `GuideManager.ensureLoaded()` no-ops once the cache is populated, so it runs once per session (not per join), and the synchronous load in `openGuideScreen` stays as a fallback for any pre-join open path. Same render thread and code path as before — just triggered where the loading screen hides it (the same move applied earlier to the facade scan vs. the JEI first-screen-open path).
- **Opening any GUI for the first time in a session no longer hitches for ~1.5 seconds.** JEI starts its runtime lazily on the first screen opened, and BuildCraft's [BCSiliconJeiPlugin](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/compat/jei/BCSiliconJeiPlugin.java) was the dominant cost inside that startup: `onRuntimeAvailable` let all ~1357 facade variants (every wrappable block × basic/hollow, harvested from the Facades creative tab) enter JEI's ingredient list, then stripped all but one with `removeIngredientsAtRuntime` — which rebuilds JEI's search structures and was measured at ~1.49 s on the render thread (the bulk of JEI's ~2.3 s lazy start). The facades are now kept out of the recipe viewer up front by tagging `plug_facade` with the conventional [c:hidden_from_recipe_viewers](src/main/resources/data/c/tags/item/hidden_from_recipe_viewers.json) item tag — JEI marks them invisible for free during its normal harvest — and the whole `onRuntimeAvailable` removal pass is deleted. Facades still appear in the survival/creative menu (the tag only affects recipe viewers), the Assembly Table catalyst still browses every variant, and pressing **U** on any wrappable block still surfaces its facade recipe (verified against JEI 29.5's `RecipeSlot`, which renders a uniformly-hidden cycling slot in full rather than blank). The only behavioural change: facades no longer show up in JEI's item-list panel or its text search — discovery now goes through the Assembly Table or block→facade lookup. The facade *computation* and visual dedup were already moved to world-join in an earlier pass, so this removes the last facade cost from the GUI-open path.
- **Facade assembly-table input redirects are now consistent on dedicated servers.** The "use any block that shares a facade's textures as an assembly input" convenience (e.g. crafting a bricks facade from a brick slab) is derived from baked block models, which exist only on the client — so on a dedicated server it silently did nothing while single-player honored it. The redirect table is now explicitly gated to the integrated server (single-player / LAN host) via `FacadeDeduplicator.applyRedirectAuthority`, with the invariant that `FacadeStateManager.stackRedirects` is non-empty only when the server reading it will honor it. The de-duplicated facade *list* itself is unchanged and works everywhere, and slab-type blocks still craft a visually identical facade via their own full-cube state; only the cross-block input convenience is unavailable on dedicated servers (tracked in todos for a possible client→server sync). Two game tests pin the recipe's behavior with an empty vs. populated redirect table.
- **The Architect Table connects to item pipes again**, so you can pipe blank Blueprints/Templates into it and pull finished snapshots out automatically — as it did in 1.12.2. In the 1.21 capability port a block entity's inventory is only visible to pipes if its type is registered for `Capabilities.Item.BLOCK`; an earlier sweep ([MachinePipeConnectivityTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/factory/MachinePipeConnectivityTester.java)) caught five machines but missed the Architect because its two snapshot slots had been rewritten from a `ItemHandlerManager` into plain `ItemStack` fields, exposing no handler at all. The slots are restored to the 1.12.2 `ItemHandlerManager` form — an INSERT-access input (accepts any snapshot) and an EXTRACT-access output — in [TileArchitectTable](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileArchitectTable.java) (NBT now round-trips through the shared item manager, with a one-time migration of the old `invSnapshotIn`/`invSnapshotOut` keys), and `ARCHITECT` is registered for `Capabilities.Item.BLOCK` in [BCBuilders](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/BCBuilders.java). The **Mining Well** now also renders an item-pipe connection (it pushes mined drops out itself and never had an internal buffer, so it exposes an empty handler purely for the connection, matching the **Quarry** and the role 1.12.2's `AutomaticProvidingTransactor` played) — fixed in [BCFactory](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/BCFactory.java). Two new game tests pin the Architect (a wood pipe extracts a finished blueprint from the output slot; a clay pipe inserts a blank blueprint into the input slot) and the capability-sweep regression net gains the Architect Table and Mining Well.
- **Pipes in the snapshot 3D preview now render as their real, connected selves** instead of a stack of identical **Wooden Diamond FE Pipes standing on end**. Every pipe shares the single `pipe_holder` block (type/colour/connections live in the block entity), so the preview's per-cell `new ItemStack(state.getBlock())` resolved through `Block.asItem()` → `Item.BY_BLOCK`, where `BlockItem.registerBlocks` is last-write-wins for a shared block — the winner being the last `ItemPipeHolder` registered, `pipe_diamond_wood_rf` ([BCTransportItems.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/BCTransportItems.java)). Every pipe cell therefore drew that one item's connectionless, vertical 3-cube *item* model ([PipeItemModel](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/model/PipeItemModel.java)). The preview now detects pipe cells and rebuilds each pipe's actual model from its captured block-entity NBT: a render-only stub [IPipeHolder](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/transport/pipe/IPipeHolder.java) lets [PipePreviewModel](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/client/render/pip/PipePreviewModel.java) construct a [Pipe](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/Pipe.java) from the stored `"pipe"` tag (the `Pipe` constructor restores per-side connections from the packed `"con"` field), then `Pipe.getModel()` yields the true `PipeModelKey` and new `PipeModelKey` overloads on [ModelPipe](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/model/ModelPipe.java) emit the same connection-aware cutout + paint-overlay block-model quads the pipe shows in-world (into the PiP buffer on the block atlas, like the fluid-cell path). The quads go through **back-face-culling** render types (`entityCutoutCull`, plus a new culling `BCLibRenderTypes.entityTranslucentCull` for the paint overlay, since the only stock culling-translucent type targets the wrong framebuffer): the pipe model emits front + inverted-"inside" coplanar quad pairs and relies on culling to drop the inside one, so the no-cull entity types used elsewhere made the depth-writing cutout pair z-fight (flickering as the preview spins), exactly as the in-world pipe avoids by rendering through the culling block sheet. [BlueprintPipRenderer](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/client/render/pip/BlueprintPipRenderer.java) gains a pipe branch ahead of the generic item path and falls back to it if a capture has no usable pipe data; the captured NBT reaches it through a new `ISchematicBlock.getTileNbtForRender()` ([ISchematicBlock](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/schematics/ISchematicBlock.java)) that [SchematicBlockDefault](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/SchematicBlockDefault.java) overrides to expose its `tileNbt`. Connections come from the pipe's *scan-time* `con`, so they include real connections to neighbouring machines as well as pipes; a pipe that was connected to something outside the captured region shows a short outward stub toward it. Three game tests in [PipePreviewModelTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/builders/client/render/pip/PipePreviewModelTester.java) pin the model-key reconstruction without a GL context: **every** registered pipe definition rebuilds to a key carrying its own definition (also proving offline `Pipe` construction never touches the world), the packed connection bits decode into the key's per-side distances, and missing/unknown NBT degrades to `null` for graceful fallback.
- Restored the **3D hover preview for used Templates**, which had rendered nothing since the port (used Blueprints previewed fine). The 1.21 port's [BlueprintRenderer](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/client/render/BlueprintRenderer.java) hard-rejected any snapshot that wasn't a `Blueprint`, with a comment asserting this "matched the 1.12.2 behavior where templates rendered empty." That assertion was wrong: 1.12.2's `FakeWorld.uploadSnapshot` painted every set bit of a [Template](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/Template.java) as a solid quartz block, giving the rough 3D outline of where blocks would go. The fix follows the original porter's own in-code steer ("broaden the PiP state rather than branching here"): [BlueprintPipRenderState](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/client/render/pip/BlueprintPipRenderState.java) now carries a `Snapshot` rather than a `Blueprint`, and [BlueprintPipRenderer.renderToTexture](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/client/render/pip/BlueprintPipRenderer.java) branches per cell — Blueprints keep their 3D block-item-model + fluid path unchanged, while Templates now draw a translucent green ghost cube at each filled cell, styled to match the Architect Table's in-world scan cubes (the `scan.png` "digitizing" texture through `RenderTypes.entityTranslucent`) at 50% opacity. Faces shared with an adjacent filled cell are culled, so a solid template reads as a clean outer shell instead of a haze of stacked translucent quads. The same render path feeds every snapshot preview call site (item tooltip, Architect Table, Replacer), so all of them gain template support uniformly. Strikes the **Investigate how templates render in 3D** finalization bullet from [todos.md](todos.md).
- Removed the leftover **Integration Table** placeholder from the guide book — the block is gated to dev-only and isn't shipping in this release, so its auto-stubbed "(WIP)" entry is dropped along with its `place` registration in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) and its inventory entry in [blocks_buildcraft_inventories.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/builders/buildcraft/blocks_buildcraft_inventories.json). No other guide page referenced it; the block itself, its lang strings, item model, and mining tag are left intact (still registered, dev-gated).
- **Guide Book: custom table-of-contents ordering.** Entries can now carry an explicit sort weight, so chapters and pages are no longer forced into strict alphabetical order. [PageEntry](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/entry/PageEntry.java) reads an optional `"sort"` int from its registration JSON (default 0) onto the page's [PageLink](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/contents/PageLink.java); [ContentsNode.sort](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/contents/ContentsNode.java) orders by weight first then alphabetically, and a chapter inherits the **lowest** weight among its members (so weighting a subtype's pages also positions the subtype itself). All-zero weights reproduce the historical alphabetical order exactly, and the **Sort Alphabetically** view deliberately ignores weights so it stays a strict A–Z list (the `ContentsNode` for that order is flagged `ignoreSortWeight`). New opt-in `_s` aliases in [util.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/util.txt) (`pipe_item_s` / `pipe_fluid_s` / `pipe_power_s` / `pipe_rf_s`, plus the shared `pipe_s` / `item_stack_s` bases) thread the weight through the existing `add_basic` JSON, leaving every unweighted entry untouched. Applied to the Pipes chapter in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt): the subtypes are banded (Item 0+, Fluid 1000+, Power 2000+, Structure 3000, FE 9000+) so it now reads Item Transport → Fluid → Power → Structure → FE Transport, each group led by its Wooden pipe, while the Pipes chapter keeps its alphabetical place among Blocks/Items (its lowest member weight is 0). Pinned by [ContentsNodeSortTest](src/test/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/ContentsNodeSortTest.java).
- Fixed four **Guide Book table-of-contents / sorting** regressions against 1.12.2. **(1)** Clicking the **Sort By Type** icon opened the search box instead of re-sorting: 1.12.2 hit-tested the three order icons and the search tab in one handler (icons first, with an early return), but the port split search-tab focus into [GuidePageContents.mouseClicked](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/contents/GuidePageContents.java) — which `GuiGuide.mouseClicked` runs *before* the order handler in `handleMouseClick` — and the search tab's generous 40×34 hitbox (carried over verbatim from 1.12.2) overlaps the first icon's top-right corner, so it swallowed the click. A guard (`isOverOrderIcon`) now lets a click on any order icon fall through to the re-sort. **(2)** On a window too narrow for the side chapter tabs, the **"Chapters" tab** at the top of the right page — which opens a centered overlay menu as a compromise — had been dropped during the port ([drawOpen](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/GuiGuide.java) just hid the chapter list with "Simplified for small screens"). Restored the `showingContentsMenu` toggle, the tab, the floating menu, and its open/close/select click handling in [GuiGuide](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/GuiGuide.java) — the `FLOATING_CHAPTER_MENU` constant and `GuideChapter`'s central-draw path already existed but were unreachable. **(3)** **Sort By Mod** showed three top-level chapters (`Actions`, `BuildCraft`, `Triggers`) instead of one `BuildCraft`, and **(4) Sort Alphabetically** kept chapter groupings instead of going flat. Both stem from [GuideManager.generateContentsPage](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/GuideManager.java) filing auto-iterated entries (Triggers/Actions, and the consolidated category links like Filler Patterns / Pipe Signals) as a top-level chapter in *every* sort order, ignoring the order — whereas regular Block/Item/Pipe entries place via `JsonTypeTags.getOrdered` and respect it. A new order-aware `fileExtraEntry` / `placeExtraEntryInOrder` files them flat under Alphabetical (no chapters), nested under the single `BuildCraft` mod chapter (sub-grouped by type) under Sort By Mod, and as their own top-level chapter under Sort By Type (unchanged). Pinned by [GuideContentsOrderTest](src/test/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/GuideContentsOrderTest.java).
- The nine **FE (Forge Energy) Pipes** now have real guide-book writeups, mirroring the kinesis power-pipe pages: [wood_rf](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/pipe/wood_rf.md), cobble, stone, quartz, iron, gold, sandstone, diamond, and the [Wooden Diamond FE Pipe](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/pipe/diamond_wood_rf.md) — previously auto-stubbed "(WIP)" leaves under Pipes → FE Transport. They reuse the power pages' structure but are corrected for what genuinely differs on the FE side: the names (`… FE Pipe`); the default caps from [BCTransportConfig.registerRfTransferData](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/BCTransportConfig.java) (Cobblestone 40 → Stone 80 → Wooden / Sandstone 160 → Quartz / Iron 320 → Golden 1,280 → Diamond / Wooden Diamond 2,560 FE/t at the default `baseRfRate`, i.e. 10× the MJ figures); the absence of transfer loss (`RedstoneFluxTransferInfo` carries no resistance term, so the lossiest/least-lossy language from the MJ pages is dropped); and FE-appropriate sourcing — the Wooden / Wooden Diamond inputs draw FE from an [MJ Dynamo](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/mj_dynamo.md) or another mod's generator and feed the [FE Engine](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/engine_rf.md) and other consumers, not the MJ engines / Pipe Adapter the kinesis pages cite. A new `pipe_rf` alias in [util.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/util.txt) flips the nine `place "pipe_*_rf" "pipe" "pipe_rf"` rows in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) to it (files now under `pipe/`, rendering under Pipes → FE Transport rather than as runtime stubs); the Iron / Diamond FE cross-links in [concept/set_power_limit.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/concept/set_power_limit.md) are repointed from `placeholder/` to `pipe/`. The Iron / Diamond FE limiters reuse the per-pipe Set Power Limit groups added above, so their "Linked To" already lists only their own seven RF levels. The diamond-wood FE/RF pipe is also renamed in [en_us.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/lang/en_us.json) from "Emerald FE/RF Pipe" to **"Wooden Diamond FE/RF Pipe"**, so all four of its categories (Transport, Fluid, Kinesis, FE) share the consistent "Wooden Diamond" name — the neglected FE variant had carried over the pipe's pre-rename emerald naming. The same pass retitles the pipe's filter-GUI menu key `gui.buildcraftunofficial.pipe_diamond_wood.title` from "Emerald Pipe" to "Wooden Diamond Pipe" — a referenced-but-unrendered title ([GuiDiamondWoodPipe](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/gui/GuiDiamondWoodPipe.java) suppresses the vanilla label draw), so the leftover name is gone everywhere it is wired even though it does not show on screen.
- The nine **MJ Kinesis (power) Pipes** now have real, basic guide-book writeups instead of auto-stubbed "(WIP)" placeholders: [wood_power](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/pipe/wood_power.md), cobble, stone, quartz, iron, gold, sandstone, diamond, and [diamond_wood_power](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/pipe/diamond_wood_power.md). Each page names the pipe's role and its default transfer cap from [BCTransportConfig.registerPowerTransferData](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/BCTransportConfig.java) (Cobblestone 4 → Stone 8 → Wooden / Sandstone 16 → Quartz / Iron 32 → Golden 128 → Diamond / Wooden-Diamond 256 MJ/t at the default `basePowerRate`), and spells out the three behaviours that actually distinguish them: the **Wooden** and **Wooden Diamond** pipes are the network's power *input* — engines feed them because only receiver pipes expose `CAP_RECEIVER` ([PipeBehaviourWoodPower](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourWoodPower.java) + the `isReceiver` path in [PipeFlowPower](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/flow/PipeFlowPower.java), gated by [EngineConnector.canConnect](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/engine/EngineConnector.java)) and won't connect to one another; the **Iron** and **Diamond** pipes are 7-step power limiters cycled by wrench or set by a gate's Set Power Limit actions ([PipeBehaviourLimiter](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourLimiter.java)); and **Sandstone** connects only to other pipes, never to a block, so it routes power straight past a machine ([PipeBehaviourSandstone](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourSandstone.java)). A new `pipe_power` alias in [util.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/util.txt) (mirroring `pipe_item` / `pipe_fluid`, replacing the stale "no pipe_power … gone soonish" note) flips the nine `place "pipe_*_power" "pipe" "pipe_power"` rows in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) to `pipe_power` entries, so the `.md` files are `git mv`'d from `placeholder/` to `pipe/` and render under Pipes → Power Transport rather than as runtime stubs. The two MJ-pipe cross-links in [concept/set_power_limit.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/concept/set_power_limit.md) are repointed from `placeholder/` to `pipe/`; the Iron / Diamond **RF** links there are left as placeholders since those pipes are still stubs. Writing the pages also surfaced a grouping bug: each limiter pipe's auto **"Linked To: Set Power Limit"** list was showing all 28 limit actions (both MJ tiers *and* the FE/RF variants) because all four limiter pipes shared one `set_power_limit` guide group whose entries are actually partitioned per pipe (unlike `paint_pipe_colour` / `set_pipe_direction`, whose actions are genuinely shared by every key pipe). The single group is split into four single-pipe groups in [GuideGroupManager](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/ref/GuideGroupManager.java) — each keyed to one pipe with only its own seven actions, plus four `buildcraft.guide.group.to.buildcraft.set_power_limit_*` lang keys — so an Iron Kinesis page now lists only its seven MJ levels; the original aggregate group is kept key-less, purely to back the umbrella "Set Power Limit" category page under Actions. The **Pipes / Power** bullet is struck from [todos.md](todos.md)'s guide-book punch list.
- The **Gate Copier** now has a real guide-book writeup at [item/gate_copier.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/gate_copier.md) — covers the copy / paste / clear loop the tool actually implements: interacting with a configured [Gate](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/plug_gate.md) reads its configuration onto an empty copier and a configured copier pastes onto another gate, both routed through [PluggableGate.interactWithCopier](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/plug/PluggableGate.java) (checked ahead of the gate GUI in `onPluggableActivate`, so holding the copier paste-clicks down a row of gates without the screen opening). The page is explicit about the two things players trip on: it transfers <bold>configuration only</bold> — the connections and trigger/action statement pairs from [GateLogic.writeToNbt](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/gate/GateLogic.java) / `readConfigData`, never the gate's `variant`, so it can't change an AND gate to OR or an Iron gate to Gold — and pasting onto a gate with fewer slots keeps only the statements that fit (the read loop is bounded by the *destination* gate's `statements.length`). Also documents the filled-vs-blank item texture (the `CustomModelData` switch in [ItemGateCopier.updateModelData](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/item/ItemGateCopier.java)), the "this gate has no configuration to copy" guard (`GateLogic.hasConfiguration`), and the sneak-use-in-air clear (`ItemGateCopier.use`). The `place "gate_copier" "item" "tool"` row in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) flips to `tool "gate_copier"`, the `.md` file is `git mv`'d from `placeholder/` to `item/`, and the **Items / Tools** bullet is struck from [todos.md](todos.md)'s guide-book punch list.
- The Timer pluggable now has a real guide-book writeup at [item/plug_timer.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/plug_timer.md) — covers the three repeating gate triggers it exposes to any Gate on the same pipe (the 5 / 10 / 15 Sec Timers, each a one-tick pulse fired every 100 / 200 / 300 game ticks per [TriggerTimer](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/statement/TriggerTimer.java)), the one-plug-serves-all-three design (the rate is picked in the Gate's trigger menu, not on the plug, so a single Timer covers every cadence), and the standard any-pipe-face placement that severs the connection it sits between. Cross-links the three trigger pages ([timer_short](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/trigger/timer_short.md), [timer_medium](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/trigger/timer_medium.md), [timer_long](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/trigger/timer_long.md)) the same way [plug_light_sensor.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/plug_light_sensor.md) links its Bright/Dark triggers; the Assembly Table recipe (a vanilla Clock for 500 MJ) surfaces through the standard `<recipes>` / `<usages>` widgets. The `place "plug_timer" "item" "pipe_plug"` row in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) flips to `plug "plug_timer"`, the `.md` file is `git mv`'d from `placeholder/` to `item/`, and `plug_timer` is struck from the **Items / Pluggables** bullet on [todos.md](todos.md)'s guide-book punch list.
- Clocks and compasses no longer leak the live world time/heading when drawn in the guide book and BuildCraft's own GUIs — the Plug (timer) crafting recipe in the guide was the reported case, where the rendered clock ran with the day cycle. In MC 26.1 the `GuiGraphicsExtractor.item(stack, x, y)` convenience overload resolves the item model against the live `minecraft.player` + `minecraft.level`, so the dynamic `minecraft:time` / `minecraft:compass` range-dispatch models drew their *current* frame. The six sites that display a player-supplied stack now use the `fakeItem` (null-holder) overload, which short-circuits `NeedleDirectionHelper.get` to `0.0` — the static `clock_00` (noon) / north frame, exactly as vanilla renders these items out-of-world: [GuidePartItem.drawItemStack](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/GuidePartItem.java) (guide recipe grids: crafting/smelting/assembly), [GuiStack.drawAt](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/GuiStack.java), [GuiAutoCraftItems](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/gui/GuiAutoCraftItems.java) (material filters), [GuiList](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/list/GuiList.java) (list examples), [ParameterRenderer](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/statement/ParameterRenderer.java) (gate parameters), and [GuiFilteredBuffer](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/gui/GuiFilteredBuffer.java) (filter slots). Fixed-icon call sites (engine gears, Builder mode/chest/barrier icons) keep the live overload since they never display a clock or compass. The same leak also hit the machine **preview/ghost slots** — the Advanced Crafting Table and Auto Workbench blueprint grids and result previews — which render through vanilla's `AbstractContainerScreen.renderSlotContents`; that path already chooses `fakeItem` vs `item` based on `Slot.isFake()`, so [SlotPhantom](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/slot/SlotPhantom.java) (filter/template/blueprint ghosts) and [SlotDisplay](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/slot/SlotDisplay.java) (read-only result previews) now report `isFake() = true`. This fixes the same family of intangible slots mod-wide — the diamond/wood/emzuli pipe filters, Filtered Buffer, Logistics List, Assembly/Integration table outputs, and Builder preview — while genuinely tangible slots (`SlotBase` / `SlotOutput`) keep live rendering. (`isFake()` is render-only — vanilla reads it nowhere else — and vanilla's own pickup-able crafting `ResultSlot` is `isFake`, so flagging these is behavior-safe.) The same leak also hit the machine **preview/ghost slots** — the Advanced Crafting Table and Auto Workbench blueprint grids and result previews — which render through vanilla's `AbstractContainerScreen.renderSlotContents`; that path already chooses `fakeItem` vs `item` based on `Slot.isFake()`, so [SlotPhantom](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/slot/SlotPhantom.java) (filter/template/blueprint ghosts) and [SlotDisplay](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/slot/SlotDisplay.java) (read-only result previews) now report `isFake() = true`. This fixes the same family of intangible slots mod-wide — the diamond/wood/emzuli pipe filters, Filtered Buffer, Logistics List, Assembly/Integration table outputs, and Builder preview — while genuinely tangible slots (`SlotBase` / `SlotOutput`) keep live rendering. (`isFake()` is render-only — vanilla reads it nowhere else — and vanilla's own pickup-able crafting `ResultSlot` is `isFake`, so flagging these is behavior-safe.)
- Rewrote the **Path Mark** guide-book page at [block/marker_path.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/marker_path.md), which the original BuildCraft team had only ever used as a rendering test-bed — the shipped text was misspelled placeholder filler ("woops that was spelt wrong lol", "Path markers are really useless", "HI THIS SHOULD BE ON ANOTHER PAGE") exercising bold/italic/colour/note/new-page markup rather than describing the block. The real writeup covers linking marks into an ordered route with a [Marker Connector](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/marker_connector.md) (preview lasers render only while the connector is held — [MarkerRenderer.renderPossibleConnections](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/render/MarkerRenderer.java)), the free-form (non-axis-locked, unlike a [Land Mark](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/marker_volume.md)) hops bounded by the shared 64-block `markerMaxDistance` limit ([PathSubCache.getValidConnections](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/marker/PathSubCache.java)), the empty-hand right-click that reverses route direction ([BlockMarkerPath.useWithoutItem](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/block/BlockMarkerPath.java) → [PathConnection.reverseDirection](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/marker/PathConnection.java)), the last→first loop, the split/shorten behaviour when a mark is broken ([PathConnection.removeMarker](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/marker/PathConnection.java)), and the two consumers of an `IPathProvider` route: a [Builder](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/builder.md) placed behind one end (copies the route and pops the marks on placement — [TileBuilder.onPlacedBy](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileBuilder.java)) and a clean Map Location that records it ([ItemMapLocation.useOn](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/item/ItemMapLocation.java), `PATH` / `PATH_REPEATING`).
- **Logic Gates recipe display, phase 2: cycling panels.** The OR gate variants and the 24 AND↔OR swap recipes — held back from the previous pass — now appear as compact, animated entries instead of doubling the recipe list. Each gate's Assembly Table entry is a single panel that cycles its AND and OR variants in lock-step (inputs, output and MJ cost all advance to the next recipe together); the swaps become exactly two panels — one AND→OR, one OR→AND — each cycling through all 12 material/modifier variants. A new generic `<recipe_cycle match="substr" [type="assembling"]/>` guide tag ([XmlPageLoader.loadRecipeCycle](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/loader/XmlPageLoader.java)) folds every recipe whose id (or, with `type="assembling"`, registry name) contains `match` into one [GuideCrafting](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideCrafting.java) / [GuideAssembly](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideAssembly.java) panel whose per-slot [ChangingItemStack](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/recipe/ChangingItemStack.java)s share one length — and since [ChangingObject](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/recipe/ChangingObject.java) picks its frame as `(System.currentTimeMillis() / timeGap) % length`, equal-length stacks stay synchronized for free, so recipe N's input and output always show together. The merge lives in [GuideCraftingFactory.getCyclingFactory](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideCraftingFactory.java) and [GuideAssemblyRecipes.getCyclingFactory](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideAssemblyRecipes.java); the substring gathering in [GuideCraftingRecipes.gatherByIdMatch](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideCraftingRecipes.java) / [GuideAssemblyRecipes.gatherByNameMatch](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideAssemblyRecipes.java). [plug_gate.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/plug_gate.md) now lists each gate's crafting recipe followed by its cycling assembly panel, with the two swap panels last — the gate-specific layout stays in page data, the tag stays generic (no gate knowledge in `lib`). The `guide_gate_recipe_cycle_selectors` game test ([GateRecipeVariantTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/silicon/GateRecipeVariantTester.java)) pins that every assembly `match` selects exactly one variant's AND+OR pair and each swap direction has its full 12 crafting recipes; documented in [guide_page_format.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/config/guide_page_format.md).
- The Logic Gates guide page now lists **every AND-logic gate's crafting-table recipe immediately followed by its Assembly Table recipe** — Basic (clay-brick; crafting only) → Iron → Nether Brick → Gold → the modifier upgrades — so a player sees the hand-craftable route (slower, no machine needed) and the assembly route (efficient) side by side. Previously *no* gate crafting recipe showed at all, because the guide's two recipe lookups match a recipe's output differently against the page's query stack: [GuideAssemblyRecipes](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideAssemblyRecipes.java) matches by item only (`ItemStack.isSameItem`), so every gate *assembly* recipe matched the bare `plug_gate` query, whereas [GuideCraftingRecipes](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideCraftingRecipes.java) matches by full components (via [ChangingItemStack](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/recipe/ChangingItemStack.java) → `ItemStack.isSameItemSameComponents`), so no gate *crafting* recipe — whose output always carries the `gate` data components — matched the component-less query. Rather than relax the crafting match (which would drag in the 24 AND↔OR swap recipes plus modifier upgrades in arbitrary order), the `<recipe>` guide tag gained a generic `id` attribute that pins one specific recipe regardless of components: a crafting recipe by ResourceLocation (`<recipe id="buildcraftunofficial:gate_iron_and"/>`) or, with `type="assembling"`, an Assembly Table recipe by its registry name (`<recipe id="gate-and-IRON-NO_MODIFIER" type="assembling"/>`) — resolved in [XmlPageLoader.loadRecipeById](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/loader/XmlPageLoader.java) and [GuideAssemblyRecipes.getFactoryByName](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideAssemblyRecipes.java). [plug_gate.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/plug_gate.md) hand-authors the per-gate crafting→assembly order with these pins; the gate-specific layout stays in the page data, the new tag stays generic (no gate knowledge in `lib`). The OR variants and the 24 swap recipes are intentionally deferred to a planned follow-up that folds them into compact variant-cycling panels (the time-synced [ChangingItemStack](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/recipe/ChangingItemStack.java) the recipe display already supports) rather than doubling the list. A new `guide_gate_assembly_recipe_names_resolve` game test in [GateRecipeVariantTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/silicon/GateRecipeVariantTester.java) pins the contract that every assembly-recipe name the page references exists in [AssemblyRecipeRegistry](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/recipe/AssemblyRecipeRegistry.java) — those derived-string names (`gate-and-<MATERIAL>-<MODIFIER>`, built in [BCSiliconRecipes](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSiliconRecipes.java)) would otherwise turn the tags into red error text silently on a rename. ([GuideCraftingRecipes.getRecipeManager](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideCraftingRecipes.java) widened to `public` for the cross-package lookup.)
- Fixed a **phantom blank final page** on long guide-book entries — the Logic Gates page (a 17-page entry whose last page was empty) being the case that surfaced it. Every blank line in a guide markdown source is turned into a `GuideTextFactory(" ")` (the `line = " "` fallback in [XmlPageLoader.parsePartFactories](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/loader/XmlPageLoader.java)) that renders as an invisible full-height line — deliberate paragraph spacing between paragraphs, but a *trailing* run of them advances the layout cursor onto a fresh page with nothing visible on it, so [GuidePage](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/GuidePage.java)'s `numPages` includes a final page that draws blank (and, being odd, pairs with the back cover in the two-page spread). The parser now strips the trailing run of blank text parts after parsing while keeping interior ones (which are real spacing). Pinned by [XmlPageLoaderTrailingBlankTest](src/test/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/loader/XmlPageLoaderTrailingBlankTest.java) — trailing blanks trimmed, interior blanks kept, all-blank collapses to empty.
- The Gate's guide-book entry — both the **Table of Contents** leaf and the title drawn on the opened page — now reads **"Logic Gates"** instead of **"Basic Gate"**. The page documents the whole gate family (every tier, every Lapis/Quartz/Diamond modifier, and the AND/OR logic variants), but it was registered through the `plug` alias in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt), which derives a TOC title from the stack's localized item name. [ItemPluggableGate.getName](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/item/ItemPluggableGate.java) returns the *default* variant's name for the component-less `plug_gate` stack the guide renders — Clay Brick / AND / no-modifier, i.e. the in-game "Basic Gate" — so the broad family page was mislabeled as the entry-level gate (an unrelated "Basic Gate" gate-recipe display bug was fixed separately earlier in this section). The `plug "plug_gate"` row is converted to an explicit `add "item/plug_gate"` block carrying a `"title": "logic_gates"` override — the same pattern the [Pipe Wires entry](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) uses to read as a family entry rather than a per-colour leaf — backed by a new `buildcraft.guide.page.logic_gates` → "Logic Gates" key in [en_us.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/lang/en_us.json). The suffix resolves through [PageValue.getTitleOverride](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/entry/PageValue.java) (the `buildcraft.guide.page.` prefix is prepended, then localized), which feeds both the TOC leaf and the page header, so the two stay in sync. The `.md` file is untouched at [item/plug_gate.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/plug_gate.md).
- The **Single Block Schematic** now has a real guide-book writeup at [item/schematic_single_used.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/schematic_single_used.md), covering the full lifecycle of the handheld single-block capture tool: capturing a block's state with a blank schematic, placing the stored block (materials drawn from the player's inventory; fluid-bearing blocks can't be hand-placed), sneak-clearing a filled schematic back to blank, and its role as the find/replace ammunition for the [Replacer](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/replacer.md). The page is `git mv`'d from `placeholder/` to `item/` and its [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) row flips from `place "schematic_single_used" "item" "paperwork"` to `paper "schematic_single_used"`. Resolving this surfaced a latent TOC collision: both `schematic_single_clean` and `schematic_single_used` localize to the identical display name "Single Block Schematic", and [ContentsNode](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/contents/ContentsNode.java) stores a chapter's leaves in a `HashMap` keyed by lowercased title, so two same-titled siblings collapse to one — last-writer-wins, and *which* one survived depended on the unspecified iteration order of the guide registry's backing `HashMap` ([SimpleReloadableRegistry](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/script/SimpleReloadableRegistry.java)). It happened to be the `used` entry (so `_clean` "didn't show"), but moving `_used` to a new `item/` key changes that key's hash bucket and could have flipped the survivor to the still-stub `_clean` page, silently hiding the new writeup. Rather than rely on hash order, the redundant `place "schematic_single_clean" "item" "paperwork"` registration is dropped and `placeholder/schematic_single_clean.md` is `git rm`'d, leaving `schematic_single_used` as the sole, deterministic "Single Block Schematic" entry; the one inline link that targeted the clean stub — in [block/replacer.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/replacer.md) — is repointed to `item/schematic_single_used`, which is also a correctness fix since [TileReplacer](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileReplacer.java)'s find/replace slots only accept *used* (filled) schematics. The whole **Items / Paperwork** bullet is struck from [todos.md](todos.md)'s guide-book punch list: `schematic_single_used` is now written, `_clean` no longer has a TOC entry, and `decorated_laser` is not shipping for release (its eventual removal is captured as a new Finalization bullet instead).
- Fixed **gear crafting recipes (and any all-tag recipe) showing an empty input grid in the Guide Book** even though JEI displayed them correctly. The guide's ingredient resolver built its `SlotDisplay` `ContextMap` without `SlotDisplayContext.REGISTRIES`, so MC 26.1's `TagSlotDisplay` resolved every tag-based ingredient (`#c:gears/wooden`, `#c:rods/wooden`, …) to an empty stream; because the gear recipes are made entirely of tag ingredients, their whole input grid rendered blank. The result still drew (built straight from the recipe output) and recipes that reference an item directly were unaffected — which is why the "Uses" section looked fine. [GuideCraftingFactory](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideCraftingFactory.java) now sources registries from the client level through a shared `displayContext()` helper — reused by [GuideAssemblyRecipes](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideAssemblyRecipes.java) — fixing crafting, smelting, and assembly recipe display in one place. The same registry-less-context defect on the server side is fixed in [CraftingUtil.placeRecipeInBlueprint](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/CraftingUtil.java): clicking JEI's "+" button on a tag-ingredient recipe (the gears, and most recipes) now pre-fills the Advanced Crafting Table / Auto Workbench phantom blueprint with representative items instead of leaving those slots blank. A new `blueprint_place_resolves_tag_ingredients` game test pins the blueprint path.
- Restored the **Gelled Water → Water Bucket** recipe, closing a port-parity gap that had left Gelled Water with no use at all. Breaking a fully-gelled [Water Gel](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/block/BlockWaterGel.java) block still produced Gelled Water, but nothing consumed it: 1.12.2's `water_gel_to_bucket` recipe (gel + empty bucket → water bucket) was carried through the modern ports only in the legacy `assets/<ns>/recipes/` path that current Minecraft never reads, then deleted outright with the legacy-namespace sweep (commit `0e377411a`). It is re-added in current crafting format at [data/.../recipe/water_gel_to_bucket.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/water_gel_to_bucket.json) (`gelled_water` over `minecraft:bucket` → `minecraft:water_bucket`), gated by the same `buildcraftunofficial:config_value` condition as the sibling [water_gel_spawn](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/water_gel_spawn.json) recipe so the Water Gellifier feature toggles as a unit. A recipe-book unlock at [advancement/recipes/water_gel_to_bucket.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/advancement/recipes/water_gel_to_bucket.json) reveals it via `inventory_changed` the moment the player first picks up Gelled Water — the point of friction where they would ask what it is for — rather than behind an unrelated early-game gate. With a real use to document, the guide-book page is now written at [item/gelled_water.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/gelled_water.md) (`git mv`'d out of `placeholder/`; its [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) entry flipped from `place` to `item_typed "fluid"`), covering where Gelled Water comes from (Water Gellifier → spreading gel → mine the fully-gelled blocks) and the bucket conversion. `gelled_water` is struck from the **Items / Fluid** guide-book bullet on [todos.md](todos.md).
- The Fragile Fluid Shard now has a real guide-book writeup at [item/fragile_fluid_container.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/fragile_fluid_container.md), and no longer titles itself **Fragile ERROR! EMPTY FLUID! Shard** in the book. [ItemFragileFluidContainer.getName](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/item/ItemFragileFluidContainer.java) substituted the literal string `ERROR! EMPTY FLUID!` into the `Fragile %s Shard` format whenever the stack carried no fluid — which is exactly the bare, component-free stack the guide book (and the creative / JEI search) renders — so the page title came out as the error string. The empty-fluid branch now returns a dedicated `item.buildcraftunofficial.fragile_fluid_container.name.empty` lang key (= "Fragile Fluid Shard") instead of formatting a placeholder into `.name`. The page itself covers where shards come from (any fluid-holding block — [Tank](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/tank.md), [Pump](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/pump.md), [Flood Gate](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/flood_gate.md), [Distiller](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/distiller.md), [Heat Exchanger](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/heat_exchange.md), fluid pipes, the Iron Engine — returns its contents as shards via [FluidItemDrops](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/items/FluidItemDrops.java) rather than voiding them when broken), the 500 mB-per-shard capacity and per-fluid naming/tint, and how to recover the fluid (right-click a tank or other by-hand fluid machine — the [`onTankActivated`](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/FluidUtilBC.java) path drains the shard's item fluid-handler into the block; the shard's handler refuses fills and shatters the item once empty, so shards are single-use). The page also gains an automatic, bidirectional **Dropped by** cross-link: a new `buildcraft:fluid_shards` guide group in [GuideGroupManager.populateDefaultGroups](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/ref/GuideGroupManager.java) registers the shard as the group entry and every fluid-storage block that drops shards (Tank, Pump, Flood Gate, Distiller, Heat Exchanger, Iron Engine, Builder) as a source/key, so the shard's page lists those blocks under a clickable "Dropped by" heading and each of their pages gains a reciprocal "Fluid Shards" link — both rendered by the existing auto-derived group machinery with no per-page markup (new `buildcraft.guide.group.{to,from}.buildcraft.fluid_shards` lang keys). The `place "fragile_fluid_container" "item" "fluid"` row in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) flips to `item_typed "fluid" "fragile_fluid_container" "buildcraftunofficial:fragile_fluid_container"`, the `.md` file is `git mv`'d from `placeholder/` to `item/`, and `fragile_fluid_container` is struck from the **Items / Fluid** bullet on [todos.md](todos.md)'s guide-book punch list.
- Bumped NeoForge from `26.1.2.66-beta` to `26.1.2.67-beta` in [gradle.properties](gradle.properties). Upstream's single delta is one annotation-only fix (PR [neoforged/NeoForge#3188](https://github.com/neoforged/NeoForge/pull/3188): "Fix nullability on crafting player") — clarifies nullness contracts on the crafting-player API so Java consumers stop seeing `[nullness]` warnings and Kotlin consumers can compile. No runtime behavior or signature change; BuildCraft's crafting-player call sites in [WorkbenchCrafting](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/tile/craft/WorkbenchCrafting.java) / [ContainerAutoCraftItems](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/container/ContainerAutoCraftItems.java) / [ContainerAdvancedCraftingTable](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/container/ContainerAdvancedCraftingTable.java) are unaffected. `.neoforge-ref/` resynced to the new version.
- **Breaking:** renamed the five chipset item IDs to `chipset_<material>`, matching the existing `pipe_<material>_<flow>` role-prefix scheme used across the rest of the mod's IDs. The carried-over 1.12.2 naming had used `redstone_<material>_chipset` because 1.12.2 stored every chipset variant under a single `redstone_chipset` item ID disambiguated by subtype metadata, and the original porting agent had transliterated that pattern to per-material items by simply prefixing each one with `redstone_` (rather than introduce data-component variants for only five items). New IDs: `buildcraftunofficial:chipset_redstone` (was `redstone_red_chipset`), `chipset_iron` (was `redstone_iron_chipset`), `chipset_gold` (was `redstone_gold_chipset`), `chipset_quartz` (was `redstone_quartz_chipset`), `chipset_diamond` (was `redstone_diamond_chipset`). Java fields on [BCSiliconItems](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSiliconItems.java) match (`CHIPSET_REDSTONE`, `CHIPSET_IRON`, …); all internal callers updated in [BCSiliconRecipes](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSiliconRecipes.java) and [BCCoreCreativeTabs](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCoreCreativeTabs.java); the five assembly-recipe internal registry names (`"chipset_redstone"`, `"chipset_iron"`, …) are aligned with the same naming so JEI's recipe-id-to-output-item mapping stays one-to-one and self-consistent. The on-disk asset/data files are `git mv`'d so the rename diff stays reviewable: `assets/.../items/chipset_<material>.json`, `assets/.../models/item/chipset_<material>.json`, the five guide-book pages under `compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/chipset_<material>.md`, and the texture PNGs flatten out of `textures/item/redstone_chipset/<material>.png` (a now-misleading subfolder named after the 1.12.2 ID) and rename to `textures/item/chipset_<material>.png` so resource-pack authors get the standard "texture path mirrors item ID" layout. Cascading touch-ups: lang keys in [en_us.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/lang/en_us.json) (display strings unchanged — already correct), the Advanced Crafting Table recipe ingredient in [advanced_crafting_table.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/advanced_crafting_table.json), the five `chipset` lines in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt), the `recipes_usages` widget stack on every chipset guide page, and the worked example in [config/json_insn_format.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/config/json_insn_format.md). Existing worlds with chipsets in inventory: stacks under any of the historical IDs (the 1.12.2 `redstone_chipset:meta`, the first-port `redstone_<material>_chipset`, or this turn's intermediate `<material>_chipset` form) will vanish on load until a remap is wired up — the **Backwards compatibility with older block and item IDs** finalization bullet in [todos.md](todos.md) is now load-bearing for this rename, for any future similar cleanup before the RC, and for the cross-version migration that bullet always implied.
- All five chipsets now have real guide-book writeups at [item/redstone_red_chipset.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/redstone_red_chipset.md), [item/redstone_iron_chipset.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/redstone_iron_chipset.md), [item/redstone_gold_chipset.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/redstone_gold_chipset.md), [item/redstone_quartz_chipset.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/redstone_quartz_chipset.md), and [item/redstone_diamond_chipset.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/redstone_diamond_chipset.md) — deliberately short, parallel pages naming each chipset's role (Red = Advanced Crafting Table base; Iron = Iron / Nether Brick gates and Pipe Wires; Gold = Gold gates; Quartz = +1 parameter slot per set modifier; Diamond = +3 parameter slots per set modifier), with the actual assembly recipe and full usage list left to the standard `<recipes_usages>` widget. New 1-arg `chipset` alias in [util.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/util.txt) mirrors the existing `tool` / `gear` / `plug` / `paper` shortcuts; the five `place "redstone_*_chipset" "item" "chipset"` rows in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) flip to `chipset "redstone_*_chipset"`, the `.md` files are `git mv`'d from `placeholder/` to `item/`, and the **Items / Chipsets** bullet is struck from [todos.md](todos.md)'s guide-book punch list.
- Fixed the guide-book "Basic Gate" entry implying the Clay Brick Basic Gate is an ingredient in higher-tier gates. The user-reported symptom was "pressing U on the Basic Gate in JEI does nothing, even though the guide book shows it as a key component for iron/nether/gold gates" — JEI was correct (the [CLAY_BRICK gate](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/gate/EnumGateMaterial.java) is a terminal item, never a recipe input), but three guide-book / JEI-transfer code paths were stripping `DataComponentIngredient` patches off ingredient displays, and that made every gate-modifier-upgrade recipe's gate input slot render as the *default* GateVariant (CLAY_BRICK AND NO_MODIFIER — i.e. the in-game "Basic Gate") instead of the Iron AND / Nether Brick AND / Gold AND variant the recipe actually requires. Player conclusion: "the Basic Gate is the ingredient." Three call sites, all switched from `Ingredient.items()` to `Ingredient.display().resolveForStacks(ctx)` so the patch survives into the rendered slot: [GuideAssemblyRecipes.createFactory](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideAssemblyRecipes.java) (assembly-recipe rendering on every guide page that lists an assembly recipe involving a `DataComponentIngredient` input — i.e. every gate-modifier-upgrade entry), [GuideCraftingFactory.ingredientToChanging](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideCraftingFactory.java) (crafting-recipe rendering for the same family of recipes, where `gate_iron_and_lapis.json` and the other `neoforge:components` crafting-table modifier upgrades had been showing a Basic Gate input on the bench instead of the Iron AND Gate), and [CraftingUtil.ingredientToStack](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/CraftingUtil.java) (the JEI "+" button's recipe-transfer path for the Advanced Crafting Table / AutoCraft, which pre-fills the 3×3 phantom blueprint slots — clicking "+" on the Iron+Lapis crafting recipe would pre-fill the gate slot with a bare CLAY_BRICK Basic Gate, then refuse to craft because the bench's `DataComponentIngredient.test()` correctly rejected the wrong variant; the actual real-stack workflow still works, but the phantom preview lied). Pinned by four new game tests in [GateRecipeVariantTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/silicon/GateRecipeVariantTester.java) (basic gate appears as an input in ≥3 modifier recipes per material/logic via the JEI collector; every higher-level gate variant appears as an output in ≥1 collector entry; the guide-book Iron+Lapis recipe's gate input now resolves to the Iron AND variant rather than the default CLAY_BRICK; and the CLAY_BRICK Basic Gate has zero assembly-recipe usages — the design-intent check that the Basic Gate truly is a terminal item).
- Pipe Sealant (the [`waterproof`](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/BCTransportItems.java) item) now has a real guide-book writeup at [item/waterproof.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/waterproof.md) — a deliberately short page noting its role as the shapeless catalyst that converts any Item Transport Pipe into the matching Fluid Transport Pipe of the same material (the recipe pattern used by all eleven `pipe_*_fluid` recipes under [data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/)), with the three on-disk crafting paths (Slime Ball ×1, Green Dye ×1, Oil Residue bucket ×8 from a [Distiller](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/distiller.md) — the bottom of [BCEnergyRecipes](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/BCEnergyRecipes.java)'s distillation pyramid) surfaced via the standard `<recipes_usages>` widget rather than enumerated in prose. The `place "waterproof" "item" "basic"` placeholder row in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) flips to `item_typed "basic" "waterproof" "buildcraftunofficial:waterproof"`, the `.md` file is `git mv`'d from `placeholder/` to `item/`, and the **Items / Basic** bullet is struck from [todos.md](todos.md)'s guide-book punch list.
- Server startup no longer prints ~2,600 stack traces from the facade scan. [FacadeStateManager.scanBlock](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/plug/FacadeStateManager.java)'s per-state NBT and packet-buffer round-trip test was routing reads through `FacadePhasedState.readFromNbt` / `readFromBuffer`, both of which look the result up in `FacadeStateManager.validFacadeStates`. But [init()](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/plug/FacadeStateManager.java) builds into a local `nextValid` and only publishes it to that static field *after* the whole scan loop finishes — so mid-scan the lookup always missed and fell back to `defaultState` (air), and the `read.stateInfo.state != info.state` check threw `IllegalStateException: Read (from NBT) state was different!` for every single valid facade, each one caught and logged as a multi-line error. The state had already been added to `outValidStates` before the test ran, so the published map (and therefore runtime behavior) was correct — the throws were pure noise. Fix compares the raw `BlockState` written by `phasedState.writeToNbt()` / `writeToBuffer` against `info.state` directly, via `NbtUtils.readBlockState(BuiltInRegistries.BLOCK, …)` and `Block.BLOCK_STATE_REGISTRY.byId(buf.readVarInt())`, so the round-trip check no longer depends on the not-yet-published map. Cuts `run/logs/latest.log` from 7.4 MB / 72,631 lines to a clean startup.
- Laser now has a real guide-book writeup at [block/laser.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/laser.md) — covers the 6-block forward-facing cone the [TileLaser](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/tile/TileLaser.java) scans (via [VolumeUtil.iterateCone](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/VolumeUtil.java) on the `FACING` direction set at placement time by [BlockLaser.getStateForPlacement](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/block/BlockLaser.java) to the opposite of the player's nearest look direction), the round-robin target selection when several [ILaserTargetBlock](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/mj/ILaserTargetBlock.java) consumers (Assembly Table and Advanced Crafting Table — the two public-build targets, since Integration Table is `BCLib.DEV`-gated) are in range, the parallel-stacking behavior of pointing multiple Lasers at the same machine, the 1,024 MJ internal battery and the 4 MJ/t cap on `getMaxPowerPerTick`, and the half-battery throughput taper that comes from the `max *= (stored + max); max /= capacity / 2` ramp in [TileLaser.serverTick](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/tile/TileLaser.java) (so for sustained 4 MJ/t output the Laser needs ≥4 MJ/t of supply — a fueled Combustion Engine saturates one, a Stirling Engine feeds it at part-throttle, a Redstone Engine can't keep up). The `place "laser" "block" "laser"` placeholder row in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) flips to `block "laser" "laser"`, so the `.md` file now lives under `block/` instead of the runtime auto-stub path, and the placeholder file is `git rm`'d. Strikes the **Blocks / Laser** bullet from [todos.md](todos.md)'s guide-book punch list.
- New guide-book writeups for the three remaining engines at [block/engine_creative.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/engine_creative.md), [block/engine_rf.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/engine_rf.md), and [block/mj_dynamo.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/mj_dynamo.md). Covers the FE Engine's FE→MJ conversion (10,000 FE buffer, base 4 MJ/t, pulls FE from neighbors on non-output sides, chains up to 5 engines deep), the MJ Dynamo's MJ→FE conversion (1,000 MJ buffer, base 4 MJ/t input, kinesis pipes in / FE pipes out, chains up to 4 dynamos deep), the shared four-slot Iron/Gold gear upgrade pattern (+2 MJ/t per Iron, +3 MJ/t per Gold, so 16 MJ/t fully upgraded with Gold), the no-overheat behavior (heat capped at 200), and the Creative Engine's 9-step wrench-cycled output ladder (1–256 MJ/t doubling each step) with its always-Black power stage that nevertheless cannot overheat. The `place "engine_rf"` / `place "mj_dynamo"` / `place_creative "engine_creative"` placeholder rows in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) flip to `block_engine` (FE, Dynamo) and `item_stack_creative "block" "engine" …` (Creative Engine, to keep the survival-hidden flag), so the `.md` files now live under `block/` alongside the Redstone/Stirling/Combustion writeups instead of the runtime auto-stub path. Strikes the corresponding `engine_creative (WIP)` bullet from [todos.md](todos.md); the FE/Dynamo lines weren't on the WIP list — their `place` rows were unintentional carryover from the initial port.
- Right-clicking a block with a stack of clean Single Block Schematics no longer voids the rest of the stack. [ItemSchematicSingle.useOn](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/item/ItemSchematicSingle.java)'s capture path built the captured "used" schematic and then called `player.setItemInHand(hand, usedStack)` — which replaces the *entire* held stack, so a stack of 64 clean schematics collapsed to a single used schematic on the first capture. Routed through vanilla's [ItemUtils.createFilledResult](.neoforge-ref/sources-26.1.2.64-beta/net/minecraft/world/item/ItemUtils.java) (the same helper [PotionItem.useOn](.neoforge-ref/sources-26.1.2.64-beta/net/minecraft/world/item/PotionItem.java) uses for bottle → glass-bottle), which consumes one from the held stack, returns the new used schematic to the hand only if the stack went empty, otherwise inserts it into the player's inventory or drops it at their feet — and correctly skips consumption in creative. The two sneak-clear paths in `use` and `useOn` had the same shape (and additionally voided stacks of *clean* schematics down to one when the player sneak-right-clicked an already-clean stack); they're now gated on `used` so the "already clean → clear" gesture is a no-op `PASS`, and the "used → clear" gesture routes through the same `createFilledResult` helper so it stops voiding the rare case where used schematics happen to stack.
- Replacer now has a real guide-book writeup at [block/replacer.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/replacer.md) — covers the three-slot intake ([ContainerReplacer](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/container/ContainerReplacer.java) arranges a top Blueprint slot at (8, 115) and two used single-block schematic slots underneath, "find" on the left at (8, 137) and "replace" on the right at (56, 137)), the dual-purpose 3D preview ([GuiReplacer.maybeApplyPendingReplacement](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/gui/GuiReplacer.java) renders the original Blueprint until both schematic slots are filled, then switches to a hypothetical post-swap copy of the Blueprint without committing — the authoritative swap re-runs server-side from [TileReplacer.doReplace](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileReplacer.java) when Replace is clicked, via the `NET_REPLACE` payload), the inline summary line beneath the slots ("N × Find → Replace", with N being the exact cell count from [Blueprint.countMatchingCells](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/Blueprint.java)), the editable name field that ships the rename in the same payload that triggers the swap, the non-consumption design (the two single-block schematics persist across Replace clicks so a single find/replace pair can be re-applied to a stream of Blueprints — the swap output is written via [GlobalSavedDataSnapshots.addSnapshot](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/GlobalSavedDataSnapshots.java) and the top slot is in-place updated to reference the new key), and the zero-power semantics (replacement is instant on click). The placeholder file is `git rm`'d and the manifest entry in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) is switched from `place "replacer" "block" "automation"` to `block_auto "replacer"`, dropping the auto-stubbed "(WIP)" leaf from the Blocks / Automation TOC and crossing `replacer` off [todos.md](todos.md)'s guide-book punch list. The page cross-links to [item/blueprint_clean](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/blueprint_clean.md) and the still-stub [placeholder/schematic_single_clean](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/placeholder/schematic_single_clean.md) (which remains on the punch list under Items / Paperwork).
- Electronic Library now has a real guide-book writeup at [block/library.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/library.md) — covers the two-row download/upload slot layout the GUI ([GuiElectronicLibrary](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/gui/GuiElectronicLibrary.java)) arranges around the snapshot-list panel, the 50-tick progress arrow on each row, the Del button that removes only the local copy, and the two-store conceptual model that splits the always-persistent client install library from the per-world server bank — used [Blueprints](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/blueprint_clean.md) and [Templates](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/template_clean.md) carry only a key in their `CUSTOM_DATA` header, so they need to be Downloaded onto a client whose `GlobalSavedDataSnapshots.Side.CLIENT` store doesn't already have the matching entry before a [Builder](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/builder.md) can read them. The placeholder file is `git mv`'d into `block/` and the manifest entry in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) is switched from `place "library" "block" "automation"` to `block_auto "library"`, dropping the auto-stubbed "(WIP)" leaf from the Blocks / Automation TOC and crossing `library` off [todos.md](todos.md)'s guide-book punch list. Same pass audited the 26.1.1 [TileElectronicLibrary](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileElectronicLibrary.java) against the 1.12.2 source on the `8.0.x-1.12.2` branch and confirmed end-to-end feature parity: same four inventory handlers (`invDownIn` / `invDownOut` / `invUpIn` / `invUpOut`) at the same GUI positions (175/57, 219/57, 175/79, 219/79), same `selected` snapshot-key field, same NET_DOWN/NET_UP network pattern (now split across container payloads `NET_DOWNLOAD` / `NET_UPLOAD_REQUEST` / `NET_UPLOAD_DATA` in [ContainerElectronicLibrary](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/container/ContainerElectronicLibrary.java) with the upload step chunked into 32 KB packets, up from 1.12.2's 4 KB), same Del-button placement at (174, 109), and same snapshot-list-row click-to-select. The 26.1.1 build adds two ledger refinements over 1.12.2: an Owner ledger backed by the new [TileBC_Neptune.onPlacedBy](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/tile/TileBC_Neptune.java) owner-persistence path, and a `LedgerHelp` auto-attached entry per UI region (each slot, each arrow, the list, the button) with hover descriptions sourced from the `buildcraft.help.library.*` lang keys.
- Fixed the Filler Planner's translucent pattern-preview cubes rendering as a chaotic mosaic of random block textures. The renderer was emitting `setUv(0..1)` into the shared [VolumeBoxRenderer](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/client/VolumeBoxRenderer.java) consumer, which is bound to `entityTranslucent(LOCATION_BLOCKS)` and samples the block atlas — so the corner-UVs mapped to whatever blocks happen to sit at the atlas corners. The 1.12.2 version sidestepped this by sampling Forge's `ModelLoader.White.INSTANCE` sprite; that sprite no longer exists in modern NeoForge, so [IFastAddonRenderer](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/marker/volume/IFastAddonRenderer.java) now takes a `MultiBufferSource` instead of a single `VertexConsumer` and each addon picks its own render type — corner icons still use `entityTranslucent` on the block atlas, while [AddonRendererFillerPlanner](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/addon/AddonRendererFillerPlanner.java) goes through `BCLibRenderTypes.debugFilled()` (untextured POSITION_COLOR translucent quads), giving the same flat vertex-shaded cubes 1.12.2 produced.
- Fixed a `ConcurrentModificationException` server crash when an Assembly Table was ticked while the client-side facade deduplication pass was running. The three maps in [FacadeStateManager](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/plug/FacadeStateManager.java) (`validFacadeStates`, `stackFacades`, `stackRedirects`) are now `volatile` references to immutable snapshots — [FacadeDeduplicator](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/FacadeDeduplicator.java) builds new versions off to the side and publishes them atomically, so readers (server-side recipe lookup, item rendering) always see a consistent map even if the render thread re-dedups concurrently. Concretely fixes the crash logged at `2026-05-26 15:46:00` where the server thread blew up at [FacadeAssemblyRecipes.java:173](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/recipe/FacadeAssemblyRecipes.java) iterating `stackRedirects` while the render thread (triggered by JEI's first-screen-open ingredient scan) was mid-`.clear()`-and-rebuild.
- Moved the visual facade dedup pass off JEI's first-screen-open critical path. Dedup previously fired lazily the first time the FACADE_TAB_KEY creative tab was populated — which for most users is during JEI's `Registering ingredients` phase the first time they open *any* GUI in-world, adding ~44 ms to that already-slow startup window and pinning the race-prone mutation to an unpredictable user-action moment. Now it runs at `ClientPlayerNetworkEvent.LoggingIn` (in a dedicated [BCSiliconClient.GameBus](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/BCSiliconClient.java) inner class), deterministically once per world join, after model bake and `FacadeStateManager.init()` have both completed. The creative-tab call site is kept as a no-op safety net so an F3+T resource reload still re-dedups against the new textures.
- Corrected the [Builder guide page](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/builder.md) which named the wrong marker block: it told players to place the Builder next to a "Land Mark path (or with a Land Mark Connector adjacent)", but the Builder accepts a [Path Mark](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/marker_path.md) chain only — [TileBuilder.onPlacedBy](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileBuilder.java) casts the adjacent BE to `IPathProvider`, which only [TileMarkerPath](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/tile/TileMarkerPath.java) implements; Land Marks (`marker_volume`) define volumes for the Quarry / Filler / Architect and are silently ignored by the Builder. The page also failed to mention continuous path following: a multi-Path-Mark chain causes the Builder to stamp the snapshot at every interpolated position along the chain in sequence (the mechanic [paving_the_way](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/advancement/paving_the_way.json) rewards). New wording links to `block/marker_path` and `item/marker_connector` and notes both the consumption-on-placement behavior and the path-chain sequential stamping.
- Filtered Buffer now has a real guide-book writeup at [block/filtered_buffer.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/filtered_buffer.md) — covers the two-row GUI layout (top row = nine phantom filter slots, bottom row = the nine real buffer slots), the per-slot insertion contract enforced by [ItemHandlerFiltered](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/tile/item/ItemHandlerFiltered.java) (a buffer slot only accepts items that merge with its filter sample via `StackUtil.canMerge`, and with `emptyIsAnything=false` an empty filter zeroes the slot's capacity so a blank filter seals the slot rather than acting as a wildcard), the visual cues in [GuiFilteredBuffer.drawBackgroundTexture](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/gui/GuiFilteredBuffer.java) (empty-buffer-with-filter draws a 70%-opacity grey ghost of the filter item, empty-buffer-with-no-filter draws a distinct "closed slot" sprite), the all-faces I/O on the main inventory from [TileFilteredBuffer](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/tile/TileFilteredBuffer.java)'s `addInvHandler("main", ..., EnumAccess.BOTH, EnumPipePart.VALUES)`, and the phantom-slot template semantics — the filter sample is set via click ([SlotPhantom](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/slot/SlotPhantom.java) blocks vanilla pickup/place and caps at one), is never consumed or duplicated into drops (`ItemHandlerManager.addDrops` skips the PHANTOM-tagged filter handler, as called out in [BlockFilteredBuffer.playerWillDestroy](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/block/BlockFilteredBuffer.java)'s comment), and cross-links to [diamond_item](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/pipe/diamond_item.md) as the natural output-side counterpart for peeling specific items back off into separate destinations. The placeholder file is `git mv`'d into `block/` and the manifest entry in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) is switched from `place "filtered_buffer" "block" "automation"` to `block_auto "filtered_buffer"`, dropping the auto-stubbed "(WIP)" leaf from the Blocks / Automation TOC and crossing `filtered_buffer` off [todos.md](todos.md)'s guide-book punch list.
- Debugger now has a real guide-book writeup at [item/debugger.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/debugger.md) — covers both halves of the tool: the right-click overlay path that plants a live in-world highlight on the two [IAdvDebugTarget](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/debug/IAdvDebugTarget.java) tiles it supports ([Quarry](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileQuarry.java)'s force-loaded chunks via [AdvDebuggerQuarry](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/client/render/AdvDebuggerQuarry.java), [Laser](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/tile/TileLaser.java)'s reachable/blocked six-block cone via [AdvDebuggerLaser](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/render/AdvDebuggerLaser.java)) along with the corresponding `chat.debugger.*` action-bar message that names what's being highlighted, and the separate F3-debug enhancement in [BCDebugOverlay](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/BCDebugOverlay.java) that appends `[BC] ...` internal-state lines for any [IDebuggable](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/tiles/IDebuggable.java) tile whenever the player is in Creative mode or holding a Debugger ([`ItemDebugger.isShowDebugInfo`](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/item/ItemDebugger.java)).
