- Assembly Table now has a real guide-book writeup at [block/assembly_table.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/assembly_table.md) — covers the ingredient buffer / recipe catalogue layout, the bright-red / dark-red / gray click cycle for selecting, queueing and pausing recipes, the global-battery semantics of `power` in [TileLaserTableBase](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/tile/TileLaserTableBase.java) (MJ is retained across pauses and across recipe swaps, so the new active recipe inherits whatever was already in the bar), the Laser-power input parallel to the [Advanced Crafting Table](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/advanced_crafting_table.md), and a per-category overview of what the table makes (Chipsets, Plugs, Wires, Gates, Facades) with the MJ-cost tier breakdown (500 / 1,000 / 5,000 / 10,000–80,000) cross-referenced against the values registered in [BCSiliconRecipes](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSiliconRecipes.java). - Bumped Blueprint and Template crafting yields above their 1.12.2 baseline. Both shipped historically as a 1-for-1 paper-ring craft (8 paper + 1 lapis → 1 Blueprint, 8 paper + 1 black dye → 1 Template) and the port had carried those yields forward 1:1, but in practice Blueprints and Templates are consumed per Architect scan and per Builder placement, so the original ratio under-supplied the workflow they gate. [blueprint_clean.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/blueprint_clean.json) now yields 2 per craft; [template_clean.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/template_clean.json) yields 4 (Templates record occupied-vs-empty only and are 3× faster to scan than Blueprints, so they tend to be used in higher counts for repeated stamping passes — a wider ratio matches the way the two are consumed in play).
- Architect Table now has a real guide-book writeup at [block/architect.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/architect.md) — covers placement against a [Land Mark volume](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/marker_volume.md) or path, Blueprint vs Template selection via the input slot (the type follows whatever you load), the live 3D preview, naming the snapshot for [Builder](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/builder.md) / Library identification later, and that scans cost no power. The placeholder file is deleted and the manifest entry in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) is switched from `place` to `block_auto`, dropping the auto-stubbed "(WIP)" leaf from the Blocks / Automation TOC and crossing `architect` off [todos.md](todos.md)'s guide-book punch list. The Architect article cross-links to the two snapshot media it consumes, so [item/blueprint_clean.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/blueprint_clean.md) and [item/template_clean.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/template_clean.md) get real writeups in the same pass — each covers the Architect → filled-snapshot → Builder pipeline from the item's perspective, the tooltip surfaces (name on default, hash/date/owner UUID under F3+H, rotating 3D preview overlay on hover), and the per-item trade-off (Blueprint records full block states + entities, Template records only occupied-vs-empty and is 3× faster to scan). New 1-arg `paper` alias in [util.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/util.txt) mirrors the existing `tool` / `gear` / `plug` shortcuts and pre-bakes the same pattern for the remaining three paperwork stubs (`decorated_laser`, `schematic_single_clean`, `schematic_single_used`) once those get writeups too.
- Pruned 17 dead/aspirational guide-book stub entries from [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) and the matching files under `compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/placeholder/`. Removed: `blueprint_used`, `decorated_blueprint`/`decorated_destroy`/`decorated_leather`/`decorated_paper`/`decorated_template` (the five dev-gated decoration blocks — `decorated_laser` is the only survival-craftable decoration and keeps its placeholder), `glob_of_oil`, `goggles`/`guide_note`/`map_location` (all dev-gated tool items), `special_rock` (phantom — no block ever registered under that ID, in 1.12.2 or in the modern port), `spring_oil`/`spring_water` (one-tick worldgen sources, no gameplay surface), `template_used`, `tube`, `water_gel_spawn` (will be folded into the eventual `water_gel` writeup), and `zone_planner` (deferred). The `filler_planner` entry is now `place_creative` so it only appears in survival creative-mode TOCs, matching the gating of similar planner/dev items elsewhere in the manifest. The Advanced Crafting Table entry, which had been registered as a `place` stub against an unwritten placeholder and was *also* surfacing the auto-discovered real writeup as a duplicate "(WIP)" leaf in the TOC, is now wired through `block_auto` against the real [block/advanced_crafting_table.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/block/advanced_crafting_table.md). Two orphan files (`frame.md` and `volume_box.md` — never referenced by the manifest; the real Volume Box writeup lives at `placeholder/box_volume.md` because the file name doesn't match the stack id) are also gone. Remaining stubs (35) are catalogued in [todos.md](todos.md) under "Guide Book pages awaiting writeups".
- Decoration blocks (`decorated_destroy`, `decorated_blueprint`, `decorated_template`, `decorated_paper`, `decorated_leather`) are now gated behind `-Dbuildcraft.dev=true`, matching the existing dev-only treatment of POWER_TESTER / GOGGLES / MAP_LOCATION / INTEGRATION_TABLE. Only the laser variant ships in public builds — it's the one decoration block that ever had a survival recipe in 1.12.2 (8 obsidian + redstone block → 16, registered in [BCCoreRecipes.java](https://github.com/legoj15/BuildCraft/blob/8.0.x-1.12.2/common/buildcraft/core/BCCoreRecipes.java)); the other five were creative-tab-only with no survival path. Block + BlockItem registration moved into the `BCLib.DEV` `static {}` initializer in [BCCoreBlocks](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCoreBlocks.java) / [BCCoreItems](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCoreItems.java), creative-tab entries in [BCCoreCreativeTabs](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCoreCreativeTabs.java) are now `!= null`-guarded, [BCCoreClient](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCoreClient.java) tags them with the red "Dev only" tooltip alongside the other dev items, and their entries in [tags/block/mineable/pickaxe.json](src/main/resources/data/minecraft/tags/block/mineable/pickaxe.json) are now `{ "required": false }` so the tag still loads when the blocks are absent. The two `BlockDropsTester` decorated-block tests ([drops_decorated_pickaxe](src/test/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/test_instance/drops_decorated_pickaxe.json), [drops_decorated_hand](src/test/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/test_instance/drops_decorated_hand.json)) now target `DECORATED_LASER` since it's the only public decoration block left — same no-inventory baseline coverage, just on the variant that's actually in the public roster.
- `decorated_laser` is now hidden in the vanilla recipe book until the player obtains a [laser](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/block/BlockLaser.java) block (crafted or otherwise). New advancement [has_laser.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/advancement/recipes/has_laser.json) fires on `minecraft:inventory_changed` for `buildcraftunofficial:laser` and rewards the `decorated_laser` recipe — mirroring the existing `has_obsidian.json` → laser/assembly-table/advanced-crafting-table unlock chain. This pushes the unlock to the moment the player has a laser in hand and might actually want to dress its housing, rather than burying it under a universal early-game trigger.
- Restored the 1.12.2 crafting-table recipes for gates, none of which had been ported. **Basic Gate (clay brick).** The entry-level gate was creative-tab-only — registered in [BCSilicon.addCreativeTabItems](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSilicon.java) (the `!material.canBeModified` branch covers CLAY_BRICK) but with no path to obtain in survival, since [BCSiliconRecipes.makeGateAssembly](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSiliconRecipes.java) only handles IRON / NETHER_BRICK / GOLD. Added [gate_basic.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/gate_basic.json) restoring the 1.12.2 shaped recipe (brick + redstone + cobblestone, in the cross-shape `m / mrm / b`). **Iron and Nether Brick basic-gate crafting alternatives** ([gate_iron_and.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/gate_iron_and.json), [gate_nether_brick_and.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/gate_nether_brick_and.json)) — same shape with iron ingot / nether-brick item swapped in, parity with the 1.12.2 source. The Assembly Table paths still exist as the higher-throughput option; these add a chipset-free early-game route. **Iron modifier upgrades** ([gate_iron_and_lapis.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/gate_iron_and_lapis.json), [gate_iron_and_quartz.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/gate_iron_and_quartz.json)) — four lapis/quartz around an Iron AND Gate (matched by `neoforge:components` data-component ingredient on `CUSTOM_DATA` + `CUSTOM_MODEL_DATA`), producing the modifier-upgraded variant. **AND↔OR swap** — 1.12.2's shapeless 1-ingredient logic-flip is restored as 24 JSON files generated by [scripts/generate-gate-swap-recipes.py](scripts/generate-gate-swap-recipes.py) (3 materials × 4 modifiers × 2 directions; CLAY_BRICK is intentionally excluded to match 1.12.2). Pinned by nine new game tests in [GateCraftingRecipeTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/silicon/GateCraftingRecipeTester.java) covering each static recipe, both swap directions, a third-material/non-zero-modifier spot-check (Gold + Diamond), and a negative test confirming CLAY_BRICK doesn't match any 1-slot crafting recipe. **JSON gotcha**: NeoForge's custom-ingredient dispatcher reads the type from a `neoforge:ingredient_type` field, not the same `type` field the recipe itself uses — passing `type` makes the `Codec.xor(custom, vanilla)` fall through to the vanilla holder-set codec, which doesn't accept an object and silently drops the ingredient, leaving a 0-length list and the unhelpful "List is too short: 0, expected range [1-9]" error from the outer recipe codec.
- Gate modifier recipes now match the input gate by data-component variant, not just by `Item` identity — fixing a port regression in which the Gold AND + Lapis recipe (and every other modifier recipe) would consume *any* basic gate of *any* material/logic, and JEI displayed the cycling input slot as "any basic gate" because the ingredient matched every PLUG_GATE stack. All gate variants share the same [PLUG_GATE](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSiliconItems.java) item and are disambiguated by data components (the `gate` CompoundTag under `CUSTOM_DATA` plus the `CUSTOM_MODEL_DATA` variant key) — [BCSiliconRecipes.makeGateModifierAssembly](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSiliconRecipes.java) now uses NeoForge's `DataComponentIngredient.of(false, patch, item)` so each recipe matches only its specific input variant (e.g. iron AND + lapis no longer accepts a gold AND or an or-logic gate). 1.12.2 enforced the same constraint via `IngredientNBTBC`; the modern port had carried that class as an empty one-line stub which is now deleted (no callers anywhere). The explicit-patch overload is load-bearing: the ItemStack-shaped `DataComponentIngredient.of(boolean, ItemStack)` internally calls `asPatch(stack.getComponents())` and serialises every default component, so when JEI's display path later rebuilds the stack via `ItemStackTemplate.create()` the default-equal entries end up in the rebuilt `PatchedDataComponentMap`'s internal patch — and `PatchedDataComponentMap.equals` compares patches structurally, so the rebuilt stack ends up `!equals` to the canonical gate stack JEI keeps in its ingredient list, breaking R/U lookup on every basic-gate variant. Passing `toUpgrade.getComponentsPatch()` (just the two real overrides) keeps the rebuilt patch identical to the canonical. The JEI display path also had a separate symptom of the same Item-vs-data-components confusion on the *output* side: [AssemblyRecipeCollector.collectStandard](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/compat/jei/AssemblyRecipeCollector.java) enumerated `ingredient.items()` and built bare `new ItemStack(item, count)` slot entries, which dropped the variant patches set by `DataComponentIngredient` and made every gate-modifier recipe render its input as a default-variant Iron AND Gate; the collector now resolves through `ingredient.display().resolveForStacks(ctx)`, which preserves the `ItemStackTemplate` patches that `DataComponentIngredient.display()` emits, then applies the `IngredientStack.count` afterwards (the display path doesn't carry counts). Pinned by five new game tests in [GateRecipeVariantTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/silicon/GateRecipeVariantTester.java) — Gold+Lapis recipe accepts gold-plain input, rejects iron-plain (wrong material), rejects gold+lapis (wrong modifier — already upgraded), the OR-logic variant rejects an AND-logic gate, and the display-path resolution is `ItemStack.matches`-identical to the canonical gate (which is the contract JEI relies on for recipe lookup). The matching JEI subtype interpreter ([BCSiliconJeiPlugin](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/compat/jei/BCSiliconJeiPlugin.java) — added in the prior JEI fix) already keys gates on the same `GateVariant.getVariantName()` the new ingredient effectively keys on, so JEI now renders the input slot as the one specific gate variant the recipe actually wants and R/U lookup finds every gate variant's recipes.
- Test source set joins main at zero javac lint. The one remaining `[deprecation]` flag — the deferred sweep called out in the previous warning pass — was [AdvancementTester.assertNotInTag](src/test/java/buildcraft/energy/AdvancementTester.java) calling the deprecated `Block.builtInRegistryHolder()` to check tag membership; swapped for `block.defaultBlockState().is(tagKey)`, which is the same idiom vanilla uses internally ([BlockBehaviour.BlockStateBase.is(TagKey)](.neoforge-ref/sources-26.1.2.64-beta/net/minecraft/world/level/block/state/BlockBehaviour.java)). `./gradlew compileTestJava` with `-Xlint:deprecation` is now clean across the test source set, matching the main source set.
- Removed 34 dead gate item-model assets. `GateItemModel` (installed at bake time by [BCSiliconClient.onModifyBakingResult](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/BCSiliconClient.java)) renders gate items programmatically from `PlugGateBaker`, so the 188-line `minecraft:select` block in [items/plug_gate.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/items/plug_gate.json), its 25 `models/item/gates/variants/*.json` variant files, and the 9 layer textures under `textures/item/gates/` were never consulted at runtime — the only consumers were each other. [items/plug_gate.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/items/plug_gate.json) had to stay (the swap-guard `if (vanillaGateModel != null)` skips silently if no model is registered), and now collapses to the standard one-model reference matching the other plug items; the underlying [models/item/plug_gate.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/models/item/plug_gate.json) is a minimal `parent: minecraft:item/generated` stub pointing at `minecraft:item/barrier` — never rendered in practice, so a barrier icon is a clear "swap failed" indicator if anything ever breaks the bake path. Advancement icons that reference `buildcraftunofficial:plug_gate` (with and without `minecraft:custom_data` for the gate variant tag) keep working: both go through `GateItemModel.update` → `ItemPluggableGate.getVariant(stack)`, which reads component data directly and never touched the `custom_model_data` `minecraft:select` cases.
- Collapsed the 1357-entry facade explosion in JEI's ingredient panel to a single representative entry, now that the [subtype interpreter](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/compat/jei/BCSiliconJeiPlugin.java) added in the previous JEI fix had correctly distinguished every facade variant — and consequently exposed all 1357 of them in the side panel as "multiple pages of facades." A new `onRuntimeAvailable(IJeiRuntime)` hook in [BCSiliconJeiPlugin](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/compat/jei/BCSiliconJeiPlugin.java) walks the runtime ingredient list, keeps the stone-wrapped basic facade as the visible representative (or the first basic facade JEI gives us, if stone isn't a valid facade source), and calls `IIngredientManager.removeIngredientsAtRuntime` on the rest. The subtype interpreter stays active so pressing R on any specific facade held in the player's inventory still finds the cycling Assembly Table recipe focus-narrowed to that variant (via the createFocusLink wiring in [AssemblyTableCategory.setRecipe](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/compat/jei/AssemblyTableCategory.java:121)), and browsing every variant is still one click away via the Assembly Table catalyst — the existing [AssemblyRecipeCollector.collectFacade](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/compat/jei/AssemblyRecipeCollector.java) already wires both basic and hollow into a single cycling entry whose output slot rotates through every visible facade. Only the *side panel* clutter is removed; recipe lookup, search-by-name on "facade", and full browse all still work.
- JEI now distinguishes individual lens/filter colours, gate variants, and facade-wrapped block states instead of collapsing them all into one entry. Pressing **R** or **U** on a single coloured lens used to surface 17 pages of recipes — every lens and every filter in the game — because [BCSiliconJeiPlugin](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/compat/jei/BCSiliconJeiPlugin.java) had no `registerItemSubtypes` hook, so JEI saw all 32 lens stacks (16 colours × {lens, filter}), all gate variants, and all 1357 facade variants as duplicates of the same item ID (a warning in every runClient log: *"57 duplicate items were found in 'BuildCraft Pluggables' creative tab's: displayItems"* and *"1357 duplicate items were found in 'BuildCraft Facades'…"*). Three `ISubtypeRegistration.registerSubtypeInterpreter` calls now: lens keys on `colour + ":" + isFilter` (with `"clear"` for the no-colour case); gate keys on [GateVariant.getVariantName](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/gate/GateVariant.java) — the same `material + logic + modifier` tag the gate's item-model dispatch uses, so two stacks that render identically still share one JEI entry; facade keys on the entire `"facade"` NBT compound, which encodes wrapped block-state(s), phased-colour mappings and the hollow flag (and has structural equals/hashCode in 26.1's `CompoundTag`, so two facades wrapping the same state(s) collapse correctly). Net effect: R on a red lens now shows recipes for the red lens; R on a stone-wrapped facade now shows recipes for the stone-wrapped facade; the creative-tab dupe warnings are gone.
- Removed a stray debug-log probe in [CraftingUtil.onServerStarted](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/CraftingUtil.java) that was fetching the `minecraft:white_bundle` recipe and logging its concrete class name at INFO level on every world load (`[CraftingUtil] DUMPING BUNDLE RECIPE: net.minecraft.world.item.crafting.TransmuteRecipe`). The probe was port-era investigative scaffolding for bundle-recipe loading and had no remaining purpose; removed along with the now-unused `@EventBusSubscriber`, `@SubscribeEvent`, and `ServerStartedEvent` import.
- Compiler-warning sweep across the originally-surfaced 100-warning lint pass (the real total turned out to be 504; javac's default `-Xmaxwarns 100` had been clipping the output). **Real defect cleared:** [TileQuarry](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileQuarry.java)'s three inner task classes (`TaskBreakBlock`, `TaskAddFrame`, `TaskMoveDrill`) each overrode `equals` without `hashCode`, a latent contract violation — grepping confirmed none of them ever land in a hash-based collection (`currentTask` is a single-instance field), so the `equals` overrides were vestigial 1.12-era code and have been deleted. **API surface cleanup:** the `buildcraft.api.library` package (4 `@Deprecated` classes plus the unused `ILibraryTypeHandler` interface — zero callers anywhere in the codebase) is removed entirely; [StatementManager](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/statements/StatementManager.java)'s ambiguous `registerParameter(String, IParamReaderBuf)` overload is renamed to `registerParameterBuf` so SAM-typed addons can no longer hit the `[overloads]` warning, with [IStatementParameter](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/statements/IStatementParameter.java)'s Javadoc updated to match. **Modernization fixes:** [ResourceId.load](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/robots/ResourceId.java) swaps the deprecated `Class.newInstance()` for `getDeclaredConstructor().newInstance()`; [PacketBufferBC.readString](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/net/PacketBufferBC.java) drops Guava `Charsets.UTF_8` for `StandardCharsets.UTF_8`; [SchematicBlockFactory](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/schematics/SchematicBlockFactory.java) and [SchematicEntityFactory](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/schematics/SchematicEntityFactory.java) gain proper `compareTo(SchematicXxxFactory<?>)` signatures matching the declared `Comparable<SchematicXxxFactory<?>>`; [InvalidInputDataException](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/core/InvalidInputDataException.java) gains the missing `serialVersionUID`. **Suppression hygiene:** [Box.reset](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/data/Box.java) is now `final` (no subclasses anywhere, kills a `this-escape` warning at the source); targeted `@SuppressWarnings` on [SpriteHolderRegistry](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/sprite/SpriteHolderRegistry.java) (vanilla deprecated `TextureAtlas.LOCATION_BLOCKS`/`LOCATION_ITEMS` but has not yet shipped a non-deprecated replacement `Identifier`), on `getFactoryByInstance` in both schematic registries, on `ItemHandlerManager`'s unavoidable raw-array creation pattern, and on the six remaining `this-escape` constructors flagged in the pass ([AssemblyRecipeBasic](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/recipes/AssemblyRecipeBasic.java), [TileBC_Neptune](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/tile/TileBC_Neptune.java), [TileFiller](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileFiller.java), [TileBuilder](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileBuilder.java), [Snapshot.BuildingInfo](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/Snapshot.java)). **Second sweep cleared the remaining ~408**: 96 `dangling-doc-comments` (a Python script downgrading the leading `/**` copyright headers to `/*` on 81 files and replacing the 15 `/////////////////////////` banners in [NodeTypeBase](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/expression/NodeTypeBase.java) with `//-------------------------` — Java 25's JEP 467 treats `///` at line start as a Markdown Javadoc comment); 23 `lossy-conversions` (explicit casts at the assignment site, hardening the GUI-int / vertex-float / `MjBattery.extractPower(long)` → int boundaries that had been implicit); the lone `fallthrough` in [FunctionSignature.parse0](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/expression/FunctionSignature.java); a redundant cast pair on `level.getCapability(Capabilities.Item.BLOCK, …)` in [PipeFlowItems](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/flow/PipeFlowItems.java) where the typed capability already returns `ResourceHandler<ItemResource>`; the static-method-via-instance call in [GuiArchitectTable](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/gui/GuiArchitectTable.java); `Charsets.UTF_8` → `StandardCharsets.UTF_8` aside. Stale "TEMPORARY DO NOT USE" `@Deprecated` markers were removed from [AssemblyRecipe](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/recipes/AssemblyRecipe.java), [AssemblyRecipeBasic](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/recipes/AssemblyRecipeBasic.java) and [StackDefinition](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/recipes/StackDefinition.java) (all three were load-bearing — Assembly Table, JEI, guide pages — and the deprecations had been misleading since the port), from the three anonymous-no-name [FunctionContext](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/expression/FunctionContext.java) constructors (the non-anonymous variants discourage themselves in their own Javadoc, so the deprecation was net-negative), and from [IFakePlayerProvider.getBuildCraftPlayer](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/core/IFakePlayerProvider.java) (worldgen/spring fallback usage is legitimate); `AssemblyRecipe.setRegistryName(String)` and `setRegistryName(Object)` are now `final` so the subclass constructor's call cannot escape `this`. Bulk-applied class-level `@SuppressWarnings` annotations for the rest — vanilla deprecations (TextureAtlas atlas-Identifier constants, `Item.appendHoverText` legacy 5-arg signature, `BlockStateModel` / `BlockStateBase` / `Ingredient.items` / `BlockBehaviour` / etc., none of which have a non-deprecated replacement on the pinned NeoForge build) and the bulk of `unchecked` / `rawtypes` (generic registry / handler casts that Java erasure makes unavoidable). Class-level annotations are bulk-mergeable when a new category appears, so future sweeps stay tractable. `./gradlew compileJava` with `-Xlint:all -Xmaxwarns 9999` and `./gradlew test` are now both completely clean — zero warnings on the main source set, the only remaining lint Note is a single `[deprecation]` flag in [AdvancementTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/energy/AdvancementTester.java) (test source set, separate sweep).
- Facades of biome- or state-tinted blocks (grass, leaves, redstone wire, water-cauldron, melon/pumpkin stems, lily pads, sugar cane, tall grass) now render with the wrapped block's colour again. MC 26.1 replaced the old per-pluggable `getBlockColor` callback with `BlockTintSource` objects registered per-block, and the port had only registered two slots on `pipe_holder` (NO_TINT at 0, PIPE_COLOUR_TINT at 1 — the painted-pipe overlay). [PlugBakerFacade.bakeForKey](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/model/plug/PlugBakerFacade.java) was already remapping facade quads' tintindex into a `data*6+side` space, but that space landed entirely outside the two registered slots — `BlockColors.getTintSource(state, layer)` returned null and the chunk renderer dropped the tint, so grass/leaves facades came out greyscale and a redstone-wire facade rendered un-powered black. Two-part fix: the facade encoding shifts past the reserved pipe slots (now `2 + data*6 + side.ordinal()`, so it cannot collide with `PIPE_COLOUR_TINT` — a latent bug where painted-pipe dye would bleed onto a grass-facade UP face), and [PipeBlockColourHandler](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/PipeBlockColourHandler.java) now registers one `FacadeTintSource` per `(wrappedTintIndex, side)` slot (4 layers × 6 sides = 24 sources; vanilla maxes at tintindex 1, the 4-layer cap gives modded-block headroom and out-of-range entries render untinted rather than aliasing to a wrong slot). Each `FacadeTintSource.colorInWorld` walks `level → TilePipeHolder → getPluggable(side) → PluggableFacade.states.phasedStates[activeState].stateInfo.state` and delegates to the wrapped block's vanilla `BlockTintSource` at the pipe's BlockPos, so a grass facade sampled in a swamp shows swamp grass colours, an oak-leaves facade tracks foliage by biome, redstone-wire facades carry the captured power level's red gradient, and so on. Untinted facades (the common case — stone, planks, glass, etc.) are unaffected: `PlugBakerFacade` only remaps quads whose wrapped tintindex is ≥ 0, and non-tinted block models emit `tintindex = -1`. Item-form facades fall through to `color(state)` which returns `-1` (the facade item's own model path renders untouched).
- The Heat Exchanger and Distiller now have functional Help ledgers — and adding a new GUI to the mod gets one automatically. Both screens had a `LedgerHelp` panel attached (a side-effect of every `GuiBC8` subclass getting one) but neither registered any help content, so the ledger opened to an empty panel. Both GUIs now register an `ElementHelpInfo` per UI region: [GuiHeatExchange](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/gui/GuiHeatExchange.java) covers its four fluid tanks (hot in / cooled out on the START end, cold in / heated out on the END end) plus the centre PREPARING/RUNNING/STOPPING wipe overlay, and [GuiDistiller](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/gui/GuiDistiller.java) covers its three fluid tanks (input / gas out / liquid out) plus the centre running-vs.-stuck pipe schematic. While in there, the `LedgerHelp` attachment moves into the base class instead of being duplicated per-GUI: [GuiBC8](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/GuiBC8.java) gained a `shouldAddHelpLedger()` opt-out (default true, matching 1.12.2's `standardLedgerInit`) and auto-attaches the ledger after each subclass's `initGuiElements()` runs. The 21 GUI subclasses that previously instantiated `LedgerHelp` themselves lose those duplicated lines, and the two recipe-book screens ([GuiAutoCraftItems](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/gui/GuiAutoCraftItems.java), [GuiAdvancedCraftingTable](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/gui/GuiAdvancedCraftingTable.java)) — whose vanilla recipe-book panel needs the left side free — opt out explicitly via the new override. Net effect: future GUIs added to the mod get a Help ledger by default; opt-out is one explicit method; an empty ledger is now a content gap rather than something a contributor has to remember to opt into.
- Dropped the placeholder "Json Registry Overview" guidebook page. The .md file at [`compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/config/registry_overview.md`](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/config/registry_overview.md) was empty, so [GuideManager](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/GuideManager.java)'s stub-synthesis path was surfacing it under the Config book as "Json Registry Overview (WIP)" with the generic placeholder body — a visible TOC entry with no plan to fill it. Removed: the file, its `cfg_res "registry_overview"` registration in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt), and the matching lang entry. An orphan stub at `block/engine_basics.md` (one-line title, never registered, so never user-visible) is deleted in the same pass.
- The placement-preview outline now sizes itself to the pluggable the player is holding, instead of always drawing a gate-sized 6×6 panel. The original [PipePlacementHighlight](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/render/PipePlacementHighlight.java) hardcoded a single slab matching a gate's footprint — fine for gates, pulsars, timers and the light sensor (all the same dimensions), but actively misleading for the larger plugs: a facade (full 16×16 face), a power adaptor (10×10×4), or a lens (10×10) completely overshadowed the outline, so a player aiming at a face that already had one of those couldn't see where their next pluggable would land. The size is now driven by a new `IItemPluggable.getPlacementBoundingBox(stack, side)` interface default — gate-sized by default, overridden in [ItemPluggableLens](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/item/ItemPluggableLens.java) / [ItemPluggableFacade](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/item/ItemPluggableFacade.java) to delegate to the matching `PluggableLens` / `PluggableFacade` static box, and parametrised in [ItemPluggableSimple](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/item/ItemPluggableSimple.java) via a new constructor argument that PLUG_BLOCKER and PLUG_POWER_ADAPTOR in [BCTransportItems](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/BCTransportItems.java) now wire to `PluggableBlocker::boundingBoxFor` / `PluggablePowerAdaptor::boundingBoxFor`. Each `Pluggable*` class gained a `public static boundingBoxFor(Direction)` accessor for its existing per-side `BOXES`, and its instance `getBoundingBox()` now delegates to the same static — so the preview and the actual placed pluggable cannot drift apart. Pinned by four new game tests in [PipePlacementHighlightTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/transport/client/render/PipePlacementHighlightTester.java) (blocker, power adaptor, lens, facade) asserting `getPlacementBoundingBox(stack, side)` equals the corresponding `boundingBoxFor(side)` on all six faces, so a future renaming or resizing of either side will fail the contract instead of silently desyncing.
- Heat Exchangers can be rotated by wrenching them again, restoring 1.12.2 behaviour. [TileHeatExchange.rotate](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/tile/TileHeatExchange.java) — which rotates a single exchanger 90° or swaps the start/end of a multi-block chain 180° — was wired and tested in the port, but had no caller from any user-facing path: [BlockHeatExchange.useItemOn](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/block/BlockHeatExchange.java) unconditionally opened the chain's GUI for *any* held item, so a wrench right-click was swallowed before it could reach the wrench's own `useOn` → `CustomRotationHelper.attemptRotateBlock` dispatch. `BlockHeatExchange` now implements `ICustomRotationHandler` and detects `IToolWrench` in `useItemOn`: non-crouch+wrench returns `PASS` so [ItemWrench_Neptune](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/item/ItemWrench_Neptune.java)'s `useOn` runs (which calls `attemptRotation`, plays the piston-slide sound, and grants the `wrenched` advancement); crouch+wrench opens the GUI (so a player can sneak-tweak a running chain without spinning it). This matches the established engine / distiller / dynamo wrench priority across the mod.
- Audited and fixed four regressions in BuildCraft-owned sound usage relative to 1.12.2 — every regression was a port-time call site that silently dropped a sound the 1.12.2 build had played. **(1)** The Quarry's block sound type was `SoundType.METAL` in [BCBuildersBlocks](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/BCBuildersBlocks.java); 1.12.2's `BlockQuarry#getSoundType` returned `SoundType.ANVIL`, and the quarry is the only BC machine that 1.12.2 deliberately gave a non-generic block sound (anvil clang on place/break/step) — restored. **(2)** [ItemPluggableSimple.onPlace](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/item/ItemPluggableSimple.java) (the item backing Pipe Plug and Pipe Power Adaptor) attached pluggables silently; 1.12.2's `lib/item/ItemPluggableSimple` played the place sound on every successful attach. **(3)** [ItemPluggableFacade.onPlace](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/item/ItemPluggableFacade.java) called `SoundUtil.playBlockPlace(world, pos)` without a `BlockState` argument, so the helper fell back to the pipe-holder's own state (METAL) — every facade place sounded metallic regardless of the wrapped block; the call now passes `fullState.phasedStates[0].stateInfo.state` so a stone facade clacks stone, a leaves facade rustles, glass facade sounds like glass, matching 1.12.2. [ItemPluggableLens.onPlace](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/item/ItemPluggableLens.java) had the same fall-through and now passes `Blocks.GLASS.defaultBlockState()` (an improvement on 1.12.2's `Blocks.STONE.getDefaultState()` placeholder, which the original author had flagged as a TODO/FIXME — a glass lens should sound like glass). **(4)** [SoundUtil.playBucketEmpty/Fill](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/SoundUtil.java) hardcoded the vanilla water `BUCKET_EMPTY` / `BUCKET_FILL` sounds and ignored the `FluidStack` argument entirely — so every fluid transfer (Tank right-click, fluid-handler interactions in [FluidUtilBC](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/FluidUtilBC.java)) sounded like water regardless of fluid; the helpers now delegate to `fluid.getFluid().getFluidType().getSound(stack, SoundActions.BUCKET_EMPTY/FILL)`, falling back to the vanilla water sound only when the fluid type defines none, so lava is back to *fwoosh*, oil/fuel/etc. now play whatever their fluid type registers. WaterGel's stage-dependent pitch ramp was *also* in the audit findings as suspected dead code; on closer inspection the existing `BlockWaterGel#getSoundType(BlockState)` override (`stage.soundType`) IS the dispatch endpoint of the NeoForge `IBlockExtension#getSoundType(state, level, pos, entity)` default — the audit was wrong, the ramp already fires through every vanilla place/break/step call site.
- The "Too many pipe filters" advancement is now obtainable, and is the **sole** vanilla-recipe-book unlock for the List item — restoring a 1.12.2 quality-of-life nudge that the port had dropped, and turning the moment of unlock into a discovery hook rather than a silent recipe-book entry the player never connects to a use case. The advancement parents to `minecraft:recipes/root` (so it has no advancement-screen entry by design — its sole purpose is to grant the [List](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/advancement/too_many_pipe_filters.json) recipe), and its `minecraft:impossible` criterion was unreachable because the matching Java grant in 1.12.2's `PipeBehaviourDiamond.onFilterSlotChange` was never ported. [PipeBehaviourDiamond](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourDiamond.java) now wires the filter inventory's existing `ItemHandlerSimple(size, callback)` constructor to a per-side change hook: each time a filter slot changes, it counts populated slots in that side's 9-slot bank and grants the advancement to the pipe owner once the count crosses ≥7/9 (`FILTERS_PER_SIDE - 2`, identical to 1.12.2). The grant runs server-side via `AdvancementUtil.unlockAdvancement(owner.id(), level, …)` and is short-circuited if the pipe has no recorded owner. Chunk loads stay quiet — `ItemHandlerSimple.deserializeNBT` writes through `setStackInternal`, which deliberately bypasses the callback — so the hook only fires on real player edits through the diamond-pipe GUI. The List recipe is also removed from the `has_paper` recipe-unlock bundle in [has_paper.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/advancement/recipes/has_paper.json) — previously, picking up any paper unlocked the List recipe alongside the Guide Book and the three clean paper variants, so the recipe-book entry appeared long before the player had any context for what a List is or why they'd want one. Pre-existing worlds where the player already triggered `has_paper` keep the recipe (the advancement reward fired once, the recipe is permanently in their book); the change only affects players whose paper-pickup happens after this build lands. The Guide Book and clean paper variants stay in the `has_paper` bundle — they're early-game paper tools and don't need the same kind of discovery framing.
- The Builder gains a Container Contents toggle, sitting immediately to the left of the existing Fluid Handling button. Captured container blocks (chests, hoppers, barrels, shulkers, the furnace family, dispensers/droppers, brewing stands) used to be placed with their Architect-captured inventory restored unconditionally — and the items_list JSON extractor in [blocks_simple_inventories.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/builders/vanilla/blocks_simple_inventories.json) was charging the player for that inventory through the resource panel without the player having any way to opt out. The new toggle lets the player choose at build time: **Include** (default, chest icon — current behavior; chest contents are filled and the captured items appear in the required-items list), or **Ignore** (chest+barrier overlay — the placed container is empty and the contents drop out of the resource panel so the player isn't sourcing items they won't receive). Implementation threads a new [EnumContainerContentsMode](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/EnumContainerContentsMode.java) through [ITileForSnapshotBuilder.getContainerContentsMode](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/ITileForSnapshotBuilder.java) and [TileBuilder](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileBuilder.java) (NBT-persisted, ContainerData-synced under [DATA_CONTENTS_MODE](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/container/ContainerBuilder.java)), and adds mode-aware overloads to [SchematicBlockDefault.computeRequiredItems](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/SchematicBlockDefault.java) (filters out `RequiredExtractorItemsList` contributions when IGNORE) and [SchematicBlockDefault.build](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/SchematicBlockDefault.java) (strips every items_list path from the tileNbt copy before `loadWithComponents` when IGNORE — uses the same JSON rules as the extractor side, via a new [NbtPath.remove](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/NbtPath.java) helper and [RequiredExtractor.clearItemsFromBlock](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/RequiredExtractor.java) hook, so any modded rule that declares an items_list path strips uniformly without hard-coding `Items`). Cycling the toggle re-bakes [Blueprint.BuildingInfo.toPlaceRequiredItems](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/Blueprint.java) in place and snaps the resource panel to the new cost via [BlueprintBuilder.refreshDisplayForContentsMode](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/BlueprintBuilder.java) — without that, the panel would stay stale until the SnapshotBuilder's lazy `check()` pass eventually wrapped around to each container position. The new button uses vanilla `Items.CHEST` (and `Items.BARRIER` overlay) so it adapts to resource packs. Cosmetic block-entity data (custom name, lock string, loot table seed, brewing fuel level) is preserved under IGNORE — only items_list paths go. Pinned by four new game tests in [ContainerContentsScanTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/ContainerContentsScanTester.java): INCLUDE-mode lists chest contents in required items, INCLUDE-mode restores those contents into the placed chest, IGNORE-mode drops contents from required items (chest item itself is still required), and IGNORE-mode places the chest with an empty inventory.
- The "Paving the way" and "Start of something big" Builder advancements are now obtainable. Both shipped as data only — unreachable `minecraft:impossible` criteria with no code-side grant — and the 1.12.2 attempt at "Paving the way" was dead code (the condition `currentBasePosIndex == basePoses.size()` was unreachable under its outer `< basePoses.size() - 1` guard); "Start of something big" was never wired in any branch. Both grants now run on the false→true edge of [TileBuilder.isDone](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileBuilder.java) for each base-pos completion. **Paving the way** fires when the builder finishes the last position of a multi-segment path (`path != null && path.size() >= 2 && currentBasePosIndex == basePoses.size() - 1`) — i.e. it consumed a path-marker chain at placement and just finished stamping the snapshot at every waypoint. **Start of something big** accumulates a new [Snapshot.countNonAirCells](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/Snapshot.java) into a per-builder counter on each base-pos completion and grants when the running total reaches 1024 cells; the count excludes `SchematicBlockAir` palette entries on Blueprints (Templates count every set bit), so air doesn't qualify but fluid sources do — `SchematicBlockFluid` doesn't override the default `isAir() = false`. The threshold sits comfortably above small test builds (a 5×5×5 cube is 125 cells) yet is reachable in normal play (a 32×32 floor or a 16×4×16 wall both qualify). Both latches are one-shot and persisted to NBT, and each only flips once the grant call actually reaches a `ServerPlayer` — owner-offline calls leave the latch armed for the next online tick, matching the pattern used by the Diggy Diggy Hole fix. The counter is also persisted, so a path-marker-fed Builder can accumulate cells across chunk reloads or server restarts mid-build without losing progress. Pinned by 10 new game tests across [SnapshotCountNonAirCellsTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/SnapshotCountNonAirCellsTester.java) (Template cardinality, Blueprint air exclusion, fluid-source positive case, null/empty safety) and [BuilderAdvancementsTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/BuilderAdvancementsTester.java) (paving predicate at start/middle/end of path, threshold constant matches spec, NBT round-trip of the four new persistent fields, fresh-builder defaults).
- Builders fed by a path-marker chain now show the route they will traverse, and survive chunk reload. When a Builder is placed against a path-marker chain it consumes the markers and remembers the route in [TileBuilder.path](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileBuilder.java), but the field was never serialized — so the client never saw it (the path-laser render in [BCBuildersEventDist.renderAllBuilders](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/BCBuildersEventDist.java) was dead code) and the server itself lost the route on chunk unload/reload, collapsing `updateBasePoses()` to the single-position fallback. The path now rides the same `saveAdditional`/`loadAdditional` cycle as every other persistent field, fixing both. The render switches from `STRIPES_WRITE` to `STRIPES_WRITE_DIRECTION` (directional stripes) with a 0.1-block endpoint inset, matching the visuals in 1.12.2's `RenderBuilder`. Pinned by a new `builder_path_survives_nbt_roundtrip` game test ([BuilderDropsTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/builders/BuilderDropsTester.java)).
- The "All plugged up" advancement is now obtainable, with x/8 progress visible in the advancement screen. The advancement shipped as data only — an unreachable `minecraft:impossible` criterion with no code-side grant — and was never wired even in 1.12.2. The [JSON](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/advancement/all_plugged_up.json) now declares one criterion per kind shown in the Pluggables creative tab (8 total — `blocker`, `power_adaptor`, `wire`, `gate`, `lens`, `pulsar`, `light_sensor`, `timer`) so the advancement screen displays incremental "x/8" progress automatically — the framework shows this whenever an advancement has more than one criterion. Per-player progress is tracked through a new NeoForge `AttachmentType` ([PluggablesPlaced](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/BCTransportAttachments.java)) — an 8-bit mask, one bit per `PluggablesPlaced.Kind` ordinal, persisted to player NBT and carried across respawns. Each pluggable's `onPlacedBy` (Blocker, PowerAdaptor, Gate, Lens, Pulsar, LightSensor, Timer) now calls [BCTransportAttachments.recordPluggablePlacement](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/BCTransportAttachments.java); the `wire` bit is set from [BlockPipeHolder](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/block/BlockPipeHolder.java)'s wire-placement branch in the same place that grants `colorful_electrician`, collapsing all 16 wire colours into a single placement signal. Facades sit in their own creative tab and deliberately do not count. Pinned by three new game tests in [PluggablesPlacedTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/transport/PluggablesPlacedTester.java) covering the fresh-attachment state, the first-sighting return value, and the all-eight completion threshold.
- Quarries now record the player who placed them, fixing two advancements that depended on it. [TileQuarry.onPlacedBy](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileQuarry.java) overrode the placement hook to do marker / IAreaProvider resolution but never chained to `super.onPlacedBy`, so `getOwner()` stayed null forever on every quarry — every other builders tile (Builder, Architect, Electronic Library, Filler) sets the owner one way or another, the quarry was the lone holdout. **"Diggy diggy hole"** was blocked because the mining-completion trigger gates on `getOwner() != null` and short-circuited every tick; **"Destroying the world"** was blocked because [BCBuildersEventDist.findOwnersToAward](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/BCBuildersEventDist.java) filters quarries with null-owner UUIDs before counting pairs. Adding the missing `super` call unblocks both. Pre-fix quarries already in the world keep their null owner — the fix only takes effect for newly placed quarries. Also tightened the Diggy latch: `advancementGranted = true` was set unconditionally after the award call, so if the owner happened to be offline at the moment the quarry finished (`unlockAdvancement` returns `false` in that case), the award was dropped and never retried on subsequent ticks — the latch now flips only when the award actually reached a `ServerPlayer`. Pinned by a new `quarry_on_placed_by_records_owner` game test ([TileQuarryOwnerTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileQuarryOwnerTester.java)).
- The "Paper collector" advancement is now obtainable, with x/4 progress visible in the advancement screen, and the Map Location item is dev-gated. The advancement shipped as data only — an unreachable `minecraft:impossible` criterion with no code-side grant — and was equally inert in 1.12.2 (the JSON has been carrying a single placeholder criterion since AEnterprise added it in 2017 with no matching grant). The criterion is now split into four — `write_to_list`, `write_to_blueprint`, `write_to_template`, `capture_with_schematic` — each required, so the advancement screen displays incremental "x/4" progress that the framework shows whenever an advancement has more than one criterion. The grants fire at the natural write site for each paper variant: [ContainerList.ListPhantomSlot.set](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/list/ContainerList.java) on every phantom-slot write into a List, [TileArchitectTable.scanComplete](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileArchitectTable.java) when the Architect finalizes a Blueprint or Template (one criterion or the other based on `snapshotType`), and [ItemSchematicSingle.useOn](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/item/ItemSchematicSingle.java) when a clean schematic captures a block. Criterion names are centralised in a new [PaperAdvancement](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/PaperAdvancement.java) constants class — a mismatch with the JSON keys silently prevents progress, so one source of truth — and [AdvancementUtil](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/AdvancementUtil.java) gained a UUID-based per-criterion overload to support the Architect's owner-by-UUID grant path. The Map Location paper item itself moves to the `BCLib.DEV`-gated registration block alongside the Power Tester, Goggles, Integration Table and Zone Planner: its only ever-shipped consumers were the Zone Planner (still a no-op tick stub) and the 1.7.10 Robotics waypoint system (never ported); the in-world overlay that gave it visual feedback in 1.12.2 was lost in the port and never re-added. In a public build the item is unregistered (creative-tab entry and a `BCTooltips.markDevOnly` line are null-guarded), and the lang description tightens from "Use every piece of paper" to "Write to every kind of paper" to match the new criterion shape. The advancement remains parented under `:list` and is still ungated by Map Location, so no progress depends on the dev-gated item.
- The "Mining Max Depth" config now means what it says for the Quarry, and existing quarries pick up changes on world load. [TileQuarry](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileQuarry.java) sized its mining box from the *frame top* (`max.getY() - 1 - miningMaxDepth`), so with the default 4-block-tall frame a config value of 12 only let the rig dig 9 blocks below the quarry block — out of step with the Mining Well and Pump, which both measure from their own position. The formula now anchors to `worldPosition.getY()`, matching the other two miners: 12 means 12 blocks below the quarry block, period. Separately, the mining box was computed once in `onPlacedBy` and persisted to NBT, so editing `miningMaxDepth` had no effect on already-placed quarries — `tick()` now reconciles `miningBox.min().getY()` against the current config every tick (a single int compare in the steady state, and the box iterator is nulled on shape change so the next pick is taken against the new bounds). The mining-box maximum still tracks the frame interior, so only the floor moves.
- The "Destroying the world" advancement is now obtainable. The advancement shipped as data only — an unreachable `minecraft:impossible` criterion with no code-side grant — and was never wired even in 1.12.2 despite a "Have two or more 64×64 sized quarries running at once at full speed" description. [TileQuarry](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileQuarry.java) now stamps `lastFullSpeedTick` each tick its battery is in unrestricted-power mode (`stored > capacity/2` — the gate inside `tick()` that unlocks the 512 MJ/t ceiling) AND its `currentTask` is something other than `TaskAddFrame` (i.e. actively destroying, not placing frame). [BCBuildersEventDist](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/BCBuildersEventDist.java) gains a `ServerTickEvent.Post` driver — registered from [BCBuilders](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/BCBuilders.java) — that throttles to one scan per second over the existing per-level quarry registry, groups by owner UUID, and grants the advancement when one owner has ≥2 quarries on 64×64+ frames whose stamps fall within the last 40 ticks (≈2s; wide enough to absorb engine sputter and inter-break drill-move ticks, narrow enough that "at once" is honest). The throttle interval is half the freshness window so no qualifying pair can slip through between consecutive scans, and the scan short-circuits immediately on any level with fewer than two tracked quarries — typical-server cost is one `HashMap` lookup per second. Pinned by five game tests in [DestroyingTheWorldTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/DestroyingTheWorldTester.java) covering the five eligibility filters that gate the predicate: same-owner pair positive, different-owners negative, undersized-frame negative, stale-stamp negative, and never-stamped negative — the never-stamped case originally fired the advancement on placement of two unpowered 64×64 quarries because `lastFullSpeedTick`'s `Long.MIN_VALUE` default overflowed the freshness subtraction into a large negative, falsely passing the "currently at full speed" gate; the predicate now short-circuits on the sentinel before the arithmetic.
- Quarries now collect the items their destruction lasers break during the frame-volume pre-clearing phase (the lasers fired from the corners that clear any obstructions inside the future frame box before the rig is built). [TileQuarry](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileQuarry.java)'s clearing path queues a `TaskBreakBlock` with `drillPos = null`, but the drop-routing inside `TaskBreakBlock.finish` was gated on `if (drillPos != null)` — a stale guard carried over from the original 1.21.11 port — so the drops returned by [BlockUtil.breakBlockAndGetDropsWithXp](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/BlockUtil.java) (which calls `destroyBlock(pos, false)` and never spawns the items in-world) were silently discarded. A user clearing a 64×4×64 volume to start a 64×64 quarry would watch the lasers chew through dozens of blocks while no items reached the adjacent chest. The guard is removed, matching the existing comment ("both tiers route drops 'as if mined by the rig itself,'" i.e. through `addToBestAcceptor` at the quarry's neighbours) and the spec the user already had in mind when asking about it. Pinned by two new game tests in [TileQuarryDropsTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileQuarryDropsTester.java) covering both phases: the frame-clearing path (`drillPos = null`) and the active-mining path (`drillPos` set).
- Pinned the [PipeBehaviour](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/transport/pipe/PipeBehaviour.java) `writeToNbt`/`readFromNbt` symmetry across the remaining sorting/filtering pipes. After the stripes-pipe direction fix immediately below, an audit found that the diamond (sorting), wood-diamond (emerald) and emzuli pipes all override `writeToNbt` without a matching `readFromNbt` — same shape as the stripes bug. None of these had a visible regression today (the filter contents the GUI shows are container-synced when the menu opens), but every in-place server→client sync silently dropped the freshly-written filter inventory, the emzuli's `currentSlot` round-robin pointer, the wood-diamond's `filterMode` / `currentFilter`, and the emzuli's per-slot dye colours — so anything later trying to read that state on the client (a render hook, a tooltip, an addon mod) saw whatever the constructor had defaulted to. [PipeBehaviourDiamond](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourDiamond.java), [PipeBehaviourEmzuli](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourEmzuli.java) and [PipeBehaviourWoodDiamond](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourWoodDiamond.java) gained the matching `readFromNbt` overrides; wood-diamond also recomputes its derived `filterValid` flag from the restored inventory. The dead `writeToNbt` stub on [PipeBehaviourObsidian](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourObsidian.java) (a no-op `return super.writeToNbt()`) was deleted. Pinned by three new tester classes ([PipeBehaviourDiamondSyncTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourDiamondSyncTester.java), [PipeBehaviourEmzuliSyncTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourEmzuliSyncTester.java), [PipeBehaviourWoodDiamondSyncTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourWoodDiamondSyncTester.java)) — same shape as the stripes tester: round-trip via `readFromNbt`, absent-tag-clears-state, and cold-load via the `(IPipe, CompoundTag)` constructor.
- Fixed the stripes pipe's gold laser beam never rendering on the client. The server's [PipeBehaviourStripes.onTick](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourStripes.java) correctly computes the laser direction (opposite of a single connected face) and rides it to the client in the pipe's NBT via the BE update packet, but `PipeBehaviour.readFromNbt` is a default no-op and `PipeBehaviourStripes` never overrode it — so the in-place sync path ([Pipe.readFromNbt](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/Pipe.java) → `behaviour.readFromNbt`) silently dropped the direction every chunk-update tick, leaving the client at `direction = null` and the renderer's early-return path always taken. Adding the override (and re-reading the battery NBT for the same reason) restores the laser visually whenever the pipe has exactly one connection. Pinned by three new unit tests in [PipeBehaviourStripesSyncTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourStripesSyncTester.java) covering the in-place sync round-trip, the absent-tag clear path, and the cold-load constructor.
- Filler now clears tall grass, short grass, snow layers, vines and other replaceable plant cover inside its build area. [TemplateBuilder](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/TemplateBuilder.java)'s `isBlockCorrect` previously flagged any non-air block as already-built, so positions holding a replaceable block (`canBeReplaced=true`) were marked CORRECT and the Filler never queued a break OR place task for them — enabling Excavate didn't help, because the check ran before the excavate decision. The fillable-slot check now also accepts non-fluid replaceable blocks, routing them through the place path so the inventory block overwrites them via vanilla `useOn` (which respects replaceable semantics). Fluids stay excluded so the fluid-mode logic continues to own water/lava handling. Pinned by eight new `template_fillable_*` game tests covering air, tall_grass, short_grass, snow_layer, and the negative cases (water source, lava source, solid blocks, waterlogged fence) in [TemplateBuilderFillableSlotTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/TemplateBuilderFillableSlotTester.java).
- JEI recipe lookup now works on BuildCraft fluid tanks. Hovering a tank widget (Tank block, Heat Exchanger, Distiller, Builder, Combustion Engine coolant tank, …) and pressing JEI's recipes (`R`) or uses (`U`) hotkey now focuses on the fluid currently held in that tank, the same as hovering a regular item slot. [BCGuiContainerHandler](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/compat/jei/BCGuiContainerHandler.java) gained a `getClickableIngredientUnderMouse` override that walks the screen's shown elements, finds the [GuiElementFluidTank](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/elem/GuiElementFluidTank.java) under the mouse, and exposes its non-empty fluid contents as a `FluidStack` clickable ingredient anchored to the tank's screen rectangle. An empty tank returns nothing, so the hotkey falls through to JEI's default cursor lookup.
- The "Refine and redefine" advancement is now obtainable, with x/10 progress visible in the advancement screen. The advancement shipped as data only — an unreachable `minecraft:impossible` criterion with no code-side grant — and was equally inert in the 1.12.2 advancement era despite a "Produce a tank full of every single type of oil and fuel" description. The advancement is granted to the owner of the Distiller / Pump that finally tops up the tenth counter. Per-player progress is tracked through a new NeoForge `AttachmentType` ([OilAndFuelProduction](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/BCFactoryAttachments.java)) — a 10-slot `int[]` keyed by [BCEnergyFluids.BASE_NAMES](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/BCEnergyFluids.java), one counter per base fluid, each saturating at one tank's worth (16,000 mB) and heat-agnostic so any of the three temperature variants of a base name counts toward the same target. The [JSON](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/advancement/refine_and_redefine.json) now declares one criterion per base fluid (10 total) so the advancement screen shows incremental "x/10" progress — the framework displays this whenever an advancement has more than one criterion. [TileDistiller_BC8](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/tile/TileDistiller_BC8.java) credits both the gas and liquid output of every committed distillation step to its owner's tracker; [TilePump](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/tile/TilePump.java) credits drained crude oil — the only one of the ten base names the Distiller never produces (it's the recipe input). Pinned by four new game tests in [OilAndFuelProductionTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/factory/OilAndFuelProductionTester.java) covering fresh-attachment, saturate-and-clamp, unknown/non-positive rejection, and the completion edge firing exactly once.
- The "Building for the Future" advancement is now obtainable. The advancement shipped as data only — an unreachable `minecraft:impossible` criterion with no code-side grant — and was never wired even in 1.12.2. [TileFiller](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileFiller.java) now grants it to the placing player the first time the Filler completes a build cycle while in LOOP mode, matching the advancement's "long term automation" description. The award is gated on the false→true transition of the `finished` flag so the tick loop doesn't re-fire the grant every tick once the builder has nothing left to do, and `setControlMode` now also resets `finished` on the ON→LOOP transition so a Filler that completed in ON mode re-arms (and can earn the advancement) when the player flips it to LOOP. Pinned by a new `filler_building_for_the_future_advancement` game test ([FillerAdvancementTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/builders/FillerAdvancementTester.java)) covering JSON contract, advancement-id constant, and the OFF→ON / ON→LOOP / LOOP→LOOP transition contracts on `setControlMode`.
- The "I can see!" (goggles) advancement is no longer registered. The goggles headpiece never finished its 1.12.2 → modern port and is dev-gated (registered only under `-Dbuildcraft.dev=true`), so the advancement could never be earned in a public build — its `minecraft:impossible` criterion would only have been granted by a wear-goggles hook that does not exist. The advancement file ([goggles.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/advancement/goggles.json)) and its two lang entries are removed; the dev-only `ItemGoggles` registration and the placeholder guidebook page are untouched, so the advancement can be reinstated alongside the item if the goggles ship in a future release.
- The "Colorful electrician" advancement is now obtainable, with x/16 progress visible in the advancement screen. The advancement shipped as data only — an unreachable `minecraft:impossible` criterion with no code-side grant — and was never wired even in 1.12.2 (the 1.12.2 file was misnamed `colorful_electricial.json` and equally inert). The advancement is granted the first time a player has placed a pipe wire of every dye colour. The [JSON](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/advancement/colorful_electrician.json) now declares one criterion per dye colour (16 total) so the advancement screen displays incremental "x/16" progress automatically — the framework shows this whenever an advancement has more than one criterion. Per-player progress is tracked through a new NeoForge `AttachmentType` ([WireColoursPlaced](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/BCTransportAttachments.java)) — a 16-bit mask, one bit per `DyeColor.getId()`, persisted to player NBT and carried across respawns — incremented by [BlockPipeHolder](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/block/BlockPipeHolder.java) in the same wire-placement branch that now grants `logic_transportation`; first-sighting of a colour awards the matching criterion by `DyeColor.getName()` ("white", "orange", "light_blue", …). The lang description tightened from "Use 16 of each color of pipe wire to make your piping system more robust" to "Place a pipe wire of every colour" to match. Pinned by three new game tests in [WireColoursPlacedTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/transport/WireColoursPlacedTester.java) covering the fresh-attachment state, the first-sighting return value, and the all-sixteen completion threshold.
- The "Logic transportation" advancement is now obtainable. The advancement shipped as data only — an unreachable `minecraft:impossible` criterion with no code-side grant. 1.12.2's `BlockPipeHolder` granted it whenever a placed wire actually completed a connection (a same-colour wire on an in-cube neighbouring corner or on an adjacent pipe), and the port had dropped that hook. [BlockPipeHolder](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/block/BlockPipeHolder.java)'s wire-placement branch now runs the same connectivity probe — six `WireNode.offset` steps from the freshly-placed corner, checking the current tile or `level.getBlockEntity(...)` for a same-colour wire — and grants the advancement to the placer when one matches. Laying down an isolated wire still does not unlock it. Pinned by four new game tests covering the predicate: isolated wire, in-cube same colour, in-cube different colour, and cross-tile same colour ([PipeWireConnectivityTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/transport/block/PipeWireConnectivityTester.java)).
- The "Black Gold" advancement is now obtainable, and oil pumps can drain oil springs submerged under water. Two bugs kept it unreachable. First, [TilePump](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/tile/TilePump.java)'s oil-spring scan looked one block too high — at `minY + 1`, where the spring's oil sits, instead of `minY`, where the spring block is — so `oilSpringPos` was always null, the spring's `onPumpOil` code grant never ran, and `black_gold` was unachievable everywhere, not just at sea. Second, the pump's downward search stopped at the first fluid it met, so ocean water flooding a depleted well's vertical shaft would lock the pump onto water and hide the oil source on the spring beneath it. The pump now probes straight down through air, tubes and fluid alike (`TilePump.probeDown`), drilling past water to reach BuildCraft oil below it, and idles — rather than locking onto water — when it finds a dry spring waiting to regenerate. [BlockSpring](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/block/BlockSpring.java) now regenerates its fluid through a non-oil fluid occupying the block above it, so an ocean-borne spring is no longer left permanently sterile once water seeps in above it. Pinned by new `pump_probe_*`, `core_spring_oil_regenerates_through_water` and `core_spring_oil_keeps_solid_above` game tests.
- The "Flooding the world" advancement is now obtainable, and the Flood Gate tracks its owner. The advancement shipped as data only — an unreachable `minecraft:impossible` criterion with no code-side grant. [BlockFloodGate](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/block/BlockFloodGate.java) now records the placing player on [TileFloodGate](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/tile/TileFloodGate.java) (persisted to NBT, shown in the F3 debug overlay), and the gate grants the advancement to that owner each time it successfully floods a block — matching 1.12.2's `TileFloodGate`, which wired this and the port dropped. Pinned by a new `flood_gate_flooding_the_world_advancement` game test.
- The "Heating and Distilling" advancement is now obtainable, and the Distiller tracks its owner. The advancement shipped as data only — an unreachable `minecraft:impossible` criterion with no code-side grant — and was never wired even in 1.12.2. [BlockDistiller](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/block/BlockDistiller.java) now records the placing player on [TileDistiller_BC8](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/tile/TileDistiller_BC8.java) (persisted to NBT, synced to clients), surfaced through a new ownership ledger on the Distiller GUI. The advancement is granted to that owner the moment the Distiller starts distilling oil at a heat tier its dimension does not spawn naturally — i.e. oil that was run through a Heat Exchanger first. Overworld oil spawns cool, so distilling hot or searing oil qualifies; the predicate also has a Nether branch (searing is the natural tier there) ahead of the planned Nether oil feature. Pinned by a new `distiller_heating_and_distilling_advancement` game test.
- The "Sorting all the things" advancement is now obtainable: right-clicking a List item to open its GUI triggers the unlock, matching 1.12.2 behaviour. The advancement existed in data but was never wired to any code-side grant.
- Fixed the "Lava Power" advancement never triggering. [TileEngineStone_BC8](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/tile/TileEngineStone_BC8.java) granted `powering_up` when any fuel was consumed but never checked whether that fuel was a lava bucket to award `lava_power`; the advancement has always used a code-triggered `minecraft:impossible` criterion, so it was permanently unachievable. Pinned by a new `advancement_lava_power_loaded` game test.
- Pipes now record the player who placed them. [TilePipeHolder](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/tile/TilePipeHolder.java)'s `getOwner()` was a stub returning `null` ("Owner tracking not yet ported"), so the Stripes pipe — the only pipe that reads the owner — attributed its block-breaking and stripe actions to a generic BuildCraft fake player instead of the placer, bypassing the placer's identity for claim/protection mods and block-break events. `TilePipeHolder` now records the placer's `GameProfile` in `onPlacedBy` and persists it to NBT (`ownerUUID`/`ownerName`), mirroring the owner tracking [TileBC_Neptune](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/tile/TileBC_Neptune.java) already provides to the mod's machine tiles. Pinned by a new `pipe_records_owner_on_placement` game test ([PipeOwnerTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/transport/PipeOwnerTester.java)).
- The Integration Table is now dev-only. No integration recipes are registered, so the block is non-functional in survival; it joins the Power Tester, Zone Planner and Goggles in being registered only under `-Dbuildcraft.dev=true` — absent from public releases, obtainable from the creative tab in a dev workspace, and carrying a red "Dev only" tooltip. Block, block-entity, item and menu registrations follow the established `BCLib.DEV ? … : null` pattern across [BCSiliconBlocks](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSiliconBlocks.java), [BCSiliconBlockEntities](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSiliconBlockEntities.java), [BCSiliconItems](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSiliconItems.java) and [BCSiliconMenuTypes](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSiliconMenuTypes.java), with null-guards at the capability, screen, creative-tab and guide-group use sites. Its survival craft recipe is removed (and dropped from the `has_gear_diamond` recipe-unlock advancement), and its `minecraft:mineable/pickaxe` tag entry made `required: false`. Its block loot table is removed as well: a block loot table is parsed at datapack load whether or not its block exists, so one naming a dev-gated item logs a parse error in every public build — the Zone Planner shipped with that exact latent fault, so its loot table is deleted in the same pass. Dev-only blocks now match the Power Tester, which carries no loot table file. Verified by launching the game-test server with `-Dbuildcraft.dev=false`: it boots clean with no recipe, advancement, tag or loot-table errors.
- Wooden item pipes no longer drain the Assembly Table's crafting resources. Its resource inventory was registered with `EnumAccess.BOTH`, exposing it to pipes as extractable — but the Assembly Table has no pipe-facing output slot (it ejects finished output itself, like a Quarry), so that inventory holds only input materials. [TileAssemblyTable](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/tile/TileAssemblyTable.java) now registers it as `INSERT`. Pinned by a new `assemblytable_wood_pipe_skips_resources` game test ([MachinePipeConnectivityTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/factory/MachinePipeConnectivityTester.java)).
- Simplified the "Categorizing with colors" advancement to a single unlock: placing a Daizuli pipe. It previously had three triggers — wrenching a Lapis or Daizuli pipe to recolour it, or placing an Emzuli pipe — but the Lapis and Emzuli pipes only *paint* items, whereas the Daizuli pipe is the one that actually *routes* by colour. It is now granted directly in [TilePipeHolder.onPlacedBy](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/tile/TilePipeHolder.java), gated on the placed pipe being a Daizuli, alongside the existing pipe-placement advancements (`pipe_dream`, `pipe_diversification`, `pipe_fanatic`). [PipeBehaviourDaizuli](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourDaizuli.java), [PipeBehaviourLapis](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourLapis.java) and [PipeBehaviourEmzuli](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourEmzuli.java) drop their advancement code entirely. The advancement icon ([categorizing_with_colors.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/advancement/categorizing_with_colors.json)) changes from the Emzuli pipe to the Daizuli pipe to match.
- Wooden item pipes now pull crafted output from the Auto Workbench's result slot, not its crafting ingredients. Two port-era bugs combined here. **(1)** The materials inventory — the insert side a pipe feeds resources into — was registered with `EnumAccess.BOTH` instead of `EnumAccess.INSERT`, so it was exposed to pipes as extractable; because [ItemHandlerManager](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/tile/item/ItemHandlerManager.java) lists the materials handler before the result handler in the combined pipe-facing handler, a wood pipe iterating slots reached the ingredient slots first and drained them. [TileAutoWorkbenchBase](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/tile/TileAutoWorkbenchBase.java) now registers `materials` as `INSERT`, matching 1.12.2 and the sibling Advanced Crafting Table. **(2)** With (1) fixed, [PipeFlowItems.tryExtractItems](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/flow/PipeFlowItems.java) still extracted nothing: its slot scan `break`s on the first slot matching the pipe's filter, but did so even when that slot refused extraction — so an insert-only materials slot holding an ingredient blocked the scan before it could reach the result slot. 1.12.2 scanned via `IItemTransactor.extract`, which skips non-extractable slots; the modern inline scan now likewise keeps going, breaking only once it finds a slot that genuinely yields items. The GUI and the workbench's internal crafting are unaffected — they use the raw handler, not the pipe-facing wrapper. The `autoworkbench_wood_pipe_extracts` game test ([MachinePipeConnectivityTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/factory/MachinePipeConnectivityTester.java)) now seeds the materials inventory and asserts the wood pipe drains the result slot while leaving the ingredients untouched.
- The Extended Logic advancement icon rendered as the plain basic (clay-brick) gate instead of the gold diamond-modifier gate 1.12.2 used. [extended_logic.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/advancement/extended_logic.json) selected the icon's gate variant through the `minecraft:custom_model_data` component — the routing key for the `minecraft:select` model in `items/plug_gate.json`. But that select model never runs at item-render time: [BCSiliconClient.onModifyBakingResult](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/BCSiliconClient.java) swaps the gate item's baked model for the programmatic [GateItemModel](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/model/GateItemModel.java), which builds its geometry from the gate variant read out of the `minecraft:custom_data` `{gate:{…}}` NBT via [ItemPluggableGate.getVariant](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/item/ItemPluggableGate.java) — the same data a crafted gate item carries — and ignores `custom_model_data` entirely. With no `custom_data` present, `GateVariant` fell back to its all-zero default (clay-brick material, AND logic, no modifier), so the icon drew the basic gate. `extended_logic.json` now carries the proper `custom_data` NBT for the gold + diamond-modifier + OR-logic gate. [pipe_logic.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/advancement/pipe_logic.json) carried the same inert `custom_model_data`; its icon is correctly the basic gate (as in 1.12.2), so the dead component was simply removed.
- Fixed a regression where creative-mode players could no longer drop ice blocks into a Combustion Engine's coolant tank. Vanilla ice, packed ice and blue ice are registered as solid coolants — clicking the coolant tank with one on the cursor converts it to water — but [WidgetFluidTank](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/widget/WidgetFluidTank.java)'s creative branch had gained an unconditional `return` after its bucket-handling block, so a creative player holding any non-fluid-container item hit that `return` before the solid-coolant conversion could run. The `return` now fires only when the held item actually is a fluid container, letting other items fall through to the solid-coolant path exactly as the survival branch already did. Survival was unaffected. Pinned by a new `combustion_engine_coolant_accepts_ice` game test ([EngineTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/energy/EngineTester.java)) exercising both modes.
- BuildCraft machines with an internal MJ battery now accept Forge Energy directly when the `powerMode` config enables MJ↔RF autoconversion. Previously only the Quarry, Filler and Builder exposed `Capabilities.Energy.BLOCK` — and unconditionally, ignoring `powerMode` — while the Pump, Mining Well, Distiller, Chute and Laser had MJ batteries but no FE surface at all, so an FE cable powered a Quarry but not a Pump.
