All eight now share one config-gated registration (`MjBatteryEnergyHandler.createIfRfEnabled`): FE is exposed under `MJ_AUTOCONVERT_RF` / `DISPLAY_RF` and withheld under `MJ_ONLY`, where machines stay MJ-only. [MjBatteryEnergyHandler.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/mj/MjBatteryEnergyHandler.java), [BCFactory.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/BCFactory.java), [BCSilicon.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSilicon.java), [BCBuilders.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/BCBuilders.java)
- Gate item-filter triggers, and the Builder's required-items display, no longer lose their items. Modern Minecraft needs a registry to write an `ItemStack` to NBT, and several port-era stubs skipped it. [StatementParameterItemStack](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/statements/StatementParameterItemStack.java)'s NBT constructor ignored its argument and `writeToNbt` wrote nothing — so the five gate triggers that take an item filter (Items in Inventory, Inventory Level, Fluid Container, Fluid Container Level, Items Traversing) silently lost their configured item on world reload and never showed it in the gate GUI; [StatementParameterItemStackExact](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/statements/StatementParameterItemStackExact.java) shared the gap. Both now encode through `ItemStack.CODEC` with `NBTUtilBC.registryAwareOps()`, the registry-aware path already used by `ItemHandlerSimple` and `ListHandler`. The Builder's "remaining items" display had the matching stub in [BlueprintBuilder](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/BlueprintBuilder.java) / [SnapshotBuilder](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/SnapshotBuilder.java) — it wrote empty tags into the client sync, so the list rendered blank — and now sends the real stacks, with a separate count field so display totals above `ItemStack.CODEC`'s 99-cap survive. Three game tests ([StatementSerializationTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/core/statements/StatementSerializationTester.java)) pin the round-trip.
- Quarries keep their work area chunk-loaded again. [ChunkLoaderManager](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/chunkload/ChunkLoaderManager.java) had been a stub since the 1.21 port — the old `ForgeChunkManager` ticket API was gone, so `updateChunksFor`/`releaseChunksFor` only logged — and a running Quarry stopped the moment the player walked far enough for its chunks to unload. It now uses NeoForge's `TicketController`: a controller registered on the mod event bus from [BCLib](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/BCLib.java) force-loads each chunk in a tile's `getChunksToLoad()` set and releases them when the tile is removed. `TileQuarry` already called `loadChunksForTile`/`releaseChunksFor` at the right points.
- The MJ passive-provider capability is now real, completing a task the previous audit entry deferred. `MjAPI.CAP_PASSIVE_PROVIDER` and `CAP_READABLE` were `Object` constants left `null` by a stub `CapabilitiesHelper`; they are now proper `BlockCapability`s alongside `CAP_RECEIVER`/`CAP_CONNECTOR`. [PipeFlowPower.tryExtractPower](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/flow/PipeFlowPower.java) — a `// TODO` that returned 0 — now performs the real `IMjPassiveProvider` lookup, matching the Redstone-Flux pipe's twin fixed earlier. No BuildCraft block exposes the capability yet, so this is API-surface correctness for addon machines that do.
- Placing a Facade or a Gate on a pipe now plays the block-place sound, like every other pluggable. [ItemPluggableFacade](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/item/ItemPluggableFacade.java) had a `// TODO` where the `SoundUtil.playBlockPlace` call belonged, and [ItemPluggableGate](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/item/ItemPluggableGate.java) had it commented out; both now call it as the Lens and Pulsar items already do.
- Fixed logic gates with a redstone trigger desyncing on the client — a gate could evaluate "Redstone Signal On" correctly on the server yet render stuck on/off after a lever toggle or after a world reload, only snapping back once the lever was toggled again. The server recomputes a gate's display state (`isOn`, `triggerOn`, `actionOn`) from scratch every tick in [GateLogic.resolveActions](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/gate/GateLogic.java), but `writeToNbt` also persisted it — and that one method backs *both* the on-disk save and the block-entity update tag a client rebuilds the gate from on chunk load. Persisting it to disk let a stale state survive reloads; and because the glow packet (`sendIsOn`) is edge-triggered, a client that rebuilt the gate from a tag missing the live state was never corrected until the next change. The two roles are now split: the disk save carries configuration only, while runtime display state rides the client update tag in a separate `plugsClient` section — written by [TilePipeHolder.getUpdateTag](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/tile/TilePipeHolder.java), applied client-side on receipt, and serialised live so it is always current. New `PipePluggable.writeClientUpdateData`/`readClientUpdateData` hooks generalise this for any pluggable. Covered by three game tests ([GateRedstoneSyncTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/silicon/gate/GateRedstoneSyncTester.java)): the server recompute tracks redstone deterministically, the disk save excludes runtime state, and a gate rebuilt from the client update tag comes up in the correct state.
- Placing a gate, pluggable, or wire on a pipe now previews where it will land. A pipe's selection outline highlights the hovered *segment* — for a hit on the central core, the whole core cube — but a pluggable mounts on a specific *face* and a wire on a specific *corner*, which a uniform cube outline can't convey (aiming at a core face flush against a connection arm was especially misleading: the outline showed the core, the gate went on the face). While you hold a pluggable or wire, [PipePlacementHighlight](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/render/PipePlacementHighlight.java) replaces the segment outline with an outline of exactly what would be placed — a panel on the target face, or the target corner box — resolved by the same [BlockPipeHolder](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/block/BlockPipeHolder.java) code (`resolveTargetFace` / `resolveTargetWirePart`) that performs the placement, so the preview and the result always agree. An already-occupied face or corner keeps the normal outline; sneak-placement is unaffected.
- Item pipes connect to the Auto Workbench, Assembly Table, Integration Table, Advanced Crafting Table, and Electronic Library again. Each exposes a pipe-facing inventory through `ItemHandlerManager`, but the matching `Capabilities.Item.BLOCK` registration was missing after the 1.21 capability-system port, so pipes found no handler and refused to attach. [BCFactory.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/BCFactory.java), [BCSilicon.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSilicon.java), [BCBuilders.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/BCBuilders.java)
- Iron FE and Diamond FE pipes: fixed a missing inventory-item texture and an untranslated wrench message. **Item texture** — [pipe_iron_rf.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/models/item/pipe_iron_rf.json) and [pipe_diamond_rf.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/models/item/pipe_diamond_rf.json) referenced `pipes/` sprites — `iron_rf_clear`, `iron_rf_filled`, `diamond_rf` — that no longer exist, so both pipes rendered the missing-texture sprite as their inventory/held item (the in-world block model was unaffected). The item-texture de-duplication pass had repointed each pipe item model from its private `item/pipe_*.png` copy onto the matching in-world `pipes/*` sprite — valid then, those three sprites still existed — but the later pipe-texture prune deleted them as unreferenced, its scan not seeing the references the de-dup pass had just added. Both FE item models now use the `_m128` limiter-state variant (the unlimited/default frame), mirroring the working [pipe_iron_power.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/models/item/pipe_iron_power.json) / [pipe_diamond_power.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/models/item/pipe_diamond_power.json); the in-world model draws the full `*_rf_m{0,4,8,16,32,64,128}` limiter set through the pipe model generator. **Wrench message** — [PipeBehaviourLimiter](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourLimiter.java) builds its action-bar key as `chat.pipe.<rf|power>.iron.mode` from the flow type, but only the `power` key existed in [en_us.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/lang/en_us.json) — so wrenching an FE pipe's transfer limit showed the raw `chat.pipe.rf.iron.mode` key. Added it as "Switched to %s FE/t limit", with a fixed `FE/t` unit matching the creative-engine / kinesis-pipe precedent (`chat.pipe.power.iron.mode` = "Switched to %s MJ/t limit"): the FE/RF naming toggle is client-scope config while this message is built server-side, so a toggle-aware key can't resolve per-client.
- Right-clicking an engine with a pipe in hand no longer silently does nothing. Engines treated every pipe as "place me" and handed off to vanilla placement, so when the target cell was blocked — e.g. a pipe already sitting beside the engine — the click did nothing instead of opening the engine GUI. Each engine now places only the pipe types that connect to it ([EnginePipeInteraction](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/block/EnginePipeInteraction.java)): the [Combustion engine](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/block/BlockEngineIron_BC8.java) takes fluid pipes and wooden kinesis pipes, the [Stirling engine](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/block/BlockEngineStone_BC8.java) takes item pipes and wooden kinesis pipes, the [MJ Dynamo](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/block/BlockDynamoMJ.java) takes all kinesis pipes and wooden FE pipes, and the [FE engine](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/block/BlockEngineFE.java) takes all FE pipes and wooden kinesis pipes. Any other pipe — or an accepted pipe that has nowhere to go — opens the GUI instead of failing quietly. Sneak-clicking still places any pipe via vanilla rules.
- List item MATERIAL matching no longer treats every ingot as the same material. [ListMatchHandlerTags](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/list/ListMatchHandlerTags.java) reads each item tag's path as a `type/material` pair — `c:ingots/iron` is type `ingots`, material `iron` — but a single-segment tag with no slash (`c:ingots`, `minecraft:planks`) was counted as both a type *and* a material. Because every ingot also carries the umbrella `c:ingots` tag, a List in MATERIAL mode matched iron, gold, copper, netherite… all against one another. Single-segment tags now feed MATERIAL only as a fallback — used when an item carries no slashed tag at all, so planks (whose sole tag is `minecraft:planks`) still match each other by material, while anything with a precise `…/<material>` tag (ingots, ores, storage blocks, nuggets) is matched on that material part alone. TYPE mode is unchanged.
- Engine piston animation no longer stair-steps, and all six engine types now animate through one shared code path. The piston is driven by [engine_base.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat_models/engine_base.json)'s `progress_size = progress * 15.99` expression. The Combustion, Stirling, FE and MJ Dynamo engines render through [BCEnergyModels](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/BCEnergyModels.java), whose per-frame bake cache quantised the animation `progress` before feeding it to the model — originally to 1/16, so each step moved the piston a full ~1 pixel and it visibly jumped between 16 discrete positions per stroke instead of gliding. The Creative and Redstone engines render through [BCCoreModels](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCoreModels.java), which had no cache — it rebaked every frame at the exact un-quantised `getProgressClient()` value, staying perfectly smooth but churning ~22 `MutableQuad`s plus their backing objects per engine per frame straight into the GC. The cache logic is now one shared [EngineModelCache](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/render/tile/EngineModelCache.java) used by every engine, quantising to 1/128 (~0.125 px per step — sub-pixel, smooth in motion). All six engines now get both the smooth animation and the bake cache; the per-engine-type cache bound is 6 (stage) × 129 (progress) × 6 (facing) = 4644 `MutableQuad[]` reference slots, still negligible. (The original code comment's claim that the model had an inherent 1-pixel resolution was mistaken — model element vertices bake to sub-pixel float coordinates.)
- PNG textures palettized for size. Every PNG under [src/main/resources/assets/](src/main/resources/assets) was reviewed — NeoForge 26.1.2 loads 8-bit indexed (palette) PNGs identically to truecolor, and an indexed sprite stores one byte per pixel rather than three or four. 273 textures were already palette-mode and left untouched; the other 385 were each re-encoded two ways — a lossless 8-bit palette PNG (only when the image holds ≤256 distinct colours) and an optimized truecolor PNG — both with ancillary metadata (text / ICC / dpi chunks) stripped and zlib at maximum compression, after which the smaller of the two was written back, and only when it also beat the file already on disk. 237 ended up as palette PNGs; 144 stayed truecolor because the palette form came out *larger* — on a 16×16 sprite with a handful of colours the extra `PLTE`+`tRNS` chunks can outweigh the per-pixel saving, and 8 GUI textures (`gui/buttons.png`, the six `gui/guide/` book pages, `gui/heat_exchanger.png`) hold >256 colours and so cannot be indexed without lossy quantization. Those truecolor keepers were still re-saved in their smallest lossless form — grayscale `L`/`LA`, or `RGB` when fully opaque — with metadata stripped; 4 were already optimal and left as-is. All 381 rewritten files were verified pixel-identical (decoded back to RGBA and compared against their pre-change originals), so there is no visual change. The processed set shrank from 662,353 to 291,927 bytes (−55.9%) and the whole on-disk asset tree from 783,497 to 413,071 bytes (−47.3%).
- Pipe-texture cleanup: 108 unreferenced or duplicate sprites pruned from [textures/pipes/](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/textures/pipes), all of which were being stitched onto the vanilla blocks atlas by the `pipes` directory source despite nothing referencing them. **Deleted (37):** the misspelled `diamnd_*` orphans, the `_silver` colour files (byte-identical to `_light_gray` — "silver" is the pre-1.13 dye name), and the `_fe` energy family (31 files, each byte-identical to its `_rf` twin — FE and RF are the same energy system and only `_rf` pipes are registered). **Archived to [misc/unused_textures/](misc/unused_textures) (71):** the `_power_old` set (no old-power pipe exists), the andesite/diorite/granite material sprites (no such pipes — their orphan `dye_replace` entries were also dropped from [blocks.json](src/main/resources/assets/minecraft/atlases/blocks.json)), the unused `m1`/`m2` limiter steps (the limiter uses only m0/m4/m8/m16/m32/m64/m128), the `robot_station*` sprites (robotics unported), and assorted strays (`test_fluid*`, orphaned `mask_*` files, `transparent_facade`, `power_top`/`rf_top`/`rf_flow`). The mask-name table in [PipeBaseModelGenStandard](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/model/PipeBaseModelGenStandard.java) was then pruned to only its live entries, dropping every speculative key for a pipe or texture that never existed; this also corrected a latent mis-key where light-gray daizuli/lapis pipes were looked up under the pre-1.13 name `silver` and so resolved no shared mask.
- Trigger and wire texture cleanup: 50 unreferenced trigger sprites archived and a duplicate wire sprite deleted. `textures/triggers/` is stitched onto the vanilla blocks atlas wholesale by [blocks.json](src/main/resources/assets/minecraft/atlases/blocks.json)'s `minecraft:directory` source, so a file being present in the folder is not the same as a file being used — 50 of its 160 PNGs were never resolved through a `SpriteHolder` ([BCCoreSprites](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCoreSprites.java), [BCTransportSprites](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/BCTransportSprites.java) and [BCSiliconSprites](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSiliconSprites.java) are the only consumers) and were moved to [misc/unused_textures/triggers/](misc/unused_textures/triggers). 21 are art for the unported robots / robot-stations subsystem (`action_robot_*`, `action_station_*`, `trigger_robot_*` — kept against a future port, alongside the already-archived `robot_*` entity textures); the other 29 are genuinely superseded: the legacy 15-icon `redstone_01`–`redstone_15` redstone-level set (live code uses `parameter_redstone_0`–`15`), the off-scale `m4`/`m32` icons of both the MJ and RF power-limiter sets (the limiter has seven steps — `m256 m128 m64 m16 m8 m2 m0` — since [PipeBehaviourLimiter](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourLimiter.java)'s `MAX_SHIFT` is 6), `trigger_energy_storage_below25/50/75` (the modern storage trigger is a binary high/low), `trigger_pipecontents_containsenergy`/`_empty`/`_toomuchenergy` (only the items / fluids / requests-energy variants are wired), `trigger_coolant_below_threshold` and `trigger_fuel_below_threshold` (no trigger class references either), `action_pulsar_off` (the pulsar action exposes only its on/single sprites), and the legacy combined `guitriggers_3_4` GUI sheet. Separately, `textures/wires/silver.png` was deleted outright — it is a byte-identical duplicate of `light_gray.png`, and [PipeWireRenderer](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/render/PipeWireRenderer.java) only ever resolves wire sprites by `DyeColor.getName()` (`light_gray`), so the pre-1.13 alias `silver` was never requested. The long-empty `textures/station/` directory was also removed (its one file `base.png` had already been archived as `misc/unused_textures/station_base.png` when the robotics subsystem was shelved). No code or atlas edits were needed: all 110 still-referenced trigger sprites and all 16 wire colours are untouched.
- Item-texture de-duplication and orphan cleanup — 68 redundant or dead files cleared out of `textures/item/`, with no visual change (every swapped sprite is byte-identical to the one it replaced, verified by hash). **Pipe items (59 files):** every `item/pipe_*.png` sprite was an exact copy of the corresponding in-world pipe texture under `textures/pipes/`; the 46 pipe item models now reference the `pipes/*` originals directly (e.g. `item/pipe_wood_item` → `pipes/wood_item_clear`, `item/pipe_diamond_rf` → `pipes/diamond_rf`) and the duplicate copies are deleted, taking 59 sprites off the vanilla blocks atlas. **Paintbrush (3 files):** the root `paintbrush.png` (identical to `paintbrush/clean.png`, which [paintbrush.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/models/item/paintbrush.json) actually uses) plus the legacy-named `paintbrush/lightblue.png` and `paintbrush/silver.png` (identical to the modern `light_blue`/`light_gray`) are deleted; [paintbrush_light_gray.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/models/item/paintbrush_light_gray.json) was still pointing at the legacy `silver` name and now uses `light_gray`, the colour name the code already uses everywhere else. **Fragile Fluid Shard (1 file):** `fragile_fluid_container.png` was an orphaned single-layer leftover — the item model composes `fragile_fluid_shard_base` + `fragile_fluid_shard_fluid` instead — deleted. **Plug icons (5 files):** the flat `plug_gate_base`, `plug_gate_logic`, `plug_lens`, `plug_light_sensor` and `plug_timer` icons, orphaned when those plug items moved to 3D models that sample `block/plugs/*`, were moved to [misc/unused_textures/item/](misc/unused_textures/item) alongside the already-archived `plug_pulsar.png`.
- Per-tick chunk re-mesh fix extended to the Laser, laser tables, Filler, and Builder. The same `level.sendBlockUpdated()` misuse fixed for the fluid and mining tiles — a block-change broadcast that re-meshes the whole chunk section client-side and stutters FPS in terrain-dense chunks — was also driving frequent client syncs in four more block entities: [TileLaser](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/tile/TileLaser.java) re-meshed every server tick, [TileLaserTableBase](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/tile/TileLaserTableBase.java) (assembly table, advanced crafting table, …) every tick its stored laser power rose, and [TileFiller](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileFiller.java) / [TileBuilder](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileBuilder.java) every 5 ticks while building. All four now sync via [MessageUtil.sendUpdateToTrackingPlayers](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/MessageUtil.java), which pushes only the block-entity data packet with no re-mesh. Discrete one-off syncs in the same files — block placement, scan/build completion, GUI mode changes, assembly-table recipe-state changes — were deliberately left as block updates, since a re-mesh on a genuine rare event is correct.
- Old laser-beam textures archived. The six pre-BC8 laser textures in `textures/lasers_old/` — the `red`/`green`/`blue`/`yellow` colored beams and `stripes_blue`/`stripes_yellow` — were moved out of the live resource tree to [misc/unused_textures/lasers_old/](misc/unused_textures/lasers_old). They belonged to the old `EntityLaser` colored-beam renderer, superseded back in April 2016 by the BC8 textured-laser system ([BuildCraftLaserManager](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/client/BuildCraftLaserManager.java) / `LaserRenderer_BC8`) and `git mv`'d to `lasers_old/` at that time; nothing has referenced them since — no code, and [blocks.json](src/main/resources/assets/minecraft/atlases/blocks.json) stitches only the live `lasers/` directory into the atlas, never `lasers_old/`. They had simply been carried dead through every port (1.12.2 → 26.1). The in-use `textures/lasers/` set (marker, stripe, and power-laser sprites) is untouched and still fully referenced via [BCCoreSprites](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCoreSprites.java).
- Unfinished and experimental content is now gated behind dev mode instead of being shipped, deleted, or left lingering. The **Zone Planner** (GUI and inventory present but `serverTick()` a no-op — never finished in 1.12.2, and its port never completed) and the **Goggles** headpiece (likewise never finished) join the **Power Tester** in being registered only when the game is launched with `-Dbuildcraft.dev=true`: absent from public releases, but kept in code and obtainable in a dev workspace rather than being lost track of. All three now carry a red "Dev only" line appended to their tooltip — a new `markDevOnly` registry in [BCTooltips](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/BCTooltips.java) feeds the existing `ItemTooltipEvent` handler, populated from the client-setup hooks in [BCCoreClient](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCoreClient.java) and [BCRoboticsClient](src/main/java/buildcraft/robotics/client/BCRoboticsClient.java). The Zone Planner's block / item / block-entity / menu registrations and the Goggles item follow the Power Tester's `BCLib.DEV ? … : null` pattern, with null-guards at the startup use sites (creative-tab contents and the Zone Planner's menu-screen registration); all three dev-only items appear in the creative tab when in dev mode. The Zone Planner's `minecraft:mineable/pickaxe` tag entry became optional (`required: false`) so it no longer errors when the block is absent from a public build. New `tip.dev_only` lang key.
- Fixed a chunk **re-mesh storm** behind intermittent FPS stutters near working machines. Tanks, mining wells, quarries, flood gates, heat exchangers, and distillers synced their fluid/state to clients with `level.sendBlockUpdated()`, which rebuilds the entire chunk section — a filling tank did it every tick (20×/sec). Unnoticeable in a flat test world, a real stutter in terrain-dense generated chunks. They now push the block-entity packet straight to tracking players via [MessageUtil.sendUpdateToTrackingPlayers](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/MessageUtil.java) — no re-mesh.
- Filler texture cleanup: three unreferenced sets of filler textures moved out of the live resource tree into [misc/unused_textures/](misc/unused_textures). (1) `textures/filling/` — an 18-file partial redesign of the Filler's pattern/parameter selector icons (`axis/`/`facing/`/`pattern/`/`type/`) that was never wired into [BCBuildersSprites](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/BCBuildersSprites.java) and only covers 9 of the 22 patterns — moved wholesale to `misc/unused_textures/filling/`; it is stale leftover art erroneously kept in the live tree, not the basis for the eventual "Updated Filler mode icons" feature (which is a fresh start, not yet begun). (2) `textures/block/filler/patterns/` — 10 block-style pattern icons left over from the `blocks/`→`block/` port-era migration; the Filler block model ([block/filler/main.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/models/block/filler/main.json)) only samples its four face textures, never the patterns subfolder — moved to `misc/unused_textures/block_filler_patterns/`. (3) The four diagonal arrows `arrow_{dl,dr,ul,ur}.png` under `textures/filler/parameters/` — `BCBuildersSprites` maps only the four cardinal directions to `arrow_left/right/up/down` — moved to flat files. The live selector set (`textures/filler/patterns/` + `parameters/`) and the Filler block's four face textures are untouched and still fully referenced.
- Two port-era latent bugs fixed. **`MjBattery.addPower`** ([MjBattery](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/mj/MjBattery.java)) never capped at capacity and always returned `0`. A battery could therefore overfill past `capacity` (only bled back down above 2× capacity by the `tick` safety net), and — because that return value is the *unaccepted* power that `addPowerChecking` and [MjBatteryReceiver.receivePower](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/mj/MjBatteryReceiver.java) hand back as their `IMjReceiver` excess — a power sender was always told `0` was rejected even into a full battery, silently mis-accounting MJ at every full battery. `addPower` now caps positive additions at `capacity` and returns the genuine excess; negative amounts (used by network-sync delta paths such as [MjBatteryEnergyHandler](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/mj/MjBatteryEnergyHandler.java)) still pass straight through to remove power. **`BCDebugging`'s dev-environment detection** ([BCDebugging](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/core/BCDebugging.java)) probed reflectively for `Level.getTileEntity` — a method renamed to `getBlockEntity` in the 1.13 flattening — so the lookup always threw and `isDev` was permanently `false`, meaning BuildCraft's debug logging never auto-enabled in a dev workspace as intended. Replaced with the canonical `buildcraft.dev` system property, which every `build.gradle` run config sets and which `BCLib.DEV` already reads.
- Engine chaining is back, matching 1.12.2. A row of engines of the same type, all facing the same way, can once again all feed a single machine at the end of the line: [TileEngineBase_BC8.getReceiverToPower](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/engine/TileEngineBase_BC8.java) now walks through up to `getMaxChainLength()` same-type, same-facing engines to find the receiver, instead of giving up the instant it sees another engine. That stop-on-first-engine behaviour was also a regression in its own right — two adjacent same-type engines left the back one unable to deliver power at all; chaining restores it. Per-engine chain limits match 1.12.2: Stirling 2 (the base-class default, restored from the port's `0`), Combustion and FE engine 4, MJ Dynamo 3, and the Redstone Engine `0` — redstone engines stay deliberately non-chainable, which is 1.12.2's own fix for the 1.7-era exploit of stacking their free power trickle into one machine. `getMaxChainLength()` had been dead code (defined, never called); it drives the walk again. The MJ Dynamo's FE-side equivalent — [TileDynamoMJ.getFeReceiver](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/tile/TileDynamoMJ.java) — got the same chain-walk (limit 3). One porting nuance: 1.12.2's `TileDynamoMJ` was a standalone `TileBC_Neptune`, but the modern port makes it a `TileEngineBase_BC8` subclass, so the chain check keys on the exact engine class (chains never cross engine types) rather than 1.12.2's literal `instanceof TileEngineBase_BC8` test — same observable behaviour, and it still lets an engine power an adjacent Dynamo through the Dynamo's MJ receiver capability.
- The Debugger item's "advanced debugging" overlay is alive again. Right-clicking a Quarry or a Laser with the Debugger now draws an in-world overlay of that machine's internal state and shows an action-bar popup explaining it: the Quarry highlights every chunk it keeps force-loaded (a translucent green volume per `getChunksToLoad()` chunk, inset 0.5 from each chunk edge so neighbouring highlighted chunks show a clean border gap, spanning the frame box's Y range), and the Laser highlights its targeting cone (a solid cube at each cone position — green where reachable, red where line-of-sight is blocked). The 1.12.2 `IAdvDebugTarget`/`BCAdvDebugging` plumbing had been carried into the port but was dead (`ItemDebugger.useOn` bailed on the client and the server logic was never ticked); it was rewritten as a **client-authoritative, zero-networking** design — everything the overlay needs is already client-synced or client-computable, so [ItemDebugger.useOn](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/item/ItemDebugger.java) runs on both sides, recording the clicked `BlockPos` in [BCAdvDebugging](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/debug/BCAdvDebugging.java) on the client and sending the popup via `sendOverlayMessage` on the server, with no packets. A new client-side [AdvDebugRenderer](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/debug/AdvDebugRenderer.java) `RenderLevelStageEvent` handler reads that target and dispatches to [AdvDebuggerQuarry](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/client/render/AdvDebuggerQuarry.java) or [AdvDebuggerLaser](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/render/AdvDebuggerLaser.java). `IAdvDebugTarget` is now a one-method interface (`getAdvDebugMessage()`) implemented only by `TileQuarry` and `TileLaser` (not every tile). Boxes are drawn filled through `DebugRenderHelper.renderFilledBox`, which feeds a [RenderPartCube](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/render/tile/RenderPartCube.java) into vanilla's translucent debug filled-box render type (exposed as `BCLibRenderTypes.debugFilled()`) — a box's per-vertex alpha decides whether it reads as a see-through volume or a solid marker. Added `chat.debugger.quarry`/`chat.debugger.laser` lang keys.
- Audit follow-up: filled one pipe stub and excised dead code. **Redstone-Flux pipe extract** — [PipeFlowRedstoneFlux.tryExtractPower](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/flow/PipeFlowRedstoneFlux.java) was a `// TODO` stub that always returned 0; it now performs the real `Capabilities.Energy.BLOCK` extract through a transaction, mirroring the insert path already in the same file. The MJ-pipe twin `PipeFlowPower.tryExtractPower` is left stubbed — it needs `IMjPassiveProvider`, a separate port task — and neither method has a caller yet, so this is API-surface correctness rather than a behaviour change. **Dead code removed:** `getMaxTransferForRender` (both power flows — an uncalled method whose body was unreachable behind an `if (true) return`); `Section.clientDisplayAverage` (an `AverageInt` constructed per pipe-section but never ticked or read — dead since 1.12.2); `Section.debugPowerInput` (a debug field never assigned anywhere, so the F3 "power: IN" readout was permanently zero — dropped along with the "IN" segment of the debug string, leaving the live "OUT"/"OFFERED" figures); and [TileHeatExchange](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/tile/TileHeatExchange.java)'s `inputCoolantAmountCharge`/`inputHeatantAmountCharge` (loaded from NBT and written straight back every save but never read by the exchange logic — a no-op round-trip ported verbatim from 1.12.2; the `coolantCharge`/`heatantCharge` save keys are now ignored orphan tags, harmless to existing worlds). **`BCEnergyItems`** had a second `DeferredRegister.createItems` created solely for `glob_of_oil` under a comment claiming a separate `buildcraftenergy` asset namespace — there is none in this single-mod build, both registers used the identical `buildcraftunofficial` id, so it folded into the primary `ITEMS` register with no behaviour change. **`PluggableGate`** shed its dead expression-subsystem scaffolding — six commented-out `MODEL_*` field declarations, a ~40-line commented `static {}` block, a dead `BCSiliconGuis` import comment, and two empty `setClientModelVariables` methods with no callers (plus the three now-unused `EnumGate*`/`java.util` imports). The Zone Planner — GUI and inventory present, `serverTick()` a no-op, zero gameplay function — was deliberately left untouched; it should be dev-mode-gated before release.
- Gate Copier crouch-clear now confirms itself, the icon reflects its state again, and the "to clear" tooltip shows real keybinds. Crouch-using the Gate Copier wipes its stored settings — it now shows "Cleared copied settings" on the action bar (new `chat.gateCopier.dataCleared` key, sent via `sendOverlayMessage` from [ItemGateCopier.clearData](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/item/ItemGateCopier.java), matching the copier's other feedback) instead of clearing silently. The item icon switches between an "empty" and a "full" texture depending on whether the copier holds settings — 1.12.2 did this via `getMetadata()`, but the port shipped a static `items/gate_copier.json` pointing at one model, so the `full.png` texture was orphaned and the copier always rendered empty. Restored using the same mechanism the port already uses for the [List](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/item/ItemList_BC8.java) and [Map Location](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/item/ItemMapLocation.java) items: `ItemGateCopier` sets/clears the `minecraft:custom_model_data` component (new private `updateModelData`, called from `setCopiedGateData`/`clearData`), and `items/gate_copier.json` is now a `range_dispatch` selecting `item/gate_copier_full` (new model) at threshold 1 over the empty fallback. The shared `buildcraft.item.nonclean.usage` tooltip — used by both the Gate Copier and the Map Location — was the hard-coded string "Shift + right-click to clear"; it is now "%s + %s to clear" with the two slots filled by `Component.keybind("key.sneak")` and `Component.keybind("key.use")`, so it renders each player's *actual* bound controls (e.g. "Right Ctrl + Right Mouse Button" for a player who rebound sneak and/or use-item) rather than assuming default keybinds.
- Wrench and tool status messages restored to the action bar (the overlay above the hotbar). Cycling a Creative Engine's power output, shifting an iron/RF kinesis pipe's transfer limit, the Gate Copier's copy/paste/no-configuration feedback, and the three schematic-placement errors (not-enough-items, requires-fluids, invalid-schematic) had all regressed to printing in the chat log. **Root cause** — 1.12.2's `EntityPlayer.sendStatusMessage(component, actionBar)` and the 1.21.11-era `Player.displayClientMessage(component, boolean)` both carried an `actionBar` boolean; passing `true` routed the message to the overlay. MC 26.1 removed that overloaded method and split it into two dedicated, boolean-free methods — `sendSystemMessage(Component)` (chat) and `sendOverlayMessage(Component)` (action bar). The 26.1 "buildcraft-core compiles clean" migration pass hit the now-broken `displayClientMessage` calls and replaced them with `sendSystemMessage` — the chat half of the split — silently dropping the action-bar intent, as the `true` argument no longer had anywhere to go. **The fix** — the seven regressed call sites switch to `sendOverlayMessage`: [TileEngineCreative](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/tile/TileEngineCreative.java), [PipeBehaviourLimiter](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/behaviour/PipeBehaviourLimiter.java), [PluggableGate](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/plug/PluggableGate.java) (×3), and [ItemSchematicSingle](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/item/ItemSchematicSingle.java) (×3). `SoundTestCommand`'s `sendSystemMessage` calls are left as-is — command output belongs in chat. Not meaningfully unit/game-testable — `GameTestHelper.makeMockPlayer` returns a bare `Player` whose `sendOverlayMessage` and `sendSystemMessage` are both empty base-class methods, so no assertion can distinguish them; verified `./gradlew compileJava` clean with `sendOverlayMessage` confirmed present in the decompiled 26.1 `Player` source.
- Gate Copier works again. The item was registered with a recipe and tooltip, but its core copy/paste was commented-out scaffolding — [PluggableGate.interactWithCopier](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/plug/PluggableGate.java) just did the `instanceof` check and `return true`, so right-clicking a gate with the copier did nothing. Restored: an empty copier right-clicked on a configured gate stores the gate's NBT (connections + trigger/action statements, minus the runtime-only `wireBroadcasts`); a copier already holding data pastes that configuration onto the target gate via [GateLogic.readConfigData](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/gate/GateLogic.java) — `readConfigData` deliberately does not touch the gate's `variant`, so the copier transfers configuration but can never change a gate's type. The old 1.12.2 `stored.size() == 1` empty-gate guard no longer works (the port's `writeToNbt` always emits `connections`/`triggerOn`/`actionOn`, so the tag is never that small), so a new `GateLogic.hasConfiguration()` — true when any connection or trigger/action statement is set — drives the "no configuration to copy" message instead. Paste marks the holder tile changed, schedules a render update, and calls `sendResolveData()`, mirroring [ContainerGate](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/container/ContainerGate.java)'s statement-change path. Added the three `chat.gateCopier.*` lang keys (copied/pasted/noInformation); player feedback goes through `sendOverlayMessage` (the above-hotbar action bar), matching 1.12.2.
- Two config options that did nothing now do something. `miningMultiplier` ("Multiplier for the speed of mining machines") was registered but never read — [BlockUtil.miningMultiplier](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/BlockUtil.java), the field that scales every mining machine's MJ-per-block cost, stayed hardcoded at `1.0`. A new `ModConfigEvent` listener in [BCCore](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCore.java) now threads the config value into that field on config load *and* reload. `worldGen` ("Set true to allow world generation for BuildCraft") was likewise registered but unread; [BCEnergyWorldGen.init](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/BCEnergyWorldGen.java) now also gates oil generation on it, making it the global worldgen kill switch its TODO described — it sits above the existing per-subsystem `enableOilGeneration` toggle, so either being false disables oil gen.
- Dead code removed. Deleted eight unreferenced files left over from the 1.12.2 port: `api/BCBlocks` and `api/BCItems` (legacy `@ObjectHolder` stubs whose every field was `null` — the annotations were commented out, so nothing ever populated them); `api/enums/EnumRedstoneChipset` (its `getStack()` read the always-`null` `BCItems.Silicon.REDSTONE_CHIPSET`, so it always returned `ItemStack.EMPTY`, and `fromStack()` ignored its argument — the real chipsets are five separate items in `BCSiliconItems`); `lib/script/SimpleScriptFileLog` (an `IScriptFileLog` implementation that was never instantiated — `RecordingScriptFileLog` is the live one — with ten methods that just threw `AbstractMethodError`); `lib/migrate/LibraryMigration` (a single `return null` stub with no callers); `lib/BCLibEventDist` (an empty `class BCLibEventDist {}`); and the `lib/delta/` package (`DeltaInt`/`DeltaManager` — a mutually-referencing pair nothing outside the package touched, the 1.12.2 client-interpolated-animation system the port superseded with direct field sync). [FacadeAssemblyRecipes](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/recipe/FacadeAssemblyRecipes.java) had its now-unused `BCItems` import removed, and a stale `BCBlocks.Silicon` mention in a [GuideAssemblyRecipes](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/recipe/GuideAssemblyRecipes.java) comment was trimmed.
- Cleaned up the dead legacy `textures/items/` (plural) tree — a leftover flatten of the old 1.12.2 submod texture trees that nothing resolved against (modern models all use the singular `textures/item/`). 60 files byte-identical to live `textures/item/` assets were deleted; 47 unique unported 1.12.2 textures (board/, icons/, gates/, pipewire/, …) were moved to [misc/unused_textures/items/](misc/unused_textures/items); the now-empty `textures/items/` directory was removed. The three guide-book `<image>` tags that still pointed into the plural tree (`marker_path`, `guide_book`, `wrench`) were repointed to their live singular `item/` equivalents. Also relocated `textures/item/plug_pulsar.png` to [misc/unused_textures/item/](misc/unused_textures/item): it is a 32×384 frame strip that looked like an unanimated texture, but tracing the model showed nothing samples it — the pulsar plug item and its on-pipe render both use the 3D `models/item/plug_pulsar.json` box textured from `block/plugs/pulsar_static` + `pulsar_dynamic_off/on`. The strip is the old 1.12.2 gate-expansion-pulsar *chip* icon; gate expansions were a pre-1.13 feature absent from shipped 1.12.2's compiled code (the only reference lived in the build-excluded `src_old_license/` tree), so it has been dead art since before the 1.12.2 release.
- Replacer inventory now persists. [TileReplacer](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileReplacer.java)'s three slots (blueprint + from/to schematic) were standalone `ItemHandlerSimple` instances never registered with the tile's `ItemHandlerManager`, so they had no NBT save/load path — items placed in a Replacer evaporated on chunk unload (and weren't even dropped when the block was broken). Registered all three via `itemManager.addInvHandler(..., EnumAccess.NONE)` — `NONE` preserves the no-pipe-access behaviour they had as standalone handlers — and added `saveAdditional`/`loadAdditional` that round-trip `itemManager.serializeNBT()`, matching the canonical pattern in [TileElectronicLibrary](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileElectronicLibrary.java) and [TileFiller](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/tile/TileFiller.java). Slot filters/checkers unchanged.
- Blocks-atlas mip collapse, the sequel — the `minecraft:textures/atlas/blocks.png: dropping miplevel from 4 to 0` resource-load warning was back, and this time no BuildCraft texture was at fault. **What was wrong** — [atlases/blocks.json](src/main/resources/assets/minecraft/atlases/blocks.json) stitched BuildCraft's GUI textures onto the vanilla blocks atlas with a `minecraft:directory` source (`"source": "gui"`), but vanilla's `DirectoryLister` lists `textures/<source>/` across *every loaded namespace* — so the `gui` entry also dragged all 523 vanilla `minecraft:textures/gui/**` sprites (the entire GUI sheet: boss bars, scrollers, advancement tabs, …) onto the blocks atlas. 155 of them are odd-sized, and `SpriteLoader.stitch` clamps the whole atlas's mip level to `log2` of the smallest `lowestOneBit` over all sprites — so a single odd sprite (e.g. `minecraft:gui/sprites/boss_bar/purple_progress` at 182×5) takes every BuildCraft *and* vanilla block down to mip 0, defeating distance mipmapping game-wide. (The earlier "Runtime log cleanup" fix — `block/invisible.png` 1×1 → 16×16 — was a real but separate offender.) **The fix** — the `gui` atlas source turned out to be unnecessary, and was deleted outright. BuildCraft's GUI screens load their backgrounds as plain standalone textures (`Identifier.parse("buildcraftunofficial:textures/gui/<x>.png")`, drawn through [GuiIcon](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/GuiIcon.java)'s `SpriteRaw` path — a direct `blit`, never an atlas). Of BuildCraft's 54 `textures/gui/` PNGs, exactly two were ever read back from an atlas: `empty_filtered_buffer_slot` / `nothing_filtered_buffer_slot`, the Filtered Buffer's empty-slot icons, which [BCTransportSprites](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/BCTransportSprites.java) wrapped in `SpriteHolder`s for [GuiFilteredBuffer](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/gui/GuiFilteredBuffer.java) to draw. Those two are now plain 16×16 direct-texture `GuiIcon`s like every other BuildCraft GUI sprite — `GuiIcon` already supports that, it's the same `SpriteRaw` path the backgrounds use — so the two `SpriteHolder`s are gone from `BCTransportSprites` and nothing references the `gui` atlas source any more. With it deleted, no BuildCraft texture lands on the blocks atlas via `textures/gui/` at all. **Result** — verified before/after with `runClient`: blocks atlas `Created: 8192×4096×0` → `Created: 4096×2048×4` — full mip level 4 restored, and the atlas area drops to a quarter of the broken size now that neither the 523 vanilla GUI strays nor BuildCraft's own 54 GUI sheets (mostly 256×256) are stitched onto it. `./gradlew compileJava` clean.
- Energy-fluid textures de-duplicated and derived at runtime. **What they were** — `assets/buildcraftunofficial/textures/block/fluids/` shipped 136 files: every BC energy fluid (oil, fuel, and their dense/heavy/residue/distilled/mixed/gaseous variants) had three heat tiers × two frames of pre-recolored PNG. But the three heat tiers of any fluid were byte-identical — heat only changes the animation `frametime` (3/2/1) — and each fluid PNG was an exact per-pixel recolor of one shared grayscale base: the `heat_<n>_<frame>` texture, itself the historical 1.12.2 `buildcraftenergy:blocks/fluids/heat_*` base that 1.12.2's `AtlasSpriteFluid` recolored per-fluid at texture-stitch time. So 60 of the 68 PNGs were pure duplication, losslessly reconstructible from 2 base textures plus the per-fluid colour table already in code. **The change** — new [FluidLerpSpriteSource](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/sprite/FluidLerpSpriteSource.java) (a NeoForge `SpriteSource`, the same atlas extension point as the existing `DyeReplaceSpriteSource`) recolors the single heat base into all 60 fluid sprites at stitch time, applying the 1.12.2 per-channel intensity lerp `out = (dark·(256−W) + light·W) / 256` with the light/dark endpoints from [BCEnergyFluids.FLUID_DATA](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/BCEnergyFluids.java). Output is bit-identical to the deleted PNGs — verified pixel-exact across all 10 fluids × {still, flow}. Each fluid×frame emits its three heat tiers as separate sprites carrying `frametime` 3/2/1 via `AnimationMetadataSection`, so the per-heat animation-speed cue is unchanged. Registered in [BCLibClient](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/BCLibClient.java); driven by 20 `fluid_lerp` entries appended to [atlases/blocks.json](src/main/resources/assets/minecraft/atlases/blocks.json). Sprite IDs are unchanged, so [BCEnergyFluidsClient](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/client/BCEnergyFluidsClient.java) and [FluidUtilBC](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/FluidUtilBC.java) resolve them exactly as before. **Result** — the `fluids/` directory drops from 136 files to 2 (`heat_still.png` + `heat_flow.png`, collapsed from the byte-identical `heat_0/1/2` trio; animation metadata now lives in code). A resource pack can restyle every BC fluid at once by overriding that single base texture. Also deleted `fuel_still.png` / `fuel_flow.png` — orphan un-tiered fuel sprites with no remaining model, Java, or datapack reference.
- Pipe flow-rate tooltips clarified. Kinesis (MJ) and FE pipe tooltips now end in "per face" to reflect that the listed number is the per-face pull-side cap, not total segment throughput — multi-face convergence in [PipeFlowPower](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/flow/PipeFlowPower.java) (push side: `internalNextPower += sent`, no cap) and [PipeFlowRedstoneFlux](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/flow/PipeFlowRedstoneFlux.java) (push side: hard-capped per face but still 6× per-segment when multi-fed) means a single pipe segment can carry up to 6× the listed rate when fed by sources on multiple faces. Fluid pipes are unaffected (true per-segment cap via the center-section bottleneck in [PipeFlowFluids](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/flow/PipeFlowFluids.java)). Edit lives in [ItemPipeHolder.appendHoverText](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/item/ItemPipeHolder.java); same change also adds a flow-rate tooltip line to FE pipes (which previously had none).
- Power-pipe flow renderer no longer leaves visible gaps between adjacent overloaded pipes. When more power flowed than the pipe's `maxPower` per tick (e.g. five creative engines at 256 MJ each pushing through a 256 MJ/t diamond kinesis pipe), `displayPower / MJ` could exceed 1.0, which made `centreRadius = 0.252 - 0.248 * centrePower` go negative in [PipeFlowRendererPower](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/render/PipeFlowRendererPower.java). The negative term inverted the side-stem AABB along the connection axis (`min > max`); the cell-clipped scroll renderer's `if (pMinX >= pMaxX) continue;` guard then skipped every cell, so the stems vanished while the centre cube kept rendering — producing the visible gaps. Fix clamps `power` and `centrePower` to `[0, 1]` in the extracted `sideFlowBox` helper. Coverage: unit-test [PipeFlowRendererPowerGeometryTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/transport/client/render/PipeFlowRendererPowerGeometryTester.java) pins the geometry math across the full input range (saturation, overload, negative-input defence) — this is the actual regression catcher, since it tests the exact mathematical input domain of the bug. Game-test [PipeFlowPowerTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/flow/PipeFlowPowerTester.java) is the server-side bookend: a creative engine → wood-diamond → diamond → tester end-to-end transfer chain, polled tick-by-tick via `succeedWhen` to absorb game-test arena startup jitter. The `gameTestServer` run config now sets `-Dbuildcraft.dev=true` so the Power Tester block is registered as the sink (its unlimited capacity beats a Dynamo MJ, whose 1000-MJ battery fills in ~4 ticks at 256 MJ/t and tips the assertion into a tick-ordering race). Game test count 139 → 140.
- Power Tester ported. Dev-only debug block from 1.12.2 — sinks up to 100,000 MJ/t on any side and reports last/tick/total received via [IDebuggable](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/tiles/IDebuggable.java) on the F3 overlay (rendered by [BCDebugOverlay](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/BCDebugOverlay.java)). Gated on `BCLib.DEV` (set `-Dbuildcraft.dev=true`) in [BCCoreBlocks](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCoreBlocks.java), [BCCoreBlockEntities](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCoreBlockEntities.java), [BCCoreItems](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCoreItems.java), the [creative tab](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCoreCreativeTabs.java), and the `RegisterCapabilitiesEvent` hook in [BCCore](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCore.java) that exposes the tile as an `IMjReceiver`; ternary against `BCLib.DEV` keeps the registry entry absent in shipping builds, matching 1.12.2 behaviour. The orphan `power_tester.png` texture left over from the original port is now load-bearing again — blockstate/block/item JSON added under `assets/buildcraftunofficial/`, plus lang entry "Power Tester".
- Submod-era leftovers excised. Pre-1.13 BuildCraft shipped as 8 mods fatjarred together (`buildcraftcore`, `buildcrafttransport`, `buildcraftenergy`, `buildcraftbuilders`, `buildcraftsilicon`, `buildcraftfactory`, `buildcraftrobotics`, `buildcraftlib`); the modern port has been a single mod (`buildcraftunofficial`) since the 1.21.11 jump, but a [BCModules](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/BCModules.java) enum that pretended each one was still separately loadable lingered in the API. It computed mod IDs like `buildcrafttransport` and asked `ModList.get().isLoaded(...)` for them — those mod IDs no longer exist, so every `BCModules.X.isLoaded()` call silently returned `false`, leaving four downstream code paths dead. **Bug #1 — MJ↔RF auto-conversion silently disabled.** [IMjToRfStatus.MjToRfStatusHolder.get0](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/mj/IMjToRfStatus.java) gated its reflective load of `BCLibConfig$MjToRfStatus` on `BCModules.LIB.isLoaded()` → always false → always fell back to the no-op holder whose `isAutoconvertEnabled()` was hardcoded `false`. So `MjAPI.isRfAutoConversionEnabled()` returned `false` regardless of the `powerMode` config; `MjToRfAutoConvertor.create(...)` always returned `null`; BC engines refused to power FE/RF consumers via auto-convert even when the player set `MJ_AUTOCONVERT_RF` or `DISPLAY_RF`. Masked in the default `MJ_ONLY` mode (autoconvert is meant to be off in that mode) and by the engine MJ↔RF math going through `MjRfConversion.createParsed(...)` directly in [TileEngineFE](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/tile/TileEngineFE.java), [TileDynamoMJ](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/tile/TileDynamoMJ.java), and [MjBatteryEnergyHandler](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/mj/MjBatteryEnergyHandler.java). Fixed by inlining `IMjToRfStatus` into [MjAPI](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/mj/MjAPI.java) — `getRfConversion()` now reads `BCLibConfig.mjRfConversionAmount` directly, `isRfAutoConversionEnabled()` reads `BCLibConfig.powerMode.get().autoconvert` directly. `IMjToRfStatus.java` and `BCLibConfig.MjToRfStatus` inner class deleted. The api → lib import this introduces is fine for a monolith — the historical "api can't see lib" boundary was a submod-era constraint that no longer applies. **Bug #2 — gate→wire-system signaling dead, masked by an every-tick recompute bodge.** [GateLogic:527](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/gate/GateLogic.java) called into transport's `SavedDataWireSystems.gatesChanged` via reflection, guarded on `BCModules.TRANSPORT.isLoaded() && ...` → always false → the wire system was never notified when a gate's output changed. Someone hit the symptom (wires never glowing, receive-gates never firing until the world reloaded) and worked around it by removing the `gatesChanged = false` reset from [SavedDataWireSystems.tick()](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/wire/SavedDataWireSystems.java) — that comment ("intentionally NOT reset here") was the workaround, not the design. Replaced the reflective branch with a direct package import + `.gatesChanged = true` assignment. **Follow-up audit (2026-05-19) confirmed every wire-system wakeup point fires correctly,** so the every-tick recompute bodge has been removed. Wakeup matrix as audited: wire placed/removed → [WireManager.addPart](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/wire/WireManager.java)/`removePart`/`removeParts` → `buildAndAddWireSystem` / `removeWireSystem` → `markStructureChanged`; pipe BE loads → `WireManager.tick()` first call (`!initialised`) → `buildAndAddWireSystem` → `markStructureChanged`; pipe BE invalidates → `BlockPipeHolder` → `WireManager.invalidate` → `removePartsFromSystem` → `markStructureChanged`; pluggable add/remove gated on `IWireEmitter` → [TilePipeHolder.replacePluggable](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/tile/TilePipeHolder.java) → `rebuildWireSystemsAround` → `buildAndAddWireSystem` → `markStructureChanged`; gate emit-state change → `GateLogic.resolveActions` → direct `SavedDataWireSystems.gatesChanged = true`. `GateLogic` is the only `IWireEmitter` implementation (`PluggableGate.isEmitting`/`emitWire` just delegate to its `GateLogic` instance), and `resolveActions` is the only path that mutates `wireBroadcasts` outside of construction + NBT load — and NBT load happens during chunk load, which triggers `WireManager.tick()` → `markStructureChanged` independently. Tick ordering: pluggable `onTick` runs during `LevelTickEvent` (sets `gatesChanged = true`); `SavedDataWireSystems.tick()` runs on `LevelTickEvent.Post` (sees the freshly-set flag), so a gate state change propagates on the same Minecraft tick. Restored the `gatesChanged = false` reset at the end of `tick()`; the every-tick recompute is gone. The bodge comment that called out the old failure mode ("wires never glowing and receive-gates never firing until the world was closed and reopened") was replaced with the wakeup matrix above so future readers can verify rather than guess. Three new game tests in [WireSystemTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/transport/WireSystemTester.java) pin the new behavior: `testSteadyStateLeavesGatesChangedFalse` runs three no-op ticks after a structure change and asserts `gatesChanged` stays false on every one of them (this is the test that fails immediately if the recompute-every-tick bodge ever returns), `testGateEmitPropagatesAndFlagResets` proves a gate emit + `gatesChanged = true` sequence powers the wire on the next tick AND clears the flag after the recompute, and `testGateResolveActionsClearingMarksGatesChanged` exercises the direct call that replaced the dead reflective branch — seeds the gate with `[RED]`, ticks (wire on), calls `resolveActions()` on an unconfigured gate (clears `wireBroadcasts` to `[]`, differs from previous `[RED]`, fix path fires), asserts `gatesChanged == true` (proves the signal works), ticks again, asserts the wire de-powers AND the flag is reset. Game test count 131 → 134. **Bug #3 — guide UI showing raw `buildcraftunofficial`.** [GuideContentsData.generate](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/guide/GuideContentsData.java) called `BCModules.getBcMod(domain)` expecting resource namespaces like `buildcrafttransport`; with everything under `buildcraftunofficial` the `bcmods` set was always empty and the per-submod display-name logic ("BuildCraft (all)", "BuildCraft Lib", "BuildCraft Core", …) was unreachable, leaving the guide's loaded-mods section showing the raw mod ID. Stripped the BCModules logic; single-line special-case maps `buildcraftunofficial` → `"BuildCraft"` for the display. **Cleanup — dead import.** [BCDebugging](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/core/BCDebugging.java) imported `BCModules` without referencing it anywhere in its body; while we were in there, also removed the dead `ModList` and `ModContainer` imports next to it. **Then the dead code itself.** [BCModules.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/BCModules.java) and its supporting [IBuildCraftMod](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/IBuildCraftMod.java) interface deleted entirely — nothing else referenced them. **Repo cleanup.** Nine top-level `buildcraft-*/` directories (`buildcraft-all`, `buildcraft-builders`, `buildcraft-core`, `buildcraft-energy`, `buildcraft-factory`, `buildcraft-lib`, `buildcraft-robotics`, `buildcraft-silicon`, `buildcraft-transport`) and the empty `sub_projects/` were leftover Gradle build-artifact and submodule-stub directories — none contained any git-tracked content, [settings.gradle](settings.gradle) hadn't referenced them since the 1.21.11 monolithic refactor, and they were the first thing a new contributor saw doing `ls` at the repo root. Deleted. The `.gitignore` already excludes `build` / `run` patterns so they won't grow back as tracked dirs even if Gradle reconstructs them. **Documentation.** [CLAUDE.md](CLAUDE.md) gained a "History — this is one mod, not eight" section explaining the transition, and the old "Module Layout" + "Initialization Pattern" wording was updated to talk about packages and per-subsystem registration helpers instead of "module class" construction. [todos.md](todos.md)'s "Module Status Overview" table is now "Subsystem Status Overview" with a one-line preamble. The "Initialize all modules" / "Module initializers" comment block in [BCCore.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCore.java) is now "Initialize each subsystem" / "Per-subsystem registration helpers". Verification: `./gradlew compileJava` clean, `./gradlew test` all unit tests pass, `./gradlew runGameTestServer` reports `131 GAME TESTS COMPLETE` / `All 131 required tests passed`.
- Asset cleanup: deleted orphaned `redplasma_still`/`redplasma_flow` fluid textures (+ mcmetas), the entire `block/plain_pipe/` directory (`default`/`side`/`end`), and the entire `block/tube/` directory (`default`/`side`/`end`) — none had any remaining model, blockstate, Java, or datapack reference. The tube block is `RenderShape.INVISIBLE` (visuals come from [TubeRenderer](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/render/TubeRenderer.java)'s laser system), so its old `cube_all` texture only ever showed as fallback break/hit particles. Replaced that fallback with a reusable [NoParticleClientExtensions](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/NoParticleClientExtensions.java) — an `IClientBlockExtensions` whose `addHitEffects` and `addDestroyEffects` both `return true` (NeoForge contract: "I handled it" → no vanilla particles spawned). Running/landing particles live on `Block` itself rather than the client-extensions interface and weren't needed here — the tube is `destroyTime(-1.0f)` unbreakable in survival, 8/16 wide, and capped by the miner block, so an entity can't realistically stand or land on one. Registered on `BlockTube` in [BCFactoryClient](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/BCFactoryClient.java); the tube model collapsed to a `particle: block/invisible` stub matching `pipe_holder.json`. Picked suppression over pointing the model at one of TubeRenderer's two laser sprites (`block/pump/tube`, `block/mining_well/tube`) because there isn't a single canonical "tube" sprite and over leaving the model to resolve to MC's missing-texture sentinel because that would spam a resource-reload warning on every pack load. The pipe path was left alone — `PipeHolderClientExtensions` already spawns pipe-specific particles when the BE is available and only falls through to `block/invisible` for non-BE contexts like JEI, which is intentional. Side note on the preceding "Runtime log cleanup" entry's point (3): the `tube/end.png` and `plain_pipe/end.png` 8×8 → 16×16 upscales it added were preventive against a future atlas-mip regression, but those two PNGs were never stitched onto the blocks atlas (no model reference, no directory source in [atlases/blocks.json](src/main/resources/assets/minecraft/atlases/blocks.json)) — so the upscales were unnecessary and the deletions in this entry don't risk re-triggering the mip collapse. The `invisible.png` 1×1 → 16×16 fix in that entry was the real one and stays in place.
- Wrench now rotates vanilla blocks again, matching the 1.12.2 behaviour that had been silently lost in the port. **What was broken** — [CustomRotationHelper.registerHandlerForAll](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/blocks/CustomRotationHelper.java) iterated `new Block[0]` (an empty array — the modern-port equivalent of the 1.12.2 `Block.REGISTRY` walk), so any class-based handler registration was a silent no-op. There was also no `VanillaRotationHandlers` class in the modern port at all — the 1.12.2 file under `common/buildcraft/lib/block/` never got carried over. Result: right-clicking a furnace, dispenser, lever, etc. with a wrench did nothing. **The interception problem (caught after first ship)** — even with rotation handlers registered, vanilla blocks that have a `useWithoutItem` interaction (trapdoor + door toggle, furnace/dispenser/chest menu, lever toggle, button press, …) still intercepted the wrench in their own block-interaction chain before `wrench.useOn` could ever fire. The chain in [ServerPlayerGameMode.useItemOn](https://github.com/neoforged/NeoForge): block-side `useItemOn`/`useWithoutItem` runs first, and is only suppressed when `suppressUsingBlock` is true — which requires `(sneaking && hasItem) && !(both hands' doesSneakBypassUse return true)`. The wrench already returns `true` from `doesSneakBypassUse` (intentional, so engine/dynamo blocks can intercept crouch+wrench to open their GUI instead of being short-circuited to rotation); the gotcha is that [ItemStack.doesSneakBypassUse](https://github.com/neoforged/NeoForge/blob/main/src/main/java/net/neoforged/neoforge/common/extensions/IItemStackExtension.java) short-circuits to `true` for an empty stack via `self().isEmpty() || ...`, so a player crouching with the wrench in main + nothing in offhand has both hands "bypassing" and the block wins every time. Reported in-game by clicking a copper trapdoor with a wrench while crouched: trapdoor toggled open instead of rotating. **The fix** — added an [onItemUseFirst](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/item/ItemWrench_Neptune.java) override that fires before `block.useItemOn` in both `ServerPlayerGameMode.useItemOn` and `MultiPlayerGameMode.useItemOn`, gated on **both** `player.isShiftKeyDown()` AND `!(block instanceof ICustomRotationHandler)`. The crouch gate matches 1.12.2's UX where the wrench was an explicit "switched-on" tool: non-crouch wrench on a vanilla block falls through to the block's normal interaction (trapdoor toggles, lever flips, furnace opens its menu), crouch wrench claims the interaction and rotates instead. The `ICustomRotationHandler` exclusion preserves BC machines' two-path behaviour unchanged — engine/dynamo non-crouch=rotate via `wrench.useOn`, crouch=GUI via the block's own `useItemOn`. Regression test [testWrenchOnItemUseFirstCrouchGate](src/test/java/buildcraft/lib/block/VanillaRotationTester.java) covers both branches: non-crouch wrench on a copper trapdoor returns PASS and leaves FACING untouched (the trapdoor's own `useWithoutItem` is what then toggles OPEN), crouch wrench returns SUCCESS, rotates FACING NORTH→EAST, and explicitly asserts OPEN is still `false`. **The fix** — [CustomRotationHelper.registerHandlerForAll](src/main/java/buildcraft/api/blocks/CustomRotationHelper.java) now walks `BuiltInRegistries.BLOCK` (must be called after registry population, i.e. from `FMLCommonSetupEvent`). New [VanillaRotationHandlers](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/block/VanillaRotationHandlers.java) wires up the same coverage matrix as 1.12.2, adapted for modern block-class restructuring: **6-face free rotation** for dispenser/dropper, observer, end rod, shulker box, piston (piston refuses with FAIL when `EXTENDED=true`); **4-face horizontal rotation** for tripwire hook, fence gate, repeaters/comparators, carved pumpkin & jack-o'-lantern (vanilla pumpkin has no facing so it's a no-op), glazed terracotta, anvil, ender chest, every furnace variant (registered against `AbstractFurnaceBlock` so blast furnaces and smokers are also covered); **horizontal with attach-validation** (skips orientations where `canSurvive` fails, returns FAIL if none work) for cocoa, ladder, wall torch, wall banner, wall sign, wall hanging sign, wall skull; **specials** preserving the 1.12.2 quirks — doors propagate FACING to both halves and flip HINGE whenever current FACING is the first in cycle (8-position cycle through 4 facings × 2 hinges; uses `setBlock(..., UPDATE_CLIENTS)` for both halves to suppress vanilla's `DoorBlock.updateShape` resync which would otherwise revert the hinge mid-update), trapdoor and stairs flip top/bottom HALF on the same wrap condition, double-chest detection flips both halves 180° in unison with the LEFT/RIGHT TYPE designations swapping, hopper rotates through E→S→W→N→D (vanilla's `FACING_HOPPER` excludes UP), lever and button rotate horizontal FACING within the current FACE (FLOOR/WALL/CEILING); **16-step in-place spin** via `ROTATION_16` for standing banners, standing signs, ceiling hanging signs, and floor skulls (modern MC promoted skull rotation from a TE field reached via reflection to a regular BlockState property). Notable adaptations from 1.12.2: floor torch ↔ wall torch conversion isn't ported (modern MC stores these as separate block classes — `TorchBlock` for floor, `WallTorchBlock` for wall — and the cross-class conversion would need per-variant hard-coding for regular/soul/redstone, so wrenching a floor torch is a no-op while wall torches rotate among the 4 horizontals); levers no longer cycle FLOOR/WALL/CEILING positions (modern MC's FACE+FACING split would need a 12-position cycle that overshoots the "player-friendly" feel — sticking to the 4-horizontal rotation within the current FACE matches the spirit). Wired up from [BCCore.init(FMLCommonSetupEvent)](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/BCCore.java) alongside the existing `VanillaPaintHandlers.fmlInit()` call. **The "illegal-orientation" problem (caught after the crouch-gate fix)** — buttons and levers could be rotated into nonsensical states because the modern (FACE + FACING) split changed the shape of their state space relative to 1.12.2: (a) the handler only cycled the 4 horizontal FACING values, never visiting the FLOOR/CEILING positions that the FACE property makes available (in 1.12.2 buttons had a single 6-position FACING enum that the wrench cycled through naturally, including up/down — modern MC moved the floor/ceiling cases into AttachFace, which the first handler ignored), and (b) the handler had no `canSurvive` validation, so a button or lever could be rotated to face air. **The fix** — [rotateFaceAttached](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/block/VanillaRotationHandlers.java) was rewritten to cycle through all 12 (FACE × FACING) combinations — 4 WALL facings, then 4 FLOOR, then 4 CEILING, then back — using `candidate.canSurvive(world, pos)` to skip orientations whose attach face has no sturdy mount, FAILing if none in the cycle survive. So a button on a freestanding pillar wraps cleanly between its 4 valid orientations (whichever face has the pillar), a button between two blocks alternates between the two supported faces, and a button with one supporting block stays put while still cycling FACING. **Trapdoors were intentionally NOT validated** — verified in 1.12.2 by direct testing that trapdoors rotated freely with no attach-side restriction; a freestanding trapdoor cycled through all 8 (FACING × HALF) positions exactly the same as a supported one. An earlier draft of this fix added hinge-side `isFaceSturdy` validation to trapdoors and broke them entirely for the freestanding case (the wrench would FAIL and play only the failure-pitched slide sound). Reverted; the rotateTrapDoor handler is back to the pure 8-cycle with no attach check. **Tests** — [VanillaRotationTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/lib/block/VanillaRotationTester.java) gained three new game tests: `testTrapDoorRotatesFreestanding` places a trapdoor with no neighbours, asserts 8 consecutive clicks complete the full 1.12.2-parity cycle (E,BOT) → (S,TOP) → (W,TOP) → (N,TOP) → (E,TOP) → (S,BOT) → (W,BOT) → (N,BOT) → (E,BOT) — this is the regression check that catches "validation snuck back in"; `testButtonCyclesThroughAllTwelveOrientations` builds a 6-direction stone cocoon around a stone button and walks the full 12-step cycle, asserting both FACE and FACING at each step; `testButtonSkipsAttachToAir` places a button on a single floor block and asserts four consecutive clicks all stay on FACE=FLOOR while advancing FACING E→S→W→N→E. **Tests** — new [VanillaRotationTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/lib/block/VanillaRotationTester.java) with 15 game tests: furnace 4-face cycle, dispenser 6-face cycle, hopper 5-face cycle, extended-piston FAIL, banner ROTATION_16 wrap, skull ROTATION_16 step, trapdoor half-flip-on-wrap (with negative assertion that subsequent steps don't flip), door both-halves-and-hinge-on-wrap (same negative assertion), wall-torch attach-skip (only one supported orientation → FAIL), double-chest paired 180° flip, end-to-end integration through `ItemWrench_Neptune.useOn`, the trapdoor `onItemUseFirst` regression, and the three new validation tests above. Game test count 116 → 131, all green.
- Flood gate: wrenching a side to toggle it now grants the `wrenched` advancement (was silently skipping it because the toggle lived in `useWithoutItem`, which bypasses `ItemWrench_Neptune.useOn` entirely). Moved the toggle to `useItemOn` and manually call `wrench.wrenchUsed(...)` — same pattern as `BlockEngineCreative` for actions that can't go through `ICustomRotationHandler`. The floodgate's toggle still uses `UPDATE_CLIENTS` rather than `UPDATE_ALL` (preserving the existing fix that prevents pipes from rebaking their model on every side flip). Also added a vanilla iron-trapdoor audio cue on the toggle — `SoundEvents.IRON_TRAPDOOR_OPEN` when opening, `IRON_TRAPDOOR_CLOSE` when closing, with the same volume 1.0 + pitch random[0.9, 1.0] that `TrapDoorBlock.playSound` uses (vanilla's variant pool keeps the per-click sound distinct without us hand-rolling pitches). Metallic clunk matches the block's iron-tinted look. Three new game tests in [FloodGateTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/factory/FloodGateTester.java): wrench toggles a non-UP side both directions, UP-face click falls through with `TRY_WITH_EMPTY_HAND`, non-wrench item falls through too. Game test count 113 → 116.
- Runtime log cleanup: a 2-minute runClient session surfaced one ERROR and a stack of WARNs that all needed BuildCraft-side fixes. **(1) `pipe_obsidian_fluid` data ERROR** — the orphaned recipe at `data&buildcraftunofficial&recipe&pipe_obsidian_fluid.json` produced an item that doesn't exist (and never did; 1.12.2's obsidian pipe was item-only too — `PipeItemsObsidian` only, no `PipeFluidsObsidian` to port). Deleted the recipe; removed the line from `has_glass.json`'s recipe-unlock list. **(2) 22 camelCase texture paths rejected as datapack-invalid** — `textures&block&advancedCraftingTable&`, `textures&block&chargingTable&`, `textures&block&fillerBlock&`, `textures&block&hopperBlock&`, `textures&block&laserBox&`, `textures&block&pipes&pipeLensClearOverlay.png`, `textures&block&pipes&pipeRobotStation*_cb.png`, `textures&pipes&pipePowerAdapter{Bottom,Side,Top}.png` and their `mask_*` siblings. None were referenced by any blockstate&model&Java code (the three `pipePowerAdapter*` MASK_MAP entries in [PipeBaseModelGenStandard](src&main&java&buildcraft&transport&client&model&PipeBaseModelGenStandard.java:179) were stale leftovers — the actual plug uses `power_adapter` snake_case, registered immediately below). All 22 moved to `misc&unused_textures&` with disambiguating prefixes (`advancedCraftingTable_default.png` etc.); five now-empty texture subdirs removed; the three MASK_MAP lines deleted. **(3) Blocks-atlas mip collapse from level 4 to 0** — caused by `block&invisible.png` being **1×1**, used as the `particle` slot of `pipe_holder.json`. A 1px sprite forces every mip level on the entire blocks atlas to 0, defeating mipmaps for every BC block at distance. Replaced with a 16×16 fully transparent PNG (same visual, just doesn't poison the atlas). Also caught two secondary offenders that would have re-emerged as "drop mip from 4 to 3" after the 1px fix — `block&plain_pipe&end.png` and `block&tube&end.png`, both 8×8 — upscaled to 16×16 nearest-neighbour so the atlas keeps full mip-4 quality. **(4) 12 models missing `particle` texture slot** — `block&builder&slot_{template,blueprint}`, `block&flood_gate&face_{n,s,e,w,d}_{open,closed}` (10 files), `item&distiller`. The builder slots and flood_gate faces are sub-mesh geometry for the parent BE render and never appear as standalone blocks, so they got a no-op `particle` pointing at their existing texture (silences the warning, no atlas impact). Distiller is a real placed block — added a real particle pointing at `block&distiller&tank_sprite_a` so break particles get a sensible texture. **(5) Animated fluid sprites with unused frames** — `redplasma_still.png` and `fuel_still.png` were both 16×512 (32 frames) but their mcmetas only referenced frames 0..19, leaving 20..31 as dead animation data. Frame hashes confirm all 12 "unused" frames are distinct artwork (not padding); the flow versions already cycle through all 32 frames via implicit auto-detection. Extended both still mcmetas to use all 32 frames: fuel_still simplified by removing the explicit `frames` list (lets MC auto-detect), redplasma_still extended its 38-entry ping-pong sequence to a 62-entry ping-pong 0..31..1 (preserving the deliberate palindrome animation pattern). **(6) Oil spring tile entity never attached + cascade of "Unprimed heightmap OCEAN_FLOOR_WG" errors** — [BlockSpring](src&main&java&buildcraft&core&block&BlockSpring.java) didn't implement `EntityBlock`, so MC had no way to create the BE when the spring block was placed by [OilGenStructure.Spring.generate](src&main&java&buildcraft&energy&generation&OilGenStructure.java:472) — every oil deposit logged "Setting the blockstate didn't also set the tile" and the `totalSources` counter (which gates the `black_gold` advancement at 87.5%) was silently lost. Fixed by adding `implements EntityBlock` to BlockSpring with a late-bound `oilTileFactory` static supplier; the energy module wires `BlockSpring.oilTileFactory = TileSpringOil::new` from `BCEnergyBlockEntities.init()`, preserving the existing core→energy layering (core defines the block, energy defines the BE, neither imports the other directly). Same change moved the spring from y=`minY+1` (-63) to y=`minY` (-64) per the design intent of "spring at the floor of the world, acts and looks like bedrock", with the tube start shifted from `minY+3` to `minY+2` to stay connected through the bedrock gradient and force-placed oil at `pos.above()` covering the spring. The "Unprimed heightmap" errors were a separate cause: [PatternTerrainHeight.generateWithin](src&main&java&buildcraft&energy&generation&OilGenStructure.java:293) and [SurfacePool.generateWithin](src&main&java&buildcraft&energy&generation&OilGenStructure.java:357) called `level.getHeightmapPos()` on neighbour chunks during ChunkEvent.Load before their heightmaps were primed; replaced both heightmap calls with two new downward-scan helpers `findWorldSurfaceTop` (mirrors WORLD_SURFACE: first non-air) and `findSolidSurfaceTop` (mirrors OCEAN_FLOOR_WG: first non-air non-replaceable) that scan from `level.getMaxY()` down using `getBlockState()`, which works regardless of heightmap state. **(7) Untranslated `c:gears&*` item tags** — added `tag.item.c.gears.{wooden,stone,iron,gold,diamond}` keys to `en_us.json` so JEI&EMI display readable names for tag-ingredient recipes.
- Pipe drops: pipe + cargo + pluggables + wires now drop correctly across all four survival break paths (click a plug / click a wire / pickaxe-break the whole pipe / hand-break the whole pipe). **Pipes are intentionally hand-breakable** — that's a 1.12.2 design feature, not a bug to fix. A bare-hand break returns the pipe item + every pluggable + every wire + every traversing item (via `PipeFlowItems.addDrops`) + traversing fluid contents as fragile fluid-shard items (via `PipeFlowFluids.addDrops`) + per-behaviour drops like the Emzuli filter slots — same set as a pickaxe break, the pickaxe just speeds up the break action via the `#minecraft:mineable/pickaxe` tag. `pipe_holder` deliberately does NOT set `requiresCorrectToolForDrops` (an earlier draft of this work briefly did, mirroring the engine/machine pattern — that was wrong: pipes were always hand-breakable in 1.12.2, and forcing a pickaxe to recover a placed pipe would punish players for tearing down a network without first swapping tools). **What was already correct** — confirmed by reading the code: `dropPipeItems` (in [TilePipeHolder](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/tile/TilePipeHolder.java)) pops the pipe item with its paint colour preserved, calls `pipe.addDrops` (which delegates to flow + behaviour, covering cargo + filter slots), iterates all 6 sides for pluggables and pops each one's `getPickStack` plus calls `plug.onRemove()`, and pops wire items from `wireManager.parts.values()`.
