The flow `addDrops` returns every non-phantom `TravellingItem.stack`, and the fluid flow sums every section's amount and pops the total through `FluidItemDrops` as fragile fluid-shard items. Click-targeted partial breaks (player aiming at a single plug or wire) are handled by [BlockPipeHolder.onDestroyedByPlayer](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/block/BlockPipeHolder.java) returning `false` after popping just the targeted part — the pipe stays in place. **Tests** — new [PipeDropsTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/transport/PipeDropsTester.java) with 5 game tests: pluggable click-break (only `plug_blocker` drops + pipe stays + tile pluggable slot cleared), wire click-break (same for a red wire on the WEST_UP_NORTH corner), pickaxe full break (pipe + plug + wire + emerald cargo all drop), hand full break (same drop set as pickaxe — explicit assertion that pipes ARE hand-breakable), and fluid pipe pickaxe break (cobble fluid pipe carrying 1000mB water drops the pipe item + a `FRAGILE_FLUID_CONTAINER` shard). Click-break tests use a new `playerLookingDownAt(helper, absPos, localX, localZ, item)` helper that positions a mock player two blocks above the pipe at the chosen local x/z, with pitch 90° and `setOldPosAndRot()` so the partialTicks=0 interpolation vanilla's pick uses returns the just-set values; the wire variant aims at local (~0.219, ~0.219) because wire bboxes sit at the 8 corners of the inner cube rather than along the centre axis (the plug variant aims at (0.5, 0.5) because the UP plug AABB does include the centre). Full-break tests reuse the `breakAs` shape from `BlockDropsTester` — the mock player's pick returns no hit on the pipe so `playerWillDestroy`'s partial-break check short-circuits and the full `dropPipeItems` path runs. All five tests use radius 4.0 for the item-presence assertion: under MC gravity (~0.04 m/t² accelerating) a popResource'd item falls ~2 blocks in 10 ticks, putting it right at the boundary of a radius-2.0 search and flaking on ~40% of runs (caught by 10 back-to-back local runs after the first version of the tests landed with radius 2.0 — 3 wire failures, 1 plug failure across the 10 runs). Test instance manifests at `src/test/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/test_instance/pipe_*.json`. Game test count 107 → 112, 10/10 consecutive runs green after the radius fix.
- Block drops: every BuildCraft block now returns the right thing when broken, gated by the right tool. **What was wrong** — only two blocks (`builder`, `architect`) had loot tables on disk, so every other BuildCraft machine — engines, pipes, the Filtered Buffer, the Auto Workbench, the Quarry, the Pump, every laser table, every decorated block — silently dropped nothing on break. Inventories were equally inconsistent: a few blocks (Tank, Distiller, Heat Exchanger, Iron Engine, Builder, Architect) popped their fluid/item contents in `playerWillDestroy`, but the Pump's fluid tank, the FloodGate's tank, the Chute's 4 slots, the Filler's resource grid, the Library's 4 download/upload slots, the Replacer's 3 schematic slots, the Stirling Engine's fuel slot, the FE Engine's and Dynamo's upgrade slots, the Zone Planner's 7 slots, and the Auto Workbench's materials/result slots all vanished when broken. There was also no tool gating — 1.12.2's `Material.IRON`/`Material.ROCK` blocks all required a pickaxe via vanilla's material defaults, but the modern port hadn't set `requiresCorrectToolForDrops` or the `#minecraft:mineable/pickaxe` tag on anything except builder/architect/filtered_buffer. **The fix** — three layers: (1) Expanded `data/minecraft/tags/block/mineable/pickaxe.json` to include every block that was `Material.IRON` or `Material.ROCK` in 1.12.2 (29 blocks: 6 decorated variants, 6 engines + dynamo, every factory machine except water_gel/spring/tube, every builders block including frame, every laser/laser-table, pipe_holder, filtered_buffer, zone_planner). (2) Added `.requiresCorrectToolForDrops()` to all 29 registrations in the `BC*Blocks` files so vanilla's drop logic actually consults the tag. Markers (`marker_volume`, `marker_path`) stay hand-breakable since they were `Material.CIRCUITS` in 1.12.2; springs stay unbreakable; tube stays unbreakable when a miner sits above (existing `BlockTube.onDestroyedByPlayer` guard) and unbreakable in survival regardless (`destroyTime(-1.0f)`). Water gel keeps its custom `getDrops` that returns the `gelled_water` item rather than a block form, matching 1.12.2's `Material.CLAY` hand-break. (3) Created loot tables at `data/buildcraftunofficial/loot_table/blocks/<block>.json` for every gated block (22 new files, all of the "drop self with `minecraft:survives_explosion` condition" shape that mirrors the existing builder/architect tables). Loot tables only fire when `canHarvestBlock` is true, so empty-hand breaks correctly drop no block while pickaxe breaks correctly drop the block item. **Inventory drops** — added or extended `playerWillDestroy` overrides on every block whose tile holds items or fluids, dropping the contents *regardless* of tool (an accidental hand-break shouldn't eat the player's stored items even though it shouldn't return the machine block itself). A new [BlockDropsUtil](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/BlockDropsUtil.java) helper centralises three patterns: `dropTileContents(level, pos, tile, ...fluidTanks)` for tiles using `ItemHandlerManager` (which already skips `EnumAccess.PHANTOM` handlers — see line 81 of [ItemHandlerManager](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/tile/item/ItemHandlerManager.java) where PHANTOM handlers are excluded from `handlersToDrop`), `dropItems` for tiles holding raw `ItemHandlerSimple` instances outside the manager, and `dropFluidShards` for direct fluid tanks. **Ghost-slot suppression** — the spec says template/filter slots (Auto Workbench blueprint + material_filter, Filtered Buffer filter) must NOT drop on break, since those slots never consumed the items they display; they're displays, not storage. PHANTOM access already encodes this — `dropTileContents` only iterates the non-PHANTOM handlers from `ItemHandlerManager`, so adding `tile.addDrops(toDrop, 0)` automatically gets the right behaviour without code on each block. The new tests below explicitly verify this for both the Auto Workbench (seeded Nether Star and Dragon Egg in PHANTOM slots; asserts they do NOT drop while real materials/result do) and the Filtered Buffer (seeded same rare items in filter slots; asserts only `invMain` drops). **Per-block inventory wiring** — Chute / Filler / Auto Workbench / Filtered Buffer / Library use `dropTileContents` (itemManager-backed); Replacer uses `dropItems` on its 3 schematic slots; Zone Planner uses `dropItems` on its 16-slot paintbrush bank + 6 in/out slots (the only tile with the full 7-inventory layout); Stirling Engine uses `dropStack` on its loose `fuelStack` field; FE Engine + Dynamo use `dropItems` on their upgrade slots; Pump's existing `playerWillDestroy` (which only cleaned up tubes) now also calls `dropFluidShards` on the internal tank; FloodGate gets a new `playerWillDestroy` that drops its 2-bucket tank as shards. Frame's previously-empty `getDrops` override was removed entirely; the standard loot table + tool-gate now handles the same intent (quarry cleanup via `level.removeBlock(pos, false)` still skips drops, so dismantling the quarry rig doesn't dump frame items everywhere). FilteredBuffer's `getDrops` override was replaced with a `playerWillDestroy` so inventory drops regardless of tool (the loot table handles self-drop on pickaxe). **Tests** — new [BlockDropsTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/BlockDropsTester.java) with 11 game tests covering 7 representative block categories: decorated block (no-inventory baseline, both tool states), chute (itemManager real inventory, both states), auto workbench (PHANTOM/real mix verifying ghost-slot suppression), tank (fluid-only contents as shards, both states), Stirling engine (loose ItemStack outside itemManager, both states), filtered buffer (PHANTOM filter suppression), path marker (hand-breakable parity check). The tests deliberately bypass `helper.destroyBlock` — that path uses `dropBlock=false` which skips the loot table entirely, so a misconfigured tool gate would silently pass; instead the tests replay the `playerWillDestroy → removeBlock → playerDestroy` sequence the way `ServerPlayerGameMode.destroyBlock` does it, gating the `playerDestroy` call on `canHarvestBlock` exactly like vanilla. Without that gate the empty-hand tests would have all passed despite the loot table firing unconditionally, which is precisely the bug that an earlier iteration of the test suite caught (4 failures: chute/decorated/stirling/tank all dropped the block on hand-break because the test driver was calling playerDestroy regardless of canHarvest). Test instance manifests added at `src/test/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/test_instance/drops_*.json` for each. Game test count 96 → 107, all green.
- Guide book: creative-only entries (Creative Engine, Debugger, Volume Box) are now hidden from survival players who can't obtain them. **What was wrong** — the guide TOC and search both surfaced these three entries to every player, even though all three have no survival recipe in 1.12.2 or 26.1.x and can only be acquired through creative mode, `/give`, or commands. A survival player browsing the guide would see the entry, read about the item, and have no way to get one. **The gate** — new `creative_only` flag on [PageEntry](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/entry/PageEntry.java) propagates through to [PageLink](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/contents/PageLink.java); both `resetVisibility()` and `setVisible(matches)` AND the existing visibility logic with a new static `canAccessCreativeOnlyContent()` predicate. The predicate returns true if the local player has `getAbilities().instabuild`, holds `Permissions.COMMANDS_GAMEMASTER` (the modern equivalent of OP level 2 — the client's LocalPlayer gets this from the server via `ClientboundEntityEventPacket` events 24-28, so it works in both SP and MP), or is hosting a singleplayer/LAN world with `WorldData.isAllowCommands()` on. Returns false if any of `Minecraft.getInstance()`, `mc.player`, or the abilities chain is null — covers unit-test JVMs and the title screen. Re-evaluated on every guide tick via the existing `resetVisibility()` call chain ([GuidePageContents.updateScreen](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/contents/GuidePageContents.java)), so switching gamemodes with the book open updates the TOC on the next tick without needing a reload. **Entry markup** — new `place_creative` and `item_stack_creative` aliases in [util.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/util.txt) mirror the existing `place` and `item_stack` aliases but emit `"creative_only": true` in the JSON; switching an entry from gated to ungated is a one-word change in [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt). The three flagged entries: `engine_creative`, `debugger`, `box_volume`. **Search gating** — search matches also respect the flag: a survival player typing "debugger" into the guide search field gets zero results rather than a clickable link that opens a page for an item they can't have. **Tests** — six new unit tests in [PageLinkCreativeOnlyTest](src/test/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/contents/PageLinkCreativeOnlyTest.java) cover the gate-denied-by-default case, non-creative entries unaffected, creative entries hidden from both `resetVisibility()` and `setVisible()` paths, and the field-exposure pin. Total unit test count 322 → 328, all green.
- Recipe-book unlocks filled in for every BuildCraft recipe that previously had no advancement, plus six recipes newly added or recovered from 1.12.2 so machines that were registered but uncraftable can now be obtained in survival. **The missing-unlock problem** — the survival recipe book only surfaces a recipe once an `advancement/recipes/<x>.json` fires `rewards.recipes`. BuildCraft hand-writes its advancements (no datagen), and 12 recipes had been added over time without their corresponding unlocks — `guide_book`, `architect`, `blueprint_clean`, `builder`, `filler`, `quarry`, `template_clean`, `engine_iron`, `engine_stone`, `distiller`, `tank`, `decorated_laser` — so they were craftable only by typing the ingredients into a crafting grid blind. Each one now has a thematic trigger: guide_book unlocks on wooden gear or paper; architect/builder unlock on diamond gear, marker_volume, or blueprint_clean; blueprint_clean on lapis or paper; filler on gold gear or marker_volume; quarry on diamond gear or diamond pickaxe (durability/enchantment-agnostic via `inventory_changed`'s default item matching); engine_iron/engine_stone on the matching tier gear; distiller on diamond gear or the tank; template_clean on paper. Tank moved to a new `has_glass_cheap.json` triggered on `#c:glass_blocks/cheap` (kept separate from the existing `has_glass.json` so pipe recipes — which still require `#c:glass_blocks/colorless` specifically — aren't shown to players who only have colored glass). Tank recipe ingredient also broadened from `#c:glass_blocks/colorless` to `#c:glass_blocks/cheap` so mixed colored sand-glass works. **Six newly added/recovered recipes for previously-uncraftable blocks** — `engine_rf`, `mj_dynamo`, `library`, `schematic_single_clean` ported faithfully from 1.12.2 (engine_rf and mj_dynamo from `buildcraft_resources/assets/buildcraftenergy/recipes/`, library from the old-license `BuildCraftBuilders.loadRecipes()`, schematic_single_clean from the commented-out intent in `common/buildcraft/builders/BCBuildersRecipes.java`); `replacer` is novel since 1.12.2 never had one (architect in centre, two single-block schematics top/bottom-middle, gold gears in corners, quartz blocks on the middle sides — quartz fits the precision/programming feel of selecting which block to swap, with pistons left for engines and mechanical appliances; gold-gear tier keeps it below the diamond-gear cost of the architect itself). Nine RF kinesis pipe recipes added as shapeless MJ-pipe-plus-redstone-dust upgrades, mirroring the 1.12.2 `addPipeUpgradeRecipe` approach but extended from 1.12.2's three variants (wood/cobble/stone) to all nine (adds sandstone/quartz/iron/gold/diamond/diamond_wood) for symmetry with the 26.1 port's nine MJ kinesis pipe shaped recipes. The 1.12.2 "escape route" inverse — drop an RF pipe alone into a crafting grid to get the equivalent MJ pipe back — is also ported for all nine, named `pipe_<material>_power_from_rf.json` following the existing `pipe_sealant_from_green_dye` alt-recipe naming convention; the redstone dust spent on the upgrade is not refunded (matches 1.12.2 behaviour) so the inverse is a recover-the-pipe move rather than a free undo. RF pipes unlock when the player picks up any redstone dust via a new `has_dust_redstone.json` (the upgrade catalyst, semantically distinct from `has_redstone_torch.json` which gates markers). Replacer unlocks on architect pickup via a new `has_architect.json`. engine_rf and mj_dynamo join the iron-gear bucket; library joins the blueprint-clean bucket; schematic_single_clean joins both paper and lapis buckets — same dual-trigger pattern as blueprint_clean since they share ingredients. Decorated_laser remains the one recipe still without an unlock (it's a decoration block, not a machine).
- Oil worldgen: per-biome-category formation menus restructured for better hierarchy, every rich-land formation now has an infinite spring. **Rich land (desert/mesa)** has a dedicated two-formation rate table that ignores the base config and the tier bonus, replacing the previous "scale base by 1.5x" approach: 0.25% chance of a medium pool + sphere + tall spout + tube + spring (the headline-common infinite-spring formation), 0.06% chance of a large pool + sphere + tall spout + tube + spring (the rarer jackpot). The previous third slot — a 0.5% small standalone pool with no spring — is gone, intentionally, so that the `fine_riches` advancement (which gates on rich-design biomes and fires when any oil rolls in one of them) now carries the promise that earning it means the player actually struck infinite oil rather than just an ambient finite puddle. Total rich-land formation rate drops to 0.31% per chunk (down from 0.96% in the historical design) but every single one is a spring. Both rich-land formations share the tall 3x3 spout silhouette so players recognise an infinite spring at a glance regardless of pool size. **Deep ocean** loses the standalone LAKE roll entirely — the 0.75% surface-only tendril formation is gone, leaving only the existing MEDIUM (tendril + sphere + short spout, no spring; 0.15%) and LARGE (tendril + sphere + tall spout + tube + spring; 0.06%) rolls. Total deep-ocean formation rate drops from 0.96% to 0.21% per chunk; the user accepted this rate loss in exchange for "every standalone lake is a spring" being trivially true (because the only thing in deep ocean that produces a standalone-lake-shaped surface — i.e. without an accompanying spout — no longer exists). **Light ocean (regular ocean)** picks up the discarded LAKE roll as a new "small lake" variant via a 50/50 sub-roll inside MEDIUM: when a MEDIUM rolls there (0.125% × 1.25 bonus = 0.156%), half become the existing tendril + sphere + short spout, half become a new small tendril alone (no spout, no sphere). Total light-ocean rate unchanged at 0.225%. **Non-rich land** (jungle / standard / reduced / mountainous) unchanged — same base-rate × tier-bonus rolls as before. **Deep ocean MEDIUM also gets a spring** so the "any oil in a rich-design biome = guaranteed infinite spring" promise extends from rich land into deep ocean too. The deep-ocean MEDIUM formation goes from "tendril + sphere + short spout, no spring" to "tendril + sphere + tall spout + tube + spring", matching deep-ocean LARGE in structure and differing only in tendril radius (5-15 vs 25-45) and sphere radius (4-7 vs 8-16). Spring rate in deep ocean climbs from 0.06% (LARGE only) to 0.21% combined; spring rate across all rich-design biomes (deep ocean + rich land) is now 0.52% per chunk, all infinite. **Implementation** — [OilGenerator.getStructures](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/generation/OilGenerator.java) splits into two roll branches (rich-land's hardcoded rate table vs. everything else's base-config × tier-bonus path). Two private constants `RICH_LAND_LARGE_SPRING_PROB` (0.06%) and `RICH_LAND_MEDIUM_SPRING_PROB` (0.25%) hold the rich-land rates; the `oilWellGenerationRate` global multiplier and `forceExcessiveOilBiomes` 30x override still apply. The spring/tube condition simplifies to `richBiome && (LARGE || MEDIUM)` covering all four spring-producing cases (rich land LARGE+MEDIUM and deep ocean LARGE+MEDIUM). Pool factory remapping: rich land LARGE → `createSurfacePoolLarge`, MEDIUM → `createSurfacePoolMedium`; the now-orphaned `createSurfacePoolSmall` factory is removed along with the LAKE roll path through rich land. **Config changes** — removed `smallOilGenProb` (no longer referenced; rich-land has hardcoded rates, the LAKE roll for light ocean uses the MEDIUM rate). Updated `mediumOilGenProb`/`largeOilGenProb` comments to note they apply only to non-rich-land biomes. Users on existing config files will see `smallOilGenProb` silently ignored at load (NeoForge logs a warning).
- Oil worldgen: non-rich-tier spouts get a visually distinct silhouette so they no longer look like infinite springs. **The bug** — in-client testing in a snowy_plains biome (reduced tier, 0.5x rate) showed a LARGE roll producing a tall 3x3 oil column rising 10-20 blocks above the surface, indistinguishable at a glance from the rich-tier infinite-spring formations the player expects to see in desert/mesa/deep ocean. The previous round's `richBiome` gate on the bedrock spring/tube stopped the actual *spring* from spawning (no infinite regen in non-rich biomes), but the spout itself was still using the same shape parameters (`largeSpoutMinHeight/MaxHeight` = 10-20 blocks tall, radius 1 = 3x3 column), producing the same tower silhouette. **The fix** — in [OilGenerator.getStructures](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/generation/OilGenerator.java) the spout shape parameters now branch on rich-vs-non-rich: rich LARGE keeps the tall 3x3 tower (`largeSpout` heights, radius 1) and everything else (non-rich LARGE, non-rich MEDIUM) becomes a short 1x1 surface bump (new `finiteSpout` heights, radius 0). The sphere-to-surface tube fills for both — that vertical connection from underground reservoir to overflow point is intentional, it's just the above-ground height + width that differs. The two formations are now trivially distinguishable at a glance: a tall 3x3 tower means infinite spring, a small 1x1 bump means finite deposit. **Config changes** — replaced `smallSpoutMinHeight/MaxHeight` (semantically tied to a now-defunct case: smallSpout was the MEDIUM range, but rich MEDIUM is a POOL and non-rich MEDIUM now uses finiteSpout) with new `finiteSpoutMinHeight` (default 7) and `finiteSpoutMaxHeight` (default 10). `largeSpoutMinHeight` bumped from 10 to 13 (kept distinct from the finite-spout max of 10) with `largeSpoutMaxHeight` unchanged at 20; their comment now clarifies they apply ONLY to rich-tier infinite springs. Users on existing config files will see the old `smallSpout` keys silently ignored (NeoForge logs a warning at load) and need to add the new `finiteSpout` keys to customise, or delete the config file to pick up the new defaults.
- Oil worldgen: vanilla rivers excluded by default, infinite-spring formations are now strictly rich-tier-only, and the standard 1.0x tier picks up two more low-value biomes. **Standard tier additions** — `snowy_beach` (a thin frozen transition strip) and `frozen_river` (iced-over transit biome — distinct enough from a regular river that oil reads as a frontier formation rather than a polluted creek) are now defaults in `standardSurfaceDepositBiomes`, joining jungle variants and ice_spikes at the 1.0x rate. Frozen rivers stay OUT of `excludedBiomes` for this to take effect (the exclusion check runs before tier classification); vanilla rivers remain excluded — their open-water surface tends to surface a spout's vertical column awkwardly across the narrow river bed.
- Oil worldgen: rivers excluded by default, and infinite-spring formations are now strictly rich-tier-only. **River fix** — observed in-client: oil deposits were spawning inside river biomes (the narrow blue arteries that wind through other biomes), and a spout's vertical column of source blocks surfacing across a 3-block-wide river bed looks like polluted infrastructure rather than a natural formation. Added `minecraft:river` and `minecraft:frozen_river` to the default `excludedBiomes` list in [BCEnergyConfig](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/BCEnergyConfig.java), with a comment explaining the rationale. Users who want river oil can remove the entries. Note: NeoForge configs persist across runs in `run/config/`, so existing configs need to be deleted (or manually edited to add the entries) to pick up the new defaults — fresh worlds and fresh configs get the new behaviour automatically. **Spring scope fix** — observed in-client: a LARGE roll in a non-rich biome (plains, forest, jungle, etc.) was still emitting the bedrock spring + vertical tube, breaking the design promise that the infinite-regen formation is reserved for deep ocean + desert + mesa. The original `if (type == GenType.LARGE)` guard around the spring/tube generation in [OilGenerator.getStructures](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/generation/OilGenerator.java) now also requires `richBiome`; LARGE rolls in non-rich biomes degrade to "finite deposit, no infinite regen" (sphere + spout only, identical in shape to MEDIUM but with the larger sphere radius and taller spout). The visible difference between LARGE and MEDIUM in non-rich biomes is now just scale, which matches how the formation feels in-world without the spring tag.
- Oil worldgen revamp: clean desert/mesa pools, spout-only land formations, granular per-biome rarity. **Visual change** — surface oil now follows three rules depending on the biome category. (1) Ocean biomes are unchanged — the "lake with tendril arms" aesthetic that looks organic underwater is preserved for every LARGE/MEDIUM/LAKE roll. (2) Rich land biomes (desert / mesa by default) get a new clean-disc `SurfacePool` instead of tendrils: LARGE rolls a medium pool around a visible tall spout, MEDIUM rolls a small puddle with no underground or spout (so only LARGE's spout signifies "infinite spring"), and LAKE rolls a medium-large pool. (3) Common land biomes (jungle / regular / mountainous) get **no pre-placed surface structure at all** — the spout pushes a column of oil source blocks above the terrain (punching through any tree in its 1-3 block column via the tube's `ReplaceType.ALWAYS`) and vanilla fluid flow does the rest, creating a natural spreading mess around the eruption point. Skips the tendril aesthetic on land entirely (it looked pasted-on) and also skips the tree-clear footprint (which looked like a scar of dead canopy where the tendril was). **Rate change** — biomes are now sorted into five tiers (rich 1.5×, light-ocean 1.25×, standard 1.0×, reduced 0.5× new-default, mountainous 0.1×). Jungles + ice_spikes default to standard tier (1.0×, unchanged). Mountain/peak biomes default to mountainous (0.1×, much rarer — oil seeping through bedrock-grade rock is unrealistic). Everything else drops from the historical 1.0× default to 0.5× reduced — vanilla forest/plains/taiga/savanna get half as much oil as before. Rich/light-ocean tiers unchanged. **Implementation** — new `OilGenStructure.SurfacePool` component (filled disc with ±1 block radial noise; uses `OCEAN_FLOOR_WG` heightmap + downward walk for true ground; defensively tree-aware via `clearTreesAndFindGround` so it handles wooded_badlands and any modded biome added to the rich list with trees). Tree-clear BFS uses enqueue-time filtering (only logs/leaves go on the queue, so each unit of budget = one cleared block instead of ~20 wasted pops on air-neighbour dequeues that the naive design would suffer from), an 8192-block budget (covers connected canopy clusters from several touching megajungles), 26-connectivity (over-clears slightly — diagonally overlapping canopies clear cleanly), writes clamped to loading-chunk box + 4-block expansion for cross-chunk tree follow-through, and `UPDATE_CLIENTS` flag to avoid neighbour-change cascades. The downward sweep in `clearTreesAndFindGround` is the critical save: even if budget exhausts midway, the next cell's column-walk catches surviving stumps that an upward-only scan would miss (the heightmap goes stale immediately after the first BFS so the upward scan finds only air). New `OilGenerator.createSurfacePoolSmall/Medium/Large` factories build the disc with deterministic per-cell noise. `BiomeTags.IS_OCEAN` distinguishes ocean from land for the tendril/pool/nothing branch. Tier classification uses simple biome-ID list membership matching the existing rich/light pattern (new config keys `standardSurfaceDepositBiomes` and `mountainousSurfaceDepositBiomes`). **Advancement** — `fine_riches` is unchanged: still fires only in rich (desert/mesa/deep ocean) + excessive biomes. Standard/reduced/mountainous land biomes produce visible surface oil from the spout overflow but are intentionally excluded so the advancement remains a "found a true oil-design biome" signal, not "found ambient oil somewhere." Migration: changing the default base rate from 1.0× to 0.5× is a balance change visible on new worlds; existing worlds keep already-generated oil and will see the new rate on freshly-loaded chunks. **Tests** — two new synchronous game tests in [OilGenStructureTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/energy/generation/OilGenStructureTester.java): `oilgen_surface_pool_clean_shape` verifies the disc shape (centre oil, far corners untouched); `oilgen_surface_pool_clears_tall_tree_fully` plants a 15-log jungle trunk with a 5×5×2 leaf cap (~65 tree blocks — enough to overflow the historical 2048-budget-with-26-fanout that caused the floating-log regression observed in early in-client testing) and asserts every single log in the trunk is cleared by the pool's BFS. Test count up by 2.
- Engine wrench UX overhaul + overheating port. **The previous behaviour** was that only crouch+RMB with a wrench rotated an engine, played the wrench sound, and granted the "Wrenched!" advancement — every other engine handled non-crouch wrench differently (Stirling/FE/Dynamo opened the GUI instead of rotating, Combustion rotated via a separate code path that bypassed the wrench's own success hook, Creative cycled power) and overheating an engine **always exploded** because the proper "sit in the overheated state" loop from 1.12.2 was never ported. **The new behaviour** unifies the engine family: non-crouch+wrench rotates (sound + advancement), crouch always opens the GUI (Redstone/Creative have no GUI), and **overheated Stirling/Combustion engines no longer explode** by default — they sit in the OVERHEAT stage producing no power until cooled, and a wrench-tap clears the overheat, plays the slide sound, and now wires up the previously-dead "Too much power!" advancement. New config option `general.canEnginesExplode` (default `false`, in the in-game NeoForge config screen) restores 1.12.2-style explosions for users who want them. Engines with no valid rotation target play the vanilla `block.lever.click` sound pitched up (1.3×) instead of the piston sound and grant no advancement, so the player gets audio + arm-swing feedback that the wrench fired but had nothing to do without trivialising the achievement. Creative engine retains its non-crouch=cycle-power behaviour but now also grants the wrench advancement on each cycle and plays the same lever click pitched *down* (0.7×) as a distinct confirmation tone; crouch+wrench rotates if possible (no power step-back when surrounded — too clever to be intuitive). Every wrench interaction that "did something meaningful" (rotation, overheat-clear, power-cycle, soft-fail no-op) now swings the arm — previously only successful rotations swung. Combustion engine's dual rotation code path is consolidated into the single base `ICustomRotationHandler` path. FE engine's crouch UX is inverted to match the rest of the family (was: crouch=rotate; now: crouch=GUI).

- "Abbreviate Large Numbers" now actually applies to MJ readouts, and fluid abbreviation shifts the unit from millibuckets to buckets instead of using k-suffixed millibuckets. **What was broken (MJ side)** — the original abbreviation design in [LocaleUtil](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/LocaleUtil.java) deliberately routed `formatDouble` *without* the abbreviation branch, so MJ-side formatters (`localizeMj`, `localizeMjFlow`) bypassed the toggle entirely. The intent at the time was to preserve precision for JEI recipe-cost labels, but it caught every MJ surface as collateral, so the assembly-table power ledger kept rendering "Required: 10,000.00 Minecraft Joules" / "Stored: 2,158.09 Minecraft Joules" with the toggle on. New layout: a private `formatMjAmount(double mj, int decimals, boolean abbreviate)` helper centralises the branching (≥ 1000 → `formatAbbreviated` → "10.0k"; otherwise raw `formatDouble`). `localizeMj` and `localizeMjFlow` both route through it with `shouldAbbreviate()` flag; the JEI category labels in `AssemblyTableCategory` and `DistillerCategory` keep calling raw `formatDouble(mj, 1)` directly, so the 80,000-MJ recipe-cost label stays at full precision while the in-game ledger compacts. **What was wrong (fluid side)** — `formatFluidFlow` routed through `formatLong`, which abbreviates with k/M/G/T suffixes on top of the existing unit; a golden-pipe-rate 1600 mB/s rendered as the awkward "1.6k mB/s" instead of the natural-reading "1.6 buckets per second". Real fluid systems read in buckets once values cross that threshold (industrial mods all do this), so the abbreviation branch for fluids now shifts the unit instead of appending a k: ≥ 1000 mB → divide by 1000, unit becomes "buckets" / "B", with k/M/G/T applied on top of the bucket count only if the bucket count itself crosses 1000 (so a 2,000,000 mB/s pipe reads "2.0k B/s"). Toggle off keeps the historical "1,600 mB/s" raw form with the configured thousands separator. **Implementation** — new private `formatFluidAmount(long mb, boolean fullSuffix, boolean abbreviate)` helper does the bucket-shift branching; package-visible `formatMjFlow` and `formatFluidFlow` both gain an explicit `boolean abbreviate` parameter (existing flow tests pick up `, false` to keep their non-abbreviated expectations). Six new tests cover the abbreviation paths against MJ scalars, MJ flow, fluid bucket-shift at the 1000-mB threshold, fluid BOTH-mode where per-sec abbreviates while per-tick stays raw, fluid-toggle-off raw fallback, and fluid k/M/G/T-on-top-of-buckets at very large rates; full `LocaleUtilNumberFormatTester` suite now sits at 34 tests all green.
- Renamed the "Spell Energy Units In Full" config to **"Spell Units in Full"** and broadened it to cover (a) the per-second / per-tick time suffix, matching 1.12.2's spelled-out wording, and (b) fluid pipe tooltips. With the toggle on (default), MJ/RF/FE flow readouts render as "100.00 Minecraft Joules per second" / "5.00 Forge Energy per tick" instead of "100.00 Minecraft Joules/s" / "5.00 Forge Energy/t", and the fluid pipe tooltip reads "40 millibuckets per tick" instead of "40 mB/t". Turning the toggle off gives the compact "MJ/s" / "FE/t" / "mB/t" form back. Fluid pipe tooltips now also respect **"Flow Rate Display"** — previously hardcoded to PER_TICK, they now render as "800 mB/s" (PER_SECOND), "40 mB/t" (PER_TICK), or "800 mB/s (40 mB/t)" (BOTH), matching the MJ/RF formatters; the integer count is now also routed through `formatLong` so the thousands separator config applies (`1,234 mB/t` with default COMMA grouping). Config-side: `BCEnergyConfig.useFullEnergyNames` → `BCEnergyConfig.useFullUnitNames` (the config-file key changes too, so anyone who had explicitly set `useFullEnergyNames=false` will silently revert to the default `true` on upgrade — acceptable in beta, and the rename matches the broader scope of "all unit display", not just energy). Implementation: [LocaleUtil.formatMjFlow](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/LocaleUtil.java) and [formatRfFlow](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/LocaleUtil.java) gained a `fullSuffix` parameter; [localizeFluidFlow](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/LocaleUtil.java) routes through a new `formatFluidFlow(int, FlowDisplay, boolean)` that mirrors the RF formatter's shape (including `* 20L` widening to prevent overflow at extreme tick rates). The public `localizeMjFlow` / `localizeRfFlow` / `localizeFluidFlow` wrappers all pass `BCEnergyConfig.useFullUnitNames` so every existing caller (engine ledger, dynamo screen, RF engine screen, energy/fluid pipe tooltips, JEI cost labels) picks up the new behaviour without touching their call sites. The internal `shouldUseFullNames()` helper now backs `mjUnit()`/`energyUnit()` too — same toggle drove unit names already, this just collapses the duplicated null check. Six new unit tests cover the spelled-out form and all three FlowDisplay modes against MJ, RF/FE, and fluid codepaths; the existing seven flow tests pick up `, false` arguments to keep their original "/s"/"/t" expectations. Lang key `buildcraftunofficial.configuration.useFullEnergyNames` → `buildcraftunofficial.configuration.useFullUnitNames` with label updated to "Spell Units in Full".
- Final tube rendering tuning: epsilon-offset the laser start by 1mm below the well's bottom face, restore `partialTicks` interpolation for smooth descent animation, and re-enable per-face diffuse shading. **The earlier integer-snap fix was wrong** — it eliminated the flicker but lost the smooth descent animation entirely, and the diagnosis was incomplete. The user clarified the real issue: the topmost segment was flickering between "world shading" (gradient including the dark interior of the well block) and "block shading" (uniform bright from the open block below the well), with no texture-seam involvement. Tracing through the start-elastic config, the start segment's top vertex sits at `y = well.y` exactly — `BlockPos.containing` resolves that to the **well block itself**, an opaque block with block-light = 0 in its interior. When the start segment is full (~middleWidth tall, length just below an integer), the quad's lightmap interpolates from `light(well-block-interior)` at top → `light(below-well)` at bottom: dark → bright gradient. When `numMiddle` increments and the start collapses to a sliver, the visible first block is occupied by a new middle whose top vertex is just below the well block — both vertices in the bright below-well block, uniform lightmap. Same world pixel, two different lightmap-interpolation states, flips each `numMiddle` increment as `length` crosses an integer. **The fix** — `Vec3 start = new Vec3(pos.getX() + 0.5, pos.getY() - 1e-3, pos.getZ() + 0.5)` in [TubeRenderer](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/render/TubeRenderer.java). The 1mm offset pushes the start segment's top vertex out of the opaque well block and into the bright below-well block. Now both segmentation configurations sample lighting from the same block, the alternation can't happen, and the smooth `partialTicks` animation is back. The 1mm-thin strip at exactly `y = well.y` is no longer rendered, but it was inside the opaque well block's footprint anyway — invisible either way. Also re-enabled `enableDiffuse=true` on the tube's `LaserData_BC8` — this was disabled earlier on the assumption that per-face diffuse plus per-vertex world-light was contributing to the flicker, but they're independent mechanisms: per-face diffuse computes one brightness per quad from the laser's rotation matrix (constant per-laser-render, doesn't depend on `numMiddle`), while the per-vertex lightmap samples world block-light at each vertex's actual position. Restoring diffuse gives the tube vanilla-style block shading (sides at ~0.6/0.8 brightness based on which world-horizontal direction they face, caps at 1.0/0.5 for up/down) without reintroducing any of the segmentation-dependent flicker. End state: smooth length easing, per-face block-like shading, per-vertex world-light gradient down the column, no frame-to-frame artifacts.
- Pruned stale TileMiner entries from [TubeRenderer's](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/render/TubeRenderer.java) `ACTIVE_MINERS` set, fixing per-frame flicker at the top tube segment after world reload. **The symptom** — observed on the mining well: a subtle alternating-frame visual difference in the tube segment directly under the well, looking like two slightly different render submissions competing each frame. The flicker became more obvious after the previous lighting fix because the per-vertex world-light + segmented start-segment math means even small geometry differences are now visible (with the broken fullbright defaults from earlier, every segmentation state looked identical so the duplication was invisible). **Root cause** — same WeakHashMap orphan-leak pattern as the laser renderer (see commit `885f8e027` for the parallel `RenderLaser` fix): client-side level teardown on logout / dimension change doesn't reliably call `setRemoved()` on every BE, so the *old* world's `TileMiner` lingers in the static set until GC runs while the *new* world's `TileMiner` for the same well also registers via `onLoad`. Both render their tube each frame at the same world position but with subtly different `currentLength` smoothing state — the old miner's lastLength/currentLength are frozen at whatever they were the tick before the previous world unloaded, while the new miner's are converging fresh toward the saved `wantedLength`. Two beam submissions per frame at slightly-different lengths means the segmentation boundary (where `numMiddle` increments — see [CompiledLaserType.bakeFor](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/render/laser/CompiledLaserType.java)) is in a different place for each, and the depth test alternates between them frame-to-frame. The flicker concentrates at the top segment because that's the "elastic" segment in our tube's `LaserType` config (`new LaserType(cap, middle, [middle], null, cap)` — `start=middle` makes the start segment absorb the leftover length, while `end=null` leaves the bottom fixed-size), so it's the one whose geometry diverges most between the two miner instances' length values. **The fix** — same one-liner pattern as `silicon.client.RenderLaser`: `ACTIVE_MINERS.removeIf(miner -> miner.isRemoved() || miner.getLevel() != mc.level)` at the top of `onRenderLevel`, plus removing the now-redundant `if (miner.isRemoved()) continue` inside the loop. Self-heals each frame: stale entries get dropped the moment their level reference doesn't match `mc.level`. The previous bullet's `(false, false, 0)` lighting choice stays — that's still correct for the tube's intended look (smooth world-light gradient along the column without per-face brightness jumps); the flicker was a separate lifecycle bug riding on top of it that the lighting change just made visible. **Why this wasn't caught earlier** — pre-port the tube was fullbright everywhere via the broken 4-arg constructor default (`minBlockLight=15`), which meant even with two miners rendering, both produced identical fullbright pixels so the duplication was invisible. The lighting fix in `ecace8685` exposed it by making lighting depend on per-vertex position, and the per-beam override in `885f8e027` doubled down on per-vertex lightmap sampling.
- Per-beam lighting overrides on top of the restored 4-arg defaults: assembly-table lasers back to fullbright, mining well / pump tubes get world-lit gradient without per-face brightness jumps. **Why the previous bullet's fix wasn't quite right** — flipping the 4-arg default to `(true, false, 0)` made the mining well tube *look right per-vertex* (darker as it extends underground) but introduced a separate visual issue: with `enableDiffuse=true`, [LaserContext.setFaceNormal](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/render/laser/LaserContext.java) pre-computes a single diffuse factor per face from a vanilla-style normal map (1.0 top, 0.5 bottom, 0.8 sides), so each of the tube's four sides is uniformly tinted to a different brightness. Stacked against the per-vertex world-light gradient that runs *along* the tube's length, the result is two visual effects in tension — a smooth gradient down the column AND discrete brightness jumps between the visible faces. As the camera rotates around the tube, the dominant visible face flips and the apparent brightness snaps between 0.5x and 1.0x, which the user accurately described as *"as if two rendering systems are competing, one has gradient shading, and the other has more averaged shading"* (they're both real effects from the *same* renderer, not actual duplicate rendering). For the assembly-table laser specifically, the previous bullet's switch to `enableDiffuse=true` also broke the user's expected look — lasers are self-illuminating and the pre-port appearance was fullbright and unshaded, which the world-light + diffuse combination doesn't reproduce. **The fix** — keep the 4-arg default at 1.12.2's `(true, false, 0)` so it still serves the quarry frame / drill / builder build-line / robot beam callers correctly (those *want* the face-shading look), and override at the two callers that need different behaviour: (a) [silicon.client.RenderLaser](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/RenderLaser.java) explicitly passes `(false, false, 15)` — no face shading, fullbright, matches the pre-port assembly-table laser appearance; (b) [factory.client.render.TubeRenderer](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/render/TubeRenderer.java) explicitly passes `(false, false, 0)` — no face shading, world block-light per vertex. The tube now darkens smoothly along its length as it descends into dark rock (the desired effect) without the per-face brightness jumps that produced the camera-angle-dependent flicker. Result: the mining well tube reads as a single continuous tinted beam; the laser reads as a self-illuminating blue beam at full brightness regardless of ambient.
- Restored 1.12.2 lighting defaults for the 4-arg `LaserData_BC8` convenience constructor — fixes the mining well / pump tube rendering at full-bright the whole way down (instead of darkening with depth) and unshaded (no face-normal diffuse). **The bug** — observed on a mining well tube: as the drill extended through dark underground chunks, the tube stayed uniformly fullbright with no shading variation between faces, looking flat and out-of-place against the surrounding stone. **Root cause** — [LaserData_BC8](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/render/laser/LaserData_BC8.java)'s 4-arg convenience constructor delegated to the 7-arg form with `(false, false, 15)` for the trailing `(enableDiffuse, doubleFace, minBlockLight)` triple. 1.12.2 used `(true, false, 0)` for the same defaults. `minBlockLight = 15` short-circuits [LaserRenderer_BC8.computeLightmap](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/render/laser/LaserRenderer_BC8.java) (line 99 `if (minBlockLight >= 15) blockLight = 15`) to force fullbright on the block-light channel, ignoring world block-light entirely; `enableDiffuse = false` disables face-normal-based shading. Net effect: every 4-arg caller — quarry frames, drill beams, builder build-line beams, robot lasers, the assembly-table laser, and the pump/well tube — rendered fullbright and unshaded since the port, regardless of the actual lighting at the beam's location. 1.12.2's defaults pre-dated every modern caller (the file is verbatim from the 1.12.2 lib package), so the swap was a port-time mistake rather than an intentional behaviour change. **The fix** — flip the 4-arg default back to `(true, false, 0)`. All three explicit 7-arg call sites stay as they are: [PathConnection](src/main/java/buildcraft/core/marker/PathConnection.java) (`false, false, 0`), [MarkerRenderer](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/render/MarkerRenderer.java) (`false, false, 15` — markers want unconditional visibility, that's intentional), and [LaserBoxRenderer](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/render/laser/LaserBoxRenderer.java) (`enableDiffuse, false, 15` — variable diffuse for box outlines, also intentional). Visual changes the player will notice: (a) mining well tubes darken as they extend into dark caves/dirt, brightening when they punch through to lit areas; (b) pump tubes likewise track world light; (c) quarry frames and drills pick up shading (faces oriented toward the sun look brighter than ones facing away); (d) the assembly-table laser beam darkens at night and underground. All of these are exactly what 1.12.2 looked like; the previous fullbright-everything appearance was the regression. **End-to-end check** — place a mining well, watch the tube extend into darker rock; the tube now visibly darkens with depth instead of staying neon-bright.
- Removed the broken-since-day-one BE renderer for the laser, kept the level-stage one as the single render path, and merged 1.12.2's visual polish into it. **What the dual-renderer investigation actually found** — `TileLaser` had two render paths registered: a `BlockEntityRenderer<TileLaser>` at `silicon.client.render.RenderLaser` (the "proper" architecture, registered via `EntityRenderersEvent.RegisterRenderers`, looking like a faithful port of 1.12.2's `FastTESR<TileLaser>`), and a `RenderLevelStageEvent.AfterTranslucentBlocks` handler at [silicon.client.RenderLaser](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/RenderLaser.java) (custom, with a static `WeakHashMap`-backed `ACTIVE_LASERS` set populated from `TileLaser.onLoad`). The first-pass conclusion was "delete the level-stage one, the BE renderer is the architecturally correct choice" — but it turns out the BE renderer **has never rendered anything**. Its `submit()` passed *world* coordinates to `LaserData_BC8` along with `Vec3.ZERO` for the camera offset, but vanilla pre-translates the BE pose stack by `(blockPos − cameraPos)` before calling `submit()`, so every vertex ended up at `worldCoord + (blockPos − cameraPos)` — i.e. off by `blockPos` (roughly ±320 blocks for the user's spawn coords, far outside the view frustum). The level-stage renderer was the only thing producing visible beams the entire time; the BE renderer's contribution was silently zero geometry. The "wasted draw calls" claim from the previous bullet was wrong — there was only ever one beam being drawn. **Why the BER path was wrong in the first place** — confirmed by [RenderQuarry's source comment](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/client/render/RenderQuarry.java) (lines 44-46): *"world-space rendering (frame/drill lasers, rigs) is still handled by BCBuildersEventDist via RenderLevelStageEvent because those cross block boundaries; this BER only covers the block-local LEDs."* The convention across this codebase is BER for block-local geometry, `RenderLevelStageEvent` for anything that spans blocks. The laser beam crosses up to 6 blocks of horizontal range; it belongs in the level-stage path, same as the quarry frame lasers and pump/well tubes. The BE renderer was a port-time misjudgement that no-one caught because the visible-rendering path (the level-stage one) made the absence invisible. **The fix** — delete the broken BE renderer (`silicon.client.render.RenderLaser` + its companion `LaserRenderState` render-state class), remove the `event.registerBlockEntityRenderer(...)` call in [BCSiliconClient.registerRenderers](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/BCSiliconClient.java) (the whole method drops since that was its only line), and port 1.12.2's `FastTESR<TileLaser>` visual logic *into* the level-stage [RenderLaser](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/RenderLaser.java): (a) `avg > 200_000` mj/t threshold (`continue` if below — no beam when the laser is essentially idle), (b) direction-aware emitter offset using `BlockLaser.FACING` so the beam emerges from the red face instead of the block centre, and (c) linear `POWERS[(int) (avg * MAX_POWER / maxPerTick)]` colour quantization clamped to `MAX_POWER`, matching 1.12.2's smoother colour transitions instead of the previous coarse 0.25/0.5/0.75 ratio buckets. The orphan-prune `removeIf(laser -> laser.isRemoved() || laser.getLevel() != mc.level)` from the previous bullet attempt stays — that *is* a real bug in the level-stage pattern (client-side level teardown on logout/dimension-change doesn't reliably call `setRemoved()` on every BE; the `WeakHashMap` keeps orphan TileLasers alive past world reload until the next GC sweep, producing visible ghost beams stuck at their pre-save `laserPos`). **Decision rationale** — `TubeRenderer` and the quarry frame/drill renderers both use the same level-stage pattern for the same reason (cross-block beam geometry), and the laser now joins them in being consistent with the codebase convention. `TubeRenderer` still has the same orphan-leak shape (`WeakHashMap` populated in `addMiner`, not pruned per-frame); flagging as a separate follow-up — fixable with the same one-liner `removeIf(miner -> miner.isRemoved() || miner.getLevel() != mc.level)`, but the bug is much harder to observe in practice because pump/well tubes only render while actively extending and the orphan miner's `getLength(partialTicks)` won't keep producing meaningful values once its level reference is dead. **End-to-end check** — full-power laser, save, exit, re-enter: beam comes back blue immediately (per the persistence fix below), single beam, emitter at the red face, debug overlay shows `active_lasers = 1`.
- Laser beam colour now persists across world save/reload, matching 1.12.2. **The bug** — a laser running at full power (blue beam) saved and reopened would come back as a low-power red beam and take ~5 seconds to climb back to blue, even though the recipe at the target table picked up exactly where it left off (so the laser was clearly still pushing the same MJ/t). **Root cause** — [TileLaser](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/tile/TileLaser.java) holds a 100-sample `AverageLong` ring buffer (`avgPower`) and a per-tick snapshot field (`averageClient`) which is what [RenderLaser.getLaserTypeForPower](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/RenderLaser.java) reads to pick `POWER_LOW/MED/HIGH/FULL`. The port saved only the snapshot value (`output.putLong("average_client", averageClient)`), but `serverTick` *unconditionally overwrites* `averageClient = (long) avgPower.getAverage()` on every tick — so the saved value was thrown away the instant the laser ticked, and `avgPower` itself was freshly constructed empty, meaning the average ramped back up from zero over the buffer's 100-tick window regardless of actual power flow. 1.12.2's [TileLaser](https://github.com/legoj15/BuildCraft/blob/8.0.x-1.12.2/common/buildcraft/silicon/tile/TileLaser.java) saved the *whole* `avgPower` ring buffer via `avgPower.writeToNbt(nbt, "average_power")` and restored it via `avgPower.readFromNbt(nbt, "average_power")`; on reload the moving average was already at the right value, so the visual was steady from frame zero. **The fix** — swap the `average_client` long for an `avg_power` `CompoundTag` storing the full buffer (the existing `AverageLong.writeToNbt`/`readFromNbt` helpers on the class are unchanged from 1.12.2; just stop calling them through a tag-codec wrapper since the new `ValueOutput` API takes `CompoundTag.CODEC` the same way the laser's `battery` field already does). On load, derive `averageClient` from `avgPower.getAverage()` so the client-side snapshot reflects the restored buffer before the first server tick fires. The unconditional `avgPower.tick() … averageClient = avgPower.getAverage()` in `serverTick` is left alone — that's the right steady-state behaviour, and now it picks up a populated buffer instead of an empty one. Old worlds saved with the buggy code have no `avg_power` tag and will still see the 5-second ramp-up on their *first* reload after the fix, but subsequent saves preserve state correctly — no save migration needed. The sister field on [TileLaserTableBase](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/tile/TileLaserTableBase.java) (`avgPowerClient`, used by [LedgerTablePower](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/gui/LedgerTablePower.java) for the GUI flow rate) has the same overwrite pattern, but 1.12.2 didn't persist it either, so leaving it as-is preserves the original behaviour rather than introducing a new divergence. End-to-end check: build a laser+assembly table, wire enough engines to drive the laser to `POWER_FULL` (blue), save, exit, re-enter — beam comes back blue immediately instead of red→yellow→blue over five seconds.
- "Precision crafting" advancement now actually fires when the assembly table starts a craft, matching 1.12.2 and the advancement's description ("Start crafting with an assembly table"). **The bug** — observed after the owner-tracking fix in `9176336eb`: even with the owner correctly set on placement, the advancement never appeared. Root cause: the `AdvancementUtil.unlockAdvancement` call in [TileAssemblyTable.serverTick](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/tile/TileAssemblyTable.java) was buried inside both `if (getTarget() > 0)` AND `if (power >= getTarget())`, AND fired only after `power -= getTarget()` and `activateNextRecipe()` — so it required not just an active recipe but also a laser pointed at the table and enough accumulated MJ to consume one whole craft worth of power. 1.12.2's equivalent ([common/buildcraft/silicon/tile/TileAssemblyTable.java:183-185](https://github.com/legoj15/BuildCraft/blob/8.0.x-1.12.2/common/buildcraft/silicon/tile/TileAssemblyTable.java#L183)) fires unconditionally inside the outer `if (getTarget() > 0)` block — as soon as the table has an active recipe, no power required. **The fix** — move the advancement call up one level out of the power-check; fires every tick a recipe is active regardless of power state. `tracker.award` is idempotent so repeated calls after the first are no-op HashMap lookups; cost matches 1.12.2's behaviour. **New test** — `testPrecisionCraftingAdvancementLoaded` in [AdvancementTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/energy/AdvancementTester.java) asserts the advancement JSON loads with a `minecraft:impossible` criterion named `code_trigger`. Catches both "JSON criterion type changed" (handler still calls AdvancementUtil but no impossible criterion to write to) and "criterion renamed away from code_trigger" (handler writes to a name that no longer exists in the JSON). Implementation looks the trigger up in `BuiltInRegistries.TRIGGER_TYPES` and compares to `minecraft:impossible` — robust against future renames of the trigger class itself. **Bonus fix in the existing sticky_dipping test** — it used `c.trigger().toString().contains("impossible")` to detect impossible triggers, but `ImpossibleTrigger.toString()` is `ImpossibleTrigger@hash` (capital I) and `String.contains` is case-sensitive, so the check was effectively `false` for every trigger including impossible. Test was passing for the wrong reason and would have silently accepted a regression to the broken stub state. Refactored both tests to share an `isImpossibleTrigger(Criterion)` helper that uses the registry lookup. Test count 89 → 90, all green.
- Restored the Assembly Table's and Advanced Crafting Table's right-side ledgers to match 1.12.2: the **Owner** ledger (showing who placed the block, with their face icon) and the **animated power icon** (engine sprite that animates while power flows in, static when idle). The animated icon goes through the blocks atlas via `SpriteHolderRegistry`, so `engine_active.png.mcmeta` is honoured automatically — resource packs can retune frametime or frame order without code changes. Ledger order is ownership → power → (help), matching every other machine GUI (the Advanced Crafting Table still omits the help ledger to leave room for vanilla's recipe book, same as 1.12.2). Owner tracking itself was broken: `BlockLaserTable` never overrode `setPlacedBy`, so `tile.onPlacedBy(...)` was never called and the owner field stayed null on every laser table (Assembly, Advanced Crafting, Integration). Fixed by overriding `setPlacedBy` in `BlockLaserTable` to wire the placer through to the tile, plus a `level.sendBlockUpdated(..., Block.UPDATE_CLIENTS)` so the post-placement NBT reaches the client immediately (otherwise the owner only synced as a side effect of the first power-change tick — opening the GUI before that left the ledger blank). Also added a `setChanged()` to `TileBC_Neptune.onPlacedBy` so the owner field persists for *any* tile using the base class, not just ones whose subclass remembered to call it themselves.
- Lasers now detect assembly tables / advanced crafting tables / integration tables that are placed *after* the laser was already loaded. **The bug** — a laser placed before its target would scan its cone exactly once on load, find nothing, and never re-scan; placing the table afterwards left the laser stuck at `target = null` despite full battery and correct facing. Workaround was to break and re-place the laser. **Root cause** — [LocalBlockUpdateNotifier](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/block/LocalBlockUpdateNotifier.java) was stubbed out during the 1.21 port because `IWorldEventListener.notifyBlockUpdate` was removed; `notifySubscribersInRange` existed but nothing was wired to call it. **The fix** — `LocalBlockUpdateNotifier` now subscribes to NeoForge's `BlockEvent.EntityPlaceEvent`, `BreakBlockEvent`, and `BlockEvent.NeighborNotifyEvent` and forwards them to subscribers in range. As a safety net for sources that bypass those events (mod-placed blocks, `/setblock` without neighbor-update flags), [TileLaser](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/tile/TileLaser.java) now also force-rescans its cone every 40–60 ticks via a new `rescanInterval` `SafeTimeTracker`.
- "Fine riches" scan radius widened from ±1 chunk to ±3 chunks around the player so swimming through LAKE-tier oil grants the advancement even when the LAKE's origin chunk is several chunks away. **The bug** — observed in a mesa+desert spawn where walking up to lakes of oil only granted the advancement when the player happened to stand on the *one* origin chunk; the player could swim through visible oil (getting `sticky_dipping` as expected) without ever getting `fine_riches`. Root cause: [OilGenerator](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/generation/OilGenerator.java)'s LARGE and LAKE deposits both use `tendrilRadius = 25 + rand.nextInt(20)` — surface tendrils extending up to 45 blocks ≈ 2.8 chunks from the origin chunk where the RNG roll fires. The handler's old ±1 scan only covered ~16 blocks from the player, so when the player stood on tendril spillover from a LAKE whose origin was 2-3 chunks away, the rolled-oil chunk was outside the scan and the advancement didn't fire. MEDIUM tendrils only reach ±1 chunk (`5 + rand.nextInt(10)` = up to 15 blocks) so MEDIUM-only deposits weren't affected — only the bigger LAKE/LARGE ones, which is what the mesa/desert tester was actually seeing because rich tier is the only tier eligible for LAKE. **The fix** — new `FINE_RICHES_SCAN_RADIUS = 3` constant in [BCEnergyWorldGen](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/BCEnergyWorldGen.java), with the loop bounds replaced by `±FINE_RICHES_SCAN_RADIUS`. The scan is now 7×7 = 49 chunk RNG replays per check instead of 3×3 = 9; each replay is microseconds and the check is throttled to once per second per player, so the perf delta is negligible. Sizing rationale (in the constant's javadoc): exactly enough to cover 45-block tendril max-radius rounded up, no further — going to ±5 (matching `OilGenerator.MAX_CHUNK_RADIUS`) would more than double the chunk count without catching any real visible-oil case the ±3 misses, since horizontal spread beyond ±3 only happens via spillover from chunks already inside ±3. Trade-off: per-check probability of "any chunk rolled oil" in a dense rich biome goes from ≈9% (9 chunks × ~1%) to ≈39% (49 chunks × ~1%) — fires within ≈2-3 seconds of entering instead of ~10. Matches the user's intent: walking close to visible oil grants, not requiring direct overlap with the origin chunk. **Tests** — unchanged. Predicate-negative test samples ±2 around the test arena which is still well-bounded; biome-tier-gate test is independent of the scan radius. 89/89 still green.
- "Fine riches" now requires the player to physically be IN an oil-design biome, not just have one in render distance. **The bug** — observed when a player spawned in a savanna next to an ocean and got the advancement immediately without moving, just because deep ocean chunks (LAKE-tier surface tendrils, large spouts visible from spawn) were within their render distance. Also reproduced from a stony_shore spawn near a deep ocean. Root cause: `ChunkWatchEvent.Watch` fires for every chunk inside the player's render distance — 4225 chunks at render distance 32 — and the handler then evaluated the **watched** chunk's biome, not the player's. So the predicate was semantically "is there an oil biome with oil anywhere in my render distance," not "have I gone to an oil biome." The description literally says "Find an oil biome" → finding requires arriving, not just looking. **The fix** — handler swapped from `ChunkWatchEvent.Watch` to `PlayerTickEvent.Post` in [BCEnergyWorldGen](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/BCEnergyWorldGen.java). New flow: every 20 server ticks (once per second per player, well above the chunk-transition rate even at sprint speed) check the player's current chunk — if its biome is in the rich/excessive tier per `OilGenerator.isOilDesignBiomeAt` AND any chunk in the 3×3 neighbourhood around the player rolled oil per `wouldGenerateOilForOriginChunk`, award the advancement. The 3×3 neighbourhood preserves the user-friendly "you don't have to stand exactly on the oil block" feel, and crucially covers the small-rich-biome-patch case the user flagged: a 1-chunk deep ocean or desert spawning in vanilla worldgen still grants the advancement if the player steps onto it and any of the surrounding chunks rolled oil (rich biomes have ≈1% per-chunk roll probability at 1.5× bonus, so a 3×3 around a player in dense rich biome fires within ~10 throttled checks ≈ 10 seconds). Neighbourhood scan uses the biome-agnostic predicate intentionally — once we know the player's chunk is a rich biome, any rolled oil nearby is valid evidence ("I'm in the oil biome and there IS oil here"); we don't gate neighbour chunks on tier because oil that spills from a rich origin into an adjacent non-rich chunk is still meaningful evidence. Server-only via `ServerPlayer` instanceof check, since `PlayerTickEvent` fires on both sides. ServerLevel obtained via `player.level() instanceof ServerLevel` (this version of MC dropped `ServerPlayer.serverLevel()`). **New helper** — [OilGenerator.isOilDesignBiomeAt(Level, int, int)](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/generation/OilGenerator.java) wraps the existing private `sampleBiomeForChunkRoll` + `isOilDesignBiome(Identifier)` pair so the handler doesn't reach into chunk-RNG plumbing directly. **Predicates retained** — `wouldGenerateOilForOriginChunkInOilBiome` is no longer called from the handler but kept for diagnostic use; the corresponding game test still exercises its negative behaviour in the test arena. Test count unchanged (89, all green) — biome-tier classification logic (the heart of the new handler's gating) is the same as before, so `testFineRichesBiomeTierGate` still covers it. End-to-end verification still requires a live client: spawn in a non-oil biome adjacent to a rich biome and confirm the advancement does NOT fire until you actually walk into the rich biome.
- "Fine riches" no longer false-fires when crossing small light-tier (shallow ocean) biome patches. **The bug** — observed when a player walking over a ~2.5-chunk patch of cold_ocean nestled inside a taiga got the advancement immediately, with no visible oil in the cold ocean. Root cause: the surface "tendril" for MEDIUM rolls is placed at y=62 with `lakeRadius=2` (a 4-block-diameter oil pool). In a shallow ocean the water surface is y=63, so the entire tendril sits inside the water column — easy to swim right past without noticing. Meanwhile the underground sphere is at y=`minY+25..34` (≈ y=-39..-30 in modern overworld), and the spout extends only 6-12 blocks up from there (defaults `smallSpoutMinHeight=6, smallSpoutMaxHeight=12`), ending around y=-33..-18 — still ~80 blocks below the seafloor. So a MEDIUM roll in shallow water = invisible tendril + buried sphere + buried spout = the advancement promises "Find an oil biome" but the player sees no oil anywhere. With light tier's 1.25× bonus, P(any oil per cold_ocean chunk) ≈ 0.175%; a 3-chunk patch has ≈ 0.5% chance of any chunk rolling, so it eventually catches an unlucky player. **The fix** — [OilGenerator.isOilDesignBiome](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/generation/OilGenerator.java) no longer counts `surfaceDepositBiomes` (the light tier — default: ocean / warm_ocean / lukewarm_ocean / cold_ocean / frozen_ocean) as oil-design biomes for the advancement's purpose. Only `richSurfaceDepositBiomes` (defaults: deep oceans, deserts, badlands variants) and `forceExcessiveOilBiomes` (admin opt-in) trigger fine_riches. Worldgen behaviour is unchanged — shallow oceans still get 1.25× oil generation, still produce extractable oil for pumping (so `black_gold` / `oil_platform` / `draining_the_world` still grant normally if the player finds and pumps the hidden oil), they just don't grant the discovery advancement. Rich-tier biomes avoid the visibility issue because (a) deep oceans have a much deeper seafloor so the y=62 surface pool is reachable by swimming down from the surface and (b) deserts/badlands are terrestrial so the y=62 tendril sits at or near ground level and is unambiguously visible. Trade-off: players spawned in worlds with only shallow oceans (no deep oceans, no deserts, no badlands within travel range) can't get fine_riches even though oil does generate around them. Accepted because (a) such worlds are uncommon and (b) the alternative — granting the advancement for invisible oil — is worse UX than granting nothing. **Test updated** — [testFineRichesBiomeTierGate](src/test/java/buildcraft/energy/AdvancementTester.java) gains a third assertion block: every default light-tier biome (`ocean`, `warm_ocean`, `lukewarm_ocean`, `cold_ocean`, `frozen_ocean`) is asserted NOT to be an oil-design biome. Failure message names the specific regression that re-adding light tier would reintroduce. Rich-tier positives (desert, badlands, deep_ocean) still asserted positive. Test count unchanged (89, still all green) since the change is to an existing test rather than a new one.
- "Fine riches" no longer false-fires in unrelated biomes at large render distances. **The bug** — reported when a real player got the advancement at spawn in a forest biome (no oceans/deserts/badlands visible from flying up in creative) within ~2 minutes at render distance 32. Root cause: [OilGenerator.getStructures](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/generation/OilGenerator.java) only uses biome tier for the bonus multiplier and LAKE-eligibility — LARGE and MEDIUM rolls happen in **every** biome at the base 1.0× rate (largeOilGenProb=0.04%, mediumOilGenProb=0.1% → P(any oil rolled per chunk) ≈ 0.14% in a non-oil biome). Render distance 32 loads (2·32+1)² = 4225 chunks → expected positive rolls ≈ 6 per spawn, making the advancement effectively guaranteed within a couple minutes regardless of biome. The chunk-watch handler asked "did this chunk roll oil?" when the description ("Find an oil biome") promises "did the player find a biome designed for oil?" Two very different questions. **The fix** — added [OilGenerator.isOilDesignBiome(Identifier)](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/generation/OilGenerator.java) returning true iff the biome ID is in `richSurfaceDepositBiomes` (1.5× bonus, LAKE-eligible — defaults: deep oceans + deserts + badlands), `surfaceDepositBiomes` (1.25× bonus — defaults: shallow oceans), or `forceExcessiveOilBiomes` (debug 30× tier). Added [wouldGenerateOilForOriginChunkInOilBiome](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/generation/OilGenerator.java) as a stricter sibling of `wouldGenerateOilForOriginChunk` that gates the RNG roll behind the biome-tier check. The handler in [BCEnergyWorldGen.onChunkWatch](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/BCEnergyWorldGen.java) now calls the stricter predicate. Biome lookup uses the same chunk-RNG-derived sample point as `getStructures` (extracted into a `sampleBiomeForChunkRoll` helper) so chunks straddling a biome border don't get one biome here and another at roll time; biome lookup runs twice (once for the tier check, once inside `getStructures`) — accepted for simplicity since both are cheap HashSet lookups and chunk-watch fires only a handful of times per second per player. The original `wouldGenerateOilForOriginChunk` predicate is retained for diagnostic/general use; only the advancement path needs the stricter variant. Trade-off: a player walking through 100 desert chunks where the RNG never rolls oil still won't get the advancement; matches the user-chosen "find a designed oil biome with oil actually in it" semantic (not just "stood in a desert"). End-to-end: player enters desert chunk → biome-tier gate passes → per-chunk RNG roll evaluated → if non-empty, advancement fires. **New test** — [testFineRichesBiomeTierGate](src/test/java/buildcraft/energy/AdvancementTester.java) directly exercises `isOilDesignBiome` against fixed biome IDs (catches the bug case directly, unlike the predicate-negative test which only exercised the level-veto path because the game-test arena is flat). Positive assertions for default rich/light tier members (desert, badlands, deep_ocean, ocean); negative assertions for the biomes a real player would actually spawn in (plains, forest, taiga, snowy_taiga, snowy_plains). Test count 88 → 89; existing advancement tests still pass. Pre-existing predicate-negative test updated to call the new stricter predicate.
- Game-test coverage for the two new oil advancements + fixed a latent false-positive bug in the `fine_riches` handler that the test design surfaced. **The bug:** [BCEnergyWorldGen.onChunkWatch](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/BCEnergyWorldGen.java) called `OilGenerator.getStructures(level, cx, cz)` directly, but `getStructures` only performs the biome-exclusion + per-chunk RNG roll — it does NOT short-circuit on flat worlds or excluded dimensions the way `OilGenerator.generateForChunk` does. In a flat world or an excluded dimension (the nether and the end by default), `generateForChunk` early-returns and places no oil, but `getStructures` keeps rolling its deterministic RNG and may still report non-empty for some chunks. Net effect: `fine_riches` could have been awarded in worlds where zero oil blocks actually exist — exactly the false-positive that the chunk-aware approach was supposed to eliminate. **Fix:** extracted two new public predicates on `OilGenerator` so the level-veto and the per-chunk roll are reusable from both `generateForChunk` and any external observer. `canGenerateOilIn(ServerLevel)` returns false for `FlatLevelSource` worlds and for dimensions in the exclude config (sharing one code path with `generateForChunk`, which now just calls it). `wouldGenerateOilForOriginChunk(ServerLevel, int, int)` is the composite the handler wants: `canGenerateOilIn && !getStructures(...).isEmpty()`. `onChunkWatch` rewrites to a single call to that, and the `OilGenStructure`/`List` imports come back out of `BCEnergyWorldGen`. The handler still only checks the watched chunk itself (not its 5-chunk neighbourhood) since neighbour chunks fire their own `ChunkWatchEvent.Watch` events as the player approaches. **The tests** — new [AdvancementTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/energy/AdvancementTester.java) registers 5 game tests in [BuildCraftGameTests](src/test/java/buildcraft/BuildCraftGameTests.java), each with a matching empty-arena `test_instance/<id>.json` under [src/test/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/test_instance/](src/test/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/test_instance/) (game tests in MC 26.1.x need both a registered TEST_FUNCTION and a test-instance manifest — registration alone silently skips, which is the "37→34" issue called out in BuildCraftGameTests' blueprint_replace comment). The 5 tests: (1) `advancement_fine_riches_loaded` and (2) `advancement_sticky_dipping_loaded` resolve `ServerAdvancementManager.get(Identifier)` against the expected IDs — catches JSON syntax errors, wrong codec shapes (the `location` criterion's `player → location_check → predicate` wrapping is fiddly enough that codec rejection just silently drops the advancement), and ID drift between code constants and JSON file paths. The sticky_dipping variant additionally asserts that at least one criterion's trigger is NOT `minecraft:impossible` — catches accidental regressions back to the broken stub state. (3) `advancement_oil_fluids_tag_contents` computes the expected oil block ID set from the live `BCEnergyFluids.ALL` registry (filter to `oil`/`oil_heavy`/`oil_dense`/`oil_distilled` × 3 heats = 12), pulls the actual contents of `#buildcraftunofficial:oil_fluids` via `registryAccess().lookupOrThrow(Registries.BLOCK).get(tagKey).orElseThrow().stream()`, and diffs both ways — reports missing and unexpected extras separately so a future "add `oil_sour` to BCEnergyFluids without updating the tag" regression points right at the gap. (4) `advancement_oil_fluids_tag_exclusivity` checks the negative case for every fluid that must not be in the tag: `oil_residue` (refinery byproduct, per spec), every `fuel_*` × 3 heats (15 total — refinery outputs), and `minecraft:water`/`minecraft:lava` (defence against someone overbroadening the tag with a vanilla-fluid `#minecraft:water` reference). (5) `advancement_fine_riches_predicate_negative` samples a 5×5 chunk grid around the test arena and asserts `wouldGenerateOilForOriginChunk` returns false everywhere — the game-test world's flat-source check (or excluded-biome check) gates the entire path, so positive rolls would mean the fix was reverted. End-to-end advancement firing for a real player isn't directly testable here because `GameTestHelper.makeMockPlayer()` returns an anonymous Player (not a `ServerPlayer`) and `AdvancementUtil.unlockAdvancement(Player, …)` short-circuits on the `instanceof ServerPlayer` guard ([GuiTester comment line 64-66](src/test/java/buildcraft/lib/test/gui/GuiTester.java) documents this constraint); the tests cover every link in the chain except the final player-tracker write, which must be verified manually in a live client. All 5 pass under `./gradlew runGameTestServer` (the one pre-existing `blockutil_break_respects_tool_tier` failure that already existed on this branch is unrelated to these changes).
- "Sticky dipping" advancement now actually obtainable, and fires for every oil variant (not just one fluid block). In 1.12.2 the criterion was `minecraft:enter_block` against the single `buildcraftenergy:fluid_block_oil_heat_0` block. The 26.1.x port had been stubbed to `minecraft:impossible` with `code_trigger` (placeholder for never-written Java) — the only way to get it was `/advancement grant`. There are 12 oil source blocks across 4 base variants (`oil`, `oil_heavy`, `oil_dense`, `oil_distilled`) × 3 heat tiers (cool, warm, hot — registered as `<base>`, `<base>_heat_1`, `<base>_heat_2`, see [BCEnergyFluids.FLUID_NAMES](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/BCEnergyFluids.java) and the `registerFluidVariant` loop), so a single-block criterion would have only fired on cool crude oil and missed the other 11. The simpler tempting fix is `minecraft:enter_block` with a `#tag` — but `EnterBlockTrigger.TriggerInstance.block` is `Optional<Holder<Block>>` (single block holder), not `Optional<HolderSet<Block>>`, so it cannot consume a tag; you'd need 12 separate criteria with a `requirements` OR array. Used `minecraft:location` instead, whose `LocationPredicate.block` is a full `BlockPredicate` whose `blocks` field IS `Optional<HolderSet<Block>>` and accepts `#tag` syntax directly. The trigger fires from `ServerPlayer.doTick()` every server tick so as soon as the player's foot block is in any oil source block the advancement is awarded within a tick — same effective behaviour as `enter_block` for this use case. New block tag at [data/buildcraftunofficial/tags/block/oil_fluids.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/tags/block/oil_fluids.json) lists the 12 oil source blocks. Tag explicitly excludes `oil_residue` (per-spec a separate refinery byproduct, not "oil" in the player-facing sense), all `fuel_*` variants (refinery outputs, also out of scope), and any vanilla fluids. The wrapped `player → [{"condition": "minecraft:location_check", "predicate": {"block": {...}}}]` form is the canonical codec output for `LocationCheck`; the more compact unwrapped EntityPredicate shorthand isn't always reliable across MC versions so we go with the verbose-but-stable form. Tag is `replace: false` so datapacks adding modded oils to it (e.g. third-party "thick oil" addons) automatically extend the advancement's match set without overriding the base 12 entries.
- "Fine riches" advancement now actually obtainable.
