The 1.12.2 version used `minecraft:location` against the dedicated `buildcraftenergy:oil_desert` / `buildcraftenergy:oil_ocean` biomes, but 26.1.x deleted those biomes in favour of a config-driven probability tier over existing vanilla biomes (deep oceans, deserts, badlands get a 1.5× rich-tier bonus; shallow oceans get 1.25×; see [BCEnergyConfig.richSurfaceDepositBiomes](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/BCEnergyConfig.java)). The port had reskinned the criterion to `minecraft:inventory_changed` on `buildcraftunofficial:glob_of_oil`, but the glob item has no recipe, loot table, or drop logic anywhere in the codebase — only the creative-tab entry — so the only ways to get the advancement were `/give` or creative mode. Fixed by switching to the same `minecraft:impossible` + `AdvancementUtil.unlockAdvancement` pattern the rest of the 26.1.x advancements use, with a new `ChunkWatchEvent.Watch` handler in [BCEnergyWorldGen](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/BCEnergyWorldGen.java) that replays `OilGenerator.getStructures(level, cx, cz)` for each chunk that enters the player's view distance and awards the advancement iff that chunk actually rolled oil generation. This is more accurate than a biome-only check (you'd otherwise get the advancement walking through a barren desert) and self-corrects with config: if a server admin adjusts the rich/light biome lists or oil probabilities, the advancement automatically tracks. Replaying the per-chunk RNG is cheap (a Random construction + biome lookup + a handful of set/double comparisons; the no-oil path returns `ImmutableList.of()` before any structure allocation), and `ChunkWatchEvent.Watch` fires once per chunk-becomes-visible-to-player rather than every tick, so no caching is needed. We only check the watched chunk itself (not its 5-chunk neighbourhood like `generateForChunk` does) because oil that spills in from a neighbouring origin chunk is still caught when that origin chunk later enters view as the player approaches. The handler shares `BCEnergyWorldGen`'s existing `init()` gate on `enableOilGeneration` so disabling oil gen also disables the advancement — no advancement without the thing it rewards. JSON criterion renamed to `code_trigger` to match `AdvancementUtil.unlockAdvancement`'s default criterion name.
- Ledger open/closed state now persists across GUI close/reopen and across MC restarts, matching 1.12.2 behaviour. The 26.1.x port carried over the [Ledger_Neptune](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/ledger/Ledger_Neptune.java) animation state but the underlying persistence pipeline had been stubbed to empty classes — [GuiConfigManager](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/config/GuiConfigManager.java), [GuiConfigSet](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/config/GuiConfigSet.java), `GuiProperty`, `GuiPropertyBoolean`, `GuiConfigEntry`, `GuiPropertyConstructor` were all one-line placeholders. Net effect: `initGuiElements` constructed fresh ledgers on every GUI open with `currentDifference = 0`, so opening the Help ledger on a Filler then closing and reopening the GUI snapped it back closed. `GuiBC8.init()`'s `copyAnimationStateFrom` path only covered the window-resize case (preserves in-flight animation across the re-`init` triggered by a font/scale change), not GUI close→reopen. Rebuilt the config layer minus the 1.12.2 `IExpressionNode` generic-over-types machinery (we only need booleans for ledger flags): new [GuiPropertyBoolean](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/config/GuiPropertyBoolean.java) carries a single named bool with a `set` that short-circuits no-op writes and otherwise calls `GuiConfigManager.markDirty()`; new [GuiConfigSet](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/config/GuiConfigSet.java) is a per-GUI `TreeMap<String, GuiPropertyBoolean>` (TreeMap keeps the persisted JSON sorted for stable diffs); rewritten [GuiConfigManager](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/config/GuiConfigManager.java) is the static facade — `init(Path)` binds a file and loads existing state, `getOrAddBoolean(guiId, name, default)` returns a live reference that survives GUI churn, `markDirty()` writes synchronously (ledger clicks are user-paced so the small JSON write completes well inside one frame; no need for the 1.12.2 `MessageUtil.doDelayedClient(10, …)` debounce). File lives at `<configdir>/buildcraft/gui_state.json` alongside the other BuildCraft per-mod files — separate from the `BCUnifiedConfig` NeoForge `ModConfigSpec` files (overkill for a couple of booleans, and `ModConfigSpec` doesn't grow keys at runtime which we need). [Ledger_Neptune](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/ledger/Ledger_Neptune.java) now resolves an `openProperty` in its constructor keyed by `(parentScreenClass, ledgerSimpleClassName + ".is_open")` — per-GUI per-ledger scoping mirrors 1.12.2's `(ResourceLocation, "name.is_open")` shape, so e.g. `LedgerHelp` on a Filler is independent of `LedgerHelp` on an Engine. Persisted-value apply is deferred from constructor to first `drawBackground` because subclass `appendText` calls land between `super(...)` and the first frame, and `calculateMaxSize()` needs the full content to know the right open-state dimensions; an `appliedInitialState` guard ensures it runs once. The first-frame apply *snaps* (sets `currentDifference = 1` and `currentWidth/Height = maxWidth/Height`) rather than animating from closed→open, so a restored ledger appears already-open from frame zero with no startup flicker. `copyAnimationStateFrom` sets the same guard to true so the window-resize path (which is the legitimate "in-flight animation is more accurate than the saved boolean" case) wins over the persisted-state apply for that one frame. `onMouseClicked` writes the new state through `openProperty.set(nowOpen)`. Lifecycle wired in [BCLibClient.initClient](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/BCLibClient.java): `GuiConfigManager.init(FMLPaths.CONFIGDIR.get().resolve("buildcraft/gui_state.json"))` runs once at mod construction, synchronously loading existing state so the first GUI open already sees restored values. Graceful degradation if `init` somehow doesn't fire — the manager works as a pure in-memory map with no disk IO, which also keeps unit tests and headless server contexts safe. Four-test round-trip cover in [GuiConfigManagerTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/config/GuiConfigManagerTester.java): set→file-contents-match→reset-memory→reload→value-restored; redundant `set(true)` after `set(true)` doesn't rewrite the file (mtime preserved); `getOrAddBoolean` without `init` works in-memory; malformed JSON on disk logs and falls back to defaults instead of crashing. The previous empty stub classes (`GuiProperty`, `GuiConfigEntry`, `GuiPropertyConstructor`) are deleted — the simplified design only needs three classes, and the 1.12.2 `IVariableNode` / `NodeTypes` plumbing would have to come back wholesale to make them useful again.
- Fluid pipe dye_replace, actually wire it up + remove the fallback that hid the regression. **Why it was broken:** the 25 `buildcraftunofficial:dye_replace` entries from commit 8697acb87 lived in `assets/buildcraftunofficial/atlases/blocks.json`, but `SpriteSourceList.load(rm, atlasId)` resolves atlas configs via `rm.getResourceStack(ATLAS_INFO_CONVERTER.idToFile(atlasId))` — a path-only rewrite that preserves the namespace, so for the vanilla `minecraft:blocks` atlas it looks at *exactly* `minecraft:atlases/blocks.json` and never fans out across namespaces. Atlas configs at `assets/<modid>/atlases/<name>.json` are loaded only when a same-namespaced atlas is registered via `RegisterTextureAtlasesEvent`, which nothing in this codebase does. So `DyeReplaceSpriteSource.run()` was never called (verified by temporary instrumentation: zero invocations across a clean boot, and the blocks atlas stayed at 1024×1024 instead of growing for the 400 generated sprites), and `PipeBaseModelGenStandard.ensureDyedSprites()` fell through to `null` on every call, routing every painted fluid pipe down the legacy mask-overlay path. Cosmetically close enough to the dyed-sprite path that the original "verified in-game" sign-off didn't catch the regression. **Fix part 1 — atlas relocation:** move all 25 `dye_replace` entries into `assets/minecraft/atlases/blocks.json` and delete the now-dead `assets/buildcraftunofficial/atlases/blocks.json`. After the move, `DyeReplaceSpriteSource.run()` fires 25 times at boot and the blocks atlas grows to 8192×4096 — both signals confirm the synthesised dyed sprites are actually on the atlas and the model code's atlas lookups now hit them. Cosmetic output is pixel-identical to before per the source algorithm's pre-existing python-equivalence (so painted pipes look the same in-world), but the path is no longer faking it. Also dropped the dead `robot/` directory source from the same atlas file (`assets/*/textures/robot/` doesn't exist anywhere; the real `block/robot.png` is covered by `block/engine/` / `block/pump/`'s siblings) and updated [DyeReplaceSpriteSource](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/sprite/DyeReplaceSpriteSource.java)'s javadoc-example file path to say `minecraft:` instead of `<ns>:` so the next reader doesn't repeat the namespace mistake. **Fix part 2 — kill the silent fallback:** the regression was undetectable for two days because [PipeBaseModelGenStandard.ensureDyedSprites](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/model/PipeBaseModelGenStandard.java) returned `null` on missing-sprite and three call sites all had `if (null) fall back to undyed/mask-overlay path` clauses. That made dye_replace's success/failure visually indistinguishable. `ensureDyedSprites` now throws `IllegalStateException` with a message naming the missing atlas id + the JSON-config check to perform, and all three call sites — the chunk cutout path ([line 411](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/model/PipeBaseModelGenStandard.java:411)), the chunk overlay path ([line 547](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/model/PipeBaseModelGenStandard.java:547)), and the item-form rendering path ([PipeItemModel line 129](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/model/PipeItemModel.java:129)) — no longer carry fallback branches. Painted fluid pipes now have exactly one rendering path: dyed sprite from the atlas, or hard failure with a log line pointing at the broken config. Non-fluid pipes (item/power/RF) keep their base+overlay path unchanged — that's their primary rendering, not a fallback. The `@Nullable` annotation comes off `ensureDyedSprites`; cache size and behaviour are unchanged.
- Fix `./gradlew runClient` failing at `:downloadAssets` with `Cannot find a Java installation … matching: {languageVersion=21, …}. Toolchain download repositories have not been configured.` on a machine that only has JDK 25 installed. The moddev plugin runs the project's compile and runtime tasks on the project toolchain (Java 25, matching what NeoForge 26.1.2's `fancymodloader` and `neoform` artifacts are built for and demand at consumption), but its NFRT-side tooling tasks (`downloadAssets`, `prepareClientRun`, and friends) are built against Java 21 and request a JDK 21 toolchain independently. Without a JDK 21 install and with no toolchain download repository configured, that request had nowhere to land. Resolved by applying the [Foojay toolchain resolver](https://github.com/gradle/foojay-toolchains) plugin (`org.gradle.toolchains.foojay-resolver-convention` 1.0.0 — 0.10.x is incompatible with Gradle 9 because it references the removed `JvmVendorSpec.IBM_SEMERU` constant) in [settings.gradle](settings.gradle), which lets Gradle auto-provision Eclipse Temurin 21 into `~/.gradle/jdks/` on first build. The project's `JavaLanguageVersion.of(25)` in [build.gradle](build.gradle) is untouched — Java 25 stays the only JDK contributors install manually. Updated [README.md](README.md) (compile/setup instructions, now linking to Microsoft OpenJDK 25 per the NeoForge team's recommendation) and [CLAUDE.md](CLAUDE.md) (project overview) to call out the dual-toolchain setup explicitly so future contributors don't trip on the same error.
- Fix desynced cycling in the JEI Facade recipe display. Two compounding issues: (1) `FacadeStateManager.validFacadeStates` is keyed by `BlockState`, so multi-state blocks (a furnace has 8) contribute many `FacadeBlockStateInfo` entries sharing the same `requiredStack`, and [AssemblyRecipeCollector.collectFacade](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/compat/jei/AssemblyRecipeCollector.java) further doubled each block to pair against basic+hollow facade outputs. JEI's `CycleTicker` is shared per recipe layout but each slot picks `list.get(index % list.size())`, so length mismatches (e.g. when the `NormalizedTypedItemStack` cache collapses adjacent count-1 dupes) drift the slots apart. (2) Per-slot focus matching: when JEI is opened via "see uses" on a specific block, focus narrows the input slot to the matched index only — but the unlinked output slot keeps cycling through every facade, producing pairings like "leaves → emerald-ore facade". The collector now dedups by `ItemStackKey` and emits two JEI entries (`facadeRecipes:basic` and `facadeRecipes:hollow`) with equal-length, duplicate-free lists, and [AssemblyTableCategory.setRecipe](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/compat/jei/AssemblyTableCategory.java) calls JEI's `createFocusLink(blockSlot, outputSlot)` so a focus on one side pins the other to the same index (the JEI planks→stairs example in `createFocusLink`'s javadoc is the exact pattern). A new `focusLinkInputIndex` field on [AssemblyRecipeJei](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/compat/jei/AssemblyRecipeJei.java) carries the slot index per entry (`1` for facades, `-1` for standard recipes that don't need linking).
- Fix a TOC hover bug where the tooltip for a right-page entry would surface while the user mouses over the left page (and vice versa) at the same y-offset. `GuidePart.renderLine` already pages its hit-test rects on the current page's `x` (not the entry's true page) on purpose — click handling reuses the same rects via `pageRenderIndex=-1` and filters at the caller with `pos.page == index` — but `renderTooltip()` was being called inside `renderLine` whenever `entryHovered` was set, with no equivalent filter. So an entry on the right page would still register a phantom hover at the left page's column and emit its tooltip. Gated the tooltip emission on `didRender` (drew at least one segment on this pass), which is the same signal `GuideText.renderIntoArea` already uses for the line-level tooltip path.
- Fix a 2-px dead strip in TOC entry hit-testing that broke the highlight as the cursor crossed between the icon and the text. The visual highlight is filled from `_x − 20` (when an icon is present) to `_x + width + 2`, but the hit-test rects were narrower: icon rect `[_x − 18, _x − 2]` (the 16-px sprite bounds) and text rect `[_x, _x + width]`. The 2-px gap between `_x − 2` and `_x` sat inside the highlighted region but in neither hit rect — entering it dropped `entryHovered` to false and broke the highlight mid-traverse. Both rects in [GuidePart.renderLine](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/parts/GuidePart.java) now match the fill bounds: icon hit rect spans `[_x − 20, _x]` (20 wide, still drawn as 16×16 at `iconX`) and each wrap-segment rect spans `[_x − 2, _x + width + 2]` (`_w + 4` wide). The two overlap by 2 px at `[_x − 2, _x]` so there is no longer any pixel inside the highlight that falls outside the hit area.
- Pipe Wires guide entry, recipes, title override. (1) The shared wire writeup in [item/wire.md](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide/en_us/item/wire.md) was registered against the white wire stack, so the TOC icon and title both read "White Pipe Wire" — and white blends into the book background so the entry is easy to skim past. The entry now uses the orange wire stack as its icon (high-contrast against the page) and overrides the page title to "Pipe Wires", positioning it as the family overview rather than a per-colour leaf. A new `Available Colours` chapter at the end of the page lists all 16 wire colours as clickable item-link rows; colours other than orange resolve to the auto-synthesised recipe stand-in (recipes + usages) since they aren't registered as their own entries. (2) Title-override plumbing in [PageValue.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/entry/PageValue.java) + [PageEntry.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/guide/entry/PageEntry.java): a new 3-arg `PageValue` constructor takes a nullable title override, defaulting to `type.getTitle(value)` when null so existing callers are unchanged. The JSON `PageEntry` constructor now reads `title` / `title_raw` from the entry JSON via a new `PageValue.getTitleOverride(json)` helper (extracted from the existing `getTitle(json)` "untitled" fallback) and threads it through — `PageEntryItemStack` entries can now opt into a custom display name without subclassing or modifying the item's `getHoverName`. The existing `PageEntryExternal` path is byte-for-byte equivalent (same `title` field source, same `localized || raw` fallback chain). (3) [guide.txt](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/compat/buildcraft/guide.txt) drops the `item_stack` alias for the wire entry in favour of a raw `add` block so it can include the new `title` field (`pipe_wires`) alongside the stack swap; the matching localisation key `buildcraft.guide.page.pipe_wires` ("Pipe Wires") goes in [en_us.json](src/main/resources/assets/buildcraftunofficial/lang/en_us.json). (4) 16 wire assembly-table recipes in [BCSiliconRecipes.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/BCSiliconRecipes.java), mirroring 1.12.2's `dyeRed + dustRedstone + ingotIron → 8 wires @ 5,000 MJ` recipe per colour — 1.12.2 only registered four (RED/BLUE/GREEN/YELLOW); we register all 16 since every modern wire colour ships as a real item. `DyeItem.byColor(colour)` maps each `DyeColor` to its vanilla dye. With the recipes registered, the `<recipes>` tag at the end of the wire page now renders the orange wire's recipe instead of being empty.
- Destruction lasers, mine-not-destroy across machines — every BuildCraft machine that breaks blocks (Mining Well, Quarry, Builder destruction phase, Filler destruction phase, Stripes pipe) now harvests-via-loot-table rather than silently destroying, and spawns the XP somewhere a player can actually collect it. Central plumbing: new [BlockUtil.BreakResult](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/BlockUtil.java) record carrying `List<ItemStack> drops` + `int xp` returned by a new sibling helper `breakBlockAndGetDropsWithXp`. The XP is captured (not auto-spawned) so each machine can re-anchor the orb at its own block — avoids the duplication concerns of a "spawn at brokenPos then teleport to machine" approach, since the orb is only ever created at one location. `ITileForSnapshotBuilder` gets two new defaultable hooks: `getBreakingTool()` (default diamond) and `onBlockBroken(brokenPos, drops, xp)` (default no-op). `SnapshotBuilder.tick()` now routes through both hooks so Builder and Filler can apply per-tile policy without that file knowing about either tile type. **Per-machine tier + routing:** **Mining Well** — iron tier, drops via the existing `addToBestAcceptor` (adjacent inv → pipe → drop), XP at well. **Quarry** — diamond tier (rig chews through obsidian / ancient debris), drops via the same `addToBestAcceptor` the rig already used for mining, XP at quarry block. **Builder destruction** — iron tier (matches the `mining_well` ingredient transitively nested in the Builder recipe), drops inserted into the Builder's `invResources` via the same transactor pipes use; overflow spills at the broken position; XP at the Builder block. **Filler destruction** — iron tier (same nested-ingredient reasoning), drops inserted into adjacent non-pipe inventories with explicit `IPipeHolder` skip so BuildCraft pipes don't siphon (matches the user-spec "non-pipe inventory block"); overflow drops at the broken position; XP at the Filler block. **Stripes pipe** — diamond tier (unchanged), drops continue down the pipe via `sendItem`, XP at the broken-block position (the pipe is transient and there's no "machine" the orb should follow — the player is typically standing where the break happened). **`NEEDS_DIAMOND_TOOL` fallback**: under iron tier (Builder/Filler), obsidian / ancient debris / netherite-family blocks destroy as before without yielding drops or XP via a `BlockUtil` tier gate — `state.requiresCorrectToolForDrops() && !tool.isCorrectToolForDrops(state)` short-circuits drops to empty and XP to 0 while still destroying the block. The gate lives in `BlockUtil` (not in the loot table) because vanilla ore/stone loot tables only carry `match_tool` for silk_touch and fortune branches — they don't encode the tier check — and calling `Block.getDrops` directly bypasses the player-path tier check at `Block.dropFromBlock` (`Player.hasCorrectToolForDrops`), so the gate has to be re-applied in BlockUtil for machines to honour their declared tier. **Fluid-source capture for the Builder**: `BreakResult` also carries a `capturedFluid` field populated when the broken block is a `LiquidBlock` source (1000 mB of the source type; flowing fluid is explicitly NOT captured because it's transient state, not a bucket-worth — would otherwise let CLEAR mode generate water out of nothing on a leaky boundary). `TileBuilder.onBlockBroken` absorbs the captured fluid into its existing four 8-bucket tanks via `tankManager.insert(...)` *only when* `getFluidMode() == CLEAR` (NO_REPLACE never fires this path; REPLACE handles fluids in the place phase, not the break path, so the defensive guard is for forward-compat). Tank-full overflow is silently lost rather than spilled back at brokenPos — spilling would recreate exactly the source CLEAR was meant to remove, and the tanks are generous enough (32 buckets total) that "full" means the player needs to plumb an output pipe. Other tiles (Filler/Quarry/Mining Well/Stripes) ignore the captured fluid — Filler has no tanks, Quarry/Well don't have schematic-fluid use-cases, Stripes is single-block. Tests added: [testBreakBlockAndGetDropsWithXpCapturesFluidSource](src/test/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/FluidHandlingModeTester.java) (water source → 1000 mB Water) and `testBreakBlockAndGetDropsWithXpSkipsFlowingFluidCapture` (flowing water → empty fluid). XP coverage: [testBreakBlockAndGetDropsWithXpReportsXp](src/test/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/FluidHandlingModeTester.java) covers the helper's XP branch end-to-end on iron ore.
- Mining Well, tool-tier fixes — two coordinated changes in [TileMiningWell.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/tile/TileMiningWell.java) and [BlockUtil.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/misc/BlockUtil.java). (1) **Loot context regression**: `BlockUtil.breakBlockAndGetDrops` was calling `Block.getDrops(state, level, pos, blockEntity)` — the 4-arg overload, which builds a `LootContext` with `TOOL = ItemStack.EMPTY`. Two coupled symptoms: (a) every `match_tool` branch that reads an enchantment off TOOL (silk_touch on stone/ores, fortune's `apply_bonus` on ore drop counts) silently took its no-enchantment fallback — a wielded silk-touch pickaxe couldn't preserve iron ore as the block, and fortune III dropped 1 raw_iron instead of 1–4; (b) vanilla's tier check at `Block.dropFromBlock` (`Player.hasCorrectToolForDrops` → empty drops + 0 XP) was bypassed AND not re-implemented locally, so every machine effectively had no tier enforcement at all — iron-tier Builder/Filler would happily yield obsidian / ancient debris drops, contradicting the per-machine `getBreakingTool()` design. Two-part fix: (i) rewired to the 6-arg `Block.getDrops(state, level, pos, blockEntity, entity, tool)` overload so the wielded tool feeds the loot context (silk_touch / fortune now resolve correctly), and (ii) added an `if (state.requiresCorrectToolForDrops() && !tool.isCorrectToolForDrops(state))` short-circuit in BlockUtil that returns empty drops + 0 XP while still destroying the block. Together these match 1.12.2's fake-player `canHarvestBlock` + `harvestBlock` pipeline — vanilla ore loot tables don't encode the tier check (only silk_touch / fortune branches), so the gate had to be re-applied around the loot-table call. (2) **Mining Well capability nerf**: the well wielded a `Items.DIAMOND_PICKAXE` at runtime despite the recipe asking for an iron pickaxe, so a freshly-crafted well would happily chew through obsidian and ancient debris. Tool ItemStack is now `Items.IRON_PICKAXE` matching the recipe ingredient, and `canBreak()` short-circuits to `false` for any block in `BlockTags.NEEDS_DIAMOND_TOOL` (obsidian, ancient debris, crying obsidian, respawn anchor, netherite-family blocks) — `nextPos()` then falls into its existing "impassable, stop" branch, mirroring how the well already stops at lava and oil. Without this `canBreak` veto the BlockUtil tier gate would still catch the under-tier break (empty drops + 0 XP, block destroyed), but the well would have drilled through obsidian and ancient debris yielding nothing — worse than stopping. Two regression tests added to [FluidHandlingModeTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/builders/snapshot/FluidHandlingModeTester.java): `testBreakBlockAndGetDropsHonoursToolForLoot` (iron pickaxe on iron ore must drop raw iron) and `testBreakBlockAndGetDropsRespectsToolTier` (wooden pickaxe on iron ore must drop nothing). Same BlockUtil fix improves drops for the Quarry / Builder-CLEAR / Stripes paths transparently — they still wield diamond pickaxes so their effective tier is unchanged. (3) **XP drops restored**: 1.12.2 spawned ore XP through the fake-player `harvestBlock` pipeline; the modern `Block.getDrops` path doesn't, so redstone/lapis/diamond/emerald/coal/copper/iron ore breaks under the well were silently dropping zero XP. Now the well snapshots `state.getExpDrop(level, pos, blockEntity, null, tool)` BEFORE the BlockUtil call (the helper destroys the block as a side effect, so the state and BE need to be captured ahead) and after a successful break calls `state.getBlock().popExperience(serverLevel, worldPosition, xp)` — note `worldPosition` (the well), not `currentPos` (the broken block). This avoids the "spawn at A, teleport to B" failure modes (orb captured by a tick boundary between the two operations, item-frame entity duplication, etc.) by simply never creating the orb at the broken position in the first place. `ExperienceOrb.award` (called from `popExperience`) splits the integer XP into appropriately-sized orbs at one location, respects the `BLOCK_DROPS` gamerule and the `restoringBlockSnapshots` flag, and the entity passes through the well block (no collision) so the player can pick it up from where they placed the machine. XP is only restored for the Mining Well in this patch per user request; Quarry / Builder-CLEAR / Stripes pipe XP is a follow-up.
- Gears, cross-mod tag interop — publish `c:gears/wooden`, `c:gears/stone`, `c:gears/iron`, `c:gears/gold`, `c:gears/diamond` Common item tags ([data/c/tags/item/gears/](src/main/resources/data/c/tags/item/gears/)) and rewrite each gear recipe's previous-tier slot to consume the tag instead of the exact resource id ([gear_stone.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/gear_stone.json), [gear_iron.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/gear_iron.json), [gear_gold.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/gear_gold.json), [gear_diamond.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/gear_diamond.json)). Prior recipes hard-coded `buildcraftunofficial:gear_wood` / `_stone` / `_iron` / `_gold` in the inner-core slot, so gears from Mekanism, Immersive Engineering, Thermal etc. couldn't substitute despite sitting at the same conceptual tier — carry-over from 1.12.2 oreDict (`gearWood`, `gearStone`, …) which on Forge of that era was a forge-wide registry but on modern NeoForge has been replaced by the `c:` Common tag namespace. Tag-driven recipes are the canonical migration. **Stone-gear ingredient parity with the furnace**: stone gear's outer ingredient moves from `#c:cobblestones/normal` → `#minecraft:stone_crafting_materials`, the same vanilla tag the furnace itself consumes (cobblestone, blackstone, cobbled deepslate — three entries, exactly). Deepslate-only bases no longer have to detour to the surface for a stone gear, and Nether-only starts can now feed blackstone into the same recipe — the principle being "if you can craft a furnace from it, you can craft a stone gear from it." Mossy / infested cobble are deliberately not included since the vanilla tag itself omits them. Iron, gold, and diamond outer ingredients already used the right Common tag (`#c:ingots/iron`, `#c:ingots/gold`, `#c:gems/diamond`), unchanged. Wood gear left strict to `#c:rods/wooden` — entry-tier should stay cheap and avoid accepting blaze rods.
- Builder + Filler, crafting recipes — add the missing shaped recipes for both blocks ([builder.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/builder.json), [filler.json](src/main/resources/data/buildcraftunofficial/recipe/filler.json)); neither legacy 1.12.2 recipe had been ported, so up to now you had to `/give` both. **Filler**: legacy shape (dyes border, gold gears at the bottom corners, chest bottom-middle, volume marker top-middle) with a **Mining Well** in the center replacing the crafting-table — the Mining Well represents the break-blocks engine the Filler actually drives. **Builder**: top row is **Pump** / volume marker / **Flood Gate** (fluid clear + fluid place), middle row is **diamond gear** / **Chute** / **diamond gear** (item-routing buffer + diamond-tier mechanical-arm gating that matches Architect/Quarry; Chute replaces the legacy plain chest so the Builder centre evokes "items get fed in and routed" rather than passive storage, and transitively consumes a wooden chest through the Chute recipe), bottom row is **Tank** / **blank blueprint** / **Filler** — the Filler ingredient transitively pulls in a Mining Well (so the Builder still requires "break" capability through its sub-ingredients rather than directly), and the Tank in the bottom-left fills what would otherwise be empty while thematically pairing with the Pump/Flood Gate fluid handling in the top row. Recipe is intentionally asymmetric in the bottom row to signal the Builder is the higher-tier composite of the Filler.
- Help ledgers, parity sweep — restore the left-side `LedgerHelp` tab on every machine GUI that had one in 1.12.2. Background: 1.12.2 attached a help ledger automatically via `GuiBC8.standardLedgerInit()` (opt-out only); the 26.1.x port kept the [LedgerHelp](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/ledger/LedgerHelp.java) + [ElementHelpInfo](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/help/ElementHelpInfo.java) + [DummyHelpElement](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/gui/help/DummyHelpElement.java) infrastructure but switched to opt-in per screen, so ledgers were missing on ten ported GUIs and empty/partial on three more. Newly added/completed: **Chute** ([GuiChute](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/gui/GuiChute.java)) — one region covering the 4-slot T-buffer at (62,18); **Tank** ([GuiTank](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/gui/GuiTank.java)) — reuses the existing `buildcraft.help.tank.generic` body with a new `tankGeneric` title; **Diamond Pipe** ([GuiDiamondPipe](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/gui/GuiDiamondPipe.java)) — single 9×6 filter-grid region; **Diamond Wood Pipe** ([GuiDiamondWoodPipe](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/gui/GuiDiamondWoodPipe.java)) — filter row + 3-button mode strip; **Emzuli Pipe** ([GuiEmzuliPipe](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/gui/GuiEmzuliPipe.java)) — 4 filter slots + 4 paint buttons iterated via constant position tables; **Assembly Table** ([GuiAssemblyTable](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/gui/GuiAssemblyTable.java)) — input grid (8,36, 3×4), recipe-state grid (116,36, 3×4), and the existing `RECT_PROGRESS` gauge, coexisting with the right-side `LedgerTablePower`; **Integration Table** ([GuiIntegrationTable](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/gui/GuiIntegrationTable.java)) — 3×3 input grid at (19,24) with 25px pitch, display+output combined block at (101,36)→(154,66), progress bar at (164,22); **Zone Planner** ([GuiZonePlanner](src/main/java/buildcraft/robotics/client/gui/GuiZonePlanner.java)) — single map-viewport region as a placeholder until the renderer is ported; **Gate** ([GuiGate](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/gui/GuiGate.java)) — fills the previously-empty ledger with five region types looped over `horizontalSlotCount × verticalSlotCount` (trigger column, trigger params, connector column, action column, action params) sized off the same `slotPairStart` / `slotPairWidth` / `numTriggerArgs` / `numActionArgs` runtime values the slot layout uses; **Filler Planner** ([GuiFillerPlanner](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/gui/GuiFillerPlanner.java)) — adds pattern slot (32×32) and parameter strip (72×18) help regions sharing the new `buildcraft.help.filler.pattern.*` / `.params.*` keys with the Filler. Documented opt-outs: **Auto Craft Items** ([GuiAutoCraftItems](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/gui/GuiAutoCraftItems.java)) and **Advanced Crafting Table** ([GuiAdvancedCraftingTable](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/gui/GuiAdvancedCraftingTable.java)) keep their 1.12.2 opt-out (vanilla recipe book slides out leftward from the GUI and would clash with a left-anchored ledger) — added inline comments above `initGuiElements()` so the absence is documented intent, not an oversight. Tier-A screens (Builder, Architect Table, Electronic Library, Replacer, Filler, Stone Engine, Iron Engine, RF Engine, MJ Dynamo, List item, Filtered Buffer) were already at parity from earlier ports and were not touched. **Programming Table** remains the one outstanding 1.12.2 GUI with no 26.1.x port at all — help-ledger work is gated on the screen port. Twenty-six new `buildcraft.help.*` translation keys added under the existing JSON conventions (`.title`, `.desc` or `.desc1` / `.desc2` for multi-line bodies). All ledgers register via `mainGui.shownElements.add(new LedgerHelp(mainGui, false))` (left side) and coexist with the right-side `LedgerOwnership` / `LedgerTablePower` / `LedgerEngine` that other screens already use — no positional conflicts because the `expandPositive` boolean keeps the two families on opposite edges.
- Silicon gates, item-model rendering — fix two regressions against the 1.12.2 reference. (a) **Top/bottom-face UVs were wrong.** When [PlugGateBaker.bakeForItem](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/model/plug/PlugGateBaker.java) was ported, the geometry was pre-rotated from 1.12.2's WEST-mounted orientation (thin X, wide Y+Z) to NORTH-facing (thin Z, wide X+Y) so the gate face would point at the camera without needing a runtime rotation, but `makeGateItemUVs` only got two branches — front/back at the 6×6 face region and *everything else* at the 2×6 WEST/EAST strip. The UP/DOWN faces of the rotated box are 6×2 (X-wide, Z-thin), and `ModelUtil.createFace` maps `U←X, V←−Z` on the top face, so the 2×6 strip ended up oriented 90° to where the material's grain should run — most visible on nether-brick variants where the brick courses run sideways across the top edge. Added a third UV branch keyed on `face.getAxis() == Y` returning `[5/16, 2/16] → [11/16, 4/16]`. (b) **Items rendered at 1.8× in every display context.** [GateItemModel](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/model/GateItemModel.java)'s cache loader applied `scalef(1.8f)` around the model centre unconditionally and `update()` ignored `ItemDisplayContext`, so dropped entities / first-person hand / third-person hand / item frame / head all rendered at the showcase scale that was originally only intended for the inventory cell — gates on the ground looked roughly the size of the player's head. Rewritten to cache by `record CacheKey(GateVariant variant, ItemDisplayContext context)` and replicate 1.12.2's `ModelItemSimple.TRANSFORM_PLUG_AS_ITEM_BIGGER` (= `TRANSFORM_PLUG_AS_ITEM` with each context's scale × 1.8) via a static `EnumMap<ItemDisplayContext, ContextXform>`: GUI/HEAD keep `scale 1.8` with no rotation (the front-facing inventory look the user explicitly wanted preserved), GROUND drops to `scale 0.9` with `+3/16` Y translation, FIXED is `1.53` (item frame), FIRST_PERSON hands tilt `Y=±45°` at `0.72` and translate `−4/16` on Z, THIRD_PERSON hands tilt `X=75° Y=±45°/±225°` at `0.675` and translate `+2.5/16` on Y. The transform pipeline pivots to centre (`translatef(-0.5, …)`), rotates, scales, pivots back, then applies the world-space translation; `setCalculatedNormal()` runs after so the (now-rotated) normal is correct for any shading path that reads it. GUI rotation is identity instead of 1.12.2's `Y=90°` because our base geometry is already NORTH-facing — the 1.12.2 90° was bringing a WEST-mounted face around to the camera, which our pre-rotation already does. Cache size is bounded at `25 variants × 9 ItemDisplayContext values = 225` entries with the same `expireAfterAccess(1 min)` policy as before. `appendModelIdentityElement(displayContext)` is added so the render state's identity hash differentiates contexts and the correct cache entry is picked up. **Same fix applied to** [LensItemModel](src/main/java/buildcraft/silicon/client/model/LensItemModel.java) — it had the identical "1.8× around centre everywhere" pattern (lenses and filters looked huge when dropped or in-hand for the same reason gates did), now uses the same `ContextXform` EnumMap + `CacheKey(LensKey, ItemDisplayContext)` pattern. The pre-existing WEST -> NORTH face rotation that runs once per quad before the display transform is kept inside `transformForItem` — that's geometry pre-rotation (the baker emits WEST-mounted lens geometry), not a per-context op, so it sits ahead of the per-context pivot/rotate/scale/pivot/translate pipeline. Cutout (frame, white vertex colours via `toBakedItem`) and translucent (coloured glass overlay via `toBakedTranslucent`) batches both go through the same transform; the `resetColors` parameter still gates whether vertex colours get nuked to white afterward, so the dye tint set by `bakeTranslucentQuads` survives on the translucent batch as before. Lens cache size is bounded at `~32 lens keys × 9 contexts ≈ 288` entries.
- Drop the `@OnlyIn(Dist.CLIENT)` annotations from the new `DyeReplaceSpriteSource` (added in the dye-synthesis landing below). Modern NeoForge no longer strips members marked with `@OnlyIn` and logs a one-off "the runtime member-stripping behaviour of this annotation is no longer present" warning at mod-load time when it sees the annotation. The class is already effectively client-side via its imports (`NativeImage`, `SpriteContents`, `SpriteSource`, the LazyLoadedImage/sprite-loader plumbing) and the registration site (`BCLibClient.initClient` is a client-only entry point), so the annotations weren't load-bearing — they were copy-pasted off vanilla's `PalettedPermutations` template. Removing them silences the warning without changing behaviour.
- Pipe paint, two follow-ups while the dyed-texture path was in flight. (a) **Translucent overlay was effectively invisible** for non-fluid pipes: alpha was being multiplied twice — once in `generateTranslucentMutable` via `multColouri(0xFF, 0xFF, 0xFF, 76)` on the mask-sprite quads, and again by [`PipeBlockColourHandler.PIPE_COLOUR_TINT`](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/PipeBlockColourHandler.java) returning `(OVERLAY_ALPHA << 24) | RGB`. Net result was `76 × 76 / 255 ≈ 22` (≈9% alpha) instead of the intended 76 (≈30%). Fixed by having the `BlockTintSource` contribute colour only (alpha=255); the 1.12.2 model had the texture's own alpha as the final alpha, and the mask path's `multColouri(76)` now mirrors that — the fallback path on `overlay_stained.png` (alpha=76 baked in) works the same way through the tint without a second alpha contribution. (b) **Paint changes didn't propagate to clients until the chunk re-baked for another reason** (e.g. painting an adjacent pipe a different colour, world reload, F3+A). [`Pipe.setColour`](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/Pipe.java) only called `markForUpdate()`, which queues a connections recompute — the `scheduleNetworkUpdate` path inside that recompute is gated on "connections actually changed" (a deliberate optimisation from the gate-toggle FPS-spike fix), so the colour-only case skipped the BE sync entirely. Added a `holder.scheduleRenderUpdate()` call right after the colour assignment: on the server it sets the `sendBlockUpdated` flag for the next tick, on the client it does the immediate `requestModelDataUpdate` + `sendBlockUpdated(UPDATE_CLIENTS)`. The pattern matches what [PipeFlowFluids.setFluid](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/flow/PipeFlowFluids.java) explicitly references as "paint... [has its] own scheduleRenderUpdate calls".
- Fluid pipe dyeing: stop shipping the 400 pre-baked `*_dyed_<colour>.png` files. A new [DyeReplaceSpriteSource](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/sprite/DyeReplaceSpriteSource.java) (registered as `buildcraftunofficial:dye_replace` via `RegisterSpriteSourcesEvent`) synthesises all 16 dyed variants of each fluid-pipe base sprite at atlas stitch time. The algorithm mirrors the historical `tools/generate_dyed_pipes.py` exactly — replace waterproofing-green pixels (`#24451B ± 3`) inside `mask_shared_fluid`'s opaque region with each `DyeColor`'s `ColourUtil.getLightHex` value, preserving source alpha — so the stitched atlas is pixel-identical to before. Atlas memory is unchanged (still 16 variants per family), but the mod jar drops the 400 PNGs that used to live in `textures/pipes/`. Twenty-five `dye_replace` entries in `atlases/blocks.json` cover every fluid pipe base + colourblind variant (`andesite_fluid`, `clay_fluid`, `cobblestone_fluid`, all six `diamond_fluid_<dir>` + `diamond_fluid_west_cb` + `diamond_fluid` + `diamond_fluid_itemstack`, `diamond_wood_fluid_clear`/`_filled`, `diorite_fluid`, `gold_fluid`, `granite_fluid`, `iron_fluid_clear`/`_filled`, `quartz_fluid`, `sandstone_fluid`, `stone_fluid`, `void_fluid`, `wood_fluid_clear`/`_filled`). The chunk render path, mask lookup, and `ensureDyedSprites()` plumbing in `PipeBaseModelGenStandard` are all unchanged — the source's outputs land at the same atlas names (`<base>_dyed_<colour>`) the model code already resolves. Once the synthesised path was confirmed working in-game (paint applies, colours match the pre-deletion baseline), the 400 PNG files were removed from `textures/pipes/` via `git rm` — the on-disk savings are realised, `SpriteSource.Output.add` is last-writer-wins so the directory source's loads are never executed for these names anyway.
- Filler: add status LEDs on all four horizontal faces (front + back + both sides, pump-style placement). 1.12.2 shipped two LED textures for the filler (`led_green.png`, `led_red.png`) but never wired them up in code — the renderer only drew the marker box, and the block model only declared `facing`. Position math interrogated with PIL against the 1.12.2 PNGs: green pixel at `(u=6, v=2)` and red at `(u=4, v=2)` — translating through the default cube-model NORTH-face UV convention these land at `sideOffset = 1.5/16` and `3.5/16` respectively, `Y = 13.5/16`. **These are pixel-identical to the pump's LED offsets** (the 1.12.2 art team placed both blocks' LEDs at the same physical spot, just hand-drawn into different overlay textures for each); the new BER reuses those constants verbatim. State semantics are power-based with a deliberate loop-vs-one-shot tell, driven by `(controlMode, hasPower, isFinished)`: **OFF** mode → both dark (filler manually disabled); **no power** (mode ≠ OFF + battery empty) → red lit full, green dark; **running one-shot** (mode = ON + powered + not finished) → green lit full, red dark; **running looping** (mode = LOOP + powered) → green <em>half-lit</em> (`COLOUR_GREEN_HALF = 0xFF_3F_77_3F`, roughly half each ABGR channel of `COLOUR_GREEN_ON 0xFF_77_DD_77`), red dark — the at-a-glance "this filler will run forever" indicator that lets the player tell a one-shot from a looping filler without opening the GUI; **finished** (mode = ON + powered + finished) → both lit full (only reachable in ON mode because `TileFiller.isFinished()` short-circuits to `mode != LOOP && finished`). New [RenderFiller](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/client/render/RenderFiller.java) replaces the previous no-op stub class. `TileFiller.setControlMode` now calls `setChanged() + level.sendBlockUpdated()` — the existing periodic sync inside `tick()` is gated on `mode != OFF && !isFinished()`, so transitions *into* OFF (or LOOP→ON-finished) would otherwise leave the client stuck on the pre-transition LED pattern until the next chunk reload; the explicit push fixes that. New `TileFiller.hasPower()` accessor matches the quarry's API surface (`battery.getStored() > 0`). The `COLOUR_GREEN_HALF` constant is kept local to `RenderFiller` for now — first user of "dim green", lift to `LedRenderUtil` if another block needs it.
- Architect Table LEDs, follow-up — expand the binary valid/invalid model into four states by reading the snapshot-in/out slot occupancy in addition to {@code getIsValid()}. The previous landing only distinguished "valid box" (green) from "invalid box" (red), which left the most operationally interesting state — *the architect is actively writing a blueprint right now* — visually identical to *the architect has nothing to do*. Updated state table in [RenderArchitectTable](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/client/render/RenderArchitectTable.java): (a) **Invalid** = marker box missing/malformed → red lit, green dark; (b) **Idle** = valid box, both slots empty → green lit, red dark; (c) **Scanning** = valid + input present + output empty (the same condition `TileArchitectTable.tick` at line 178 uses to gate the actual scan loop) → both lit at full intensity; (d) **Done** = valid + output occupied (a finished blueprint is waiting for the player) → green lit, red half-lit at a new `COLOUR_RED_HALF = 0xFF_11_11_77` (roughly half each ABGR channel of the full `COLOUR_RED_ON`). Order of checks puts `hasOutput` before `hasInput` so the transient state where both slots briefly hold items lands on Done rather than Scanning — matches the tick gate's "output must be empty to scan" rule. Required one server-side sync fix: `TileArchitectTable.writeSnapshot` was calling `setChanged()` on scan completion without a corresponding `level.sendBlockUpdated`, which meant the slot-change wouldn't propagate to clients except via chunk reload or GUI open — added the block-update push so the LED transitions live as the snapshot pops into the output slot. The constant is kept inline in `RenderArchitectTable` rather than hoisted into `LedRenderUtil` because "half-lit" is currently an architect-specific semantic; if another block needs it later it can be lifted.
- Architect Table: modernise the front-face LED indicator from baked-texture to live BER. The 1.12.2 architect had a hand-drawn LED indicator baked into two front-face variants — `front_on.png` (green LED lit, "valid marker box neighbour") and `front_off.png` (red LED lit, "invalid"), swapped via a `PROP_VALID` blockstate property on `block/architect/architect_on.json` / `architect_off.json`. The 26.1.x port carried over both files but they ended up pixel-identical (the LED graphic was lost during the texture migration), so the property toggled between two indistinguishable models — a no-op visually. New [RenderArchitectTable](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/client/render/RenderArchitectTable.java) BER renders two `RenderPartCube`s on the front face at the exact pixel positions where the 1.12.2 `led_green.png` (u=5, v=12 — texture coords interrogated empirically with PIL since the assets shipped without documentation) and `led_red.png` (u=3, v=12) overlay textures would have landed, translated to block-local coordinates via the default cube-model UV convention (texture u=N → world x = (16-N)/16 on the north face; texture v=N → world y = (16-N)/16 on every side face). That works out to green at `sideOffset = +2.5/16, Y = 3.5/16` and red at `sideOffset = +4.5/16, Y = 3.5/16` — same Y as the mining well's LEDs, both LEDs sitting low on the face (centre at 3.5 px from the bottom) and offset right-of-centre. Reads `TileArchitectTable.getIsValid()` for state — green lit and red dark when the architect has a valid marker box neighbour, swapped when not. Sync is unchanged — `isValid` was already written to NBT in `saveAdditional` and pushed via `level.sendBlockUpdated` in `onPlacedBy`, so dropping `PROP_VALID` (the blockstate property + setValue call + state def entry) removed a redundant sync channel without breaking the client-side view. Routes through `BCLibRenderTypes.led()` so it inherits the depth-correct opaque pipeline. The two duplicate `front_on.png` / `front_off.png` textures collapse into a single `front.png`; the unused `led_green.png` / `led_red.png` overlay textures and the two model-variant JSONs (`architect_on.json` + `architect_off.json` → single `architect.json`) are deleted. Blockstate JSON drops the 8-variant `facing × valid` matrix down to a 4-variant `facing`-only matrix. Item model parent updated to the unified path.
- Asset cleanup, vestigial LED textures: deleted twelve unreferenced `led_*.png` files left over from the 1.12.2 → 26.1.x port. Architect's `led_green.png` / `led_red.png` were the seed (covered above); a wider grep across the resources tree (`grep -r led_green\\|led_red --include='*.java' --include='*.json' src/main/`) for any code or model reference came back empty for: `block/fillerBlock/led_green.png` + `led_red.png` (filler never shipped LEDs — even in 1.12.2 the model only declared `facing`, no `valid`-style swap); `block/led_green_off.png` + `led_green_on.png` + `led_red_0_3.png` through `led_red_3_3.png` (six top-level generic LED textures that look like an early shared-asset pattern that was superseded by per-block subdirectory variants and never wired up in the port); `block/mining_well/led_green.png` + `led_red.png` and `block/pump/led_green.png` + `led_red.png` (these *were* meant to texture the mining-well/pump LEDs in the 1.12.2 BER, but the modern port switched to procedural vertex colour on the `buildcraft:led` render type, so the textures became dead weight). All twelve files now removed. Note: `textures/block/fillerBlock/` still contains `front.png` and `side.png` from the same orphan directory, also unreferenced (the actual filler model points at `block/filler/front.png` and `block/filler/side.png`) — left in place for a wider unused-resource sweep alongside the previously-noted `block.png` / `slot.png` / `ledger.png` / `generic_one_slot.png` / etc.
- LED rendering, follow-up — fix depth-ordering between adjacent LEDs. The initial untextured-pipeline switch landed on vanilla's `RenderPipelines.DEBUG_FILLED_BOX`, which inherits `DEBUG_FILLED_SNIPPET`'s `DepthStencilState(LESS_THAN_OR_EQUAL, false)` — depth test on, but **depth write OFF**. That's correct for vanilla's debug-overlay use cases (you want gizmos visible through themselves), but wrong for opaque indicator LEDs: with write disabled, the second LED in a batch always paints over the first regardless of which is actually nearer the camera, so at grazing angles a mining-well viewed from the side would show the green status LED in front of the red power LED even when geometry says the red should occlude it. Fix is to define our own pipeline ([BCLibRenderTypes#LED_PIPELINE](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/render/BCLibRenderTypes.java)) that inherits everything from `DEBUG_FILLED_SNIPPET` (shaders `core/position_color`, `POSITION_COLOR` vertex format, `TRANSLUCENT` blend, `QUADS` mode, cull on, MATRICES_PROJECTION uniforms) but overrides `withDepthStencilState(DepthStencilState.DEFAULT)` — same `LESS_THAN_OR_EQUAL` test but with `writeDepth=true`. Registered on the mod event bus via `RegisterRenderPipelinesEvent` in [BCLibClient#initClient](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/BCLibClient.java) before any `RenderType` querying it is dispatched. The wrapping `RenderType` (still named `buildcraft:led`) and the `VIEW_OFFSET_Z_LAYERING` are unchanged — the layering still helps the LED-against-block-face seam at far view distance, and depth-write handles the LED-vs-LED case the layering alone couldn't. The pipeline reuses vanilla's existing `core/position_color` shader pair (no new shader asset on disk needed; NeoForge's pipeline registrar wires up everything from the snippet inheritance). Side effect: the `TRANSLUCENT` blend mode is now slightly more meaningful — if a future LED ever wants alpha < 0xFF it would still need explicit back-to-front sorting because translucent + depth-write is the classic "transparent stuff hides what's behind it" foot-gun — but our current LEDs are all opaque (alpha=0xFF) so blending degenerates to "replace pixel" and the depth-ordering fix is unambiguously correct.
- LED rendering overhaul: stop drawing the pump/mining-well/quarry status LEDs as tinted snow-texture quads through the cutout block atlas, and start drawing them as pure vertex-coloured quads through their own untextured render type. The old path locked every LED vertex's UV to a hand-picked solid-white pixel on the vanilla snow sprite and submitted to `Sheets.cutoutBlockSheet()` so the textured-block shader would multiply white × vertex colour and arrive at the desired LED colour — a 1.12.2-era workaround for there being no easy "just give me a coloured quad" path. With 1.21's RenderPipelines API this is now trivial: new [BCLibRenderTypes](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/render/BCLibRenderTypes.java)`#led()` wraps vanilla's `RenderPipelines.DEBUG_FILLED_BOX` (shaders `core/position_color`, vertex format `DefaultVertexFormat.POSITION_COLOR` — three position floats plus packed RGBA, no UV, no UV2, no normal, no overlay) under a project-owned RenderType name `buildcraft:led`. The pipeline's `VIEW_OFFSET_Z_LAYERING` shifts emitted geometry a sub-pixel toward the camera in clip space so LEDs sitting flush against a block face never z-fight with it at distance — a pure win over the previous setup which relied solely on the LED's 0.1-pixel mechanical protrusion to stay visible. Side effects of the switch: (a) **LEDs are now fully unlit**, i.e. their colour does not modulate with surrounding block light or sky light any more — this is the intended behaviour for indicator LEDs (real LEDs emit, they don't reflect), and means a status LED reads as identically bright in a sunlit field and a cave; (b) the per-frame `LightLayer.BLOCK` / `LightLayer.SKY` brightness reads from the adjacent block are gone from all three BERs (cheap, but pointless work given the pipeline ignores lightmap input); (c) the block atlas is no longer touched at all by LED rendering — removes a fragile dependency on `minecraft:block/snow` continuing to exist as a solid-white pixel in its top-left corner; (d) at far view distance the LEDs no longer pick up mipmap blurring from neighbouring atlas pixels (no texture = no mipmaps). One extra draw call per LED-bearing machine in view (LEDs no longer batch into the same buffer as the surrounding cutout blocks — they ride in their own `buildcraft:led` batch instead); at ~8 LEDs per pump and ~6 per quarry this is invisible in any profile. **Shared code factored out** from the three BERs ([RenderPump](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/render/RenderPump.java), [RenderMiningWell](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/render/RenderMiningWell.java), [RenderQuarry](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/client/render/RenderQuarry.java)) into a new [LedRenderUtil](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/render/tile/LedRenderUtil.java): the three identical colour constants (`COLOUR_OFF` near-black `0xFF_1f_10_1b`, `COLOUR_GREEN_ON` light green `0xFF_77_DD_77`, `COLOUR_RED_ON` vivid red `0xFF_22_22_DD`) and the eleven-line per-face position math that every BER was hand-rolling in its own static initialiser — now expressed as a single `setFacePosition(led, face, insetBlocks, sideOffset, y)` call. The pump's 16-step red→yellow battery gradient and the mining well's slightly-different gradient (`0xB0` step + `0x4F` floor instead of `0xE0` step + `0x1F` floor — both ABGR red ramps but with subtly different dynamic range) are left inline in their respective BERs because they're block-specific tuning, not shared infrastructure. Position math is mathematically identical to the prior inline math (verified across all four face directions for both pump and quarry). [RenderPartCube](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/render/tile/RenderPartCube.java) is also simplified: the `setWhiteTex()` atlas-pinning hack is deleted, and the per-face emit loop is rewritten to call `consumer.addVertex(pose, x, y, z).setColor(r, g, b, a)` per vertex with no normal / UV / UV2 / overlay writes — matching exactly what vanilla's `DrawableGizmoPrimitives.renderQuads` does for its own debug-filled-box gizmos. The class is now strictly "small vertex-coloured cube primitive" with no atlas coupling, which is what it was effectively trying to be all along.
- Quarry: render two state-driven LEDs on three of the four horizontal faces (front + the two sides) — the rear face is intentionally blank because that's where most players run cabling or back the quarry into a wall, so an LED there is wasted screen real estate. New BER [RenderQuarry](src/main/java/buildcraft/builders/client/render/RenderQuarry.java) borrows its LED-positioning math from [RenderPump](src/main/java/buildcraft/factory/client/render/RenderPump.java) — same `RenderPartCube` size, same per-face `Y = 13.5/16` height, same per-LED side offsets (1.5/16 and 3.5/16 from the face corner) — but the colour semantics are quarry-specific rather than mirroring the pump's "battery fill % gradient + on/off status pair." A `BlockState` lookup at `level.getBlockState(pos)` reads the `HorizontalDirectionalBlock.FACING` property (the quarry's block class is `BlockQuarry extends HorizontalDirectionalBlock` with `getStateForPlacement` setting FACING to `context.getHorizontalDirection().getOpposite()`, i.e. the direction the front face points toward the player who placed it); the BER's per-face loop skips the iteration where `dir == FACING.getOpposite()`, which is the rear face in world coordinates regardless of which way the quarry was placed. The `hasProperty(FACING)` guard handles the one-frame transient where `level.getBlockState(pos)` could lag behind a placement/removal and not yet have the property attached. **LED state machine** is driven by two new boolean accessors on `TileQuarry` — `hasPower()` (`battery.getStored() > 0`) and `isMining()` (`currentTask != null`); both rely on data already synced to the client via `saveAdditional` → `getUpdateTag`, so no extra sync work. The BER composes them into per-LED on/off flags: `greenOn = hasPower || !hasTask`, `redOn = !hasPower || !hasTask`. The four combinations of (hasPower, hasTask) land in three visual states the user actually cares about: **Green only** when actively mining (has power + has work, i.e. the quarry is running normally — `TaskBreakBlock` / `TaskAddFrame` / `TaskMoveDrill` is in flight); **Red only** when the quarry has work to do but the battery's empty (red signals the player to wire power up); **Both Red+Green** when there's no current task — which covers both "mining complete, all chunks in the bounding box exhausted" and "fresh placement, frame not yet surveyed", treating them identically so the LED is a "no work in progress" indicator rather than a literal "finished" sentinel. The fourth combination (no power, no task) collapses into the same dual-lit state since "can't work AND nothing to do" reads visually the same as "done." Colour constants are ABGR in the same byte order as `RenderPump.COLOUR_STATUS_ON` (the pump's "light green" `0xFF_77_DD_77` is `alpha=0xFF, blue=0x77, green=0xDD, red=0x77` — Minecraft's vertex pipeline expects that byte order because it matches little-endian native ordering on x86); the quarry's red is the mirror `0xFF_77_77_DD` (red component now in the low byte at 0xDD), giving the two LEDs visually-matched saturation, and the off state reuses the pump's near-black `0xFF_1f_10_1b`. Block-light boost (15) applied per-LED whenever that LED is lit, so the LEDs visibly glow at night when on and stay flush with ambient when off. Registered via `event.registerBlockEntityRenderer(BCBuildersBlockEntities.QUARRY.get(), RenderQuarry::new)` in `BCBuildersClient.registerRenderers`. The pre-existing `BCBuildersEventDist`-driven `RenderLevelStageEvent` path for frame/drill lasers and the moving rig is untouched — that path is the right one for *world-space* geometry that crosses block boundaries, and the BER is the right one for *block-local* decoration; they coexist cleanly. No new textures (`RenderPartCube.setWhiteTex()` uses `minecraft:block/snow` as a solid white sprite and lets vertex colour do the work, identical to the pump) and no JSON model changes. `RenderQuarry` was previously a one-method stub created during the port — the comment explaining why BERs weren't used for the lasers stays accurate (LEDs aren't world-space) and the class now does real work instead of just classloading.
- Fluid pipes, second round of perf work (no functional changes — the visible regime is identical, just cheaper). **Z-fight at the centre-vs-face boundary** ([PipeFlowRendererFluids](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/render/PipeFlowRendererFluids.java)): every face-section cuboid and the centre cuboid meet on a shared plane (x=0.74 for the EAST section, etc.); both cuboids were emitting a quad at that plane with the same UV and colour, and because the fluid render type (`RenderTypes.entityCutout` / `entityTranslucent`) renders with culling disabled, the GPU rasterised both at the same depth and the result shimmered whenever the two cuboids' fill ratios diverged — most visibly during a mid-pipeline break when fluid amounts redistribute. The fix threads a `skipFaceMask` through `renderFluidCuboid` → `emitFace`; face-section cuboids now suppress their *inward* face whenever the centre is also rendering, and the vertical-pillar cuboid suppresses its joining face (top for gas, bottom for liquid) when the horizontal centre cuboid was rendered alongside it. Each shared plane ends up covered by exactly one quad, vertex count per fluid pipe drops by up to ~17%, and the seam where centre meets face / pillar meets centre is now visually clean across all fill ratios. **`Section.tickClient` rewritten with primitive offset state** ([PipeFlowFluids.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/flow/PipeFlowFluids.java)): the prior implementation stored `offsetLast`/`offsetThis` as `Vec3` fields, which made `tickClient` allocate ~17 `Vec3` per CENTER tick (six face-direction adds in each of the two loops, one `Math.signum` `Vec3`, the scale+add pair, two wrap adds) plus ~3 per face section tick. Replaced with six `double` fields (`offsetLastX/Y/Z`, `offsetThisX/Y/Z`) and a primitive math rewrite that produces zero allocations — the sign-of-sum centre direction is computed component-by-component, the face-axis offset is `offsetLast + face.getStepN() * delta`, and the [-0.5, 0.5] wrap is three independent signum branches. `writeOffsetsForRender` reads the new primitives directly so the renderer side picks up the saving for free; default values (0) are correct before `tickClient` runs the first time, replacing the previous `offsetLast != null && offsetThis != null` null-check. `Vec3` and `VecUtil` imports drop out of the file. **Engine model bake cache** ([BCEnergyModels.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/energy/BCEnergyModels.java)): the JSON variable model rebakes from scratch every frame per engine — for `engine_iron` that's ~22 `MutableQuad` instances (each carrying 4 pre-allocated `MutableVertex`) plus the `ArrayList` and result array, all allocated per engine per frame. With ~3 MB/s of GC churn just from the bake at typical viewing counts, this was the next-biggest fluid-adjacent allocation source after the renderer wins above. Added a per-engine-type cache keyed by `(stage, progress quantised to 1/16, facing)` — 5 × 17 × 6 = 510 entry slots, lazily populated as states are observed. Progress is quantised to 1/16 because the model's `progress_size = progress * 15.99` expression has 1-pixel resolution at that step, so the cached animation is visually identical to the unquantised one. Cache invalidation rides on `ModelHolderVariable.getModel()` reference equality — `onTextureStitchPre` nulls the holder's `rawModel` and `loadModelFromDisk` reassigns a fresh `JsonVariableModel` instance, so any resource-pack swap or atlas restitch produces a new reference and the lookup wipes the cache automatically on the next call. The cached `MutableQuad[]` is shared across all engines of the same type and state; `RenderEngine_BC8` mutates `colour` (via `setCalculatedDiffuse`) and `lighti` on each emitted quad, but both are overwritten deterministically every render before the vertex consumer reads, so sharing is safe.
- **Fluid pipes: the actual cause of the "lag spike per pipe-transit" bug** — every call to `PipeFlowFluids.setFluid(...)` was scheduling a full BlockEntity NBT sync via `pipe.getHolder().scheduleRenderUpdate()`, which on the client (`TilePipeHolder.onDataPacket`) re-invokes `level.sendBlockUpdated()` and **marks the pipe's chunk section dirty, forcing a chunk-mesh rebuild**. That's an entire 16×16×16 section re-meshed every time a pipe transitions empty↔non-empty. In normal flow this happens at the head and tail of the flow path (no big deal), but when a downstream sink is at capacity — e.g. a combustion engine with a full fuel tank — fluid bounces against the full sink and oscillates between adjacent pipe sections. Each oscillation cycle is two empty↔non-empty transitions × every pipe in the path, so the chunk rebuilds compound very quickly (the user's repro: distiller feeding gas to a combustion engine whose tank was full, gas visibly bouncing between the engine and the upstream tank, frame-time spikes locked to fluid movement). The `setFluid` call was scheduling the chunk-rebuild specifically to get the new fluid type to the client, but the lightweight `MessagePipePayload` (`NET_FLUID_AMOUNTS`) registered for fluid flow already covers that: `writePayload` writes the fluid registry id whenever `currentFluid` is non-empty, and the per-section amount loop fires whenever `section.amount` differs from `lastSentAmount` — which is exactly the condition that pairs with `setFluid` (empty → non-empty fires when a section receives fluid in `Section.insert/fill`; non-empty → empty fires when `totalFluid` drops to 0 in `onTick`). The pipe's *block model* doesn't depend on fluid state — pipe connections / paint colour / pluggables drive the model, and those have their own `scheduleRenderUpdate` calls — so the chunk-rebuild was pure waste in the fluid path. Initial state sync on chunk load is unaffected: `writeToNbt` still writes `fluid_id` so the full NBT path picks up the fluid type when a new client starts tracking the chunk. Net effect: bouncing-against-full no longer rebuilds chunk meshes, the spike goes away. The earlier per-frame renderer optimisations from the same investigation remain in place (they're still wins, but they were tackling the *symptom* — high allocation rate during fluid transit — rather than the *cause*).
- Engines: two latent perf bugs in the shared engine renderer that compounded the fluid-pipe issue, especially noticeable when a combustion engine is actively burning fuel (the engine model bakes every frame; under load the per-engine cost was visible at any fuel type, but more pronounced when the engine was at higher power stages where the trunk/piston are animating fast). **Removed the per-engine `bufferSource.endBatch()` full flush** in [RenderEngine_BC8](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/render/tile/RenderEngine_BC8.java) — the previous code called the no-argument `endBatch()` which walks every registered `RenderType` in `MultiBufferSource.BufferSource` and drains its builder. With multiple engines visible (typical pump-room scene: combustion engine + several creative or stirling engines), this forced N full-pool flushes per frame and turned what should be a single batched draw call into a stream of separate uploads + GPU syncs. The `BlockEntityRenderDispatcher` calls `endBatch` on the shared buffer source at the natural end of all BE rendering anyway, so the per-engine call was both redundant and harmful — quads written to the cutout block buffer simply get drained at the correct time. **Made `MutableQuad.setCalculatedDiffuse` allocation-free** in [MutableQuad.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/model/MutableQuad.java) — the prior implementation routed through `getCalculatedNormal()` which allocated 7 `Vector3f` per call (four from `MutableVertex.positionvf()` constructors plus three explicit `new Vector3f(...)`), and the engine renderer's loop calls it on every emitted quad. Now the edge vectors and cross product are computed inline as `float` primitives and the result is fed straight into `diffuseLight(x, y, z)`. Visual output identical (same diffuse value, same per-vertex colour set). Every quad-emitting renderer in the project picks up the saving — pipe wires, plug renderers, the builders ghost preview, the laser table, fluid pipes — but engines benefit the most because their bake produces 22 face-quads per engine per frame and each one went through `setCalculatedDiffuse` in the render loop.
- Fluid pipes: kill the per-frame allocation storm in the fluid flow renderer that was producing constant high frametimes (in the order of 40-70 ms per frame at 19 FPS on the test setup — a distiller feeding a combustion engine with fuel + water both in transit) and visible "flickering" between adjacent pipes as the GC pauses fell across renders out of phase with each other. Three layered fixes, all isolated to fluid pipe rendering plus one shared lib helper used by every renderer in the project. **Sprite/tint cache** ([PipeFlowFluids.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/pipe/flow/PipeFlowFluids.java), [PipeFlowRendererFluids.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/transport/client/render/PipeFlowRendererFluids.java)) — the previous renderer rebuilt the still-texture `Identifier`, RGBA tint colour, and translucent-vs-cutout flag every frame for every fluid pipe in view, which under fuel transit (fuel has 3 heat-state Fluid singletons per variant, each with its own sprite path) was three string-built `Identifier.parse`/`fromNamespaceAndPath` allocations + a `FluidStateModelSet` registry lookup + a try-catch'd dispatch per pipe per frame. The eight render-only fields (`renderCacheFluid`, `renderCacheSpriteId`, `renderCacheTint{R,G,B,A}`, `renderCacheTranslucent`) live on the flow as `transient`, populated only when the `Fluid` singleton reference differs from the cached one; the atlas sprite itself is still looked up per frame via `atlas.getSprite(cachedId)` so atlas reloads (resource pack swaps, F3+T) self-heal without an explicit listener. Field types are shared-side classes (`Fluid`, `Identifier`) so the dedicated server build still compiles and never touches the fields. **Scratch-buffer interpolation** — the old `getAmountsForRender(float)` allocated a `double[7]` per call and `getOffsetsForRender(float)` allocated a `Vec3[7]` plus three transient `Vec3` per section (two `Vec3.scale` + one `Vec3.add` = 21 short-lived `Vec3` per call); both are now `writeAmountsForRender(float, double[])` and `writeOffsetsForRender(float, double[], double[], double[])` taking caller-supplied scratch, with `ThreadLocal<double[]>` storage on the renderer reused across every pipe in the render pass. **Direct vertex emit** (the big one) — the inner `renderFluidCuboid` triple loop was the single largest allocator. Per face-cell pair it allocated: one `AABB` (`uvBox`), one `Vector3f` per centre and per radius (×2), and one `MutableQuad` via `ModelUtil.createFace`, which internally allocates the 4-element `Vector3f[]` from `getPointsForFace`, four `Vector3f` from `getPoints`'s `new Vector3f(centerFace)` initialisers, and four more from `addOrNegate(faceRadius, …)` — call it ~13 `Vector3f` plus 1 `MutableQuad` per face per cell. Then `MutableQuad.render` allocated another 2 `Vector3f` per vertex × 4 vertices = 8 more `Vector3f` for the pose-transform scratch. With ~7 cuboids per pipe × ~6 face-cells per cuboid × (~21 Vector3f + 1 MutableQuad + 1 AABB) the per-pipe-per-frame allocations were in the high hundreds, and at 60 fps × ~30 visible pipes the resulting ~1.5 MB/s pure `Vector3f` churn was producing G1 evacuation pauses landing right inside the render thread. The new `renderFluidCuboid` carries geometry as primitive `double`s (no `Vec3`, no `AABB`, no `UvFaceData`), emits vertices directly to the `VertexConsumer` via a per-face dispatch table (no `MutableQuad`), and uses `ThreadLocal<Vector3f>` scratch for the pose-transform pair (no per-vertex allocations). The per-face dispatch table is the hand-traced equivalent of `ModelUtil.createFace` after inlining `getPointsForFace` → `getPoints` → `addOrNegate` for each of the 6 face directions; for each face the table picks the correct cuboid corner positions for vertices 0..3 and pairs each with the right UV corner so the back-face winding stays identical to the old path. The UV mapping switch in `renderFluidCuboid` mirrors `ModelUtil.mapBoxToUvs` directly. **Shared lib helper:** `MutableQuad.renderVertex` ([MutableQuad.java](src/main/java/buildcraft/lib/client/model/MutableQuad.java)) now uses two `ThreadLocal<Vector3f>` scratches instead of allocating per vertex — fluid pipes don't go through that path anymore but every other quad-emitting renderer in the project does (pipe wires, item flow render, plug renderers, builders ghost preview, the laser table, …), so the win is shared. **Regression coverage:** [PipeFlowRendererFluidsGeometryTester](src/test/java/buildcraft/transport/client/render/PipeFlowRendererFluidsGeometryTester.java) drives `emitFace` for all 6 facings on a unit cube against a recording `VertexConsumer`, asserting position and UV for each of the 4 emitted vertices match the hand-traced expected values (themselves derived by walking `ModelUtil.createFace`'s 0..3 vertex assignment under both invert and non-invert paths) — guards against silently regressing the back-face winding or the per-face UV mapping in any future refactor. Plus a separate test verifies the normal vector matches the face step vector for all 6 facings, so lighting and culling stay correct.
- Pump: tighten the "infinite water source" detection so the verdict is per-position under vanilla's own regen rule instead of a once-per-BFS global flag tripped by any qualifying block somewhere in the explored volume. The pre-fix `buildQueue0` walked the flood-fill, and the first block it found with `count >= 2` (orthogonal-or-up source neighbours via `SEARCH_NORMAL`) plus a water-or-solid block below set `isInfiniteWaterSource = true` and broke out of `outer`; the cached flag was then the sole gate on whether `mine()` called `BlockUtil.drainBlock(level, currentPos, true)` to actually remove the source. The pathological case is a horizontal 1×3 strip `[S1][S2][S3]` resting on stone: only the centre `S2` would regenerate after a vanilla bucket scoop (it has S1 and S3 as horizontal source neighbours), but the pre-fix BFS hit `S2` at iteration two with `count = 2` and flipped the global, so a pump positioned over either edge preserved every block of the strip forever rather than consuming all three for three buckets total. New behaviour: a static helper `TilePump.isInfiniteSourceAt(Level, BlockPos)` evaluates the vanilla rule at a single position — `>=2` horizontally-adjacent source-water neighbours via `Direction.Plane.HORIZONTAL` (deliberately not UP/DOWN — a source above does not seed a regenerated source below; water just flows down through air) plus a non-air supporting block below via the existing `getFluidWithFlowing(below) == WATER || below.isSolid()` predicate (water below is kept as valid support to recognise "1×3 strip floating on a deeper pool" as infinite at its centre). `buildQueue0` precomputes `targetPosIsInfinite = isWater && isInfiniteSourceAt(level, targetPos)` once at the top — the anchor block is the tube's landing position, set in `buildQueue` by walking down from the pump until the first non-empty/non-tube block — and only short-circuits the BFS when that one-shot check is true; if it's false (e.g. tube over the edge of a 1×N strip), the BFS now fully explores the connected source volume so the finite tail blocks actually land in `queue` and get consumed instead of being silently skipped past by the early-exit. The inner `count` variable is dropped entirely since the BFS no longer makes its own infinite verdict. The consumption gate in `mine()` re-evaluates the helper against `targetPos` each drain rather than reading the cached flag, so any state change since the queue was built — player scooped a neighbour with a bucket, mob placed a block in the strip, vanilla flow redistributed sources — flips the pump back to consume mode on the very next tick instead of having to wait for a queue rebuild that may never come (a pump's queue rebuilds on drain-attempt failure or config bump, neither of which fires while the pump is happily sitting on a "preserved" infinite source). The class field `isInfiniteWaterSource` is kept but now reflects the latest drain's verdict rather than a sticky once-set BFS flag — the debug-info ledger row `infinite = ...` still works. Knock-on effect that wasn't in the original report but falls out of the same change: a long 1×N strip with the pump over an edge now drains end-to-end correctly. Pre-fix the BFS short-circuited at iteration 2 once it reached an interior block with `count >= 2`, so for `[S1][S2][S3][S4][S5]` with the pump over `S1` only `{S1, S2, S3}` ever made it into `queue`; even with the consumption gate flipped to "finite", `S4` and `S5` stayed orphaned in the world. With the BFS now gated on `targetPosIsInfinite`, an edge anchor falls through to full exploration up to `pumpMaxDistance` (default 64), so the entire connected strip gets queued and consumed. Performance under the original ocean-edge case is unchanged: corners of a 5×5+ pond have ≥2 horizontal source neighbours so `targetPosIsInfinite` is true, BFS still breaks after the first outer iteration (queue ends up with the anchor plus its 5 neighbours from `SEARCH_NORMAL`), and the pump still sits on `currentPos` indefinitely — the only cost is one extra `isInfiniteSourceAt` call per drain (four `getFluid` lookups + one `getBlockState` + one `getFluidWithFlowing` on the below block, all cheap). `pumpsConsumeWater = true` continues to bypass everything (the isWater gate short-circuits to false, so `targetPosIsInfinite` is false and every drain consumes); `CONFIG_REVISION`-driven rebuilds from the recent live-config-toggle fix are unaffected.
