Eight `PumpInfiniteDetectionTester` game-test cases exercise the helper directly against a `ServerLevel`: 1×3 strip with stone floor verifies S2 infinite + S1/S3 finite; isolated 1×1 source returns false; every corner of a 2×2 pond returns true; 1×5 strip verifies interior S2/S3/S4 infinite + edges S1/S5 finite; a 1×3 strip with no support below returns false at the centre (water without support can't sustain a new source); two diagonally adjacent sources sharing one common corner both return false (regen is orthogonal-only); a 1×3 strip floating on a deeper water layer returns true at the centre (water counts as support); and null-safety short-circuits both arguments so the per-drain hot path won't NPE during tile teardown. End-to-end in-client verification (place a pump over the centre vs. an edge of a hand-dug 1×3 strip, watch the tank fill and the source blocks either remain or vanish) is unchanged and remains the realistic acceptance signal — the helper test is the regression guard against ever silently reverting to the global-flag heuristic.
- Mob pathfinding: pipes, quarry frames, tanks, mining tubes, and laser tables (Assembly/Advanced Crafting/Integration) now report `isPathfindable(LAND/AIR) = false`, so vanilla land mobs treat the cell as a solid obstacle. Previously these blocks' partial-height collision shapes (pipes float at Y 0.25–0.75 with thin connection arms; frames are similar; tanks are a 2/16-inset column; the laser table is full-width but 9/16 tall; the tube fills 4–12/16 horizontally for full height) combined with the default `isPathfindable` fall-through let the pathfinder classify the cell as walkable, so mobs would shove blindly into a pipe at chest height rather than navigating around or over it. With the override, single horizontal pipes / frames / tanks become climbable like a slab (collision top at Y=0.75 for pipes/frames or Y=0.5625 for laser tables — both well under the vanilla 1-block jump clearance), but a vertical stack of two or more (e.g. a column of structure pipes used as a base wall) is unclimbable for the same reason a stone wall is. Closes the cheese where players were using cheap BC blocks to fence off hostile or friendly mobs from reaching them. Markers (`BlockMarkerBase` and its `BlockMarkerPath` / `BlockMarkerVolume` subclasses) deliberately stay passable — their collision is already `Shapes.empty()` so mobs walk through them by design, matching their decorative-marker role. The matching NeoForge extension hook `getBlockPathType(BlockState, BlockGetter, BlockPos, Mob)` is intentionally NOT overridden — the vanilla `isPathfindable` result already produces `PathType.BLOCKED`, which is the correct semantics for "solid step-up obstacle"; returning `PathType.FENCE` would have raised the path cost but still allowed bumping into the cell, and `PathType.DAMAGE_OTHER` would have caused mobs to actively flee rather than just navigate around.
- Restore the 1.12.2 `display.colorBlindMode` client-side toggle, redesigned as a tri-state `EnumValue<ColorBlindMode>` (`AUTO` / `OFF` / `ON`, default `AUTO`) that hooks into Minecraft's existing accessibility setting instead of forcing the player to flip a separate BuildCraft knob. In `AUTO` mode (default), the effective state mirrors `Minecraft.getInstance().options.highContrast().get()` — so a player who's already enabled Options → Accessibility → High Contrast at the vanilla level immediately gets BuildCraft's colourblind variants too, with no second toggle. `OFF` and `ON` override regardless of MC's accessibility setting (for players who want one without the other — e.g. enabling the BC variants without pulling in the broader high-contrast UI overlay, or vice versa). Resolution lives in a new `buildcraft.lib.client.ColorBlindUtil#isActive()` helper that's defensive against early-classload (config field unbound) and non-client contexts (`Minecraft.getInstance() == null`); the `Minecraft` import is kept out of `BCLibConfig` to preserve that class as common-side spec code. When the toggle is effectively on, the diamond pipe filter GUI swaps `gui/filter.png` for `gui/filter_cb.png` (numbered slot labels) and the diamond item/fluid pipes' west-face sprite swaps to its `_cb` variant on the block atlas — both already baked in via the `pipes/` directory atlas source in `assets/minecraft/atlases/blocks.json`, so the BC config side of the change needs no resource-pack reload. Painted diamond fluid pipes pick up the colourblind variant automatically through the existing dyed-sprite path because the 16 `diamond_fluid_west_cb_dyed_<colour>.png` files were also kept from 1.12.2; `ensureDyedSprites` chains the cb suffix in front of the dye suffix so the resolver hits the correct compound filename. Plumbed through a `maybeCbName(String, boolean)` helper in `PipeBaseModelGenStandard` that probes for a `_cb` companion sprite and falls through to the original when no variant exists (so non-diamond pipes that lack a colourblind variant aren't painted missing-pink), and per-`(definition, cb)` cache keying on `SPRITES` / `MASK_SPRITES` / `DYED_SPRITES` so both variants stay resolved after first lookup — the cb bit goes in the low bit so it can't accidentally collide with the identity-hash high half. `MASK_MAP` already contained entries for `diamond_fluid_west_cb` and `diamond_item_west_cb` mapping to the same shared `mask_shared_fluid` / `mask_shared_diamond_filled` masks as their non-`_cb` counterparts (carried over from 1.12.2), so mask resolution works without a MASK_MAP edit. Two listeners drive live updates without restart: a `ModConfigEvent.Reloading` listener in `BCCoreClient` (filtered to `BCUnifiedClientConfig.SPEC`) handles BC-config-only changes — flipping AUTO/ON/OFF — by calling `Minecraft.getInstance().levelRenderer.allChanged()`, equivalent to F3+A, since the (def, cb) cache keying means both arrays are already populated and the chunks just need to bake against the new key; and a `ResourceManagerReloadListener` in `BCLibClient` clears all three sprite caches whenever the client resource manager reloads — F3+T, resource pack changes, AND vanilla High Contrast toggling (the MC option swaps the built-in `minecraft:high_contrast` pack and triggers a reload under the hood, which restitches the block atlas). The cache clear is unconditional rather than gated on "did cb change" because the atlas restitch invalidates the cached `TextureAtlasSprite` references regardless — they'd point at freed slots from the previous stitch and render garbage UVs against the new atlas. The level renderer's own reload path triggers chunk re-bakes after listeners run, so no explicit `allChanged()` from the reload listener is needed. Seven `PipeBaseModelGenStandardCbKeyTester` JUnit cases exercise the cache-key composition (cb-bit position, dye-colour disjointness across all 16 colours per cb-state, ordinal-vs-cb-bit non-collision); end-to-end sprite-swap verification stays manual (runClient → Mods → Configure → Client → "Colourblind Mode" → AUTO/ON/OFF, plus toggling vanilla Options → Accessibility → High Contrast and observing pipes auto-update) because both `Minecraft.getInstance()`-dereferencing and atlas-stitching are unavailable under JUnit and the server-only gametest harness. Doesn't address the seven orphan `_cb` textures that came across with the port (`station/state_*_cb.png` × 4 and `block/pipes/pipeRobotStation*_cb.png` × 3) — those belong to features not yet ported and have no Java references; left for a separate cleanup pass alongside the other unused GUI textures (`block.png`, `slot.png`, `ledger.png`, `generic_one_slot.png`, `generic_ui.png`, `list.png` superseded by `list_new.png`, `blueprint/blue.png`, plus the unported-feature set `charging_table.png` / `energy_heater.png` / `packager.png` / `programming_table.png` / `refinery_filter.png` / `requester_gui.png` / `stamper.png`).
- Electronic Library: the snapshot list panel now renders 13 rows instead of 12. The dark panel in `electronic_library.png` extends from y=22 down to roughly y=126 (height ~104 px) — room for 13 rows of 8 px text — but the modern port's `LIST_MAX_ROWS` was set to 12, capping the visible list at 96 px and leaving the bottom ~8 px of the panel permanently empty regardless of how many snapshots were stored. The 1.12.2 GUI had no max-row cap at all (`iterateSnapshots` iterated `list.size()` directly) and used the panel area opportunistically; bumping the modern cap from 12 to 13 restores parity with the visible texture without changing the cap-driven scrolling story. Both the foreground row-render loop in `drawForegroundLayer` and the click-detection loop in `mouseClicked` already read `LIST_MAX_ROWS`, so the 13th row gets text + selection-highlight + click handling on the same code path as the first twelve.
- Electronic Library: populate the GUI's left-side help ledger. Same pattern as the recent Replacer / Builder / Architect fixes — `GuiElectronicLibrary.initGuiElements` already attached a `LedgerHelp` (with a leftover `// real help text is added in another session` stub comment) but never registered any widgets against it, so the panel rendered empty. Eight `DummyHelpElement`s now cover every interactive region: the 12-row snapshot list, the download input/arrow/output triplet, the upload input/arrow/output triplet, and the Delete button — each backed by a `buildcraft.help.library.*.{title,desc[N]}` string in `en_us.json`. Per-slot granularity (rather than grouping each transfer row into one entry) lets the player mouse-hover to learn the distinct mechanical role of each slot: download is a round-trip that fetches snapshot data from the server bank back into this client's local library (the input item is returned untouched through the matching output slot), while upload sacrifices the input item as a payment token and hands back a fresh used blueprint/template keyed to the just-uploaded server-side data. A new `LIST_H = LIST_ROW_H * LIST_MAX_ROWS` constant is introduced for the list-region rectangle, and the four slot coordinates are hoisted into `DOWN_IN_*` / `DOWN_OUT_*` / `UP_IN_*` / `UP_OUT_*` constants alongside the existing `ARROW_*` / `DEL_*` constants so the help-region origins share the source-of-truth with the slots they describe (which themselves still live in `ContainerElectronicLibrary.addSlot` calls). Descriptions written fresh from the tile behaviour: the upload-input line documents the "input is consumed, output is a fresh item" semantic that's surprising at first; the delete line notes that only the *client* library is affected and that re-downloading restores the entry.
- Architect Table: populate the GUI's left-side help ledger. Same pattern as the recent Replacer/Builder fixes — `GuiArchitectTable.initGuiElements` already attached a `LedgerHelp` but never registered any widgets against it, so the panel rendered empty. Five `DummyHelpElement`s now cover the main interactive regions: the 3D scan-preview viewport, the snapshot input slot, the progress-arrow strip, the snapshot output slot, and the rename text field — each backed by a `buildcraft.help.architect.*.{title,desc[N]}` string in `en_us.json`. Layout magic numbers that were previously inlined three different ways (preview blit, progress blit, EditBox init) get hoisted into a single block of `PREVIEW_*` / `SNAPSHOT_IN_*` / `PROGRESS_*` / `SNAPSHOT_OUT_*` / `NAME_*` constants so the help rectangles share the same source-of-truth as the widgets they describe, and all three call sites (preview render at (8, 8) 160×100, progress render at (77, 125) 22×16, EditBox at (8, 145) 160×12) are updated to read from those constants. Descriptions written fresh from the widget behaviour: the preview line notes the dual-mode rendering (live area while idle, captured snapshot once written); the input line documents that scanning starts automatically when the input is present, the output is empty, and the marker box is valid, and the template-vs-blueprint distinction (shape-only vs full state+tile data); the progress line explains the left-to-right fill and the on-completion hand-off to the output slot; the output line notes that an occupied output slot pauses further scanning; the name line notes that edits are committed live to the tile rather than deferred to a button press (the EditBox's `setResponder` already routes every keystroke through `NET_SET_NAME`).
- Builder: populate the GUI's left-side help ledger. Mirrors the recent Replacer fix: `GuiBuilder.initGuiElements` now attaches a `LedgerHelp` plus five `DummyHelpElement`s — over the snapshot input slot, the 3×9 resource grid, the fluid-handling cycle button, the 4×6 read-only "remaining materials" display panel, and the row of four fluid tanks — each backed by a `buildcraft.help.builder.*.{title,desc[N]}` string in `en_us.json`. The 1.12.2 GuiBuilder had a commented-out "Can Excavate" toggle stub (`// TODO: Convert this gui into JSON!`) and never shipped any help text, so the descriptions are written fresh from the widget behaviour: the snapshot line notes that building begins as soon as a used blueprint/template is present and the work area is in range; the resource line calls out that pipes and hoppers can feed the grid and that non-matching items are left alone; the fluid-mode line cross-references the button icon and tooltip; the display-panel line documents the read-only "stack-worth of pending materials" semantics and that empty cells mean the material is satisfied; the tanks line notes the three fill paths (pipe insertion, bucket right-click, and excavated-fluid pickup). Rectangle coordinates are computed from the existing slot constants in `ContainerBuilder` and the existing tank/button constants at the top of `GuiBuilder` (with a 2 px inset on the multi-slot groups so adjacent help regions don't quite touch) — no new layout magic numbers.
- Filler: the Excavate and Invert buttons in the GUI were noticeably louder than vanilla buttons despite supposedly playing the same `UI_BUTTON_CLICK` sound. Two compounding bugs in `GuiFiller.mouseClicked`: the click was being played via `this.minecraft.player.playSound(SoundEvents.UI_BUTTON_CLICK.value(), 1.0F, 1.0F)` — both arguments hard-coded to `1.0F`. Vanilla's `AbstractWidget.playDownSound` routes through `SoundManager.play(SimpleSoundInstance.forUI(SoundEvents.UI_BUTTON_CLICK, 1.0F))` where the literal `1.0F` is the pitch and the two-arg `forUI` overload defaults volume to `0.25F`; the Filler was therefore playing the click at 4× the vanilla amplitude. Compounding that, `Entity#playSound` queues a positional, attenuated, world-category sound at the player's location rather than the non-positional UI-category sound `SoundManager#play` produces — so the click also picked up distance falloff math and was routed through the wrong sound-category slider. Fixed by calling `this.minecraft.getSoundManager().play(SimpleSoundInstance.forUI(SoundEvents.UI_BUTTON_CLICK, 1.0F))` for both buttons, matching the vanilla pattern exactly.
- Replacer: populate the GUI's left-side help ledger. The ledger was already attached in `GuiReplacer.initGuiElements` but no widgets registered help info, so expanding it produced an empty panel. Six `DummyHelpElement`s now cover the main interactive regions — the 3D blueprint preview, the snapshot input slot, the rename text field, the find/replace schematic slots, and the Replace button — each backed by a `buildcraft.help.replacer.*.{title,desc[N]}` string in `en_us.json`. The 1.12.2 GuiReplacer was also a stub with no help text, so the descriptions are written fresh from the widget behaviour: the preview line calls out that filling both schematic slots renders a hypothetical-post-swap blueprint (and that nothing is committed until Replace is clicked); the name-field line notes that edits are client-side until commit; the find/replace lines explain the single-block-schematic pairing; the Replace button line documents both that it requires all three slots filled with parseable schematics and that the current text-field value rides along on commit, overwriting the original blueprint in place.
- Add a `display.flowDisplay` cycling client-side option that controls how `LocaleUtil` renders flow rates: `PER_SECOND` (default — `100.00 MJ/s`, matching 1.12.2's display convention and the previous behaviour of `localizeMjFlow(long)` / `localizeRfFlow(int)`), `PER_TICK` (`5.00 MJ/t` — the underlying API figure, which is what JEI/NEI conventionally show for FE), or `BOTH` (`100.00 MJ/s (5.00 MJ/t)` — the parenthesised secondary value drawn from the same source). Affects every callsite of the two flow formatters: the `LedgerEngine` MJ flow row, the `LedgerEngineFE` FE/RF flow row, the `LedgerTablePower` silicon-table avg-power row, both `ScreenEngineFE` / `ScreenDynamoMJ` upgrade-rate help bodies (the "Converts X RF to Y MJ/s" sentence picks up whichever side(s) the config asks for on each side independently), the kinesis-pipe transfer-rate tooltip in `ItemPipeHolder`, and the three F3-style debug overlays in `TileQuarry` / `TileEngineBase_BC8` / `TileDistiller_BC8`. The two `localizeMjFlow` overloads diverged in semantic — the `long microMjPerTick` overload multiplied by 20 internally to produce `/s`, while the `double mjPerTick` overload took raw mj/tick and rendered `/t` — but a grep of every call site confirms the `(double)` form had zero callers, so it's removed in this entry; any future caller wanting the per-tick semantic now sets `flowDisplay = PER_TICK` (or just constructs the string directly). Plumbed through two new package-visible helpers `LocaleUtil.formatMjFlow(double mjPerTick, FlowDisplay, String unit)` and `LocaleUtil.formatRfFlow(int rfPerTick, FlowDisplay, String unit)` — the unit string is taken explicitly rather than re-derived inside, both so the unit tests can exercise every mode without depending on the `mjUnit()` / `energyUnit()` defaults and so the public wrappers can pick the unit once at the call site (cheaper than re-resolving on the per-tick branch of `BOTH`). New `BCLibConfig.FlowDisplay` enum surfaces as a dropdown in Mods → Config → Client; lang label "Flow Rate Display" added so the row doesn't fall back to camelCase. The pipe-gate "Switch to N MJ/t limit" / "Switch to N FE/t limit" chat lines and their lang keys are deliberately NOT routed through this — pipe transfer limits are inherently a per-tick API concept and the chat string baking the unit is correct documentation, not display drift. Eight new `LocaleUtilNumberFormatTester` cases cover both formatters across all three modes plus a long-form-unit-string test (so a `BOTH` render with "Minecraft Joules" produces the expected "100.00 Minecraft Joules/s (5.00 Minecraft Joules/t)") and a zero-value sanity check, bringing the suite to twenty-one tests.
- Add a `display.abbreviateLargeNumbers` client-side toggle that collapses FE/RF readouts at or above 1,000 into a compact suffixed form: `1,234 FE` → `1.2k FE`, `1,500,000 FE` → `1.5M FE`, `2,500,000,000 FE` → `2.5G FE`, `4,000,000,000,000 FE` → `4.0T FE`. Default `false` (raw expanded form, current look). Plumbed entirely through `LocaleUtil.formatLong(long)` — when the toggle is on AND `Math.abs(value) >= 1000L`, the value walks down through powers of 1000 until it lands in the [1, 1000) range (or the largest available tier for extreme values), rendered at one fractional digit via the same `numberFormat(...)` machinery the unabbreviated path uses, and the matching k/M/G/T suffix is appended. The walk handles a tier-crossing rounding edge: 999,950 / 1000 = 999.95, which rounds to 1000.0 at one-decimal precision and would render as the awkward "1000.0k" — a second guarded loop iteration bumps it to the next tier instead so the output reads "1.0M", while 999,949 (rounds to 999.9) correctly stays at the k tier. The configured `decimalSeparator` applies to the fractional digit (so `2,500,000` renders as "2,5M" with `DecimalSeparator.COMMA`); the configured `thousandsSeparator` is irrelevant here because abbreviated values are always < 1000 in their integer portion. Negative values keep their sign (`-1,500` → `-1.5k`). Values below the threshold (`|value| < 1000`) always return the raw form regardless of the toggle, since the whole point is to compact unwieldy readouts. `formatDouble(double, int)` deliberately does NOT abbreviate — MJ readouts (battery storage, engine flow, heat) rarely exceed a few thousand at runtime so the visual win is mostly theoretical, and JEI category power labels (Assembly Table 80,000 MJ, Distiller per-recipe) are load-bearing precision where collapsing to "80.0k MJ" would lose the figure that distinguishes recipes from each other; both flow through `formatDouble` so they automatically opt out. New options live in `BCLibConfig.buildDisplay` next to `thousandsSeparator` / `decimalSeparator` so they share the `[display]` section. Lang label "Abbreviate Large Numbers" added so the in-game config row doesn't fall back to camelCase. New `LocaleUtilNumberFormatTester` cases cover all five tiers (raw / k / M / G / T) including the tier-crossing edge at 999,950 vs 999,949, the off-toggle behaviour at every magnitude, the sub-threshold short-circuit, negative-value sign preservation, and the decimal-separator-honouring path with COMMA — bringing the suite to thirteen tests against the (4 thousands × 2 decimal × 2 abbreviate) matrix.
- Add two cycling client-side display options that control how `LocaleUtil` formats numbers in machine readouts and JEI labels: `display.thousandsSeparator` (`COMMA` / `DOT` / `SPACE` / `NONE`, default `COMMA` → `1,000`) chooses the grouping separator for the integer portion of long and double readouts, and `display.decimalSeparator` (`DOT` / `COMMA`, default `DOT` → `1.5`) chooses the separator before the fractional portion of double readouts. The two combine independently — `1,000.50` (default), `1.000,50` (European-style), `1 000.50`, `1000,50`, etc. — so users on non-US locales can match their conventions without affecting Minecraft's own labels. Plumbed through two new helpers `LocaleUtil.formatLong(long)` and `LocaleUtil.formatDouble(double, int decimals)`, both of which build a `java.text.DecimalFormat` per call (DecimalFormat is not thread-safe and the call rate is bounded by UI refresh, so the construction cost is dominated by the surrounding render path; no caching needed). Six `LocaleUtil` formatters are rewritten on top of the helpers: `localizeMj` (`%.2f` → `formatDouble(mj, 2)` + unit), `localizeMjFlow(long)` and `localizeMjFlow(double)` (same `%.2f` swap with `/s` and `/t` suffixes), `localizeHeat` (`%.2f °C` swap so the heat ledger row picks up the decimal separator), `localizeRf` (`%,d / %,d` → `formatLong` × 2), and `localizeRfFlow` (`%,d` → `formatLong(rfPerTick * 20L)` — the 20× widens to long while we're rewriting it, eliminating an existing latent overflow at extreme tick rates). Two duplicate inline `String.format("%,d / %,d %s", current, max, energyUnit())` calls in `ScreenEngineFE` and `ScreenDynamoMJ`'s battery hover tooltips are replaced with `LocaleUtil.localizeRf(current, max)` so the formatters live in one place rather than three. The two JEI category power callsites (`AssemblyTableCategory`, `DistillerCategory`) drop the inline `String.format("%.1f", mj)` in favour of `LocaleUtil.formatDouble(mj, 1)` so the 1-decimal precision is preserved while the separators become config-aware. New options live in a new `BCLibConfig.buildDisplay` slotted into the unified `[display]` section right after `BCEnergyConfig.buildDisplay` from `BCUnifiedClientConfig`, since these knobs are general-purpose number formatting rather than energy-specific. Two new `defineEnum` rows surface as dropdowns in the in-game Mods → Config → Client tab; lang labels "Thousands Separator" and "Decimal Separator" added so the rows don't fall back to camelCase identifiers. Debug-only `String.format` paths in `TileDistiller_BC8`, `FluidSmoother`, and `TileEngineBase_BC8` (animState, smooth-fluid debug, and heat-percent debug overlays) are intentionally left as-is — they're F3-style internal readouts where consistency with Java's default formatting is preferable to user-facing localisation. New `LocaleUtilNumberFormatTester` JUnit suite covers every (4 thousands × 2 decimal) combination plus the negative/zero/sub-1000 long edges, decimal-digit count from 0 through 4, half-up rounding at the precision boundary, and the documented `null`-config-fallback path that the public no-arg `formatLong(long)` / `formatDouble(double, int)` wrappers take when run from JUnit (no NeoForge boot).
- Add a `display.useFullEnergyNames` client-side toggle that spells the energy unit suffixes in full instead of abbreviating them. Default `true` (full names, post in-game verification confirmed the spelt-out forms fit every readout the toggle reaches without overflowing or wrapping); set `false` to fall back to `MJ` / `FE` / `RF`. The toggle swaps `MJ` ↔ `Minecraft Joules`, `FE` ↔ `Forge Energy`, `RF` ↔ `Redstone Flux` everywhere `LocaleUtil` produces a unit-suffixed readout. Plumbed through one new helper `LocaleUtil.mjUnit()` plus a small extension to the existing `LocaleUtil.energyUnit()` so the FE/RF and MJ branches read both flags together; the three MJ formatters (`localizeMj`, `localizeMjFlow(long)`, `localizeMjFlow(double)`) now interpolate `mjUnit()` instead of hard-coding `"MJ"`, and the FE/RF formatters (`localizeRf`, `localizeRfFlow`) pick up the long form automatically because they already routed through `energyUnit()`. Affects every callsite of those five methods — the `LedgerEngine` MJ stored/output panel, the `LedgerEngineFE` FE/RF and MJ rows, both `ScreenEngineFE` / `ScreenDynamoMJ` battery hovers and conversion-help bodies, the iron pipe limit chat ("Switched to N Minecraft Joules/t limit"), the kinesis-pipe hover, the quarry status, the distiller display, and the silicon LedgerTablePower readout. The two JEI category power labels (`gui.jei.category.buildcraftunofficial.assembly_table.power` and `distiller.power`) were the one place the unit was baked into the lang-key value (`"%s MJ"`); they now read `"%s %s"` and the two `Component.translatable` callers in `AssemblyTableCategory` and `DistillerCategory` pass `LocaleUtil.mjUnit()` as the second placeholder so a recipe that costs 5.0 MJ renders as `"5.0 Minecraft Joules"` by default or `"5.0 MJ"` with the toggle off, preserving the 1-decimal precision the JEI categories already used. Sentence-form lang strings that happen to contain `"MJ"` mid-prose (`tip.block.engine_redstone`/`stone`/`iron`, `gui.buildcraft.{stirling,combustion}_engine.help`) are deliberately untouched — those read fine as abbreviations in flowing text and would require a `.long` sibling per key for negligible payoff. Pairs with the existing `useRfNaming` toggle: by default the engine ledger reads `"100 Forge Energy/s"`; with `useRfNaming` on `"100 Redstone Flux/s"`; with `useFullEnergyNames` off `"100 FE/s"`; with both flipped from default `"100 RF/s"`. The new field is registered in `BCEnergyConfig.buildDisplay` next to `useRfNaming` so it slots into the same `[display]` section of `buildcraftunofficial-client.toml` without a new sub-section, and a `buildcraftunofficial.configuration.useFullEnergyNames` lang label is added so the in-game config screen shows "Spell Energy Units in Full" rather than the camelCase identifier. Does not address the two outstanding power-display knobs from the audit todo (`1.2k MJ` number-abbreviation and per-tick/per-second rate toggle) — those are independent features.
- Move `oilIsSticky` out of `worldgen.oil` and into top-level `general`. The option controls how oil source blocks affect entity motion (`BCCustomFluidType.motionScale` returns `0.5` instead of `0.8` when set), which is a runtime physics knob — it has nothing to do with terrain generation. Phase 3 of the original config audit (line 9) had grouped it under `worldgen.oil` purely on the basis that "every other oil setting lives there", but the rest of that section (`enableOilGeneration`, the spout heights, the per-tier spawn probabilities, the biome/dimension list-mode pair, etc.) is genuinely worldgen — only `oilIsSticky` was sitting there as a category mismatch. **One-time migration note:** the key's on-disk path in `buildcraftunofficial-common.toml` changes from `[worldgen.oil] oilIsSticky` to `[general] oilIsSticky`, so the next world load will regenerate the entry at its new path with the default value (`false`); users who had customised it to `true` will need to re-apply that under the `general` section.
- Reword `general.pumpsConsumeWater` and its label to match what the option actually does, and make a live config toggle propagate to running pumps without a world reload. The setting's lang label "Pumps Consume Infinite Water" and the modern `.comment("Should pumps slowly drain infinite water sources?")` were both written as if the toggle let pumps gradually deplete an infinite-water pool — neither claim is true. The toggle is a binary kill-switch on `TilePump`'s infinite-source optimisation: with `false` (default), `buildQueue0` flips an `isWater` flag that, on hitting any water cell with ≥2 water-source neighbours and water-or-solid below (the same predicate `BlockDynamicLiquid.updateTick` uses to decide whether to spawn a new source), sets `isInfiniteWaterSource = true` and breaks out of the BFS — the pump then keeps adding 1000 mB to its tank per drain cycle without calling `BlockUtil.drainBlock(level, currentPos, true)`, so the source block stays put; with `true`, the BFS no longer flips that flag and `drainBlock(..., true)` runs on every cycle, actually setting the source block to AIR. There is no "slow" mode — the drain rate is identical either way, gated by the same `10 * MjAPI.MJ` per cycle in `mine()`. There is no progressive depletion either: vanilla MC's flow rules immediately re-source any 2×2+ pool from its remaining source neighbours, so a player toggling the option ON in vanilla and watching a pond expecting it to run dry sees the pool stay full forever, which is what prompted the "doesn't appear to be working" observation. The 1.12.2 comment was clearer about this — *"Should pumps consume water? Enabling this will disable minor optimisations, but work properly with finite water mods."* — and that second clause (the actual reason the toggle exists) got lost during the 26.1 port. Lang label flips to "Pumps Drain Water Source Blocks" and the Java comment is rewritten to explain the optimisation it controls and to call out that the option has no observable effect with vanilla water — it only matters as compatibility scaffolding for mods that disable infinite-water regeneration. Separately, the consume→infinite direction (toggling `true` → `false`) was failing to take effect until the world was saved and reopened, even though NeoForge's `ModConfigSpec.BooleanValue.set(...)` updates the cached value synchronously when the in-game config screen writes the toggle. Cause was state confined to `TilePump` itself: `isWater` is captured per BFS into `buildQueue0`'s local frame, and `isInfiniteWaterSource` is only re-evaluated against the live config in `mine()` at the post-drain `&= !pumpsConsumeWater.get()` line — a pump in consume mode whose `paths` map has been continuously fed by vanilla refill never trips that line in a way that flips back to infinite mode (`&= true` is a no-op on a `false` flag), and a pump whose tank is more than half full short-circuits out of `mine()` at the top guard before reaching either re-evaluation, leaving the cached BFS verdict stuck. World save+reopen "fixed" it incidentally because the BlockEntity is reconstructed with `queueBuilt = false` and `isInfiniteWaterSource = false` (neither field is in NBT), and the first post-reload tick runs `buildQueue` afresh against the current config. Fix: add a static `AtomicLong CONFIG_REVISION` on `TilePump` plus an instance `builtAtRevision` field, bump the static counter from a `ModConfigEvent.Reloading` listener registered in `BCFactory.init` (filtered to `BCUnifiedConfig.SPEC` so a CLIENT-scope display toggle doesn't churn pumps), and gate `serverTick`'s rebuild branch on `!queueBuilt || builtAtRevision != CONFIG_REVISION.get()` so any running pump rebuilds its queue on the very next tick after a config edit, regardless of tank state. The revision is captured inside `buildQueue` itself rather than at call sites, so the existing `mine()` rebuild-on-failure path also stays in sync. Mechanics are otherwise unchanged.
- Wire up `general.minePlayerProtected` and clear up its inverted user-facing description. The option was one of the six "defined but never read" knobs the phase-6 audit (line 9) left in place with a `// TODO: wire into TileQuarry / TileMiner break-block path` marker; meanwhile the lang label "Mine Player Protected Blocks" (read as `true = mine them`) and the Java comment "Set true to prevent quarries from mining player-protected areas" (read as `true = don't mine them`) had been disagreeing on polarity since the 1.12.2→26.1.1 unification, with neither being authoritative because nothing consumed the flag at runtime. Now: a new helper `BlockUtil.canMachineBreak(ServerLevel, BlockPos, GameProfile)` posts a `net.neoforged.neoforge.event.level.block.BreakBlockEvent` (the post-`26.1.2.30-beta` replacement for the old `BlockEvent.BreakEvent`, called out as a breaking change in the version-bump entry on line 27) with an owner-bound FakePlayer positioned at the target block, and returns `!event.isCanceled()`; if `minePlayerProtected = true` the helper short-circuits to `true` (override). Wired into three call sites: `TileQuarry.canMine` (the box-iterator's existing skip path naturally walks past a denied position the same way it already walks past bedrock and fluids; the in-flight `TaskBreakBlock.finish` re-checks via `canMine` and returns task-complete on a deny, so power isn't refunded — refunding would invite battery-overflow loops), `TileMiningWell.nextPos` (now `continue`s past denied positions instead of stopping the well, since claims are typically small regions with unclaimed terrain below), and `SnapshotBuilder.BreakTask.isImpossible` plus its consuming loop (impossible tasks now drain via `cancelBreakTask` + `iterator.remove()` rather than just `continue`, so a builder doesn't accumulate undeletable tasks for protected blocks until reload). Owner is read from each tile's existing `getOwner()`; tiles with a null owner (worldgen / set-block) fall back to a stable BC-namespaced `[BuildCraft]` profile whose UUID seed matches `BCCore.preInit`'s `BC_PROFILE` so protection mods that key on identity see one entity rather than many. The Java comment on the option is rewritten to state the chosen polarity (`true = override protection, default false = respect`) and call out the explicit non-goal that pumps are unaffected — fluid drainage is a separate semantic class that protection mods often rule on differently, future `pumpRespectsProtection` if anyone asks. Out of scope: `TileMiner.removeBlock` for tube self-removal (BC's own infrastructure, not external mining) and `SchematicBlockDefault` placement rollback (internal failure recovery). Verified by `compileJava` and the existing `test` suite; end-to-end with a real protection mod (FTB Chunks, GriefPrevention, OpenPartiesAndClaims, server protection plugins) is the realistic verification path going forward but no test for it ships in this change.
- Drop the dead `display.pipes.powerPipeUseOldMjTexture` config option. The toggle's only consumer was `ActionPowerLimit#getSprite`, where it caused RF kinesis limiter gate-action buttons to render with the MJ-themed icon instead of the RF-themed one — a cosmetic affordance with no further reach despite the name implying it changed pipe-block textures. With the option gone, RF limiter actions permanently use `POWER_LIMIT_RF` (the current `false` default) and MJ limiter actions continue to use `POWER_LIMIT` unconditionally. The `BooleanValue` field, the `BCTransportConfig.buildDisplay` method, the call from `BCUnifiedClientConfig`, and the lang label are all removed; the `display` section in the client config now contains only `useRfNaming`. **One-time migration note:** the `[display.pipes]` block disappears from `buildcraftunofficial-client.toml` on next load — any custom value users had set is silently dropped.
- Wire up the `display.useRfNaming` toggle and flip its default to FE. The option had been wholly cosmetic but landed in 26.1.1 with two compounding bugs: it defaulted to `true` (RF) but every user-facing string had already been rewritten in FE/Forge Energy wording, and the only `useRfNaming.get()` call site was a `BlockEngineFE` ternary whose two branches returned the same translation key — toggling did nothing even there. Default flips to `false` (FE matches modern NeoForge convention), and the toggle now actually swaps the displayed nomenclature: the FE Engine block name (custom `BlockItem` overrides `getName(ItemStack)` to pick `block.buildcraftunofficial.engine_rf` vs `.rf` sibling), the nine FE pipe item names (`ItemPipeHolder.getName` detects FE pipes via `definition.identifier.endsWith("_rf")` and adds the same suffix), the engine GUI title (`BlockEngineFE.openGui` now feeds `BCEnergyConfig.rfFeKey(...)` to the `MenuProvider`), the engine/dynamo battery hover (`%,d / %,d FE/RF`), the upgrade-rate per-second tooltip ("Forge Energy"/"Redstone Flux"), the help-overlay "FE Energy"/"RF Energy" titles and conversion bodies, the gate "Switch to N FE/t" / "RF/t" action label, the JEI "FE Transport"/"RF Transport" guide chapter, the engine and MJ-dynamo `tip.block.*` tooltips ("Forge Energy"/"Redstone Flux" wording), and the `LocaleUtil.localizeRf`/`localizeRfFlow` "FE/s"/"RF/s" unit suffixes — all driven by a single `BCEnergyConfig.rfFeKey(baseKey)` helper and a `LocaleUtil.energyUnit()` helper, with the existing translation key kept as the FE branch and a `.rf` sibling added for each affected entry. The `BCTooltips` registry-driven tooltip handler now also runs every key through `rfFeKey` and falls back to the base key when no `.rf` variant exists in the lang file, so non-energy tooltips (`tip.block.engine_stone`, `engine_iron`, etc.) are unaffected. Internal block/item registry IDs (`engine_rf`, `pipe_*_rf`) are unchanged — renaming them would break existing worlds, and the `_rf` suffix is a harmless legacy artefact.
- Config audit follow-up: drop `display.hidePower` and `display.hideFluid`. The previous config-audit pass kept these dead options on the books with `// TODO: wire into tile GUIs` markers, on the assumption they'd be re-wired the way the old pre-license-migration 1.12.2 code did it (gating the textual MJ/mB readouts in every engine/quarry/refinery/pipe-tooltip GUI). Decided not to revive that — the bars and gauges already convey the information, and re-implementing the toggle would mean threading two booleans through every BC tile GUI's `drawString` call for a feature few players asked for. The two `BooleanValue` fields, `BCCoreConfig.buildDisplay`, the call from `BCUnifiedClientConfig`, and the two lang labels are all removed; the `display` section in the client config now contains only `useRfNaming` and `pipes.powerPipeUseOldMjTexture` — both of which actually have consumers.
- Config audit, phase 1 (cleanup, no behaviour change). Removes three orphan section keys (`events`, `experimental`, `performance`) that survived the 1.12.2→26.1.1 unification but no longer correspond to any section in `BCUnifiedConfig` — the in-game config screen had been silently looking them up forever. Adds the three lang labels that were missing (`useRfNaming`, `baseRfRate`, `baseFlowRate`) so those options no longer fall back to camelCase identifiers in the UI. Adds the eleven `.comment(...)` strings that were missing on `BCEnergyConfig` options (oil burn, the four spout heights, the three tier probabilities, both excluded-list-mode booleans, and `oilIsSticky`) so the hover-tooltips on those rows now read as English sentences instead of being blank. Renames the worldgen subsection `worldgen.oil.spawn_probability` → `worldgen.oil.spawnProbability` to match the camelCase used by every other section, and renames the seven SCREAMING_SNAKE Java fields in `BCBuildersConfig` (`QUARRY_FRAME_MIN_HEIGHT`, …, `BPT_STORE_EXTERNAL_THRESHOLD`) to `quarryFrameMinHeight` / `bptStoreExternalThreshold` / etc. so the field naming matches the TOML keys (which were already camelCase) and the rest of the config classes; the six call-sites in `TileQuarry` are updated. The `excessiveBiomes` comment is also rewritten to actually explain what the option does — every biome in the list receives a flat 30× multiplier on small/medium/large oil rolls; in 1.12.2 this defaulted to BC's own oil_desert/oil_ocean biomes (which no longer exist), so the empty default is correct, but the option remains as a "force a vanilla/modded biome to gush oil" override.
- Config audit, phase 2 (translation key paths). NeoForge's `ConfigurationScreen` builds option labels as `<modid>.configuration.<leaf>` — the leaf option name only, with no enclosing-section prefix (verified against `ConfigurationSectionScreen.getTranslationKey` in `neoforge-26.1.2.30-beta-sources`, line 545: `context.modId + ".configuration." + key`). Every `pipes.*` / `oil.*` / `oil.spouts.*` / `oil.spawnProbability.*` prefixed key in `en_us.json` was therefore an orphan, and the corresponding options had been silently falling back to their raw camelCase identifiers in the UI for the entire 26.1.1 lifetime. Strips the prefixes from all 17 affected leaf-option keys (`pipes.mjPerItem` → `mjPerItem`, `oil.spouts.smallSpoutMinHeight` → `smallSpoutMinHeight`, etc.), and adds the two missing sub-section header labels (`spouts` → "Oil Spouts", `spawnProbability` → "Spawn Probability") since NeoForge looks up sub-section buttons by their own leaf name too — previously the `[worldgen.oil.spouts]` and `[worldgen.oil.spawnProbability]` sub-screens opened with camelCase headers. Three oil-tier probability labels also rephrased from "Small/Medium/Large Oil Gen Prob" to "Small/Medium/Large Oil Spawn Probability" while we're rewriting that line anyway. No code change — purely a lang-file fix.
- Config audit, phase 3 (re-categorise mis-placed paths). Five settings sat in sections that didn't match what they actually controlled: `oilIsSticky` was at top-level `general` but is a worldgen.oil concern (every other oil setting lives there); `useRfNaming` was at top-level `general` but is a pure-cosmetic display toggle that only renames the FE engine and pipes; `disableRfPipe` was at top-level `general` but every other pipe option was already nested under `general.pipes`; `bptStoreExternalThreshold` and the six `quarry*` options were at top-level `general` while the rest of the schema was already split by module/feature. Reorganised: `oilIsSticky` moves to `worldgen.oil.oilIsSticky`, `useRfNaming` moves to `display.useRfNaming` (via a new `BCEnergyConfig.buildDisplay` slotted into the unified spec), `disableRfPipe` moves under the existing `general.pipes` push, and `bptStoreExternalThreshold` plus all six quarry options nest under a new `general.builders` (and `general.builders.quarry` for the six quarry knobs). Two new section labels added (`builders` → "Builders", `quarry` → "Quarry"). **One-time migration note:** the keys' on-disk paths in `buildcraftunofficial-common.toml` change with this refactor, so the next world load will regenerate the moved entries at their new paths with default values; users who had customised any of these specific knobs (most commonly `quarryMaxBlockMineRate` or `pumpsConsumeWater`) will need to re-apply those settings under the new sections. All other config values are unaffected.
- Config audit, phase 4 (split CLIENT scope from COMMON). The unified config was registered as `ModConfig.Type.COMMON` for everything including the four `display.*` toggles (`hidePower`, `hideFluid`, `useRfNaming`, `pipes.powerPipeUseOldMjTexture`), which meant the server's choice would be applied to every connected client — wrong scope for per-player UI preferences. Split into two specs: COMMON (gameplay/balance: `general.*`, `worldgen.*`) stays in `BCUnifiedConfig` and registers from `BCCore.init()`; a new `BCUnifiedClientConfig` holds the `display.*` section and registers from `BCCoreClient.init()` as `ModConfig.Type.CLIENT`. NeoForge writes the latter to `config/buildcraftunofficial-client.toml` and serves it through the same Mods → Config screen as a separate "Client" tab. The mods screen now shows two config buttons stacked under a "Common" / "Client" header instead of one. **One-time migration note:** any non-default `display.*` value previously sitting in `buildcraftunofficial-common.toml` will be ignored on next load; users will need to re-apply those settings in the new client toml. The old `[display]` block in the common file is harmless to leave behind but can be deleted manually.
- Config audit, phase 6 (resolve dead settings). Nine config options were defined-but-never-read after the 1.12.2→26.1.1 unification — each had a label, a default, sometimes a comment, but zero `.get()` callers. Three are removed outright because the underlying feature isn't in 26.1.1 at all: `worldGenWaterSpring` (no springs in 26.1.1), `quarryFrameMoveBoth` (the both-axis frame-move animation mode wasn't ported), and `enableOilBurn` (oil flammability isn't implemented in `BCEnergyFluids`). The other six (`worldGen`, `minePlayerProtected`, `miningMultiplier`, `bptStoreExternalThreshold`, `hidePower`, `hideFluid`) gate features that DO ship in 26.1.1 but the runtime path doesn't currently consult the config — they stay defined and labelled, but each gets a `// TODO: wire into <consumer>` comment in its declaring class so the gap is visible at the source rather than only in the audit doc. Nothing user-visible changes from leaving them in this session, but the schema is now honest about which knobs do nothing yet. **One-time migration note:** the three removed keys disappear from `buildcraftunofficial-common.toml` on next load; existing customisations on those keys (typically all defaults) are lost without effect.
- Config audit, phase 7 (naming and range cleanup). Three fixes that don't affect what works but make the schema readable. (1) `excludedBiomesIsBlackList` and `excludedDimensionsIsBlackList` are double-negative booleans where flipping them silently reverses list polarity — replaced with two `EnumValue<ListMode>` (`biomeListMode`, `dimensionListMode`) that surface as a `BLACKLIST | WHITELIST` dropdown in the config UI. The two callers in `OilGenerator` were updated; same default behaviour as before (`BLACKLIST`). (2) `excessiveBiomes` is now `forceExcessiveOilBiomes`, with a comment that explains what it actually does — every biome in the list receives a flat 30× multiplier on small/medium/large oil rolls. The 1.12.2 default of `[buildcraftenergy:oil_desert, buildcraftenergy:oil_ocean]` was the original target (BC's own oil biomes), but those biomes don't exist in 26.1.1 so the modern default is `[]`. The option remains as a "force a vanilla/modded biome to gush oil" override; the rename makes that intent explicit. (3) Oil spout height bounds were `0..256`, which capped below the modern `-64..320` build height; bumped to `-64..320`. **One-time migration note:** users with custom values for `excludedBiomesIsBlackList`, `excludedDimensionsIsBlackList`, or `excessiveBiomes` in their existing TOML will see those entries ignored on next load (they're not in the new spec) and the new keys will appear at their defaults; re-apply customisations under the new names if needed.
- Assembly Table: surface every recipe in JEI under a new `buildcraftunofficial:assembly_table` category, with facades collapsed into a single cycling entry instead of one entry per source block (which would otherwise mint thousands of near-identical JEI rows). Each non-facade recipe in `AssemblyRecipeRegistry.REGISTRY` contributes one entry per `getOutputPreviews()` stack — chipsets, gates, lenses, plugs, the gate copier — with input slots gathered from `AssemblyRecipe.getInputsFor(output)` (`Ingredient.getItems()` × `IngredientStack.count`) and the per-recipe MJ cost from `getRequiredMicroJoulesFor(output)`. The facade path is special-cased: `AssemblyRecipeCollector` walks `FacadeStateManager.validFacadeStates` once and emits a single `AssemblyRecipeJei` whose two input slots and one output slot each carry a list — slot 0 is `3× pipe_structure` (fixed), slot 1 cycles through every visible source block, and the output cycles through `createFacadeStack(info, false)` and `createFacadeStack(info, true)` (basic + hollow); each source block is doubled in the input list to stay paired with its two output variants the way `FacadeAssemblyRecipes.getRecipeInputs/Outputs` already does in-game. JEI's native `addItemStacks(List)` cycling renders this as one browsable recipe — pressing U on Stone surfaces the facade entry (Stone is in the cycling input list), pressing R on a Stone Facade surfaces the same entry from the output side, and the JEI index gains exactly one row for the entire facade family rather than ~5,000. Layout mirrors `GuiAssemblyTable`: an 89×86 crop of `assembly_table.png` at `(3, 27)` provides the input grid and power bar visuals (input slots laid out at the cropped `(5,9)` origin, up to a 3×4 grid filled in row-major order based on how many inputs the recipe actually has — most use 1–2), with a single output slot to the right at `(105, 9)` drawn with JEI's `setOutputSlotBackground()`. The MJ cost renders as `"X.X MJ"` below via the new `gui.jei.category.buildcraftunofficial.assembly_table.power` lang key (matching the distiller's pattern; assembly costs span 500 MJ for a lens to 80,000 MJ for a Gold AND Gate, so the number is load-bearing). Catalyst is `BCSiliconItems.ASSEMBLY_TABLE`. The collector's facade path defensively returns null if `pipe_structure` isn't registered (rather than falling back to the cobblestone-wall placeholder the in-game recipe uses for an empty registry — a JEI entry with the wrong recipe shape would mislead more than it helps), and skips both empty-output recipes and ingredients with no matching items so a misconfigured recipe never crashes the plugin init.
- JEI fluid recipes: extend the invisible-bucket alias system on the distiller and heat-exchanger categories to also surface fragile fluid shards (and any other modded "bucket-like" fluid container that registers itself), so a survival player holding a Fragile Water Shard can U-look-up the distiller the same way they could with a water bucket. The new `buildcraft.lib.compat.jei.FluidContainerAliases` utility owns the provider list, ships built-in providers for the vanilla/NeoForge bucket (`Fluid#getBucket()`) and for `ItemFragileFluidContainer` (constructs an ItemStack with the fluid pre-loaded into the `FLUID_CONTENT` data component), and exposes `registerProvider(Provider)` so other mods can add their own forms (e.g. a hypothetical clay bucket) from their JEI plugin without us needing to scan the item registry — capability scans were considered and rejected because universal tanks would match every fluid recipe and pollute lookups. `DistillerCategory` and `HeatExchangerCategory` now both call into this utility, replacing the verbatim-duplicated `addBucketAlias` private helpers the original distiller-JEI changelog entry below explicitly punted on extracting. To keep the shard alias robust regardless of how full the player's shard is, `BCCoreJeiPlugin.registerItemSubtypes` registers an `ISubtypeInterpreter` for `FRAGILE_FLUID_CONTAINER` keyed on the fluid's resource location alone — `registerFromDataComponentTypes(FLUID_CONTENT)` would have keyed on the whole `SimpleFluidContent` (including amount), so a 250 mB and 500 mB water shard would have hashed to different ingredients and the alias (a 500 mB shard) would only have matched exactly-full shards. Per-fluid shards are intentionally not enumerated into JEI's master ingredient list — shards remain alias-only.
- Distiller: restore 1.12.2's bucket right-click behaviour and the underlying tank gating that makes it work. Three regressions to address: (1) the modern port lost `tankIn.setFilter(isDistillableFluid)`, so right-clicking the distiller with a lava bucket happily fed the lava into the input tank where it would just sit forever; (2) the modern port lost `tankIn.setCanDrain(false)`, so right-clicking with an empty bucket drained the input tank instead of falling through to the outputs — the user's distillable input would silently disappear into the bucket on a misclick; (3) the modern port lost `tankGasOut/tankLiquidOut.setCanFill(false)`, so any pipe or bucket interaction could shove arbitrary fluids into either output tank. Fix mirrors the heat exchanger's `OutputTank` pattern: `TileDistiller_BC8` gains an `InputTank` whose `isValid` defers to `isDistillableFluid` and whose `extract` returns 0 unless an internal-flag-flipped `extractInternal` call is in progress, plus an `OutputTank` (its own subclass; the heat exchanger's lives in a different tile and uses a different capacity) whose `isValid` is gated by an internal-insert flag — the craft loop now drains the input via `extractInternal` and fills the outputs via `insertInternal`, while NBT load and the heat-exchanger-style `loadTank` helper keep using `set()` directly to bypass both gates (saved fluid is trusted, and the recipe registry may not be ready during early chunk load). `BlockDistiller.useItemOn` now iterates `tankIn` → `tankGasOut` → `tankLiquidOut` calling `FluidUtilBC.onTankActivated` on each — the gates funnel each held item to the right tank: a distillable bucket fills `tankIn` (filter passes; outputs reject the insert), an empty bucket drains `tankGasOut` first then `tankLiquidOut` (input rejects the extract), a lava bucket lands nowhere and the GUI opens. Three new regression tests cover the input-tank distillable filter, the input-tank external-extract block (and that `extractInternal` still drains properly so distillation doesn't halt), and the output-tank external-insert block (with `insertInternal` still landing recipe results, and the internal flag resetting after the call).
- Distiller: restore 1.12.2's wrench-rotates-the-block behaviour. Right-clicking the distiller with a wrench was opening the GUI instead of rotating it because `BlockDistiller` neither implemented `ICustomRotationHandler` (so `ItemWrench_Neptune.useOn` → `CustomRotationHelper.attemptRotateBlock` returned `PASS`) nor short-circuited the wrench in `useItemOn`, so the block fell through to its bucket-then-GUI path and the wrench's `useOn` never ran. Mirroring the engine pattern, `BlockDistiller` now implements `ICustomRotationHandler.attemptRotation` to rotate the horizontal `FACING` clockwise (1.12.2's `IBlockWithFacing.attemptRotation` → `EnumFacing.rotateY()`, equivalent to `Direction.getClockWise()` in 1.21+) and returns `PASS` from `useItemOn` whenever the held stack is an `IToolWrench` so the wrench's `useOn` actually fires the rotation, the slide sound, and the `buildcraftunofficial:wrenched` advancement. Empty-hand right-click still opens the GUI; bucket / fluid-container right-click still drains/fills the input tank.
- Distiller: client and server tank states now stay in sync after a server-side drain, fixing the visual desync where a wooden(-diamond) fluid pipe pulling gaseous fuel out of the distiller looked like it was barely extracting a trickle while the gas tank stayed visually full — the pipe was actually draining at the expected rate (~3 mB/t, matching the 16 mB / 5.33 ticks production), the client just never saw it. `saveAdditional` only writes the `fluidIn` / `fluidGasOut` / `fluidLiquidOut` keys when the corresponding tank is non-empty, but `loadAdditional` was using `tank.insert(0, fluid, amount, tx)` which *adds* to the existing client-side stack instead of replacing it: every `getUpdateTag` round-trip topped up the client's stale value (1000 mB → server drains to 800 → client sees 1800 next packet), and an empty server tank (key omitted) left the stale client value in place forever. A world reload "fixed" it because the BlockEntity was constructed fresh from an empty starting state. Fix mirrors the heat exchanger's own `loadTank` helper from the recent post-GUI fixes: a small private helper that always calls `set(0, ...)` — passing `(EMPTY, 0)` when the saved value was empty — so client tanks track every drain. The same `insert`-instead-of-set pattern would have affected anything else that piped fluid out of the distiller (input bucket containers, JEI lookups against the live tank, comparator readouts), but only the gas-output path hit it visibly because that's the only one being drained continuously by an external machine.
- Tank: a creative Ctrl+middle-click on a full tank used to copy the contents onto the picked item, so placing the result spawned a fresh full tank — every placement minted another 16 000 mB of whatever was in the source. Modern Minecraft's pickblock-with-data path runs server-side `addBlockDataToItem`, which calls `BlockEntity#saveCustomOnly` (writes our `tank.serialize`'s `"stacks"` key) → `removeComponentsFromTag` (default no-op) → `BlockItem.setBlockEntityData`, so the tank's full fluid landed in the item's `BLOCK_ENTITY_DATA` component and `BlockItem#updateCustomBlockEntityTag` re-applied it to the new BE on placement. `TileTank` now overrides `removeComponentsFromTag(ValueOutput)` to `discard("stacks")`, leaving the tag empty for the picked-item path so `setBlockEntityData` removes the component entirely. Disk save / chunk reload still go through `saveAdditional`/`loadAdditional` directly and are unaffected — only the pickblock-into-itemstack path drops the fluid payload. BC's intended economy is that tanks must be broken (which already drops fluid as separate fluid-shard items) before being moved, so picked tanks now always come back empty.
- Fluid pipes: restore the 1.12.2 tiered transfer rates that the port was missing, so higher-tier pipes actually move fluid faster than wood. `BCTransportConfig` only registered `PowerTransferInfo`/`RedstoneFluxTransferInfo` for kinesis/RF pipes; the matching `fluidTransfer(...)` calls were dropped, so every fluid pipe fell back to `PipeApi.fluidInfoDefault`'s `(20 mB/t, 10)`. New `baseFlowRate` config (default 10 mB/t, range 1–40) plus a `registerFluidTransferData()` invoked from `FMLCommonSetupEvent` next to the existing power/RF registrations: cobble/wood = base, stone/sandstone = 2× (20 mB/t), clay/iron/quartz = 4× (40), diamond/diaWood/void = 8× (80), gold = 8× with delay 2 instead of 10 (low-viscosity routing). Symptom: a wooden/diamond/gold/etc. fluid pipe between a distiller and a tank stack drained at the same 20 mB/t as a cobble pipe, taking ~40 s per 16 000 mB tank when it should have been a few seconds for the higher tiers — and balance-shifting via tank stacking made the slowdown look like duplication because the new top tank visibly filled "instantly" while the bottom emptied.
- Distiller: light up the GUI's spare overlay assets so the screen reflects machine state instead of staying static. The four spare regions in `distiller.png` were never wired up post-port, so the input/output tanks rendered as solid fluid rectangles with no gauge marks and the central pipe schematic between them showed only the dim background art whether the distiller was running, blocked on a full output, or idle. Three changes: (1) `GuiDistiller` now passes the `(0,161) 16x38` and `(17,161) 34x17` regions as gauge overlays to the input tank and the two output tanks respectively (mirroring what the heat exchanger does with the matching sub-images in its texture), so each tank renders the recipe-coloured fluid behind the proper gauge marks. (2) The bright `(212,0) 36x57` running overlay now blits over the central `(61,12)` schematic region whenever the distiller's `isActive` is true (a recipe is matched and power was actually extracted this tick), and the dim `(176,0) 36x57` "stuck" overlay blits there instead when a new `isStuck` flag is true. (3) `TileDistiller_BC8` tracks `isStuck` as `currentRecipe != null && (!canFillLiquid || !canFillGas)`, set inside the same `serverTick()` block that already evaluates the can-fill checks, cleared back to false when no recipe matches the input, included in the per-tick `needsSync` change check that triggers `level.sendBlockUpdated`, and persisted in `saveAdditional`/`loadAdditional` so a chunk reload preserves the visual state. The two centre overlays are mutually exclusive by construction — `isActive` requires `canFillLiquid && canFillGas`, the same fills `isStuck` negates — so the GUI just picks whichever is true.
- Distiller: surface every registered distillation recipe in JEI as its own entry under a new `buildcraftunofficial:distiller` category, mirroring the in-world `GuiDistiller` layout. Each `IDistillationRecipe` from `BuildcraftRecipeRegistry.refineryRecipes.getDistillationRegistry()` maps 1:1 to a JEI entry — unlike the heat exchanger no pairing is needed because the recipe interface already carries the full operation (one input fluid, one gas output, one liquid output, one MJ cost). The category background is the inner 170×74 region of `distiller.png` starting at `(3, 4)`, masking out the GUI's outer border and the player-inventory section so the JEI panel shows only the machine itself; tank slots are placed at the `GuiDistiller` coordinates shifted by the same `(-3, -4)` offset so they line up with the tank graphics inside the cropped texture (input `(41,19) 16x38`, gas output `(95,6) 34x17`, liquid output `(95,50) 34x17`). The per-recipe MJ cost (from `IDistillationRecipe.powerRequired()`, divided by `MjAPI.MJ` through `double` so sub-MJ recipes don't render as `0`) is drawn as `"X.X MJ"` in the strip below the tanks via the new `gui.jei.category.buildcraftunofficial.distiller.power` lang key, matching the in-GUI label colour `0xFF404040` — without it, two recipes with identical fluids but different power costs would be indistinguishable, and runtime power requirements wouldn't be discoverable from JEI at all. All three slots are real INPUT/OUTPUT (not RENDER_ONLY), so JEI lookups behave as players expect: pressing U on a fluid surfaces every distillation that consumes it; pressing R on a gas or liquid output surfaces every distillation that produces it. Each fluid slot also registers the matching bucket item as an invisible lookup ingredient (same `addBucketAlias` pattern the heat exchanger uses, deliberately duplicated as a private static rather than extracted — two callers don't yet justify a shared utility), so survival-mode lookups on bucket items resolve to the same recipes without adding the bucket to the visible cycle. The enumeration helper `enumerateDistillationRecipes` defensively skips entries with an empty input or with both outputs empty, guarding against config-disabled fluids that the runtime would refuse to run anyway. The distiller block (`BCFactoryItems.DISTILLER`) is registered as the single catalyst; pressing R on it surfaces the new category.
- Heat Exchanger: surface every valid pairing in JEI, drawn as the actual machine in miniature. A single category `buildcraftunofficial:heat_exchanger` enumerates the cartesian product of the heatable and coolable registries at plugin-registration time, keeping only pairs where `coolable.heatFrom() > heatable.heatFrom()` — exactly the runtime pairing rule in `TileHeatExchange.craft()` — and wraps each as a `HeatExchangerRecipePair` JEI entry. The category background is the inner 170×84 region of `heat_exchanger.png` starting at `(3, 4)`, masking out the GUI's outer border and the player-inventory section so the JEI panel shows only the machine itself; all four fluid tanks are positioned at the `GuiHeatExchange` coordinates shifted by the same `(-3, -4)` offset so they line up with the tank graphics inside the cropped texture (`(41,8)` END input, `(41,60)` START input, `(95,8)` END output, `(113,39)` START output). The four fluids are routed across the layout the same way `TileHeatExchange.craft()` routes them at runtime: heatable input at MID-LEFT, coolable input at TOP-LEFT, heatable output at TOP-RIGHT (the runtime `h_out = end.tankOutput`), coolable output at MID-RIGHT (the runtime `c_out = start.tankOutput`). The two flows therefore cross diagonally — the same fluid type sits on each diagonal — exactly as players see it in-world when cooling hot oil with cool oil or water (cool oil enters MID-LEFT, exits heated at TOP-RIGHT; hot oil enters TOP-LEFT, exits cooled at MID-RIGHT). Earlier per-side categories with cycling RENDER_ONLY opposite tanks broke this because the cycle could land on a non-symmetric coolant; an interim paired-recipe attempt put both outputs on the same row, so a water + hot-oil cooling pair drew the cooled cool oil at TOP-RIGHT instead of MID-RIGHT. All four slots are real INPUT/OUTPUT (not RENDER_ONLY), so JEI lookups behave as players expect: pressing U on lava surfaces every entry where lava is the heat source paired with various heatables; pressing U on water surfaces the single entry that pairs water with lava; pressing R on a hot oil fluid surfaces every entry that produces it on either side. Each fluid slot also registers the matching bucket item as an invisible lookup ingredient (`addInvisibleIngredients(role).add(fluid.getBucket())` when the fluid registers a bucket), so pressing R or U on a bucket of cool oil surfaces the same recipes as pressing R or U on the cool-oil fluid entry — what a survival-mode player actually has in hand. The recipe view stays clean — the bucket is invisible, so the slot continues to render as a fluid tank rather than cycling between fluid and item rendering. Recipes whose `out()` is null (water heating, lava cooling) skip the corresponding output slot — the GUI tank background remains visible behind the missing fluid. The heat exchanger block (`BCFactoryItems.HEAT_EXCHANGE`) is registered as the single catalyst.
- Filtered Buffer: render the empty-filter funnel icon ourselves in `GuiFilteredBuffer.drawBackgroundTexture` instead of via `Slot.setBackground(...)`. The container was passing `BCTransportSprites.EMPTY_FILTERED_BUFFER_SLOT.getResourceLocation()` (`buildcraftunofficial:gui/empty_filtered_buffer_slot`) to `setBackground`, but vanilla's `AbstractContainerScreen.renderSlot` resolves slot backgrounds against the GUI sprite atlas (`Sheets.GUI_SHEET`) only — and that sprite lives on the blocks atlas via the `gui/` directory source in `assets/minecraft/atlases/blocks.json`. The atlas miss made every empty filter slot in the top row paint as the magenta/black missing-texture sprite. Drawing it via `GuiIcon.drawAt(EMPTY_FILTERED_BUFFER_SLOT, ...)` routes through `SpriteHolderRegistry`'s multi-atlas walker and finds the sprite on the blocks atlas, matching how the bottom row's `NOTHING_FILTERED_BUFFER_SLOT` already rendered correctly. The `setBackground` call is dropped from `ContainerFilteredBuffer` since `Slot#getNoItemIcon` is the only consumer and the GUI now does the rendering.
- Heat Exchanger: fix four bugs introduced with the recent restore-restrictions / add-GUI work. (1) Each cycle's four tank operations (output fill ×2, input drain ×2) now run inside a single transaction that only commits when every operation transferred exactly the expected `min_common` amount; previously each operation opened its own root transaction and committed unconditionally, so any simulation/execution mismatch leaked input fluid (e.g. the user-reported 5mb of lava + 5mb of cool oil left over after processing 2 buckets each into 2 buckets of hot oil). The Distiller already ran its `extract` + two `insert`s under one transaction; this brings the exchanger to parity. Two new `HeatExchangerTester` cases cover the balanced-commit and undersized-fill-rolls-back paths. (2) `WidgetFluidTank` now falls back to filling an empty bucket from the player's inventory when the cursor itself is holding a full bucket of the tank's fluid — without this, a single-bucket cursor goes empty → full on the first click and then every follow-up click on an output tank does nothing (the tank rejects external inserts via `OutputTank.isValid` and the cursor bucket has no room to grow), making it look like the tank stopped giving up fluid after the first 1000mb. The fallback walks `player.getInventory()`, picks the first slot that exposes `Capabilities.Fluid.ITEM` with an empty resource, and `move`s a bucket-worth from the tank into that slot via a `forPlayerSlot(...).oneByOne()` access; the cursor stays untouched, mirroring the way 1.12.2's in-world right-click happily swallowed buckets in succession. (3) Client and server tank states now stay in sync after a server-side drain. `saveAdditional` only writes the `sectionInput` / `sectionOutput` keys when the corresponding tank is non-empty (a reasonable size optimisation), but the matching `loadAdditional` was guarded by `if (!fluid.isEmpty())` and so silently kept the previous client-side value whenever the server's `getUpdateTag` round-trip omitted the key. Visible symptom (per F3 debug overlay): server saying `tank_output = empty` while the client still rendered the tank as `1000 mB buildcraftunofficial:oil_heat_1`. The four tank loads now route through a small `loadTank` helper that always calls `set(0, ...)` — passing `(EMPTY, 0)` when the saved value was empty — so client tanks track every drain. New `testTankClearsWhenLoadedFromEmptySave` regression test covers the round trip. (4) The four bucket / fluid-shard slots are constructed as `new ItemHandlerSimple(4, 1)`, but `ItemHandlerSimple.getCapacityAsLong` was hard-coded to 64 — only the `insert(...)` path was capped at 1. The slot widget reads its max-stack via that capacity (through `SlotBase.getMaxStackSize`), so vanilla container code happily dropped a 64-stack of (modded, stackable) buckets into a slot meant to hold one. The auto-fill loop then ran `tryFillContainer` on the whole stack, got back a single filled bucket, and `setStackInSlot`'d it on top of the original — silently deleting the rest. Fix: `ItemHandlerSimple` now stores the configured max-stack in a `slotCapacity` field that `getCapacityAsLong` returns, so the slot widget enforces the real limit. As defence-in-depth, `drainSlotIntoTank` and `fillSlotFromTank` bail out when the slot somehow has more than one item, so even a regressed limit can't trigger the data loss again. New `testItemHandlerRespectsConfiguredMaxStackSize` regression covers both the capacity readout and the inserter cap.
- Restore the 1.12.2 Heat Exchanger fluid restrictions. The port lost both `tankInput.setFilter(isHeatant/isCoolant)` and `tankOutput.setCanFill(false)`, so any fluid (lava, water, oil, ...) could be inserted into any tank of the multi-block via a side-touching pipe, a bucket right-click, or a click in the GUI's tank widget — making the START accept coolants, the END accept heatants, and both output tanks accept arbitrary external fluids. The START's `tankInput` now overrides `isValid` to accept only fluids registered with `IRefineryRecipeManager.getHeatableRegistry()` (water, oil, fuel, ...) and the END's `tankInput` only fluids in `getCoolableRegistry()` (lava, hot oil, hot fuel, ...). Both output tanks are now instances of a new `OutputTank` subclass whose `isValid` returns false to externals; the craft loop fills them via `insertInternal`, which flips a guard for the duration of one `super.insert` call so recipe results still land. NBT load uses `set()` directly to bypass both the heatant/coolant filter and the output gate (saved fluid is trusted, and the recipe registry may not be ready during early chunk load). New `HeatExchangerTester` covers the OutputTank gate in three game-tests: external insert returns 0, internal insert succeeds for the same fluid, and the internal-insert flag resets after the call so a follow-up external insert is still rejected.
- Wire up the Heat Exchanger GUI. The `heat_exchanger.png` asset has been shipped since the port but no `Container`/`Screen`/`MenuType` ever pointed at it, so right-clicking only ever did bucket transfer. `TileHeatExchange` now implements `MenuProvider`, `BlockHeatExchange` opens the menu after a failed bucket interaction (matching the Distiller pattern), and right-clicking any block in the multi-block walks clockwise to find the START tile via the new `findStart()` helper so the menu always points at the section that owns the recipe state and the `endSection` link. The screen lays out four `GuiElementFluidTank` widgets in the 1.12.2 positions — END.tankInput as the top-left vertical (1.12.2 inCoolable, hot fluid), START.tankInput as the mid-left horizontal (inHeatable, cold fluid), END.tankOutput as the top-right horizontal (outHeated), START.tankOutput as the mid-right vertical (outCooled) — each with a tank-shape gauge overlay sourced from the spare `(0,171) 16x38` and `(17,171) 34x17` regions of the texture, and hover tooltips showing fluid name and `mB / capacity`; tanks whose section isn't formed yet are skipped so an isolated or partially-built exchanger still opens cleanly. The four 1.12.2 bucket / fluid-shard container slots are wired up as a `(4, 1)` `ItemHandlerSimple` on `TileHeatExchange`: every 5 ticks the START's `processContainerSlots()` drains filled containers in slots 0/1 into END.tankInput / START.tankInput respectively and fills empty containers in slots 2/3 from END.tankOutput / START.tankOutput, with `quickMoveStack` shift-click ordering between the four slots and the player inventory; slot contents persist via NBT and drop on block break. The center processing region between the tanks gets a new wipe-in/wipe-out overlay sourced from `(176,71) 54x71`: as `ExchangeSectionStart.progressState` advances OFF→PREPARING→RUNNING→STOPPING→OFF, the overlay wipes in from the left during PREPARING (visible width grows with `getProgress(partialTicks)`), holds at full 54×71 during RUNNING, then clears from the left during STOPPING (the visible region's left edge marches rightward) — visualizing the two fluids meeting in the middle and then dispersing. The vanilla title and inventory labels are suppressed because the layout is too cramped to fit either without overlapping the pipe schematic or the slot rows. Reuses the existing `block.buildcraftunofficial.heat_exchange` lang key for the menu title.
- Restore 1.12.2's coloured colour-name labels: the dye colour name in tooltips and gate descriptions (e.g. "Red" in "Red Extraction Preset" on the Emzuli pipe's gate, the colour names on paint actions and pipe-signal triggers, the coloured prefix on a paintbrush/wire/painted-pipe item name, and the lens/filter colour name) now renders in its matching `ChatFormatting` colour. `ColourUtil.getTextFullTooltip(DyeColor)` was returning plain title-cased text post-port; now it wraps the name in the appropriate colour code (using `COLOUR_TO_FORMAT`, which already remaps black to `DARK_GRAY` for tooltip visibility) and a trailing reset, mirroring the existing `Direction` overload. Removed the redundant manual `.withStyle(convertColourToTextFormat(...))` calls at the four call sites that were compensating for the missing formatting (paintbrush, pipe holder, wire, emzuli paint button tooltip), so all colour-label callers — including the gate-action and gate-trigger descriptions that hadn't been compensating — pick up the colouring through a single source.
- Move the entire visible logic-gate body from chunk-mesh-baked geometry to per-frame BlockEntityRenderer rendering, eliminating the client-side FPS spikes (~6 ms → 80–95 ms) that occurred whenever a gate changed state — every gate ON/OFF transition (e.g. a timer-driven gate firing every 10 ticks), every redstone toggle on a driven block (the lamp's `setBlock(UPDATE_ALL)` cascading back through the pipe's `neighborChanged`), and every block placement within the 27-section dirty cube around a pipe network. The chunk-mesh path put `logic.isOn` and the gate's static parts (base material brick, logic icon, modifier dots) into the chunk geometry hash, so each transition invalidated the cached pipe geometry and forced a re-mesh whose per-vertex AO + lighting cost scaled linearly with the gate count nearby. The new `PlugGateRenderer` (using the existing `IPlugDynamicRenderer` plumbing the pulsar already had) renders all gate geometry per-frame from the live `PluggableGate.logic.isOn`, `PlugGateBaker.bake` returns an empty quad list, and `KeyPlugGate.equals/hashCode` exclude `active` so the geometry hash is stable across ON/OFF. Chunks with N gates re-mesh at the same speed as chunks with 0 gates; gates render at proper world brightness with vanilla face shading by sampling lightmap from `pipePos.relative(plug.side)` and keeping `createFace`'s correct outward normals. Several smaller fixes ride along: `Pipe.updateConnections` only schedules its network update when `connected` actually changes (cuts a feedback loop where the lamp's UPDATE_NEIGHBORS bounced back through the pipe and forced a full BE sync every redstone cycle), `TilePipeHolder.replacePluggable` rebuilds the wire system when an `IWireEmitter` pluggable is added or removed (long-standing bug where placing a gate after wires already existed meant the wires never glowed because the wire system was built without that emitter element), and the four `Block.UPDATE_ALL` → `Block.UPDATE_CLIENTS` calls on the pipe-holder render-sync paths drop a duplicate server-side `updateNeighborsAt` cascade. Pulsar pulse-state transitions ride a 3-byte custom payload via `IPipeHolder.sendMessage` instead of forcing a full BE sync via `scheduleNetworkUpdate`.
- Bump NeoForge to `26.1.2.30-beta` (was `.17`). Pulls in mod-loading restructure, `ValueInput#keySet` / `FlatLevelSource` / `ComposedModelState` / `TagEmptyCondition` fixes, fail-fast on configs whose defaults don't accept their own validators, and refreshed Sponge Mixin / FancyModLoader / NeoForge Bus dependencies. None of the breaking changes in the range (GLM priority system, `BreakBlockEvent` split, `IBaseRailBlockExtension` hook removal) touch this codebase.
- Restore the six "face the &lt;direction&gt; side" gate actions for iron, wood, and daizuli pipes; the action icons were missing from the gate GUI's action picker and triggering them did nothing. Each pipe filters which directions are offered via its existing `canFaceDirection` rule (iron and wood require an active connection, daizuli accepts all six).
- Restore the 16 "Paint Items &lt;colour&gt;" gate actions on lapis and daizuli pipes. Two regressions: no pipe added them to its gate's possible-actions list (so they never appeared in the action picker), and the sprite holder pointed at `items/paintbrush/<colour>` (legacy 1.12.2 path) instead of the canonical `item/paintbrush/<colour>` so the icons rendered as the magenta missing-texture box even after the actions were re-registered. Triggering one now sets the pipe's paint colour the same way the wrench does.
- Teach `SpriteHolderRegistry.SpriteHolder.getSprite()` to walk multiple texture atlases (blocks → items → GUI) instead of hard-coding `LOCATION_BLOCKS`. Modern Minecraft (1.21+) split the historical single atlas into per-purpose atlas pages; sprites referenced by item models — like the paintbrush colour textures gate "Paint Items" actions reuse for their icons — auto-stitch into `textures/atlas/items.png` and were unreachable from the blocks-atlas-only lookup, rendering as the missing-texture box on the guide-book contents page.
